;;; I A prayer to Vachaspati for divine illumination and help.
1.1.1 Now may Vachaspati assign to me the strength and powers of Those Who, wearing every shape and form, the triple seven, are wandering round.
1.1.2 Come thou again, Vachaspati, come with divine intelligence. Vasoshpati, repose thou here. In me be Knowledge, yea, in me.
1.1.3 Here, even here, spread sheltering arms like the two bow-ends strained with cord. This let Vachaspati confirm. In me be Knowledge, yea, in me.
1.1.4 Vachaspati hath been invoked: may he invite us in reply. May we adhere to Sacred Lore. Never may I be reft thereof.
;;; II A charm against dysentery
1.2.1 We know the father of the shaft, Parjanya, liberal nourisher, Know well his mother: Prithivi, Earth with her manifold designs.
1.2.2 Do thou, O Bowstring, bend thyself around us: make my body stone. Firm in thy strength drive far away malignities and hateful things.
1.2.3 When, closely clinging round the wood, the bowstring sings triumph to the swift and whizzing arrow, Indra, ward off from us the shaft, the missile.
1.2.4 As in its flight the arrow's point hangs between earth and firmament, So stand this Munja grass between ailment and dysenteric ill!
;;; III A charm against constipation and suppression of urine
1.3.1 We know the father of the shaft, Parjanya strong with hundred powers: By this may I bring health unto thy body: let the channels pour their burthen freely as of old.
1.3.2 We know the father of the shaft, Mitra, the Lord of hundred powers: By this, etc.
1.3.3 We know the father of the shaft, Varuna, strong with hundred powers: By this, etc.
1.3.4 We know the father of the shaft, the Moon endowed with hundred powers: By this, etc.
1.3.5 We know the father of the shaft, the Sun endowed with hundred powers: By this may I bring health unto thy body: let the channels pour their burthen freely as of old.
1.3.6 Whate'er hath gathered, as it flowed, in bowels, bladder, or in groins, Thus let the conduit, free from check, pour all its burthen as of old.
1.3.7 I lay the passage open as one cleaves the dam that bars the lake: Thus let, etc.
1.3.8 Now hath the portal been unclosed as, of the sea that holds the flood: Thus let, etc.
1.3.9 Even as the arrow flies away when loosened from the archer's bow, Thus let the burthen be discharged from channels that are checked no more.
;;; IV To the waters, for the prosperity of cattle
1.4.1 Along their paths the Mothers go, sisters of priestly ministrants, Blending their water with the mead.
1.4.2 May yonder Waters near the Sun, or those wherewith the Sun is joined, Send forth this sacrifice of ours.
1.4.3 I call the Waters, Goddesses, hitherward where our cattle drink: The streams must share the sacrifice.
1.4.4 Amrit is in the Waters, in the Waters balm. Yea, through our praises of the Floods, O horses, be ye fleet and strong, and, O ye kine, be full of strength.
;;; V To the waters, for strength and power
1.5.1 Ye, Waters, truly bring us bliss: so help ye us to strength and power That we may look on great delight.
1.5.2 Here grant to us a share of dew, that most auspicious dew of yours, Like mothers in their longing love.
1.5.3 For you we fain would go to him to whose abode ye send us forth, And, Waters, give us procreant strength.
1.5.4 I pray the Floods to send us balm, those who bear rule o'er precious things, And have supreme control of men.
;;; VI To the waters, for health and wealth
1.6.1 The Waters be to us for drink, Goddesses, for our aid and bliss: Let them stream health and wealth to us.
1.6.2 Within the Waters--Soma thus hath told me--dwell all balms that heal, And Agni, he who blesseth all.
1.6.3 O Waters, teem with medicine to keep my body safe from harm, So that I long may see the Sun.
1.6.4 The Waters bless us, all that rise in desert lands or marshy pools! Bless us the Waters dug from earth, bless us the Waters brought in jars, bless us the Waters of the Rains!
;;; VII To Indra and Agni, for the detection and destruction of evil spirits
1.7.1 Bring the Kimidin hither, bring the Yatudhana self-declared For Agni, God, thou, lauded, hast become the Dasyu's slaughterer.
1.7.2 O Jatavedas, Lord Supreme, controller of our bodies, taste The butter, Agni, taste the oil: make thou the Yatudhanas mourn.
1.7.3 Let Yatudhanas mourn, let all greedy Kimidins weep and wail: And, Agni, Indra, may ye both accept this sacrifice of ours.
1.7.4 May Agni seize upon them first, may strong-armed Indra drive them forth: Let every wicked sorcerer come hither and say, Here am I.
1.7.5 Let us behold thy strength, O Jatavedas. Viewer of men, tell us the Yatudhanas. Burnt by thy heat and making declaration let all approach this sacrifice before thee.
1.7.6 O Jatavedas, seize, on them: for our advantage art thou born: Agni, be thou our messenger and make the Yatudhanas wail.
1.7.7 O Agni, bring thou hitherward the Yatudhanas bound and chained. And afterward let Indra tear their heads off with his thunder- bolt.
;;; VIII To Indra, Brihaspati, Soma and Agni, for the destruction of sorcerers
1.8.1 This sacrifice shall bring the Yatudhanas as the flood brings foam: Here let the doer of this deed woman or man, acknowledge it.
1.8.2 This one hath come confessing all: do ye receive him eagerly. Master him thou, Brihaspati; Agni and Soma, pierce him through.
1.8.3 O Soma-drinker, strike and bring the Yatudhana's progeny: Make the confessing sinner's eyes fall from his head, both right and left.
1.8.4 As thou, O Agni Jatavedas, knowest the races of these secret greedy beings, So strengthened by the power of prayer, O Agni, crushing them down a hundred times destroy them.
;;; IX Benediction on a King at his inauguration
1.9.1 May Indra, Pushan, Varuria, Mitra, Agni, benignant Gods, maintain this man in riches. May the Adityas and the Vive Devas set and support him in supremest lustre.
1.9.2 May light, O Gods, be under his dominion, Agni, the Sun, all; that is bright and golden. Prostrate beneath our feet his foes and rivals. Uplift him to the. loftiest cope of heaven.
1.9.3 Through that most mighty prayer, O Jatavedas, wherewith thou. broughtest milk to strengthen Indra, Even therewith exalt this man, O Agni, and give him highest rank among his kinsmen.
1.9.4 I have assumed their sacrifice, O Agni, their hopes, their glory,. and their riches' fulness. Prostrate beneath our feet his foes and rivals. Uplift him to the- loftiest cope of heaven.
;;; X Absolution of a sinner after intercession with Varuna
1.10.1 This Lord is the Gods' ruler; for the wishes of Varuna the King must be accomplished. Therefore, triumphant with the prayer I utter, I rescue this man from the Fierce One's anger.
1.10.2 Homage be paid, King Varuna, to thine anger; for thou, dread God, detectest every falsehood. I send a thousand others forth together: let this thy servant live a hundred autumns.
1.10.3 Whatever falsehood thou hast told, much evil spoken with the tongue, I liberate thee from the noose of Varuna the righteous King.
1.10.4 I free thee from Vaisvanara, from the great surging flood of sin. Call thou thy brothers, Awful One! and pay attention to our prayer.
;;; XI A charm to be used at child-birth
1.11.1 Vashat to thee. O Pushan At this birth let Aryaman the Sage perform as Hotar-priest, As one who bears in season let this dame be ready to bring forth her child.
1.11.2 Four are the regions of the sky, and four the regions of the earth: The Gods have brought the babe; let them prepare the woman for the birth.
1.11.3 Puerpera (infatem) detegat: nos uterum aperimus. Lexa teipsam, puerpera. Tu, parturiens! emitte eum non carni, non adipi, non medullae adhaerntem.
1.11.4 Descendat viscosa placenta, cani, comedenda placenta; decidat placenta.
1.11.5 Diffindo tuum urinae ductum, diffindo vaginam, diffindo inguina. Matrem natumque divido, puerum a placenta divido: decidat placenta.
1.11.6 Sicut ventus, sicut mens, sicut alites volant, sic, decem mensium puer, cum placenta descende: descendat placenta.
;;; XII A prayer to Lightning, against fever, headache, and cough
1.12.1 Born from the womb, brought forth from wind and from the cloud, the first red bull comes onward thundering with the rain. Our bodies may he spare who, cleaving, goes straight on; he who, a single force, divides himself in three.
1.12.2 Bending to thee who clingest to each limb with heat, fain would we worship thee with offered sacrifice, Worship with sacrifice the bends and curves of thee who with a vigorous grasp hast seized on this one's limbs.
1.12.3 Do thou release this man from headache, free him from cough which has entered into all his limbs and joints. May he, the child of cloud, the offspring of the wind, the whiz- zing lighting, strike the mountains and the trees.
1.12.4 Well be it with my upper frame, well be it with my lower parts. With my four limbs let it be well. Let all my body be in health.
;;; XIII A prayer to Lightning, for happiness
1.13.1 Homage to thee, the Lightning's flash, homage to thee, the Thunder's roar! Homage to thee, the Stone which thou hurlest against the undevout!
1.13.2 Homage to thee, Child of the Flood whence thou collectest fer- vent heat! Be gracious to our bodies, give our children happiness and joy.
1.13.3 Yea, homage be to thee, O Offspring of the Flood! Homage we pay to thee, the dart and fiery flame: For well we know thy secret and sublimest home, where thou as central point art buried in the sea.
1.13.4 Thou, Arrow, which the host of Gods created, making it strong and mighty for the shooting, Be gracious, lauded thus, to our assembly. To thee, that Arrow,. be our homage, Goddess!
;;; XIV A woman's incantation against a rival
1.14.1 As from the tree a wreath, have I assumed her fortune and her fame: Among her kinsfolk long may she dwell, like a mountain broadly- based.
1.14.2 King Yama, let this maiden be surrendered as a wife to thee: Bound let her be meanwhile within, her mother's, brother's, father's house.
1.14.3 Queen of thy race is she, O King: to thee do we deliver her. Long with her kinsfolk may she sit, until her hair be white with age.
1.14.4 With Asita's and Kasyapa's and Gaya's incantation, thus As sisters pack within a chest, I bind and tie thy fortune up.
;;; XV A prayer for the prosperity of an institutor of sacrifice
1.15.1 Let the streams, flow together, let the winds and birds assembled come. Let this my sacrifice delight them always. I offer it with duly mixt oblation.
1.15.2 Come to my call, Blent Offerings, come ye very nigh. And, singers, do ye strengthen and increase this man. Hither come every animal: with this man let all wealth abide.
1.15.3 All river founts that blend their streams for ever inexhaustible-- With all these confluent streams of mine we make abundant riches flow.
1.15.4 All streams of melted butter, and all streams of water and of milk With all these confluent streams of mine we make abundant riches flow.
;;; XVI A prayer and charm against demons
1.16.1 May potent Agni who destroys the demons bless and shelter us. From greedy fiends who rise in troops at night-time when the moon is dark.
1.16.2 Varuna's benison hath blessed the lead, and Agni strengthens it. Indra hath given me the lead: this verily repels the fiends.
1.16.3 This overcomes Vishkandha, -this drives the voracious fiends away: By means of this have I, o'erthrown all the Pisachi's demon brood.
1.16.4 If thou destroy a cow of ours, a human being, or a steed, We pierce thee with this piece of lead so that thou mayst not slay our men.
;;; XVII A charm to be used at venesection
1.17.1 Those maidens there, the veins, who run their course in robes of ruddy hue, Must now stand quiet, reft of power, like sisters who are brotherless.
1.17.2 Stay still, thou upper vein, stay still, thou lower, stay, thou midmost one, The smallest one of all stands still: let the great vessel e'en be still.
1.17.3 Among a thousand vessels charged with blood, among a thousand veins, Even these the middlemost stand still and their extremities have rest.
1.17.4 A mighty rampart built of sand hath circled and encompassed you: Be still, and quietly take rest.
;;; XVIII A charm to avert evil spirits of misfortune and to secure prosperity
1.18.1 We drive away the Spotted Hag, Misfortune, and Malignity: All blessings to our children then! We chase Malignity away.
1.18.2 Let Savitar, Mitra, Varuna, and Aryaman drive away Stinginess from both the hands and feet: May Favour, granting us her bounties, drive her off. The Gods created Favour for our happiness.
1.18.3 Each fearful sign upon thy body, in thyself, each inauspicious mark seen in thy hair, thy face, All this we drive away and banish with our speech. May Savitar the God graciously further thee.
1.18.4 Antelope-foot, and Bullock-tooth, Cow-terrifier, Vapour-form, The Licker, and the Spotted Hag, all these we drive away from us.
;;; XIX A prayer for protection from arrows and for the punishment of enemies
1.19.1 Let not the piercers find us, nor let those who wound discover us. O Indra, make the arrows fall, turned, far from us, to every side.
1.19.2 Turned from us let the arrows fall, those shot and those that will be shot. Shafts of the Gods and shafts of men, strike and transfix mine enemies:
1.19.3 Whoever treateth us as foes, be he our own or strange to us, a kinsman or a foreigner, May Rudra with his arrows pierce and slay these enemies of mine.
1.19.4 The rival and non-rival, he who in his hatred curses us May all the deities injure him! My nearest, closest mail is prayer.
;;; XX A prayer to Soma, the Maruts, Mitra, and Varuna, for protection
1.20.1 May it glide harmless by in this our sacrifice, O Soma, God! Maruts, be gracious unto us. Let not disaster, let not malison find us out; let not abominable guiles discover us.
1.20.2 Mitra and Varuna, ye twain, turn carefully away from us The deadly dart that flies to-day, the missile of the wicked ones.
1.20.3 Ward off from this side and from that, O Varuna, the deadly dart: Give us thy great protection, turn the lethal weapon far away.
1.20.4 A mighty Ruler thus art thou, unconquered, vanquisher of foes, Even thou whose friend is never slain, whose friend is never over- come.
;;; XXI A prayer to Indra for protection
1.21.1 Lord of the clans, giver of bliss, fiend-slayer, mighty o'er the foe, May Indra, Soma-drinker, go before us, Bull, who brings us peace.
1.21.2 Indra, subdue our enemies, lay low the men who fight with us: Down into nether darkness send the man who shows us enmity:
1.21.3 Strike down the fiend, strike down the foes, break thou asunder Vritra's jaws. O Indra, Vritra-slayer, quell the wrath of the assailing foe.
1.21.4 Turn thou the foeman's thought away, his dart who fain would conquer us: Grant us thy great protection; keep his deadly weapon far away.
;;; XXII A charm against jaundice
1.22.1 As the Sun rises, let thy sore disease and yellowness depart. We compass and surround thee with the colour of a ruddy ox.
1.21.2 With ruddy hues we compass thee that thou mayst live a leng- thened life: So that this man be free from harm, and cast his yellow tint away.
1.21.3 Devatyas that are red of hue, yea, and the ruddy-coloured kine, Each several form, each several force--with these we compass thee about.
1.21.4 To parrots and to starlings we transfer thy sickly yellowness: Now in the yellow-coloured birds we lay this yellowness of thine.
;;; XXIII A charm against leprosy
1.23.1 O Plant, thou sprangest up at night, dusky, dark-coloured, black in hue! So, Rajani, re-colour thou these ashy spots, this leprosy.
1.23.2 Expel the leprosy, remove from him the spots and ashy hue: Let thine own colour come to thee; drive far away the specks of white.
1.23.3 Dark is the place of thy repose, dark is the place thou dwellest in: Dusky and dark, O Plant, art thou: remove from him each speck and spot.
1.23.4 I with my spell have chased away the pallid sign of leprosy, Caused by infection, on the skin, sprung from the body, from the bones.
;;; XXIV A charm against leprosy
1.24.1 First, before all, the strong-winged Bird was born;; thou wast the gall thereof. Conquered in fight, the Asuri took then the shape and form of plants.
1.24.2 The Asuri made, first of all, this medicine for leprosy, this banisher of leprosy. She banished leprosy, and gave one general colour to the skin.
1.24.3 One-coloured, is thy mother's name, One-coloured is thy father called: One-colour-maker, Plant! art thou: give thou one colour to this man.
1.24.4 Sama who gives one general hue was formed and fashioned from the earth: Further this work efficiently. Restore the colours that were his.
;;; XXV A prayer to fever, as a charm against his attacks
1.25.1 When Agni blazed when he had pierced the Waters, whereat the Law-observers paid him homage, There, men assever, was thy loftiest birthplace: O Fever, yield- ing to our prayer avoid us.
1.25.2 If thou be fiery glow, or inflammation, or if thy birthplace call for chips of fuel, Rack is thy name, God of the sickly yellow! O Fever, yielding to our prayer avoid us.
1.25.3 Be thou distress, or agonizing torment, be thou the son King Varuna hath begotten, Rack isthy name, God of the sickly yellow! O Fever, yielding to our prayer avoid us.
1.25.4 I offer homage to the chilly Fever, to his fierce burning glow I offer homage. Be adoration paid to Fever coming each other day, the third, of two days running.
;;; XXVI A prayer for protection, guidance, and prosperity
1.26.1 Let that Destructive Weapon be far distant from us, O ye Gods; far be the Stone ye wont to hurl.
1.26.2 Our friend be that Celestial Grace, Indra and Bhaga be our friends, and Savitar with splendid Wealth.
1.26.3 Thou, Offspring of the waterflood, ye Maruts, with your sun- bright skins, give us protection reaching far.
1.26.4 Further us rightly, favour ye our bodies with your gracious love. Give thou our children happiness.
;;; XXVII A charm to obtain invisibility
1.27.1 There on the bank those Vipers lie, thrice-seven, having cast their skins: Now we with their discarded sloughs bind close and cover up the eyes of the malicious highway thief.
1.27.2 Far let her go, cutting her way, brandishing, as it were, a club: Diverted be the new-born's mind: ne'er are the wicked prosperous.
1.27.3 Not many have had power enough; the feeble ones have not prevailed, Like scattered fragments of a reed: ne'er are the wicked pros- perous.
1.27.4 Go forward, feet, press quickly on, bring to the house of him who pays. Unconquered and unplundered, let Indranf, foremost, lead the way.
;;; XXVIII A prayer to Agni for the destruction of evil spirits
1.28.1 God Agni hath come forth to us, fiend-slayer, chaser of disease, Burning the Yatudhanas up, Kimidins, and deceitful ones.
1.28.2 Consume the Yatudhanas, God! meet the Kimidins with thy flame: Burn up the Yatudhanis as they face thee, thou whose path is black!
1.28.3 She who hath cursed us with a curse, or hath conceived a murderous sin; Or seized our son to take his blood, let her devour the child she bare.
1.28.4 Let her, the Yatudhani eat son, sister, and her daughter's. child. Now let the twain by turns destroy the wild-haired Yatudhanis- and crush down Arayis to the earth!
;;; XXIX A charm to secure the supremacy of a dethroned King
1.29.1 With that victorious Amulet which strengthened Indra's power- and might Do thou, O Brahmanaspati, increase our strength for kingly sway.
1.29.2 Subduing those who rival us, subduing all malignities, Withstand the man who menaces, and him who seeks to injure- us.
1.29.3 Soma and Savitar the God have strengthened and exalted thee: All elements have aided thee, to make thee general conqueror.
1.29.4 Slayer of rivals, vanquisher, may that victorious Amulet Be bound on me for regal sway and conquest of mine enemies.
1.29.5 Yon Sun hath mounted up on high, and this my word hath mounted up That I may smite my foes and be slayer of rivals, rivalless.
1.29.6 Destroyer of my rivals, strong, victorious, with royal sway, May I be ruler of these men, and King and sovran of the folk.
;;; XXX A benediction on a King at his consecration
1.30.1 Guard and protect this man, all Gods and Vasus. Over him keep- ye watch and ward, Adityas. Let not death reach him from the hands of brothers from hands of aliens, or of human beings.
1.30.2 Listen, one-minded, to the word I, utter, the sons, O Gods, among you, and the fathers! I trust this man to all of you: preserve him happily, and to length of days conduct him.
1.30.3 All Gods who dwell on earth or in the heavens, in air, within. the plants, the beasts, the waters, Grant this man life to full old age, and let him escape the hundred other ways of dying.
1.30.4 You, claiming Anuyajas or Prayajas, sharers, or not consumers, of oblation, You, to whom heaven's five regions are apportioned, I make companions at his sacred sessions.
;;; XXXI A prayer for protection and general prosperity
1.31.1 Here will we serve with sacrifice the great Controllers of the world, The four immortal Warders who protect the regions of the sky.
1.31.2 Ye, Guardians of the regions, Gods who keep the quarters of the heavens, Rescue and free us from the bonds of Nirriti, from grief and woe!
1.31.3 I, free from stiffness, serve thee with oblation, not lame I sacri- fice with oil and fatness. Let the strong Warder God, who keeps the regions bring to us hither safety and well-being.
1.31.4 Well be it with our mother and our father, well be it with our cows, and beasts, and people. Ours be all happy fortune, grace, and favour. Long, very long may we behold the sunlight.
;;; XXXII In praise of Heaven and Earth
1.32.1 Ye people, hear and mark this well: he will pronounce a mighty prayer: That which gives breathing to the Plants is not on earth nor in, the heaven.
1.32.2 Their station, as of those who rest when weary, is in midmost air: The base whereon this world is built, the sages know or know it not.
1.32.3 What the two trembling hemispheres and ground produced and fashioned forth. This All, is ever fresh to-day, even as the currents of the sea.
1.32.4 This All hath compassed round the one, and on the other lies at rest. To Earth and all-possessing Heaven mine adoration have I paid.
;;; XXXIII To the Waters, for health and happiness
1.33.1 May they, the golden-hued, the bright, the splendid, they wherein Savitar was born and Agni, They who took Agni as a germ, fair-coloured, the Waters, bring felicity and bless us!
1.33.2 They in the midst whereof King Varuna moveth, viewing men's righteous and unrighteous dealing. They who took Agni as a germ, fair-coloured,--those Waters bring felicity and bless us!
1.33.3 Whom the Gods make their beverage in heaven, they who wax manifold in air's mid-region, They who took Agni as a germ, fair-coloured,--those Waters bring felicity and bless us!
1.33.4 Ye Waters, with auspicious eye behold me: touch ye my skin with your auspicious body. May they, the bright and pure, distilling fatness, those Waters, bring felicity and bless us.
;;; XXXIV A young man's love-charm
1.34.0 1. From honey sprang this Plant to life; with honey now we dig thee up. Make us as sweet as honey, for from honey hast thou been pro- duced.
1.34.2 My tongue hath honey at the tip, and sweetest honey at the root: Thou yieldest to my wish and will, and shalt be mine and only mine.
1.34.3 My coming in is honey-sweet and honey-sweet, my going forth: My voice and words are sweet: I fain would be like honey in my look.
1.34.4 Sweeter am I than honey, yet more full of sweets than licorice: So mayst thou love me as a branch full of all sweets, and only me.
1.34.5 Around thee have I girt a zone of sugar-cane to banish hate. That thou mayst be in love with me, my darling never to depart.
;;; XXXV A charm to ensure long life and glory to the wearer of an amulet
1.35.1 This Ornament of Gold which Daksha's children bound, with benevolent thoughts, on Satanika, This do I bind on thee for life, for glory, for long life lasting through a hundred autumns.
1.35.2 This man no fiends may conquer, no Pisachas, for this is might of Gods, their primal offspring. Whoever wears the Gold of Daksha's children hath a long lengthened life among the living.
1.35.3 The light, the power, the lustre of the Waters, the strength of Trees, and all their forceful vigour, We lay on him as powers abide in Indra: so let him wear this Gold and show his valour.
1.35.4 With monthly and six-monthly times and seasons, with the full year's sweet essence do we fill thee, May Indra, Agni, and all Gods together, showing no anger, grant thee what thou wishest.
;;; I Glorification of the prime cause of all things
2.1.1 Vena beholds That Highest which lies hidden, wherein this All resumes one form and fashion. Thence Prisni milked all life that had existence: the hosts that know the light with songs extolled her.
2.1.2 Knowing Eternity, may the Gandharva declare to us that highest secret station. Three steps thereof lie hidden in the darkness: he who knows these shall be the father's father.
2.1.3 He is our kinsman, father, and begetter: he knows all beings and all Ordinances. He only gave the Gods their appellations: all creatures go to him to ask direction.
2.1.4 I have gone forth around the earth and heaven, I have approached the first-born Son of Order. He, putting voice, as 'twere, within the speaker, stands in the world, he, verily is Agni.
2.1.5 I round the circumjacent worlds have travelled to see the far- extended thread of Order. Wherein the Gods, obtaining life eternal, have risen upward to one common birthplace.
;;; II A charm to ensure success in gambling
2.2.1 Lord of the World, divine Gandharva, only he should be honoured in the Tribes and worshipped. Fast with my spell, celestial God, I hold thee. Homage to thee! Thy home is in the heavens.
2.2.2 Sky-reaching, like the Sun in brightness, holy, he who averts from us the Gods' displeasure. Lord of the World, may the Gandharva bless us, the friendly God who only must be worshipped.
2.2.3 I came, I met these faultless, blameless beings: among the Apsarases was the Gandharva. Their home is in the sea--so men have told me,--whence they come quickly hitherward and vanish.
2.2.4 Thou, Cloudy! ye who follow the Gandharva Visva-vasu, ye, Starry! Lightning-Flasher! You, O ye Goddesses, I truly worship.
2.2.5 Haunters of darkness, shrill in voice, dice-lovers, maddeners of the mind To these have I paid homage, the Gandharva's wives, Apsarases.
;;; III A water-cure charm
2.3.1 That little spring of water which is running downward from the hill I turn to healing balm for thee that thou mayst be good medicine.
2.3.2 Hither and onward! Well! Come on! Among thy hundred remedies Most excellent of all art thou, curing disease and morbid flow.
2.3.3 The Asuras bury deep in earth this mighty thing that healeth wounds. This is the cure for morbid flow, this driveth malady away.
2.3.4 The emmets from the water-flood produce this healing medicine: This is the cure for morbid flow, this driveth malady away.
2.3.5 Mighty is this wound-healing balm: from out the earth was it produced. This is the cure for morbid flow, this driveth malady away.
2.3.6 Bless us the Waters! be the Plants auspicious! May Indra's thunderbolt drive off the demons. Far from us fall the shafts they shoot against us!
;;; IV A charm to ensure health and prosperity by wearing an amulet
2.4.1 For length of life, for mighty joy, uninjured, ever showing strength. We wear Vishkandha's antidote, the Amulet of Jangida.
2.4.2 Amulet of a thousand powers, Jangida save us, all around. From Jambha, and from Viara, Vishkandha, and tormenting pain.
2.4.3 This overcomes Vishkandha, this chases the greedy fiends away: May this our panacea, may Jangida save us from distress.
2.4.4 With Jangida that brings delight, Amulet given by the Gods, We in the conflict overcome Vishkandha and all Rakshasas.
2.4.5 May Cannabis and Jangida preserve me from Vishkandha,-- that Brought to us from the forest, this sprung from the saps of husbandry.
2.4.6 This Amulet destroys the might of magic and malignity: So may victorious Jangida prolong the years we have to live.
;;; V Invitation to, and praise of Indra
2.5.1 Indra, be gracious, drive thou forth, come, Hero, with thy two bay steeds. Taste the libation, hither, enjoying meath and the hymn, come, fair, to the banquet.
2.5.2 O Indra, even as one athirst, fill thee with meath as 'twere from heaven. Sweet-toned, the raptures of this juice have come to thee as to the light.
2.5.3 Swift-conquering Indra, Mitra like, smote, as a Yati, Vritra dead. Like Bhrigu he cleft Vala through, and quelled his foes in Soma's rapturous joy.
2.5.4 O Indra, let the juices enter thee. Fill full thy belly, sate thee, mighty one! Let the hymn bring thee. Hear thou my call, accept the song I sing, here, Indra, with thy friends enjoy thyself, to height of rapture.
2.5.5 Now will I tell the manly deeds of Indra, the first that he achieved, the thunder-wielder. He slew the Dragon, then disclosed the waters, and cleft the channels of the mountain torrents.
2.5.6 He slew the Dragon lying on the mountain: his heavenly bolt of thunder Tvashtar fashioned. Like lowing kine in rapid flow descending the waters glided downward to the ocean.
2.5.7 Impetuous as a bull he chose the Soma, and quaffed the juices in three sacred beakers. Maghavan grasped the thunder for his weapon, and smote to death this first-born of the dragons.
;;; VI A prayer to Agni for protection
2.6.1 Half-years and seasons strengthen thee, O Agni, the years, and all the Verities, and Rishis! Flash forth with thy celestial effulgence: illumine all four regions of the heavens.
2.6.2 Kindle thee, Agni, and make this man prosper: rise up erect for high and happy fortune. Agni, be those uninjured who adore thee, and may thy priests be glorious and no others.
2.6.3 These Brahmans have elected thee, O Agni: be thou propitious in our sacred chamber. Slayer of rivals, Agni, quell our foemen: watch in our house with care that never ceases.
2.6.4 Seize, Agni, on thy power and firmly hold it: contend thou with the Friend by way of friendship. Placed in the centre of our fellows, Agni, flash forth to be invoked by kings around thee.
2.6.5 Past those who slay, past enemies, past thoughtless men, past those who hate, Yea, Agni, hear us safe past all distresses: give thou us opulence with men about us.
;;; VII A counter-charm against imprecation and malignity
2.7.1 Hated by sinners, sprung from Gods, this Plant that turns the curse away Hath washed from me all curses, as water makes clean from spot and stain.
2.7.2 All curses of a rival, each curse of a female relative, Curse uttered by an augry priest, all these we tread beneath our feet.
2.7.3 Spread on the surface of the earth, downward from heaven thy root depends: With this that hath a thousand joints keep thou us safe on every side.
2.7.4 Guard on all sides this woman, guard my children, us, and all our wealth! Let not malignity o'ercome, nor adversaries conquer us.
2.7.5 Upon the curser fall his curse! Dwell we with him whose heart is true! We split the cruel villain's ribs whose evil eye bewitches us.
;;; VIII A charm against hereditary disease (kshetriya)
2.8.1 Twin Stars of happy omen, named Releasers, have gone up. May they Loose, of inherited disease, the uppermost and lowest bond.
2.8.2 Vanish this Night, extinct in Dawn! Let those who weave their spells depart. So let the plague-destroying Plant remove inherited disease.
2.8.3 With straw of barley tawny-brown in colour with its silvery ears, with stalk and stem of Sesamum- So let the plague-destroying Plant remove inherited disease.
2.8.4 Let homage to thy ploughs be paid, our homage to the pole and yokes. So let the plague-destroying Plant remove inherited disease.
2.8.5 Homage to men with blinking eyes, homage to those who hear and act! To the Field's Lord be homage paid. So let the plague-destroying Plant remove inherited disease.
;;; IX A charm to cure dangerous disease
2.9.1 Free this man, Dasavriksha! from the demon, from Grahi who hath seized his joints and members, And raise him up again, O Tree, into the world of living men.
2.9.2 He hath arisen and come once more, rejoined the band of those who live. May he become the sire of sons, and of all men most fortunate.
2.9.3 He hath returned to consciousness, rejoined the living's firm abodes, For hundred leeches are in this, yea, and a thousand healing herbs.
2.9.4 The Gods, the Brahman-priests, and plants observed the way to gather thee: All deities described the way men gather thee upon the earth.
2.9.5 Let him who made it also heal: he, truly, is the deftest leech. Pure, with a leech he verily shall give thee medicines that heal.
;;; X Absolution and benediction
2.10.1 From family sickness, kinsmen's curse, Destruction, from Druh, from Varuna's noose I free and save thee. With spell and prayer I make thee pure and sinless: to thee be both, the Earth and Heaven, auspicious!
2.10.2 Gracious to thee be Agni with the Waters, let Soma with the Plants be kind and bless thee. From family sickness, kinsmen's curse, Destruction, from Druh, from Varuna's noose I thus release thee.
2.10.3 May kind Wind strengthen thee in air's mid-region, to thee may heaven's four quarters be auspicious. From family sickness, kinsmen's curse, Destruction, from Druh, from Varuna's curse I thus release thee.
2.10.4 These Goddesses, four regions of the heavens, on whom the Sun looks kindly, wives of Vata-- From family sickness, kinsmen's curse, Destruction, from Druh, from Varuna's noose I thus release thee.
2.10.5 For long life, in the midst of these I set thee. Away pass Nirriti, away Consumption! From family sickness, kinsmen's curse, Destruction, from Druh, from Varuna's noose I thus release thee.
2.10.6 Thou hast been freed from Phthisis and from trouble, from shame, and from the snare of Druh and Grain. From family sickness, kinsmen's curse, Destruction, from Druh, from Varuna's noose I thus release thee.
2.10.7 Joy hast thou found, and left ill-will behind thee: thou hast attained the happy world of virtue. From family sickness, kinsmen's curse, Destruction, from Druh, from Varuna's noose I thus release thee.
2.10.8 The Gods have freed from, sinfulness, redeeming the Sun, the Law from darkness and from Grahi. From family sickness, kinsmen's curse, Destruction, from Druh, from Varuna's noose I thus release thee. With spell and prayer I make thee pure and sinless: to thee be both, the Earth and Heaven, auspicious!
;;; XI Counter-charm, with an amulet, against an enemy's spell
2.11.1 Dart against dart, destroyer of destruction, thou art the missile sent to meet the missile. Reach thy superior, thou; surpass thine equal.
2.11.2 Sraktya art thou, an Amulet art thou, a counter-charm of spells, Reach thy superior, thou; surpass thine equal.
2.11.3 Use spells against the man we hate, against the man who hateth us. Reach thy superior, thou; surpass thine equal.
2.11.4 A prince art thou, giver of speech, thou art our bodies' strong defence. Reach thy superior, thou; surpass thine equal.
2.11.5 Fulgent art thou, and splendid, thou art heavenly lustre, thou art light. Reach thy superior, thou; surpass thine equal.
;;; XII A prayer for vengeance on a malicious rival worshipper
2.12.1 The spacious Firmament, and Earth and Heaven, the Field's Queen, and the wonderful Wide-Strider, Yea, the broad middle air which Vata guardeth, may these now burn with heat while I am burning.
2.12.2 Listen to this, ye Gods who merit worship. Hymns here are sung for me by Bharadvaja. Bound in the noose may he be doomed to trouble whoever mars this that our mind hath purposed.
2.12.3 Hear this my call, O Indra, Soma-drinker, as with a burning heart I oft invoke thee. I smite, as 'twere a tree felled with a hatchet, the man who marreth this my plan and purpose.
2.12.4 Together with thrice-eighty Sama-singers, Angirases, and Vasus, and Adityas, May the felicity of the Fathers guard us. I seize that man with fire that Gods have kindled.
2.12.5 O Heaven and Earth, regard me with your favour, and, all ye Gods, stand on my side and help me. Angirases, Fathers worthy of the Soma! woe fall on him who, caused the hateful outrage!
2.12.6 Whoever either scorns us, O ye Maruts, or blames devotion which we now are paying. Let his own wicked deeds be fires to burn him. May Heaven consume the man who hates devotion.
2.12.7 Thy sevenfold vital breath, thine eight marrows I rend away with prayer. With Agni as thine envoy, go, prepared, to Yama's dwelling place.
2.12.8 In Jatavedas kindled flame I set the place assigned to thee. Let fire consume thy body, and thy voice go to the general breath.
;;; XIII A youth's Investiture ceremony (godanam)
2.13.1 Strength-giver, winning lengthened life, O Agni, with face and back shining with molten butter, Drink thou the butter and fair milk and honey, and, as a sire his sons, keep this man safely.
2.13.2 For us surround him, cover him with splendour, give him long life, and death when age removes him. The garment hath Brihaspati presented to Soma, to the King, to w rap about him.
2.13.3 Thou for our w eal hast clothed thee in the mantle: thou hast become our heifers' guard from witchcraft. Live thou a hundred full and plenteous autumns, and wrap thee in prosperity of riches.
2.13.4 Come hither, stand upon the stone: thy body shall become a stone. The Universal Gods shall make thy life a hundred autumns long.
2.13.5 So may the Universal Gods protect thee, whom we divest of raiment worn aforetime. So after thee, well-formed and growing stronger, be born a multitude of thriving brothers.
;;; XIV A charm to banish vermin and noxious creatures
2.14.1 Forth from the hall the bold, the sharp, the greedy one, the single-voiced, Sadanvas, and all progeny of Chanda we exterminate.
2.14.2 We drive you forth from cattle-shed, from axle, from within the wain, Ye daughters of Magundi, we frighten and chase you from out homes.
2.14.3 Yonder let the Arayis dwell, there where that house is down below. Let utter indigence and all the Yatudhanis settle there.
2.14.4 May Bhutapati drive away, and Indra, the Sadanvas hence. Let Indra with his bolt quell those who sit upon our dwelling's floor.
2.14.5 Whether ye be of farm and field, or whether ye be sent by men, Or be ye sprung from Dasyu race, vanish, Sadanvas, and begone.
2.14.6 I have gone round their homes as runs a fleet-foot racer round the post, And in all races conquered you. Vanish, Sadanvas, and begone.
;;; XV A charm against fear
2.16.1 As Heaven and Earth are not afraid, and never suffer loss or harm, Even so, my spirit, fear not thou.
2.16.2 As Day and Night are not afraid, nor ever suffer loss or harm, Even so, my spirit, fear not thou.
2.16.3 As Sun and Moon are not afraid, nor ever suffer loss or harm. Even so. my spirit, fear not thou.
2.16.4 As Brahmanhood and Princely Power fear not, nor suffer loss, or harm, Even so, my spirit, fear not thou.
2.16.5 As Truth and Falsehood have no fear, nor ever suffer loss or harm, Even so, my spirit, fear not thou.
2.16.6 As What Hath Been and What Shall Be fear not, nor suffer loss or harm, Even so, my spirit, fear not thou.
;;; XVI A prayer for general protection
2.16.1 Guard me from death, Inhaling and Exhaling! All bliss to you!
2.16.2 Guard me from overhearing, Earth and Heaven! All hail to you!
2.16.3 Do thou, O Surya, with thine eye protect me! All hail to thee!
2.16.4 Agni Vaisvanara, with all Gods preserve me! All hail to thee!
2.16.5 Preserve me with all care. O All-Sustainer! All hail to thee!
;;; XVII A prayer to an amulet for health and strength
2.17.1 Power art thou, give me power. All hail!
2.17.2 Might art thou, give me might. All hail!
2.17.3 Strength art thou, give me strength. All hail!
2.17.4 Life art thou, give me life. All hail!
2.17.5 Ear art thou, give me hearing! Hail!
2.17.6 Eye art thou, give me eyes. All hail!
2.17.7 Shield art thou, shield me well. All hail
;;; XVIII A charm against enemies, goblins, and other evil creatures
2.18.1 Destruction of the foe art thou, give me the scaring of my foes. All hail!
2.18.2 The rival's ruiner art thou, give me to drive my rivals off. All hail!
2.18.3 Arayis' ruiner art thou, give me to drive Arayis off. All hail!
2.18.4 Pisa-chas' ruiner art thou, give me to drive Pisachas off. All hail!
2.18.5 Sadanvas' ruiner art thou, give me to drive Sadanvas off. All hail!
;;; XIX A prayer to Agni for aid against an enemy
2.19.1 Burn thou, O Agni, with that heat of thine against the man who hates us, whom we hate.
2.19.2 Flame thou, O Agni, with that flame of thine against the man who hates us, whom we hate.
2.19.3 Shine out, O Agni, with that sheen of thine against the man who hates us, whom we hate.
2.19.4 Blaze thou, O Agni, with that blaze of thine against the man who hates us, whom we hate.
2.19.5 O Agni, with the splendour that is thine darken the man who hates us, whom we hate. It appears that hymns 20-23 were omitted--JBH
;;; XXIV A charm against the magic arts of fiends
2.24.1 O Serabhaka, Serabha, back fall your arts of witchery! Back, Kimidins! let your weapon fall. Eat your possessor; eat ye him who sent you forth;
2.24.2 Srvridhaka, O Sevridha, back fall your arts of witchery! Back, Kimidins! let your weapon fall, etc.
2.24.3 O Mroka, Anumroka, back return your arts of witchery! Back, Kimidins! let your weapon fall, etc.
2.24.4 O Sarpa, Anusarpa, back return your arts of witchery! Back, 'i Kimidins! let your weapon fall, etc.
2.24.5 Back fall your witcheries, Jurni! back your weapon, ye Kimidinis, etc.
2.24.6 Back fall your spells, Upabdi! back your weapon, ye Kimidinis, etc.
2.24.7 Back fall your witchcrafts, Arjuni! your weapon, ye Kimidinis, etc,
2.24.8 Back, O, Bharuji! fall your charms, your weapon, ye Kimidinis. Eat your possessor; eat ye him who sent you forth; eat your own flesh.
;;; XXV A charm against fiends who cause abortion
2.25.1 The Goddess Prisniparni hath blest us, and troubled Nirriti. Fierce crusher of the Kanvas she: her have I gained, the mighty one.
2.25.2 Victorious in the olden time this Prisniparni was brought forth: With her I cleave, as 'twere a bird's, the head of the Detestables.
2.25.4 The hateful fiend who drinks the blood, and him who take away the growth, The Kanva who devours the germ, quell, Prisniparni! and! destroy.
2.25.5 Drive and imprison in a hill these Kanvas harassers of life: Follow them Prisniparni, thou Goddess, like fire consuming. them.
2.25.6 Drive thou away these Kanvas, drive the harassers of life afar. Whither the shades of darkness go, I send the fiends who feed on flesh.
;;; XXVI A benediction on homeward coming cattle
2.26.1 Let them come home, the cattle that have wandered, whom Vayu hath delighted to attend on, Whose forms and figures are well known to Tvashtar. These cows let Savitar drive within this stable.
2.26.2 Let the beasts stream together to this cow-pen. Brihaspati who knoweth lead them hither! Let Sinivali guide the foremost homeward. When they have come, Anumati! enclose them.
2.26.3 Together stream the cattle! stream together horses and the men! Hitherward press all growth of grain! I offer sacrifice with mixt oblation.
2.26.4 I pour together milk of kine, with butter blending strength and juice. Well sprinkled be our men, as true to me as cows are to their herd!
2.26.5 Hither I bring the milk of cows, hither have brought the juice of corn. Hitherward have our men been brought, hitherward to this house our wives.
;;; XXVII A charm against an opponent in debate
2.27.1 Let not the enemy win the cause! Strong and predominant art thou. Refute mine adversary's speech. Render them dull and flat, O Plant.
2.27.2 The strong-winged bird discovered thee, the boar unearthed thee with his snout. Refute mine adversary's speech. Render them dull and flat, O Plant.
2.27.3 Yea, Indra laid thee on his arm, to cast the Asuras to the ground. Refute mine adversary's speech. Render them dull and flat, O Plant.
2.27.4 Indra devoured the Pata plant that he might lay the Asuras low. Refute mine adversary's speech! Render them dull and flat, O Plant.
2.27.5 With this I overcome my foes as Indra overcame the wolves. Refute mine adversary's speech! Render them dull and flat, O Plant.
2.27.6 O Rudra, Lord of Healing Balms, dark-crested, skilful in thy work!-- Refute mine adversary's speech. Render them dull and flat, O Plant.
2.27.7 Indra, defeat the speech of him who meets us with hostility. Comfort us with thy power and might. Make me superior in debate.
;;; XXVIII A prayer for a boy's long and happy life
2.28.1 This Child, Old Age! shall grow to meet thee only: none of the hundred other deaths shall harm him. From trouble caused by friends let Mitra guard him, as a kind mother guards the son she nurses.
2.28.2 Mitra or Varuna the foe-destroyer, accordant, grant him death in course of nature! Thus Agni, Hotar-priest, skilled in high statutes, declareth all the deities' generations.
2.28.3 Thou art the Lord of all terrestrial cattle, of cattle born and to be born hereafter. Let not breath drawn or breath emitted fail him. Let not his friends, let not his foemen slay him.
2.28.4 Let Heaven thy father and let Earth thy mother, accordant, give thee death in course of nature, That thou mayst live on Aditi's bosom, guarded, a hundred winters, through thy respirations.
2.28.5 Lead him to life, O Agni, and to splendour, this dear child, Varuna! and thou King Mitra! Give him protection, Aditi! as a mother; All Gods, that his be life of long duration;
;;; XXIX A benediction on a sick man
2.29.1 Gods, give him all that earth hath best with bodily strength and happy fate. Agni and Surya grant him life, Brihaspati give him eminence!
2.29.2 Bestow thou life on him, O Jatavedas. Store him with future progeny, O Tvashtar. Send him, O Savitar, full growth of riches. Let this thy servant live a hundred autumns.
2.29.3 May this our prayer bring strength and goodly offspring. Give, both of you one-minded, strength and riches. Let him with might win fields and victory, Indra! setting beneath his feet the rest, his rivals.
2.29.4 As Indra's gift, by Varuna instructed the fierce one came to us sent by the Maruts. Let him, O Heaven and Earth, rest in your bosom. Let him not hunger, let him not be thirsty.
2.29.5 Ye twain endowed with vigour, grant him vigour. Ye who are rich in milk, give milk to feed him. These twain have given him vigour, Earth and Heaven, and all the Gods, the Maruts, and the Waters.
2.29.6 With health-bestowing drops thine heart I comfort: all-bright again, and undiseased, enjoy them. Drest in like robes let these two drink the mixture, wearing the Asvins' form as an illusion.
2.29.7 Erst Indra, wounded, made this strengthening portion, eternal food: thine is it, here presented. With this live full of vigour through the autumns. Let not thy strength be drained. Leeches have helped thee.
;;; XXX A man's love-charm
2.30.1 As the wind shake this Tuft of Grass hither and thither on the ground. So do I stir and shake thy mind, that thou mayst be in love with me, my darling, never to depart.
2.30.2 Ye, Asvins, lead together, ye unite and bring the loving pair. Now have the fortunes of you twain, now have your vows and spirits met.
2.30.3 When eagles, calling out aloud, are screaming in the joy of health, Then to my calling let her come, as to the arrow's neck the shaft.
2.30.4 Let what is inward turn outside, let what is outward be within: Seize and possess, O Plant, the mind of maidens rich in every charm.
2.30.5 Seeking a husband she hath come! and I came longing for a wife: Even as a loudly-neighing steed may fate and fortune have I met.
;;; XXXI A charm against all sorts of worms
2.31.1 With Indra's mighty millstone, that which crushes worms of every sort, I bray and bruise the worms to bits like vetches on the grinding stone.
2.31.2 The Seen and the Invisible, and the Kururu have I crushed: Alandus, and all Chhalunas, we bruise to pieces with our spell.
2.31.3 I kill Alandus with a mighty weapon: burnt or not burnt they now have lost their vigour . Left or not left, I with the spell subdue them: let not a single worm remain uninjured.
2.31.4 The worm that lives within the ribs, within the bowels, in the head. Avaskava and Borer, these we bruise to pieces with the spell.
2.31.5 Worms that are found on mountains, in the forests, that live in plants, in cattle, in the waters, Those that have made their way within our bodies,--these I destroy, the worms' whole generation.
;;; XXXII A charm against worms or bots in cows
2.32.1 Uprising let the Sun destroy, and when he sinketh, with his beams. The Worms that live within the cow.
2.32.2 The four-eyed worm, of every shape, the variegated, and the white I break and crush the creature's ribs, and tear away its head besides.
2.32.3 Like Atri I destroy you, Worms! in Kanva's, Jamadagni's way: I bray and bruise the creeping things to pieces with Agastya's* spell.
2.32.4 Slain is the sovran of these Worms, yea, their controlling lord is slain: Slain is the Worm, his mother slain, brother and sister both are slain.
2.32.5 Slain are his ministers, and slain his followers and retinue: Yes, those that seemed the tiniest things, the Worms have all been put to death.
2.32.6 I break in pieces both thy horns wherewith thou pushest here and there: I cleave and rend the bag which holds the venom which is* stored in thee.
;;; XXX I
2.33.1 From both thy nostrils, from both eyes, from both thine ears, and from thy chin, Forth from thy brain and tongue I root Consumption seated in thy head.
2.33.2 Forth from the neck and from the nape, from dorsal vertebrae and spine. From arms and shoulder-blades I root Consumption seated in thine arms.
2.33.3 Forth from thy heart and from thy lungs, from thy gall-bladder and thy sides, From kidneys, spleen and liver thy Consumption we eradicate.
2.33.4 From bowels and intestines, from the rectum and the belly, I Extirpate thy Consumption, from flanks, navel and mesentery.
2.33.5 Forth from thy thighs and from thy knees, heels and the fore- parts of thy feet. Forth from thy loins and hips I draw Consumption setted in thy loins.
2.33.6 Forth from thy marrows and thy bones, forth from thy tendons and thy veins I banish thy Consumption, from thy hands, thy fingers, and thy nails.
2.33.7 In every member, every hair, in every joint wherein it lies, We with the exorcising spell of Kasyapa drive far away Con- sumption settled in thy skin.
;;; XXXIV A prayer accompanying an animal sacrifice
2.34.1 May this, of all the beasts that Pasupati rules, Lord of animals,. quadruped and biped, Come, purchased, to the sacrificial portion. May growth of wealth attend the sacrificer.
2.34.2 Loosing the seed of future-time existence, give good success, O Gods, to him who worships. May what is present, duly brought, the victim, go to the deities' beloved region.
2.34.3 Those who are looking, deep in meditation, on the bound ani- mal with eye and spirit To them, the first, may Agni, God, give freedom, rejoicing in his creatures, Visvakarman.
2.34.4 Tame animals of every shape, though varied in colour, manifold. alike in nature To them, the first, may Vayu, God, give freedom, Prajapati. rejoicing in his creatures.
2.34.5 Let those who know receive before all others the vital breath proceeding from the body. Go to the sky. Stay there with all thy members. By paths which Gods have travelled go to Svarga.
;;; XXXV Expiation for an imperfectly performed sacrifice
2.35.1 We who enjoying it have grown no richer, for whom the sacred altar-fires have sorrowed, We who compounded with deficient worship,--may Visvakarman make our service prosper.
2.35.2 Rishis have called the sacrifice's patron amerced through sin, sorrowing for his offspring. Those drops of meath whereof the missed enjoyment,--may Visvakarman with those drops unite us.
2.35.3 Regarding niggard churls as Soma-drinkers, skilful in sacrifice, weak at the meeting, Whatever sin the captive hath committed, do thou for weal release him, Visvakarman!
2.35.4 Awful are Rishis: unto them be homage, and to their eye and truthfulness of spirit! Loud homage to Brihaspati, O mighty! Homage to thee, O Visvakarman! Guard us.
2.35.5 The eye of sacrifice, source, and beginning--with voice, ear, spirit unto him I offer. To this our sacrifice wrought by Visvakarman may the Gods come gracious and kindly-hearted.
;;; XXXVI A charm to secure a husband for a marriageable girl
2.36.1 To please us may the suitor come, O Agni, seeking this maid and bringing us good fortune. Approved by wooers, lovely in assemblies, may she be soon made happy with a husband.
2.36.2 As bliss beloved by Soma, dear to Prayer, and stored by Arya- man, With the God Dhatar's truthfulness I work the bridal oracle.
2.36.3 O Agni, may this woman find a husband. Then verily King Soma makes her happy. May she bear sons, chief lady of the household, blessed and bearing rule beside her consort.
2.36.4 As this lair, Maghavan! that is fair to look on was dear to wild things as a pleasant dwelling, So may this woman here be Bhaga's darling. Loved by her lord and prizing his affection.
2.36.5 Mount up, embark on Bhaga's ship, the full, the inexhaustible, Thereon bring hitherward to us the lover whom thou fain wouldst wed.
2.36.6 Call out to him, O Lord of Wealth! Make thou the lover well- inclined. Set each on thy right hand who is a lover worthy of her choice.
2.36.7 Here is the Bdellium and the gold, the Auksha and the bliss are here: These bring thee to the husbands, so to find the man whom thou. wouldst have.
2.36.8 May Savitar lead and bring to thee the husband whom thy heart desires. O Plant, be this thy gift to her!
;;; I A prayer or charm for the defeat and destruction of enemies in battle
3.1.1 Let the wise Agni go against our foemen, burning against ill-will and imprecation Let him bewilder our opponents' army, Let Jatavedas smite and make them handless.
3.1.2 Mighty are ye for such a deed, O Maruts. Go forward, overcome them and destroy them. The Vasus slew, and these were left imploring. Wise Agni as our messenger assail them!
3.1.3 O Maghavan, O Indra, thou who slayest fiends, and, Agni, thou, Burn, both of you, against these men, the foeman's host that threatens us.
3.1.4 Shot down the slope, with thy two tawny coursers, forth go thy bolt, destroying foes, O Indra! Slay those who fly, slay those who stand and follow. On every side fulfil these men's intention.
3.1.5 Indra, bewilder thou the foemen's army. With Agni's, Vata's furious rush drive them away to every side.
3.1.6 Let Indra daze their army. Let the Maruts slay it with their might. Let Agni take their eyes away, and let the conquered host retreat.
;;; II A rifaccimento or recension of I
3.2.1 May Agni, he who knows, our envoy, meet them, burning against ill-will and imprecation. May he bewilder our opponent's senses. May Jatavedas smite and make them handless.
3.2.2 This Agni hath bewildered all the senses that were in your hearts: Now let him blast you from your home, blast you away from every side.
3.2.3 Dazing their senses, Indra, come hitherward with the wish and will. With Agni's, Vata's furious rush drive them to every side away.
3.2.4 Vanish, ye hopes and plans of theirs, be ye confounded, all their thoughts! Whatever wish is in their heart, do thou expel it utterly.
3.2.5 Bewildering the senses of our foemen, seize on their bodies and depart, O Apva! Go meet them, flame within their hearts and burn them. Smite thou the foes with darkness and amazement.
3.2.6 That army of our enemies, O Maruts, that comes against us with' its might, contending-- Meet ye and strike it with unwelcome darkness so that not one. of them may know another.
;;; III A charm for the restoration of an expelled king
3.3.1 Loudly he roared. Here let him labour deftly. Spread, Agni, over spacious earth and heaven. Let Maruts who possesses all treasures yoke thee. Bring him who reverently paid oblations.
3.3.2 Though he be far away, let the red horses bring Indra, bring the sage to us and friendship, Since with Sautramani Gods for him o'erpower Gayatri, Brihati, and hymn of praises.
3.3.3 King Varuna call thee hither from the waters! From hills and mountains Soma call thee hither! Let Indra call thee hither to these people. Fly hither to these people as a falcon.
3.3.4 May the hawk bring the man who must be summoned, from far away, in alien land, an exile. May both the Asvins make thy pathway easy. Come, and unite yourselves with him, ye Kinsmen.
3.3.5 Let thine opponents call thee back. Thy friends have chosen, thee again. Indra and Agni, all the Gods have kept thy home amid the tribe.
3.3.6 He who disputes our calling thee, be he a stranger or akin. Drive him, O Indra, far away, and do thou bring this man to us.
;;; IV A benediction at the election of a king
3.4.1 To thee hath come the kingship with its splendour: On! shine as lord, sole ruler of the people. King! let all regions of the heavens invite thee. Here let men wait on thee and bow before thee.
3.4.2 The tribesmen shall elect thee for the Kingship, these five celestial regions shall elect thee. Rest on the height and top of kingly power: thence as a mighty man award us treasures.
3.4.3 Kinsmen, inviting thee, shall go to meet thee, with thee go Agni as an active herald. Let women and their sons be friendly-minded. Thou mighty one, shalt see abundant tribute.
3.4.4 First shall the Asvins, Varuna and Mitra, the Universal Gods, and Maruts call thee. Then turn thy mind to giving gifts of treasures, thence, mighty one, distribute wealth among us.
3.4.5 Speed to us hither from the farthest distance. Propitious unto thee be Earth and Heaven. Even so hath Varuna this King asserted, he who himself hath called thee: come thou hither.
3.4.6 Pass to the tribes of men. O Indra, Indra. Thou the Varunas hast been found accordant. To his own place this one hath called thee, saying, Let him adore the Gods and guide the clansmen.
3.4.7 The Bounteous Paths in sundry forms and places, all in accord, have given thee room and comfort. Let all of these in concert call thee hither. Live thy tenth decade here, a strong kind ruler.
;;; V A King's address to an amulet which is to strengthen his authority
3.5.1 This Parna-Amulet hath come, strong and destroying with its strength my rivals. The power of the Gods, the plants' sweet essence, may it incite me ceaselessly with vigour.
3.5.2 O Parna-Amulet, in me set firmly might and opulence. Within the compass of my rule may I be rooted and supreme.
3.5.3 That dear mysterious Amulet which Gods have set within the tree, May the Gods grant to me to wear together with extended life.
3.5.4 As Indra's gift, by Varuna instructed, Parna hath come, the mighty strength of Soma: This would I, brightly shining, love and cherish for long life lasting through a hundred autumns.
3.5.5 The Parna-Charm hath come to me for great security from ill. That I may be exalted, yea, above the wealth of Aryaman.
3.5.6 Sagacious builders of the car, cleaver and skilful artisans,-- Make all the men on every side, Parna, obedient to my will
3.5.7 The kings and makers of the kings, troop-leaders, masters of the horse, Make all the men on every side, Parna, obedient to my will.
3.5.8 Thou, Parna, art my body's guard, man kin my birth to me a man. With splendour of the circling year I bind thee on me, Amulet!
;;; VI Address to an amulet which is to secure the defeat of the wearer's enemies
3.6.1 Masculine springs from masculine, Asvattha grows from Kha- dira, May it destroy mine enemies, who hate me and whom I detest.
3.6.2 Crush down my foes, Asvattha! Rend, O Burster, those who storm and rage, With Indra, slayer of the fiends, with Mitra and with Varuna.
3.6.3 As thou hast rent and torn apart, Asvattha! in the mighty sea, So rend asundar all those men who hate me and whom I detest.
3.6.4 Thou who like some victorious bull displayest thy surpassing might, With thee, with thee, Asvattha! we would overcome our enemies.
3.6.5 Nirriti bind them with the bonds of Death which never may be loosed. Mine enemies, Asvattha! those who hate me and whom I detest.
3.6.6 As thou, Asvastha!, mountest on the trees and overthrowest them, So do thou break my foeman's head asunder and o'erpower him.
3.6.7 Let them drift downward like a boat torn from the rope that fastened it. There is no turning back for those whom He who Cleaves hath driven away.
3.6.8 With mental power I drive them forth, drive them with intellect and charm. We banish and expel them with the branch of an Asvattha tree.
;;; VII A charm with an amulet of buck horn to drive away hereditary disease
3.7.1 The fleet-foot Roebuck wears upon his head a healing remedy. Innate disease he drives away to all directions with his horn.
3.7.2 With his four feet the vigorous Buck hath bounded in pursuit of thee. Unbind the chronic sickness, Horn! deeply inwoven in the heart.
3.7.3 That which shines younder, like a roof resting on four walls, down on us,-- Therewith from out thy body we drive all the chronic malady,
3.7.4 May those twin stars, auspicious, named Releasers, up in yonder sky. Loose of the chronic malady the uppermost and lowest bond.
3.7.5 Water, indeed, hath power to heal, Water drives malady away. May water--for it healeth all--free thee from permanent disease.
3.7.6 Hath some prepared decoction brought inveterate disease on thee, I know the balm that healeth it: we drive the malady away.
3.7.7 What time the starlight disappears, what time the gleams of Dawn depart, May evil fortune pass from us, the chronic sickness disappear.
;;; VIII A charm to secure the submission, love, and fidelity of kinsmen
3.8.1 Let Mitra come, arranging, with the Seasons, lulling the Earth to rest with gleams of splendour. And so let Agni, Varuna, and Vayu make our dominion tran- quil and exalted.
3.8.2 May Indra, Tvashtar hear my word with favour, may Dhatar, Rati, Savitar accept it. I call the Goddess Aditi, heroes' mother, that I may be the centre of my kinsmen.
3.8.3 Soma I call, and Savitar with homage, and all the Adityas in the time of contest. Long may this fire send forth its splendour, lighted by kinsmen uttering no word against me.
3.8.4 Here, verily, may you stay: go ye no farther. The strong Herd, Lord of Increase, drive you hither! To please this man may all the Gods together come unto you and be as dames who love him.
3.8.5 We bend together all your minds, your vows and purposes we bend. We bend together you who stand apart with hopes opposed to ours.
3.8.6 I with my spirit seize and hold your spirits. Follow with thought and wish my thoughts and wishes. I make your hearts the thralls of my dominion; on me attendant come thy way I guide you.
;;; IX A charm against rheumatism (vishkondha)
3.9.1 Heaven is the sire, the mother Earth, of Karsapha and Visapha. As ye have brought them hither, Gods! so do ye move therm hence away.
3.9.2 The bands hold fast without a knot: this is the way that Manu- used. I make Vishkandha impotent as one emasculateth bulls.
3.9.3 Then to a tawny-coloured string the wise and skilful bind a brush. Let bandages make impotent the strong and active Kabava.
3.9.4 Ye who move active in your strength like Gods with Asuras' magic powers, Even as the monkey scorns the dogs, Bandages! scorn the Kabava.
3.9.5 Yea, I will chide thee to thy shame, I will disgrace the Kabava. Under our impracations ye, like rapid cars, shall pass away.
3.9.6 One and one hundred over earth are the Vishkandhas spread abroad. Before these have they fetched thee forth. Vishkandha quelling Amulet.
;;; X A new year prayer
3.10.1 The First hath dawned. With Yama may it be a cow to pour forth milk. May she be rich in milk and stream for us through many a com- ing year.
3.10.2 May she whom Gods accept with joy, Night who approacheth. as a cow, She who is Consort of the Year, bring us abundant happiness
3.10.3 Thou whom with reverence we approach, O Night, as model of the Year, Vouchsafe. us children long to live; bless us with increase of our wealth.
3.10.4 This same is she whose light first dawned upon us: she moves established in the midst of others: Great powers and glories are contained within her: a first-born bride, she conquers and bears children.
3.10.5 Loud was the wooden pass-gear's ring and rattle, as it made annual oblation ready. First Ashtaka! may we be lords of riches, with goodly children and good men about us.
3.10.6 The shrine of Ila flows with oil and fatness: accept, O Jatavedas, our oblations. Tame animals of varied form and colour--may all the seven abide with me contented.
3.10.7 Come thou to nourish me and make me prosper. Night! may the favour of the Gods attend us. Filled full, O Ladle, fly thou forth. Completely filled fly back again. Serving at every sacrifice bring to us food and energy.
3.10.8 This Year hath come to us, thy lord and consort, O Ekashtaka. Vouchsafe us children long to live, bless us with increase of our wealth.
3.10.9 The Seasons, and the Seasons' Lords I worship, annual parts and groups. Half years, Years, Months, I offer to the Lord of all existing things.
3.10.10 I offer to the Seasons, to their several groups, to Months, to Years. Dhatar, Vidhatar, Fortune, to the lord of all existing things.
3.10.11 With fatness and libation we sacrifice and adore the Gods. Wealthy in kine may we retire to rest us in our modest homes.
3.10.12 Ekashtaka, burning with zealous fervour, brought forth her babe the great and glorious Indra. With him the Gods subdued their adversaries: the Lord of Might became the Dasyus' slayer.
3.10.13 Indra's and Soma's mother! thou art daughter of Prajapati. Satisfy thou our hearts' desires. Gladly accept our sacrifice.
;;; XI A charm for the recovery of a dangerously sick man
3.11.1 For life I set thee free by this oblation both from unmarked'. decline and from consumption: Or if the grasping demon have possessed him, free him from her,. O Indra, thou and Agni!
3.11.2 Be his days ended, be he now departed, be he brought very near to death already, Out of Destruction's lap again I bring him, save him for life to last a hundred autumns.
3.11.3 With sacrifice thousand-eyed and hundred-powered, bringing a hundred lives, have I restored him, That Indra through the autumns may conduct him safe to the farther shore of all misfortune.
3.11.4 Live, waxing in thy strength a hundred autumns, live through a hundred springs, a hundred winters! Indra, Agni, Savitar, Brihaspati give thee a hundred! With hundred-lived oblation have I saved him,
3.11.5 Breath, Respiration, come to him, as two car-oxen to their stall! Let all the other deaths, whereof men count a hundred, pass away.
3.11.6 Breath, Respiration, stay ye here. Go ye not hence away from him, Bring, so that he may reach old age, body and members back again.
3.11.7 I give thee over to old age, make thee the subject of old age. Let kindly old age lead thee on. Let all the other deaths, whereof men count a hundred, pass away!
3.11.8 Old age hath girt thee with its bonds even as they bind a bull with rope. The death held thee at thy birth bound with a firmly-knotted noose, Therefrom, with both the hands of Truth, Brihaspati hath loose- ned thee.
;;; XII A benediction on a newly built house
3.12.1 Here, even here I fix my firm-set dwelling; flowing with fatness may it stand in safety. May we approach thee, House! with all our people, uncharmed and goodly men, and dwell within thee,
3.12.2 Even here, O House, stand thou on firm foundation, wealthy in horses, rich in kine and gladness. Wealthy in nourishment. in milk and fatness, rise up for great felicity and fortune.
3.12.3 A spacious store, O House, art thou, full of clean corn and lofty-roofed. Let the young calf and little boy approach thee, and milch-kine streaming homeward in the evening.
3.12.4 This House may Savitar and Vayu stablish, Brihaspati who knows the way, and Indra. May the moist Maruts sprinkle it with fatness, and may King Bhaga make our corn-land fruitful.
3.12.5 Queen of the home! thou, sheltering, kindly Goddess, wast sta- blished by the Gods in the beginning. Clad in thy robe of grass be friendly-minded, and give us wealth with goodly men about us.
3.12.6 Thou Pole, in ordered fashion mount the pillar. Strong, shining forth afar, keep off our foemen. House! let not those who dwell within thee suffer. Live we with all our men, a hundred autumns.
3.12.7 To this the tender boy hath come, to this the calf with all the beasts, To this crock of foaming drink, hither with jars of curdled milk.
3.12.8 Bring hitherward, O dame, the well-filled pitcher, the stream of molten butter blent with nectar. Bedew these drinkers with a draught of Amrit. May all our hopes' fulfilment guard this dwelling.
3.12.9 Water that kills Consumption, free from all Consumption, here I bring. With Agni, the immortal one, I enter and possess the house.
;;; XIII A benediction on a newly cut water channel
3.13.1 As ye, when Ahi had been slain, flowed forth together with a roar, So are ye called the Roaring Ones: this, O ye Rivers, is your name.
3.13.2 As driven forth by Varuna ye swiftly urged your rolling waves, There Indra reached you as you flowed; hence ye are still the Water-floods.
3.13.3 Indra restrained you with his might. Goddesses, as ye glided on Not in accordance with his will: hence have ye got the name of Streams.
3.13.4 One only God set foot on you flowing according to your will, The mighty ones breathed upward fast: hence; Water is the name they bear.
3.12.5 Water is good, water indeed is fatness. Agni and Soma, truly, both bring water. May the strong rain of those who scatter sweetness come helpful unto me with breath and vigour.
3.12.6 Then verily, I see, yea, also hear them: their sound approaches me, their voice comes hither. Even then I think I am enjoying Amrit, what time I drink my fill of you, gold coloured!
3.12.7 Here, O ye Waters, is your heart. Here is your calf, ye holy ones. Flow here, just here, O mighty Streams, whither I now am lead- ing you.
;;; XIV A benediction on a cattle pen
3.14.1 A Pen wherein to dwell at ease, abundance and prosperity, Whate'er is called the birth of day, all this do we bestow on you.
3.14.2 May Aryaman pour gifts on you, and Pushan, land Brihaspati, And Indra, winner of the prize. Make ye my riches grow with me.
3.14.3 Moving together, free from fear, with plenteous droppings in this pen, Bearing sweet milk-like Soma-juice, come hither free from all disease.
3.14.4 Come hither, to this place, O Cows: here thrive as though ye were manured. Even here increase and multiply; let us be friendly, you and me.
3.14.5 Auspicious be this stall to you. Prosper like cultivated rice. Even here increase and multiply. Myself do we bestow on you.
3.14.6 Follow me, Cows, as master of the cattle. Here may this Cow- pen make you grow and prosper, Still while we live may we approach you living, ever increasing with the growth of riches.
;;; XV A merchant's prayer for success in his business
3.15.1 I stir and animate the merchant Indra; may he approach and be our guide and leader. Chasing ill-will, wild beast, and highway robber, may he who hath the power give me riches.
3.15.2 The many paths which Gods are wont to travel, the paths which go between the earth and heaven, May they rejoice with me in milk and fatness that I may make rich profit by my purchase.
3.15.3 With fuel. Agni! and with butter, longing, mine offering I present for strength and conquest; With prayer, so far as I have strength, adoring--this holy hymn to gain a hundred treasures.
3.15.4 Pardon this stubbornness of ours. O Agni, the distant pathway which our feet have trodden. Propitious unto us be sale and barter, may interchange of mer- chandise enrich me. Accept, ye twain, accordant, this libation! Prosperous be our ventures and incomings.
3.15.5 The wealth wherewith I carry on my traffic, seeking, ye Gods! wealth with the wealth I offer, May this grow more for me, not less: O Agni, through sacrifice chase those who hinder profit!
3.15.6 The wealth wherewith I carry on my traffic, seeking, ye Gods! wealth with the wealth I offer, Herein may Indra, Savitar, and Soma, Prajapati, and Agni give me splendour.
3.15.7 With reverence we sign thy praise, O Hotar-priest Vaisvanara. Over our children keep thou watch, over our bodies, kine, and lives.
3.15.8 Still to thee ever will we bring oblation, as to a stabled horse, O Jatavedas. Joying in food and in the growth of riches may we thy servants, Agni, never suffer.
;;; XVI A Rishi's morning prayer
3.16.1 Agni at dawn, and Indra we invoke at dawn, and Varuna and Mitra, and the Asvins twain: Bhaga at dawn, Pushan and Brahmanaspati, Soma at dawn, and Rudra we invoke at dawn.
3.16.2 We all strong Bhaga, conqueror in the morning, the son of Aditi, the great Disposer, Whom each who deems himself poor, strong and mighty, a king, addresses thus, Grant thou my portion!
3.16.3 Bhaga, our guide, Bhaga whose gifts are faithful, favour this hymn and give us wealth, O Bhaga. Bhaga, augment our store of kine and horses. Bhaga, may we be rich in men and heroes.
3.16.4 So may felicity be ours at present, and when the Sun advances, and at noontide; And may we still, O Bounteous One, at sunset be happy in the Gods' protecting favour.
3.16.5 May Bhaga verily be bliss-bestower, and through him, Gods! may happiness attend us. As such with all my might I call and call thee: as such be thou our leader here, O Bhaga.
3.16.6 To this our sacrifice may the Dawns incline them, and come to the pure place like Dadhikravan. As strong steeds draw a chariot may they bring me hitherward Bhaga who discovers treasure.
3.16.7 May the kind Mornings dawn on us for ever with, wealth of kine, of horses, and of heroes. Streaming with all abundance, pouring fatness, Do ye preserve us evermore with blessings!
;;; XVII A farmer's song and prayer to speed the plough
3.17.1 Wise and devoted to the Gods the skilful men bind plough-ropes fast, And lay the yokes on either side.
3.17.2 Lay on the yokes and fasten well the traces: formed is the furrow, sow the seed within it. Viraj vouchsafe us hearing fraught with plenty! Let the ripe grain come near and near the sickle.
3.17.3 The keen-shared plough that bringeth bliss, furnished with traces and with stilts, Shear out for me a cow, a sheep, a rapid drawer of the car, a blooming woman, plump and strong!
3.17.4 May Indra press the furrow down, may Pushan guard and cherish her. May she, well stored with milk yield milk for us through each succeeding year.
3.17.5 Happily let the shares turn up the ploughland, the ploughers happily follow the oxen. Pleased with our sacrifice, Suna and Sira! make the plants bring this man abundant produce.
3.17.6 Happily work our steers and men! May the plough furrow happily, Happily be the traces bound. Happily ply the driving-goad.
3.17.7 Suna and Sira, welcome ye this laud, and with the milk that ye have made in heaven, Bedew ye both this earth of ours.
3.17.8 Auspicious Sita, come thou near: we venerate and worship thee. That thou mayst bless and prosper us and bring us fruits abundantly.
3.17.9 Loved by the Visvedevas and the Maruts, let Sita be bedewed. with oil and honey. Turn thou to us with wealth of milk, O Sita, in vigorous strength and pouring streams of fatness.
;;; XVIII A jealous wife's incantation against a rival
3.18.1 From out the earth I dig this Plant, and herb of most effectual power, Wherewith one quells the rival wife and gains the husband for one's self.
3.18.2 Auspicious, with expanded leaves, sent by the Gods, victorious Plant, Drive thou, the rival wife away, and make my husband only mine.
3.18.3 Indeed he hath not named her name: thou with this husband dalliest not, Far into distance most remote we drive the rival wife away.
3.18.4 Stronger am I, O stronger one, yea, mightier than the mightier; Beneath me be my rival wife, down, lower than the lowest dames!
3.18.5 I am the conqueror, and thou, thou also art victorious: As victory attends us both we will subdue my fellowwife.
3.18.6 I've girt thee with the conquering Plant, beneath thee laid the mightiest one. As a cow hastens to her calf, so let thy spirit speed to me, hasten like water on its way.
;;; XIX A glorification of the office of a king's household priest
3.19.1 Quickened is this my priest rank, quickened is manly strength and force, Quickened be changeless power, whereof I am the conquering President!
3.19.2 I quicken these men's princely sway, the might, the manly strength and force; I rend away the foemen's arms with this presented sacrifice.
3.19.3 Down fall the men, low let them lie, who fight against our mighty prince, I ruin foemen with my spell, and raise my friends to high estate.
3.19.4 Keener than is the axe's edge, keener than Agni's self are they, Keener than Indra's bolt are they whose Priest and President am I.
3.19.5 The weapons of these men I whet and sharpen, with valiant heroes I increase their kingdom. Victorious be their power and ever ageless! May all the Gods promote their thoughts and wishes.
3.19.66 Let their fierce powers, O Maghavan, be heightened, and upward go the shout of conquering heroes. Apart and clear, let shout and roar and shriek and lamentation rise! Let the Gods led by Indra, let the Maruts with our army go.
3.19.7 Advance and be victorious, men I Exceeding mighty be your arms! Smite with sharp-pointed arrows those whose bows are weak. With your strong arms and weapons smite the feeble foe.
3.19.8 Loosed from the bowstring fly away, thou Arrow, sharpened by our prayer. Assail the foemen, vanquish them, conquer each bravest man of theirs, and let not one of them escape.
;;; XX A prayer for riches and general prosperity
3.20.1 This is thine ordered place of birth whence sprung to life thou shinest forth. Knowing this, Agni, mount on high and cause our riches to increase.
3.20.2 Turn hither, Agni, speak to us, come to us with a friendly mind. Enrich us, Sovran of the Tribes! Thou art the giver of our wealth.
3.20.3 Let Aryaman vouchsafe us, wealth, and Bhaga, and Brihaspati, The Goddesses grant wealth to us, Sunrita, Goddess, give me wealth!
3.20.4 We call King Soma to our aid, and Agni with our songs and. hymn, The Adityas, Vishnu, Surya, and the Brahman-priest Brihaspati.
3.20.5 Do thou, O Agni, with thy fires strengthen our prayer and. sacrifice. Incite thou us, O God, to give, and send us riches to bestow.
3.20.6 Both Indra here and Vayu we invoke with an auspicious call, That in assembly all the folk may be benevolent to us, and be inclined to give us gifts.
3.20.7 Urge Aryaman to send us gifts, and Indra, and Brihaspati, Vata, Vishnu, Sarasvati, and the strong courser Savitar.
3.20.8 Now have we reached the ordering of power, and all these worlds of life are held within it. Let him who knows urge e'en the churl to bounty Give wealth. to us with all good men about us.
3.20.9 May heaven's five spacious regions pour their milk for me with all their might. May I obtain each wish and hope formed by my spirit and my heart.
3.20.10 May speech that winneth cows be mine. With splendour mount thou over me. May Vayu hedge me round about May Pushan make me pros- perous.
;;; XXI In honour of fire in all shapes, to appease Agni of the funeral pile and to quench the flames of cremation
3.21.1 All Fires that are in water and in Vritra, all those that man and stones contain within them, That which hath entered herbs and trees and bushes--to all these Fires be this oblation offered.
3.21.2 That which abides in Soma and in cattle, that which lies deep in birds and sylvan creatures, That which hath entered quadrupeds and bipeds--to all these Fires be this oblation offered.
3.21.3 The Fire that rideth by the side of Indra, the God Vaisvanara,. yea all-consuming, Whom, as the victor, I invoke in battles--to all these Fires be this oblation offered.
