3.21.4 The all-devouring God whom men call Kama, he whom they call the Giver and Receiver, Invincible, pervading, wise, and mighty--to all these Fires be this oblation offered.
3.21.5 To thee, strength-giver, glorious, rich in pleasant strains, whom. in their minds the thirteen creatures of the world, And the five sons of man regard as Hotar-priest--to all these- Fires be this oblation offered.
3.21.6 To him who feeds on ox and cow, sage, bearing Soma on his back, To all Vaisvanara's followers--to these be this oblation paid.
3.21.7 All fiery flames that follow after lightning, flashing o'er earth, through firmament and heaven, All that are in the wind and skyey regions--to all these Fires be this oblation offered.
3.21.8 The golden-handed Savitar and Indra, Brihaspati, Varuna, Mitra, and Agni, The Angirases we call, the Visve Devas: let them appease this Agni, Flesh-devourer.
3.21.9 Flesh-eating Agni is appeased, appeased is he who hurteth men. Now him who burneth every thing, the Flesh-consumer, have I stilled.
3.21.10 The mountains where the Soma grows, the waters lying calm and still, Vata, Parjanya, Agni's self have made the Flesh-consumer rest.
;;; XXII The taming and training of an elephant for a king to ride on
3.22.1 Famed be the Elephant's strength, the lofty glory, which out of Aditi's body took existence! They all have given me this for my possession, even all the Gods and Aditi accordant.
3.22.2 On this have Mitra, Varuna, Indra, and Rudra fixed their thought. May those all-fostering deities anoint and balm me with his strength.
3.22.3 The strength wherewith the Elephant was dowered, that decks a King among the men, in waters, O Agni, even with that strength make thou me vigorous to-day.
3.22.4 The lofty strength which sacrifice brings, Jatavedas! unto thee, What strength the Sun possesses, all strength of the royal Ele- phant--such strength vouchsafe to me the pair of Asvins lotus-garlanded!
3.22.5 Far as the heaven's four regions spread, far as the eye's most distant ken. So wide, so vast let power be mine, this vigour of the Elephant.
3.22.6 Now hath the Elephant become chief of all pleasant beasts to ride. With his high fortune and his strength I grace and conscorate myself.
;;; XXIII A charm to remove a woman's sterility, and to assure the birth of boys
3.23.1 From thee we banish and expel the cause of thy sterility. This in another place we lay apart from thee and far removed.
3.23.2 As arrow to the quiver, so let a male embryo enter thee. Then from thy side be born a babe, a ten-month child, thy hero son.
3.23.3 Bring forth a male, bring forth a son. Another male shall follow him. The mother shalt thou be of sons born and hereafter to be born.
3.23.4 With that auspicious general flow wherewith steers propagate their kind, Do thou obtain thyself a son: be thou a fruitfu! mother-cow.
3.23.5 I give thee power to bear a child: within, thee pass the germ of life! Obtain a son, O woman, who shall be a blessing unto thee. Be thou a blessing unto him.
3.23.6 May those celestial herbs whose sire was Heaven, the Earth their mother, and their root the ocean. May those celestial healing Plants assist thee to obtain a son.
;;; XXIV A song of harvest
3.24.1 The plants of earth are rich in milk, and rich in milk is this my word, So from the rich in milk I bring thousandfold profit hitherward.
3.24.2 Him who is rich in milk I know. Abundant hath he made our corn. The God whose name is Gatherer, him we invoke who dwelleth in his house who sacrifices not.
3.24.3 All the five regions of the heavens, all the five races of man- kind, As after rain the stream brings drift, let them bring increase hitherward.
3.24.4 Open the well with hundred streams, exhaustless, with a thousand streams. So cause this corn of ours to be exhaustless, with a thousand streams.
3.24.5 O Hundred-handed, gather up. O Thousand-handed, pour thou forth. Bring hither increase of the corn prepared and yet to be pre- pared.
3.24.6 Three sheaves are the Gandharvas' claim, the lady of the house hath four. We touch thee with the sheaf that is the most abundant of them all.
3.24.7 Adding and Gathering are thy two attendants, O Prajapati. May they bring hither increase, wealth abundant, inexhaustible.
;;; XXV A man's love-charm
3.25.1 Let the Impeller goad thee on. Rest not in peace upon thy bed. Terrible is the shaft of Love: therewith I pierce thee to the heart.
3.25.2 That arrow winged with longing thought, its stem Desire, its neck, Resolve, Let Kama, having truly aimed, shoot forth and pierce thee in the heart.
3.25.3 The shaft of Kama, pointed well, that withers and consumes the spleen. With hasty feathers, all aglow, therewith I pierce thee to the heart.
3.25.4 Pierced through with fiercely-burning heat, steal to me with thy parching lips, Gentle and humble, all mine own, devoted, with sweet words of love.
3.25.5 Away Lfrom mother and from sire I drive thee hither with a whip, That thou mayst be at my command and yield to every wish of mine.
3.25.6 Mitra and Varuna, expel all thought and purpose from her heart. Deprive her of her own free will and make her subject unto me.
;;; XXVI A charm to win the favour of all serpents
3.26.1 Ye Gods who dwell within this eastward region, entitled Weapons, Agni forms your arrows. Be kind and gracious unto us and bless us. To you be reverence, to you be welcome!
3.26.2 Ye Gods who dwell within this southward region, entitled Eager, Kama forms your arrows. Be kind, etc.
3.26.3 Ye Gods who dwell within this westward region, whose name is Radiant, Water forms your arrows. Be kind, etc.
3.26.4 Ye Gods who dwell within this northward region, whose name is Piercers, Vata forms your arrows. Be kind, etc.
3.26.5 Ye Gods whose home is in this firm-set region--Nilimpas is your name--Plants are your arrow. Be kind, etc.
3.26.6 Ye Gods whose home is in this upmost region, Yearners by name, Brihaspati forms your arrows. Be kind and gracious unto us and bless us. To you be reverence, to you be welcome!
;;; XXVII A charm consigning an enemy to the serpents for punishment
3.27.1 Agni is regent of the East, its warder is Asita, the Adityas are the arrows. Worship to these the regents, these the warders, and to the arrows, yea, to these be worship! Within your jaws we lay the man who hateth us and whom we hate.
3.27.2 Indra is regent of the South, its warder Tiraschiraji, and the shafts the Fathers. Worship to these the regents, these the warders, and to the arrows, yea, to these be worship! Within your jaws we lay the man who hateth us and whom we hate.
3.27.3 Of the West region Varuna is ruler, Pridaku warder, Nourish- ment the arrows. Worship, etc.
3.27.4 Soma is ruler of the Northern region, Svaja the warder, lightn- ing's flash the arrows. Worship, etc.
3.27.5 Vishnu is ruler of the firm-set region, Kalmashagriva warder, Plants the arrows. Worship, etc.
3.27.6 Brihaspati controls the topmost region, Svitra is warder, and the Rain the arrows. Worship to these the regents, these the warders, and to the arrows, yea, to these be worship,! Within your jaws we lay the man who hateth us and whom we hate.
;;; XXVIII A charm to change the ill-omened birth of twin calves into a blessing
3.27.1 This cow was born to bring forth offspring singly, though they created kine of every colour. When she produces twins in spite of Order, sullen, with groan and grudge she harms the cattle.
3.27.2 She brings destruction on the beasts, turned to a flesh-devouring worm. Yes, give her to the Brahman that she may bring luck and happiness.
3.27.3 Be thou auspicious to our folk, bring luck to horses and to kine. Auspicious unto all this farm, bring luck and happiness to us.
3.27.4 Let there be rain and increase here, here be thou most munifi- cient. Mother of twins, prosper our herd.
3.27.5 Where, having left all sickness of their bodies, the pious lead, as friends, their lives of gladness Nigh to that world approached the twin calves' mother. Let her not harm our people and our cattle.
3.27.6 Where lies the world of those dear friends, the pious, those who have brought due sacrifice to Agni Nigh to that world approached the twins calves' mother. Let her not harm our people and our cattle.
;;; XXIX On the means to obtain immunity from taxation in the next world
3.29.1 When yonder kings who sit beside Yama divide among them- selves the sixteenth part of hopes fulfilled, A ram bestowed as sacrifice, white-footed, frees us from the tax.
3.29.2 He satisfies each hope and want, prevailing, present and pre- pared. The wish-fulfilling ram, bestowed, white-footed is exhaustless still.
3.29.3 He who bestows a white-hooved ram, adequate to the place he holds. Ascends to the celestial height, the heaven where tribute is not paid to one more mighty by the weak.
3.29.4 He who bestows a white-hooved ram, adequate to the place he holds. Offered with five cakes, lives on that, unwasting, in the Fathers' world.
3.29.5 He who bestows a white-hooved ram, adequate to the place he holds, Offered with five cakes, lives on that, wasteless, while Sun and. Moon endure.
3.29.6 Like a refreshing draught, like sea, the mighty flood, he faileth not. Like the two Gods whose home is one, the ram white-footed, faileth not.
3.29.7 Whose gift was this, and given to whom? Kama to Kama gave the gift. Kama is giver, Kama is receiver. Kama has passed into the sea. Through Kama do I take thee to myself. O Kama, this is thine.
3.27.8 May Earth receive thee as her own, and this great interspace of air. Neither in breath and body nor in progeny may this acceptance do me harm.
;;; XXIX On the means to obtain immunity from taxation in the next world
3.30.1 Freedom from hate I bring to you, concord and unanimity. Love one another as the cow loveth the calf that she hath borne.
3.30.2 One-minded with his mother let the son be loyal to his sire. Let the wife, calm and gentle, speak words sweet as honey to her lord.
3.30.3 No brother hate his brother, no sister to sister be unkind. Unanimous, with one intent, speak ye your speech in friend- liness.
3.30.4 That spell through which Gods sever not, nor ever bear each other hate, That spell we lay upon your home, a bond of union for the men.
3.30.5 Intelligent, submissive, rest united, friendly and kind, bearing the yoke together. Come, speaking sweetly each one to the other. I make you one- intentioned and one-minded.
3.30.6 Let what you drink, your share of food be common together, with one common bond I bid you. Serve Agni, gathered round him like the spokes about the chariot nave.
3.30.7 With binding charm I make you all united, obeying one sole leader and one-minded. Even as the Gods who watch and guard the Amrit, at morn and eve may ye be kindly-hearted.
;;; XXXI A charm for the recovery of one dangerously ill
3.31.1 May Gods release from failing strength, thou Agni, from malignity! I free from every evil, from decline: I compass round with life.
3.31.2 May Pavamana free from harm, and Sakra from unrighteous deed. I free from every evil, from decline: I compass round with life.
3.31.3 Tame beasts have parted from wild beasts, water and thirst have gone apart I free, etc.
3.31.4 Parted are heaven and earth, and paths turned to each quarter of the sky. I free, etc.
3.31.5 Tvashtar prepares the bridal of his daughter; then all this world of life departs and leaves him. I free, etc.
3.31.6 Agni combines the vital airs. The moon is closely joined with breath. I free. etc.
3.31.7 The Gods have lifted up with breath the Sun whose might is everywhere. I free, etc.
3.31.8 Die not. Live with the breath of those who make and who enjoy long life. I free, etc.
3.31.9 Die not. Stay here. Breathe with the breath of those who draw the vital air. I free, etc.
3.31.10 Rise up with life, conjoined with life. Up, with the sap of growing plants! I free, etc.
3.31.11 We as immortal beings have arisen with Parjanya's rain, I free from every evil, from decline: I compass round with life.
;;; I Cosmogonical and mystico-theological doctrine
4.1.1 Eastward at first the prayer was generated: Vena disclosed bright flashes from the summit, Disclosed his deepest, nearest revelations, womb of the non- existent and existent.
4.1.2 Let this Queen come in front, her Father's daughter, found in the worlds for earliest generation. For him they set this radiant vault in motion. Let them prepare warm milk for him who first would drink.
4.1.3 He who was born as his all-knowing kinsman declareth all the deities' generations. He from the midst of prayer his prayer hath taken. On high, below, spread forth his godlike nature.
4.1.4 For he, true to the law of Earth and Heaven, established both the mighty worlds securely. Mighty when born, he propped apart the mighty, the sky, our earthly home, and air's mid-region.
4.1.5 He from the depth hath been reborn for ever, Brihaspati the world's sole Lord and Ruler. From light was born the Day with all its lustre: through this let sages live endowed with splendour.
4.1.6 The sage and poet verily advanceth the statute of that mighty God primeval. He was born here with many more beside him: they slumbered when the foremost side was opened.
4.1.7 The man who seeks the friend of Gods, Atharvan the father, and Brihaspati, with worship, Crying to him, Be thou all things' creator! the wise God, self- dependent, never injures.
;;; III A Charm against tigers, wolves, thieves and other noxious creatures
4.3.1 Three have gone hence and passed away, the man, the tiger, and the wolf. Down, verily, the rivers flow, down-goeth the celestial Tree,. down let our foemen bend and bow.
4.3.2 On distant pathway go the wolf, on pathway most remote the thief! On a far road speed forth the rope with teeth, and the malicious man!
4.3.3 We crush and rend to pieces both thine eyes, O Tiger, and thy jaws and all the twenty claws we break.
4.3.4 We break and rend the tiger first of creatures that are armed. with teeth; The robber then, and then the snake, the sorcerer, and then the wolf.
4.3.5 The thief who cometh near to-day departeth bruised and crush- ed to bits. By nearest way let him be gone. Let Indra slay him with his bolt.
4.3.6 Let the beast's teeth be broken off, shivered and shattered be his ribs! Slack be thy bowstring: downward go the wild beast that pursues the hare!
4.3.7 Open not what thou hast compressed, close not what thou hast not compressed. Indra's and Soma's child, thou art Atharvan's tiger-crushing charm.
;;; III A Charm against tigers, wolves, thieves and other noxious creatures
4.3.1 Three have gone hence and passed away, the man, the tiger, and the wolf. Down, verily, the rivers flow, down-goeth the celestial Tree,. down let our foemen bend and bow.
4.3.2 On distant pathway go the wolf, on pathway most remote the thief! On a far road speed forth the rope with teeth, and the malicious man!
4.3.3 We crush and rend to pieces both thine eyes, O Tiger, and thy jaws and all the twenty claws we break.
4.3.4 We break and rend the tiger first of creatures that are armed. with teeth; The robber then, and then the snake, the sorcerer, and then the wolf.
4.3.5 The thief who cometh near to-day departeth bruised and crush- ed to bits. By nearest way let him be gone. Let Indra slay him with his bolt.
4.3.6 Let the beast's teeth be broken off, shivered and shattered be his ribs! Slack be thy bowstring: downward go the wild beast that pursues the hare!
4.3.7 Open not what thou hast compressed, close not what thou hast not compressed. Indra's and Soma's child, thou art Atharvan's tiger-crushing charm.
;;; IV A charm to restore virile power
4.4.1 We dig thee from the earth, the Plant which strengthens and exalts the nerves, The Plant which the Gandharva dug for Varuna whose power was lost.
4.4.2 Let Ushas and let Surya rise, let this the speech I utter rise. Let the strong male Prajapati arise with manly energy.
4.4.3 Sicut tui surgentis (membrum virile) tanquam inflammatum palpitat, hoc illud tui ardentius haec herba faciat.
4.4.4 Sursum (estote) herbarum vires, taurorum vigor. Tu, Indra, corporis potens, virorum masculum robur in hoc homine depone.
4.4.5 Ros aquarum primigenitus atque arborum, Somae etiam frater es, vatum sacrorum masculus vigor es.
4.4.6 Hodie, Agnis! hodie Savitar! hodie dea Sarasvatis! hodie Brahmanaspatis! hujus fascinum velut arcum extende.
4.4.7 Velut nervum in arcu ego tuum fascinum extendo. Aggredere (mulierem) semper indefessus velut cervus damam.
4.4.8 Quae sunt equi vires, muli, capri, arietis, atque tauri, illas, cor- poris potens! in hoc homine depone.
;;; V A lover's sleep-charm
4.5.1 The Bull who hath a thousand horns, who rises up from out the sea, By him the strong and mighty one we lull the folk to rest and. sleep.
4.5.2 Over the surface of the earth there breathes no wind, there looks. no eye. Lull all the women, lull the dogs to sleep, with Indra as thy friend!
4.5.3 The woman sleeping in the court, lying without, or stretched on beds, The matrons with their odorous sweets--these, one and all, we lull to sleep.
4.5.4 Each moving thing have I secured, have held and held the eye and breath. Each limb and member have I seized in the deep darkness of the night.
4.5.5 The man who sits, the man who walks, whoever stands and clearly sees Of these we closely shut the eyes, even as we closely shut this house.
4.5.6 Sleep mother, let the father sleep, sleep dog, and master of the home. Let all her kinsmen sleep, sleep all the people who are round about.
4.5.7 With soporific charm, O Sleep, lull thou to slumber all the folk. Let the rest sleep till break of day, I will remain awake till dawn, like Indra free from scath and harm.
;;; VI A charm to make a poisoned arrow harmless
4.6.1 The Brahman first was brought to life ten-headed and with faces ten. First drinker of the Soma, he made poison ineffectual.
4.6.2 Far as the heavens and earth are spread in compass, far as the Seven Rivers are extended, So far my spell, the antidote of poison, have I spoken hence,
4.6.3 The strong-winged Bird Garutman first of all, O Poison fed on thee: Thou didst not gripe or make him drunk: aye, thou becamest food for him.
4.6.4 Whoever with five fingers hath discharged thee from the crooked bow, I from the shaft have charmed away the poison of the fastening band.
4.6.5 The poison have I charmed away from shaft, cement, and feather- ed end; Yea, from the barb, the neck, the horn, the poison have I charmed away.
4.6.6 Feeble, O Arrow, is thy shaft, thy poison, too, hath lost its strength. Made of a worthless tree, thy bow, O feeble one, is impotent.
4.6.7 The men who brayed it, smeared it on, they who discharged it, sent it forth, All these are made emasculate, emasculate the poison-hill.
4.6.8 Thy diggers are emasculate, emasculate, O, Plant art thou. The rugged mountain that produced this poison is emasculate.
;;; VII A charm to make a poisonous plant innocuous
4.7.1 So may this water guard us on the bank of Varanavati. Therein hath Amrit been infused: with that I ward thy poison off.
4.7.2 Weak is the poison of the East, weak is the poison of the North, So too this poison of the South counts as a cake of curds and meal.
4.7.3 When he hath made of thee a cake, broad, steaming, swelling up with fat, And even in hunger eaten thee, then gripe him not, thou hideous one!
4.7.4 Intoxicater! like a shaft we make thy spirit fly away, Like a pot boiling on the fire, we with our word remove thee hence.
4.7.5 We set around thee with the spell as 'twere a gathered arma- ment. Stay quiet like a rooted tree. Dug up with mattocks, gripe not thou.
4.7.6 For coverings men have bartered thee, for skins of deer and woven cloths. Thou art a thing of sale, O Plant. Dug up with mattocks, gripe not thou!
4.7.7 None have attained to those of old, those who wrought holy acts for you. Let them not harm our heroes here. Therefore I set before you this.
;;; VIII A benediction at the consecration of a King
4.8.1 The Being lays the sap of life in beings: he hath become the sovran Lord of creatures. Death comes to this man's royal consecration: let him as King own and allow this kingdom.
4.8.2 Come forward, turn not back in scorn, strong guardian, slayer of the foes. Approach, O gladdener of thy friends. The Gods have blessed and strengthened thee.
4.8.3 All waited on him as he came to meet them. He self-resplendent moves endued with glory. That is the royal hero's lofty nature: he, manifold, hath gained immortal powers.
4.8.4 Stride forth to heaven's broad regions, thou, a tiger on a tiger's skin. Let all the people long for thee. Let heavenly floods be rich in milk.
4.8.5 Heaven's waters joyous in their milk, the waters of middle air, and those that earth containeth- I with the gathered power and might of all these waters sprinkle thee,
4.8.6 The heavenly waters rich in milk have sprinkled thee with power and might. To be the gladdener of thy friends. May Savitar so fashion thee.
4.8.7 These, compassing the tiger, rouse the lion to great joy and bliss. As strong floods purify the standing ocean, so men adorn the leopard in the waters
;;; IX A charm addressed to a precious ointment for safety and wealth
4.9.1 Approach! thou art the mountain's eye, the living thing that saveth us; A gift bestowed by all the Gods, yea, the defence that guardeth life.
4.9.2 Thou art the safeguard of the men, thou art the safeguard of the kine, Thou standest ready to protect the horses that are fleet of foot.
4.9.3 Thou, also, Salve! art a defence that rends and crushes sorcerers. Thou knowest, too, of Amrit, thou art the delight of all who live, a jaundice-curing balm art thou.
4.9.4 Whomso thou creepest over, Salve! member by member, joint by joint, From him, like some strong arbiter of strife, thou banishest decline.
4.9.5 No imprecation reaches him, no magic, no tormenting fiend, O Salve, Vishkandha seizes not the man who carries thee about.
4.9.6 From lying speech, from evil dream, from wicked act and sinfulness, From hostile and malignant eye,--from these, O Salve, protect us well.
4.9.7 I, knowing this, O Salve, will speak the very truth and not a lie: May I obtain both horse and ox, may I obtain thy life, O man.
4.9.8 Three are the slaves that serve the Salve, Fever, Consumption, and the Snake. Thy father is the loftiest of mountains, named the Triple- peaked.
4.9.9 Sprung from the Snowy Mountain's side, this Ointment of the Three-peaked hill. Crushes and rends all sorcerers and every witch and sorceress.
4.9.10 If thou art from the Three-peaked hill or hast thy name from Yamuna, These names are both auspicious: by these two protect thou us, O Salve!
;;; X A charm accompanying investiture with an amulet of shell
4.10.1 Child of the wind firmament, sprung from the lightning and the light, May this the gold-born Shell that bears the pearl preserve us from distress.
4.10.2 Shell that wast born from out the sea, set at the head of things that shine! With thee we slay the Rakshasas and overcome voracious fiends.
4.10.3 We stay disease and indigence, and chase Sadanvas with the Shell. May the all-healing Shell that bears the pearl preserve us from distress.
4.10.4 Born in the heaven, sprung from the sea, brought to us hither from the flood. This gold-born Shell shall be to us an amulet to lengthen life.
4.10.5 From ocean sprang the Amulet, from Vritra sprang the Lord of Day: May this protect us round about from shaft of God and Asura.
4.10.6 Peerless 'mid golden ornaments art thou: from Soma wast thou born. Thou gleamest on the quiver, thou art beautiful upon the car: may it prolong our days of life!
4.10.7 Bone of the Good became the pearl's shell-mother endowed with soul it moveth in the waters. I bind this on thee for life, strength, and vigour, for long life lasting through a hundred autumns. May the pearl's mother keep and guard thee safely!
;;; XI A glorification of the sacrificial gharma or milk caldron
4.11.1 The Bull supports the wide-spread earth and heaven, the Bull supports the spacious air between them. The Bull supports the sky's six spacious regions: the universal world hath he pervaded.
4.11.2 The Bull is Indra o'er the beasts he watches. He, Sakra measures out three several pathways. He, milking out the worlds, the past, the future, discharges all the Gods' eternal duties.
4.11.3 Being produced among mankind as Indra, the Caldron works heated and brightly glowing. Let him not, with good sons, pass off in vapour who hath not eaten of the Ox with knowledge.
4.11.4 The Ox pours milk out in the world of virtue: in earliest time, he, Pavam5na, swells it. Parjanya is the stream, Maruts his udder, sacrifice is the milk, the meed his milking.
4.11.5 That which not sacrifice nor sacrificer, not giver nor receiver rules and governs, All-winning, all-supporting, all-effecting,--which of all quadru- peds, tell us! is the Caldron?
4.11.6 May we, fame-seekers, reach the world of virtue by service of the Gharma and through fervour, Whereby the Gods went up to heaven, the centre of life eternal, having left the body.
4.11.7 Prajapati, supreme and sovran ruler, Indra by form and by his shoulder Agni, Came to Visvanara, came to all men's Bullock: he firmly forti- fied and held securely.
4.11.8 The middle of the Bullock's neck, there where the shoulder-bar is placed, Extends as far to east of him as that is settled to the west.
4.11.9 He whosoever knows the seven exhaustless pourings of the Ox, Wins himself offspring and the world: the great Seven Rishis know this well.
4.11.10 With feet subduing weariness, with legs extracting freshening draughts, Through toil the plougher and the Ox approach the honeyed beverage.
4.11.11 Assigned are these twelve nights, they say, as holy to Prajapati: Whoever knows their proper prayer performs the service of the Ox.
4.11.12 At evening he is milked, is milked at early morn, is milked at noon. We know that streams of milk that flow from him are in- exhaustible.
;;; XII A charm to mend a broken bone
4.12.1 Thou art the healer, making whole, the healer of the broken bone: Make thou this whole, Arundhati!
4.12.2 Whatever bone of thine within thy body hath been wrenched or cracked, May Dhatar set it properly and join together limb by limb.
4.12.3 With marrow be the marrow joined, thy limb united with the limb. Let what hath fallen of thy flesh, and the bone also grow again.
4.12.4 Let marrow close with marrow, let skin grow united with the skin. Let blood and bone grow strong in thee, flesh grow together with the flesh.
4.12.5 Join thou together hair with hair, join thou together skin with skin. Let blood and bone grow strong in thee. Unite the broken part,. O Plant.
4.12.6 Arise, advance, speed forth; the car hath goodly fellies, naves, and wheels!! Stand up erect upon thy feet.
4.12.7 If he be torn and shattered, having fallen into a pit, or a cast stone have struck him, Let the skilled leech join limb with limb, as 'twere the portions of a car.
;;; XIII A charm to restore a sick man to health
4.13.1 Gods, raise again the man whom ye, O Gods, have humbled and brought low. Ye Gods, restore to life again, him, Gods! who hath committed sin.
4.13.2 Here these two winds are blowing far as Sindhu from a distant land. May one breathe energy to thee, the other blow thy fault away.
4.13.3 Hither, O Wind, blow healing balm, blow every fault away, thou Wind! For thou who hast all medicine comest as envoy of the Gods.
4.13.4 May the Gods keep and save this man, the Maruts' host deliver him. All things that be deliver him that he be freed from his offence.
4.13.5 I am come nigh to thee with balms to give thee rest and keep thee safe. I bring thee mighty strength, I drive thy wasting malady away.
4.13.6 Felicitous is this my hand, yet more felicitous is this. This hand contains all healing balms, and this makes whole with gentle touch.
4.13.7 The tongue that leads the voice precedes. Then with our tenfold- branching hands. With these two healers of disease, we stroke thee with a soft caress.
;;; XIV Accompanying the sacrifice of a he-goat
4.14.1 The Goat was verily produced from Agni. Through sorrow he beheld, at first, his father. Through him at first the Gods attained to godhead, and, meet for sacrifices, were exalted.
4.14.2 Bearing in hands seethed viands, go with Agni to the cope of heaven. Reaching the sky that touches heaven, mix with the company of Gods.
4.14.3 From earth's high ridge to middle air I mounted, and from mid- air ascended up to heaven. From the high pitch of heaven's cope I came into the world of light.
4.14.4 Mounting the sky they look not round; they rise to heaven through both the worlds, Sages who paid the sacrifice that pours its streams on every side.
4.14.5 First among all the deities, come forward, thou who art eye of Gods and men, O Agni. Imploring, and accordant with the Bhrigus, to heaven in safety go the sacrificers!
4.14.6 With milk and butter I anoint the mighty, celestial Goat, strong- winged, and full of juices. Through him will we attain the world of virtue, ascending to the loftiest cope, to heaven.
4.14.7 Set the Goat's head toward the eastern region, and turn his right side to the southern quarter. His hinder part turn to the western quarter, and set his left side to the northern region.
4.14.8 Set the Goat's backbone upmost in the zenith, and lay his belly downward in the nadir; set his midportion in mid-air between them.
4.14.9 O'er the dressed Goat lay a dressed skin to robe him prepared, in perfect form, with all his members. Rise upward to the loftiest vault of heaven: with thy four feet stand firmly in the regions.
;;; XV A charm to hasten the coming of the rains
4.15.1 Let all the misty regions fly together, let all the rain-clouds sped by wind, assemble. Let waters satisfy the earth, the voices of the great mist-enve- loped Bull who roareth.
4.15.2 Let them show forth, the strong, the bounteous Maruts: let plants and shrubs be hung with drops of moisture. Let floods of rain refresh the ground with gladness and herbs spring various with each form and colour.
4.15.3 Cause us who sing to see the gathering vapours: out burst in many a place the rush of waters! Let floods of rain refresh the ground with gladness; and herbs spring various with each form and colour.
4.15.4 Apart, Parjanya! let the troops of Maruts, roaring, swell the song. Let pouring torrents of the rain that raineth rain upon the earth.
4.15.0 5. Up from the sea lift your dread might, ye Maruts: as light and splendour, send the vapour upward! Let waters satisfy the earth, the voices of the great mist-enve- loped Bull who roareth.
4.15.6 Roar, thunder, set the sea in agitation, bedew the ground with thy sweet rain, Parjanya! Send plenteous showers on him who seeketh shelter, and let the owner of lean kine go homeward.
4.15.7 Let the boon Maruts, let the springs and coiling serpents tend! you well. Urged by the Maruts let the clouds pour down their rain upon. the earth.
4.15.8 Let lightning flash on every side: from all the regions blow the winds! Urged by the Maruts let the clouds pour down their rain upon the earth.
4.15.9 May waters, lightning, cloud, and rain, boon springs and serpents tend you well. Urged by the Maruts let the clouds pour down their rain upon the earth.
4.15.10 May he who hath become the plants' high regent, suiting our bodies, Agni of the Waters, May Jatavedas send us rain from heaven, Amrit and vital breath to earthly creatures.
4.15.11 Sending up waters from the flood and ocean Prajapati move the sea to agitation! Forth flow the moisture of the vigorous stallion! With this thy roar of thunder come thou hither,
4.15.12 Our father, Lord divine pouring the torrents. Let the streams breathe, O Varuna, of the waters. Pour the floods down: along the brooks and channels let frogs with speckled arms send out their voices.
4.15.13 They who lay quiet for a year, the Brahmans who fulfil their vows. The frogs, have lifted up their voice, the voice Parjanya hath. inspired.
4.15.14 Speak forth a welcome, female frog! Do thou O frog, accost the rain. Stretch thy four feet apart, and swim in the middle of the lake.
4.15.15 Khanvakha, ho! Khaimakha, ho! thou in the middle, Taduri! Fathers, enjoy the rain from one who strives to win the Marutes heart.
4.15.16 Lift up the mighty cask and pour down water; let the wind blow, and lightnings flash around us. Let sacrifice be paid, and, widely scattered, let herbs and plants be full of joy and gladness.
;;; XVI On the omnipresence and omniscience of Varuna
4.16.1 The mighty Ruler of these worlds beholds as though from close at hand, The man who thinks he acts by stealth: all this the Gods perceive and know.
4.16.2 If a man stands or walks or moves in secret, goes to his lying- down or his uprising, What two men whisper as they sit together, King Varuna knows: he as the third is present.
4.16.3 This earth, too, is King Varuna's possession, and the high heaven whose ends are far asunder. The loins of Varuna are both the oceans, and this small drop of water, too, contains him.
4.16.4 If one should flee afar beyond the heaven, King Varuna would still be round about him. Proceeding hither from the sky his envoys look, thousand-eyed, over the earth beneath them.
4.16.5 All this the royal Varuna beholdeth, all between heaven and earth and all beyond them. The twinklings of men's eyelids hath he counted. As one who plays throws dice he settles all things.
4.16.6 Those fatal snares of thine which stand extended, threefold, O Varuna, seven by seven, May they all catch the man who tells a falsehood, and pass un- harmed the man whose words are truthful.
4.16.7 Varuna, snare him with a hundred nooses! Man's watcher! let not him who lies escape thee. There let the villain sit with hanging belly and bandaged like a cask whose hoops are broken.
4.16.8 Varuna sends, and drives away, diseases: Varuna is both native and a stranger, Varuna is celestial and is human.
4.16.9 I bind and hold thee fast with all these nooses, thou son of such a man and such a mother. All these do I assign thee as thy portion.
;;; XVII A charm to secure freedom from various evils
4.17.1 We seize and hold thee, Conquering One! the queen of medi- cines that heal. O Plant, I have endowed thee with a hundred powers for every man,
4.17.2 Still conquering, banishing the curse, mighty, with thy reverted. bloom. Thee and all Plants have I invoked: Hence let it save us! was my prayer.
4.17.3 She who hath cursed us with a curse, or hath conceived a murderous sin, Or seized our son to take his blood, may she devour the child she bare.
4.17.4 What magic they have wrought for thee in dish unbaked or burnt dark-red, What they have wrought in flesh undressed,--conquer the sorcerers therewith.
4.17.5 Ill dream and wretchedness of life, Rakshasa, monster, stingy hags, All the she-fiends of evil name and voice, we drive away from us.
4.17.6 Death caused by famine, caused by thirst, failure of children,. loss of kine, With thee, O Apamarga, all this ill we cleanse and wipe away.
4.17.7 Death caused by thirst, death caused by stress of hunger, loss at play with dice, All this, O Apamarga with thine aid we cleanse and wipe away.
4.17.8 The Apamarga is alone the sovran of all Plants that grow. With this we wipe away whate'er hath fallen on thee: go in health!
;;; XVIII A counter-charm against the incantations of enemies
4.18.1 The moonlight equalleth the sun, night is the rival of the day. I make effectual power my help: let magic arts be impotent.
4.18.2 Gods! if one make and bring a spell on some man's house who knows it not, Close as the calf that sucks the cow may it revert and cling to him.
4.18.3 When one puts poison in a dish of unbaked clay to kill a man, It cracks when set upon the fire with the sharp sound of many stones.
4.18.4 Endowed with thousand powers! adjure the bald and those with necks awry. Back to its author turn the spell like a dear damsel to her friend!
4.18.5 I with this Plant have ruined all malignant powers of witchery. The spell which they have laid upon thy field, thy cattle, or thy men.
4.18.6 No power had he who wrought the spell: he hurt his foot, he broke his toe. His act hath brought us happiness and pain and sorrow to him- self.
4.18.7 Let Apamarga sweep away chronic disease and every curse, Sweep sorceresses clean away, and all malignant stingy hags.
4.18.8 Sweep thou away the sorcerers, all stingy fiendish hags away. All this, O Apamarga, with thine aid we wipe away from us.
;;; XIX A counter-charm and charm to secure general protection.
4.19.1 Thou breakest ties of kith and kin, thou causest, too, relation- ship: So bruise the sorcerer's offspring, like a reed that groweth in the Rains.
4.19.2 Thou hast been blessed with blessing by the Brahman, Kanva Narshada. Thou fliest like a flashing dart: there is no fear or danger, Plant! within the limit of thy range.
4.19.3 Illumining, as 'twere, with light, thou movest at the head of plants. The saviour of the simple man art thou, and slayer of the fiends.
4.19.4 As once when time began the Gods with thee expelled the Asuras, Even thence, O Plant, wast thou produced as one who wipes and sweeps away.
4.19.5 Thy father's name was Cleaver. Thou with thousand branches cleavest all. Do thou, turned backward, cleave and rend the man who treateth us as foes.
4.19.6 The evil sprang from earth; it mounts to heaven and spreads to vast extent. Reverted, shaking him with might, thence on its maker let it fall.
4.19.7 For thou hast grown reverted, and turned backward also is thy fruit. Remove all curses far from me, keep most remote the stroke of death.
4.19.8 Preserve me with a hundred, yea, protect me with a thousand aids. May mighty Indra, Lord of Plants! give store of strength and. power to thee.
;;; XX A charm for the acquisition of superhuman powers of sight
4.20.1 It sees in front, it sees behind, it sees afar away, it sees The sky, the firmament, and earth: all this, O Goddess, it beholds.
4.20.2 Through thee, O godlike Plant, may I behold all creatures that exist, Three several heavens, three several earths, and these six regions one by one.
4.20.3 The pupil, verily, art thou of that celestial Engle's eye. On earth hast thou alighted as a weary woman seeks her couch.
4.20.4 The God who hath a thousand eyes give me this Plant in my right hand! I look on every one therewith, each Sudra and each Aryan man.
4.20.5 Make manifest the forms of things; hide not their essences from sight. And, thou who hast a thousand eyes, look the Kimidins in the face.
4.20.6 Make me see Yatudhanas, make thou Yatudhanis visible. Make me see all Pisachas With this prayer, O Plant, I hold thee fast.
4.20.7 Thou art the sight of Kasyapa and of the hound who hath four eyes. Make the Pisacha manifest as Surya when he rides at noon.
4.20.8 Kimidin, Yatudhana from their hiding-places have I dragged. I look on every one with this, Sudra and Aryan man alike.
4.20.9 Make that Pisacha visible, the fiend who flies in middle air, The fiend who glides across the sky, and him who deems the earth his help.
;;; XXI Glorification and benediction of cows
4.21.1 The kine have come and brought good fortune: let them rest in the cow-pen and be happy near us. Here let them stay prolific, many-coloured, and yield through many morns their milk for Indra.
4.21.2 Indra aids him who offers sacrifice and praise: he takes not what is his, and gives him more thereto. Increasing ever more and ever more his wealth, he makes the pious dwell within unbroken bounds.
4.21.3 These are ne'er lost, no robber ever injures them: no evil-minded foe attempts to harass them. The master of the kine lives a long life with these, the Cows whereby he pours his gifts and serves the Gods.
4.21.4 The charger with his dusty brow o'ertakes them not, and never to the shambles do they take their way. These Cows, the cattle of the pious worshipper, roam over wide- spread pasture where no danger is.
4.21.5 To me the Cows seem Bhaga, they seem Indra, they seem a portion of the first poured Soma. These present Cows, they, O ye men, are Indra. I long for Indra with my heart and spirit.
4.21.6 O Cows, ye fatten e'en the worn and wasted, and make the unlovely beautiful to look on. Prosper my home, ye with auspicious voices! Your power is magnified in our assemblies.
4.21.7 In goodly pasturage, bright-hued, prolific, drinking pure water at fair drinking-places, Never be thief or sinful man your master, and may the dart of Rudra still avoid you!
;;; XXII A benediction on a newly consecrated king
4.22.1 Exalt and strengthen this my Prince, O Indra, Make him sole lord and leader of the people. Scatter his foes, deliver all his rivals into his hand in struggles for precedence.
4.22.2 Give him a share in village, kine, and horses, and leave his enemy without a portion. Let him as King be head and chief of Princes, Give up to him, O Indra, every foeman.
4.22.3 Let him be treasure-lord of goodly treasures, let him as King be master of the people. Grant unto him great power and might, O Indra, and strip his enemy of strength and vigour.
4.22.4 Like milch-kine yielding milk for warm libations, pour, Heaven and Earth! on him full many a blessing. May he as King be Indra's well-beloved, the darling of the kine, the plants, the cattle.
4.22.5 I join in league with thee victorious Indra, with whom men conquer and are ne'er defeated. He shall make thee the folk's sole lord and leader, shall make thee highest of all human rulers.
4.22.6 Supreme art thou, beneath thee are thy rivals, and all, O King, who were thine adversaries. Sole lord and leader and allied with Indra, bring, conqueror, thy foremen's goods and treasures.
4.22.7 Consume, with lion aspect, all their hamlets, with tiger aspect, drive away thy foemen. Sole lord and leader and allied with Indra, seize, conqueror, thine enemies' possessions.
;;; XXIII Magnification of Agni and prayer for his protection
4.23.1 I fix my heart on wise and ancient Agni, the Five Tribes' Lord, in many a place enkindled. We seek him who hath entered all our houses. May he deliver us from grief and trouble.
4.23.2 As thou conveyest offerings, Jatavedas! and fashionest the sacri- fice with knowledge, So bear thou to the Gods the prayer we utter. May he deliver us from grief and trouble.
4.23.3 I pray to Agni in each act successful, employed in every sacrifice, the strongest, Fiend-slayer, served with fatness, strengthening worship. May he deliver us from grief and trouble.
4.23.4 We invoke the oblation-bearer, well-born Agni Jatavedas, Him, Vaisvanara, almighty. May he set us free from trouble.
4.23.5 With whom as friend the Rishis gave their power new splendour, with whom they kept aloof the Asuras' devices, Agni, with whom Indra subdued the Panis. May he deliver us. from grief and trouble.
4.23.6 Through whom the Gods discovered life eternal, through whom they stored the plants with pleasant juices, Through whom they brought to men the light of heaven. May he deliver us from grief and trouble.
4.23.7 I, suppliant, praise and ever call on Agni, sole Lord of all this world, of all that shineth, Of what exists and shall exist hereafter. May he deliver us from grief and trouble.
;;; XXIV A hymn of prayer and praise to Indra
4.24.1 I think of Indra, only him for ever, fiend-slayer, May these lauds of mine come near him. He cometh to the pious offerer's calling. May he deliver us from grief and trouble.
4.24.2 Who with strong arms o'ercame his strong opponents, who broke and crushed the power of the demons, Who won the rivers and the kine in battle. May he deliver us from grief and trouble.
4.24.3 Ruler of men, finder of light, the hero: the pressing-stones declare his valour, master. Of sweetest sacrifice with seven Hotars. May he deliver us from grief and trouble.
4.24.4 The lord of barren cows and bulls and oxen, finder of light for whom the posts are planted, For whom the bright juice flows cleansed by devotion. May he deliver us from grief and trouble.
4.24.5 Whose favour those desire who offer Soma, whom, arrow-bearer, men invoke in battle, On whom the hymn depends, in whom is power, May he deliver us from grief and trouble.
4.24.6 Why was born, first, for active operation, whose valour as the first hath been awakened, Who raised his bolt when he encountered Ahi. May he deliver us from grief and trouble.
4.24.7 Strong Lord, who leadeth hosts to meet for battle, who sendeth riches both of earth and heaven, I, suppliant, praise and ever call on Indra. May he deliver us from grief and trouble.
;;; XXV A hymn of prayer and praise to Vayu and Savitar
4.25.1 I think on Vayu's and Savitar's holy rites, ye twain who penetrate and guard the living world: Ye who have come to be this All's pervaders, deliver us, ye two from grief and trouble.
4.25.2 Ye who have counted up the earth's expanses, and in the sky smoothed out the air's mid-region, Whose going-forth hath ne'er been reached by any, deliver us, ye two, from grief and trouble.
4.25.3 Beauteously bright! men rest in thy dominion when thou hast risen up and hastened onward. Ye, Vayu, Savitar, preserve all creatures. Deliver us, ye, twain, from grief and trouble.
4.25.4 Hence, Vayu, Savitar drive evil action, chase Simida away, drive off the demons. Ye give us store of energy and power. Deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.25.5 Of their own selves let Savitar and Vayu send favourable strength and wealth and plenty. Here give us perfect freedom from consumption. Deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.25.6 Ye, Savitar and Vayu, to assist us, enjoy the hymn and the delightful cheerer. Come hither downward from the stream of blessing. Deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.25.7 Like noblest benisons they have stayed in the God loving man's abode. I glorify bright Savitar and Vayu. Deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
;;; XXVI A hymn to Heaven and Earth
4.26.1 O Heaven and Earth, I think on you, wise, givers of abundant gifts, ye who through measureless expanses have spread forth. For ye are seats and homes of goodly treasures. Deliver us, ye twain from grief and trouble.
4.26.2 Yea, seats and homes are ye of goodly treasures, grown strong, divine, blessed, and far-extending, To me, O Heaven and Earth, be ye auspicious. Deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.26.3 I call on you who warm and cause no sorrow, deep, spacious, meet to be adored by poets. To me, O Heaven and Earth, be ye auspicious. Deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.26.4 Ye who maintain Amrit and sacrifices, ye who support rivers and human beings, To me, O Heaven and Earth, be ye auspicious, Deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.26.5 Ye by whom cows and forest trees are cherished within whose range all creatures are included, To me, O Heaven and Earth, be ye auspicious. Deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.26.6 Ye who delight in nectar and in fatness, ye without whom men have no strength or power, To me, O Heaven and Earth, be ye auspicious. Deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.26.7 The grief that pains me here, whoever caused it, not sent by fate, hath sprung from human action. I, suppliant, praise Heaven, Earth, and oft invoke them. Deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
;;; XXVII A hymn to the Maruts
4.27.1 I think upon the Maruts: may they bless me, may they assist me to this wealth in battle. I call them like swift well-trained steeds to help us. May they deliver us from grief and trouble.
4.27.2 Those who surround the never-failing fountain for ever, and bedew the plants with moisture, The Maruts, Prini's sons, I chiefly honour. May they deliver us from grief and trouble.
4.27.3 Bards, who invigorate the milk of milch-kine, the sap of growing plants, the speed of coursers To us may the strong Maruts be auspicious. May they deliver us from grief and trouble.
4.27.4 They who raised water from the sea to heaven and send it from the sky to earth in showers, The Maruts who move mighty with their waters, may they deliver us from grief and trouble.
4.27.5 They who delight in nectar and in fatness, they who bestow upon us health and vigour. The Maruts who rain mighty with their waters, may they deliver us from grief and trouble.
4.27.6 Whether with stormy might the Maruts established this All, or Gods with their celestial power, Ye, kindly Gods, are able to restore it. May they deliver us from grief and trouble.
4.27.7 Potent in battles is the Maruts' army, impetuous train, well- known, exceeding mighty. I, suppliant, praise and oft invoke the Maruts. May they deliver us from grief and trouble.
;;; XXVIII A hymn to Bhava and Sarva
4.28.1 I Reverence you--mark this--Bhava and Sarva, ye under whose control is this that shineth. Lords of this world both quadruped and biped. Deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.28.2 Lords of all near and even of what is distant, famed as the best and skilfullest of archers, Lords of this world both quadruped and biped, Deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.28.3 Thousand-eyed foe-destroyers, I invoke you, still praising you the strong, of wide dominion: Lords of this world both quadruped and biped, Deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.28.4 Ye who of old wrought many a deed in concert, and showed among mankind unhappy omens; Lords of this world both quadruped and biped, Deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.28.5 Ye from the stroke of whose destroying weapon not one among the Gods or men escapeth, Lords of this world both quadruped and biped, Deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.28.6 Hurl your bolt, strong Gods, at the Yatudhana, him who makes ready roots and deals in magic: Lords of this world both quadruped and biped, Deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.28.7 Comfort and aid us, ye strong Gods, in battles, at each Kimidin send your bolt of thunder. I, suppliant, praise and ever call on Bhav and Sarva. Set us free from grief and trouble.
;;; XXIX A hymn to Mitra-Varuna
4.29.1 You twain, O Mitra, Varuna, I honour, Lawstrengtheners, wise, who drive away oppressors. Ye who protect the truthful in his battles, deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.29.2 Ye the wise Gods who drive away oppressors, ye who protect the truthful in his battles, Who come, men's guards, to juice pressed forth by Babhru,. deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.29.3 Mitra and Varuna who help Agasti, Atri, and Angiras, and Jamadagni, Ye who help Kasyapa, who help Vasishtha, deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.29.4 Mitra and Varuna, who help Syavasva, Atri, and Purumilha, and Vadhryasva, Ye who help Vimada and Saptavadhri, deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.29.5 Ye, Varuna, Mitra, who give aid to Kutsa, Gavishthira, Bharadvaja, Visvamitra, Who help Kakshivan and give aid to Kanva, deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.29.6 Ye, Mitra, Varuna, who help Trisoka, Medhatithi, and Usana son of Kavi, Ye, Gotama's and Mudgala's protectors, deliver us, ye twain, from grief and trouble.
4.29.7 Whose straight-reined car that keeps the track of goodness assails and ruins him who walks perversely I, suppliant, praise with constant invocation Mitra and Varuna. Save us from affliction.
;;; XXX A glorification of vak or speech
4.30.1 I travel with the Rudras and the Vasus, with the Adityas and All-Gods I wander. I hold aloft both Varuna and Mitra, I hold aloft Indra and both the Asvins.
4.30.2 I am the Queen, the gatherer-up of treasures, most thoughtful, first of those who merit worship. The Gods, making me enter many places, in diverse spots have set mine habitation.
4.30.3 I, verily, myself announce and utter the word that Gods, and men alike shall welcome. I make the man I love exceeding mighty, make him a sage, a Rishi, and a Brahman.
4.30.4 Through me alone all eat the food that feeds them, each man who sees, breathes, hears, the word out-spoken. They know it not, but yet they dwell beside me. Hear, one and all, the truth as I declare it.
4.30.5 I bend the bow for Rudra that his arrow may strike and slay the hater of devotion. I rouse and order battle for the people, and I have penetrated Earth and Heaven.
4.30.6 I cherish and sustain high-swelling Soma, and Tvashtar I support, Pashan, and Bhaga. I load with wealth the zealous sacrificer who pours the juice and offers his oblation.
4.30.7 On the world's summit I bring forth the Father: my home is in the waters, in the ocean. Thence I extend o'er all existing creatures, and touch even yonder heaven with my forehead.
4.30.8 I breathe a strong breath like the wind and tempest, the while I hold together all existence. Beyond this wide earth and beyond the heavens I have become so mighty in my grandeur.
;;; XXXI A hymn to Manyu or Wrath
4.31.1 Borne on with thee, O Manyu girt by Maruts, let our brave men, impetuous, bursting forward, March on, like flames of fire in form, exulting, with pointed arrows, sharpening their weapons.
4.31.2 Flashing like fire, be thou, O conquering Manyu, invoked, O victor, as our army's leader. Slay thou our foes, distribute their possession: show forth thy vigour, scatter those who hate us.
4.31.3 O Manyu, overcome those who assail us. On! breaking, slaying, crushing down the foemen. They have not hindered thine impetuous vigour: mighty! sole born! reduce them to subjection.
4.31.4 Alone of many thou art worshipped, Manyu: sharpen the spirit of each clan for combat. With thee to aid, O thou of perfect splendour, we raise the glorious battle-shout for conquest.
4.31.5 Unyielding, bringing victory like Indra, O Manyu be thou here our sovran ruler. To thy dear name. O victor, we sing praises: we know the spring from which thou art come hither.
4.31.6 Twin-borne with power, destructive bolt of thunder the highest conquering might is thine, subduer! Be friendly to us in thy spirit, Manyu! O much-invoked, in shock of mighty battle!
4.31.7 For spoil let Varuna and Manyu give us the wealth of both sides gathered and collected; And let our enemies with stricken spirits, o'er-whelmed with. terror, sling away defeated.
;;; XXXII A hymn to Manyu
4.32.1 He who hath reverenced thee, Manyu, destructive bolt! breeds. for himself forthwith all conquering energy. Arya and Dasa will we conquer with thine aid, with thee the conqueror, with conquest conquest-sped.
4.32.2 Manyu was Indra, yea, the God was Manyu; Manyu was Hotar Varuna, Jatavedas. The tribes of human lineage worship Manyu. Accordant, with thy fervour, Manyu! guard us.
4.32.3 Come hither, Manyu, mightier than the mighty: smite, with thy fervour, for ally, our foemen. Slayer of foes, of Vritra, and of Dasyu, bring thou to us all kinds of wealth and treasure.
4.32.4 For thou art, Manyu, of surpassing vigour, fierce, queller of the foe, and self-existent, Shared by all men, victorious, subduer: vouchsafe to us superior strength in battles.
4.32.5 I have departed still without a portion, wise God! according to thy will, the mighty. I, feeble man, was wroth with thee, O Manyu. Come in thy proper form and give us vigour.
4.32.6 Come hither, I am all thine own: advancing, turn thou to me, victorious, all-bestowing. Come to me, Manyu, wielder of the thunder: bethink thee of thy friend, and slay the Dasyus.
4.32.7 Approach, and on our right hand hold thy station, then let us slay a multitude of foemen. The best of meath I offer to support thee: may we be first to drink thereof in quiet.
;;; XXXIII A prayer to Agni for protection and prosperity
4.33.1 Chasing our pain with splendid light, O Agni, shine thou wealth on us. His lustre flash our pain away.
4.33.2 For goodly fields, for pleasant homes, for wealth we sacrifice to thee. His lustre flash our pain away!
4.33.3 Best praiser of all these be he, and foremost be our noble chiefs. His lustre flash our pain away!
4.33.4 So that thy worshipper and we, thine, Agni! in our sons may live. His lustre flash our pain away!
4.33.5 As ever conquering Agni's beams of splendour go to every side, His lustre flash our pain away.
4.33.6 To every side thy face is turned, thou art triumphant everywhere. His lustre flash our pain away!
4.33.7 O thou whose face looks every way, bear off our foes as in a ship. His lustre flash our pain away!
4.33.8 As in a ship across the flood, transport us to felicity. His lustre flash our pain away
;;; XXXIV Glorification of the Vishtari sacrifice
4.34.1 The head of this is prayer, its back the Brihat, Odanas's belly is the Vamadevya; Its face reality, its sides the metre, Vishtari sacrifice produced from fervour.
4.34.2 Boneless, cleansed, purified by him who cleanseth, they go res- plendent to the world of splendour. Fire burneth not their organ of enjoyment: much pleasure have they in the world of Svarga.
4.34.3 Never doth want or evil fortune visit those who prepare oblation called Vishtari. He goes unto the Gods, he dwells with Yama, he joys among Gandharvas meet for Soma.
4.34.4 Yama robs not of generative vigour the men who dress oblation called Vishtari. Borne on his car, a charioteer, he travels: endowed with wings he soars beyond the heavens.
4.34.5 Strongest is this, performed, of sacrifices: he hath reached heaven who hath prepared Vishtari. The oval-fruited lotus spreads his fibre: there bloom the nelo- phar and water-lilies. Abundant with their overflow of sweetness, these streams shall reach thee in the world of Svarga, whole lakes with lotus- blossom shall approach thee.
4.34.6 Full lakes of butter with their banks of honey, flowing with wine, and milk and curds and water Abundant with their overflow of sweetness, these streams shall reach thee in the world of Svarga, whole lakes with lotus- blossom shall approach thee.
4.34.7 I give four pitchers, in four several places, filled to the brim with milk and curds and water. Abundant with their overflow of sweetness, these streams shall reach thee in the world of Svarga, whole lakes with lotus- blossom shall approach thee.
4.34.8 I part this Odana among the Brahmans, Vishtari, conquering worlds and reaching heaven. Let me not lose it: swelling by its nature, be it my perfect Cow to grant all wishes!
;;; XXXV Magnification of the Odana or oblation of milk and rice
4.35.1 Odana which Prajapati, the firstborn of Order, dressed with fervour for the Brahman, which guards the worlds from breaking atIthe centre,--I with this Odana will conquer Mrityu.
4.35.2 Whereby the World-Creators vanquished Mrityu, that which they found by fervour, toil and trouble, That which prayer first made ready for the Brahman,--I with this Odana will conquer Mrityu.
4.35.3 That which upholds the Earth, the all-sustainer, that which hath filled air's middle realm with moisture, Which, raised on high in grandeur, stablished heaven,--I with this Odana will conquer Mrityu.
4.35.4 From which the months with thirty spokes were moulded, from which the twelve-spoked year was formed and fashioned. Which circling day and night have ne'er o'ertaken,--I with this Odana will conquer Mrityu.
4.35.5 Which hath become breath-giver, life-bestower; to which the worlds flow full of oil and fatness, To whom belong all the refulgent regions,--I with this Odana will conquer Mrityu.
4.35.6 From which, matured, sprang Amrit into being, which hath become Gayatris lord and ruler, In which the perfect Vedas have been treasured,--I with this Odana will conquer Mrityu,
4.35.7 I drive away the hostile God-despiser: far off be those who are mine adversaries, I dress Brahmaudana that winneth all things. May the Gods hear me who believe and trust them.
;;; XXXVI A charm against fiends, human enemies, and other pests
4.36.1 Endowed with true strength, let the Bull, Agni Vaisvanara, burn them up. Him who would pain and injure us, him who would treat us as a foe.
4.36.2 Him who, unharmed, would injure us, and him who, harmed, would do us harm, I lay between the doubled fangs of Agni, of Vaisvanara.
4.36.3 Those who, what time the moon is dark, hunt with loud cry and answering shout, Flesh-eaters, others who would harm,--all these I overcome with might.
4.36.4 I conquer the Pisachas with my power, and take their wealth away. All who would injure us I slay. Let mine intention have success.
4.36.5 With Gods who flee with him, and match their rapid motion with the Sun, I with those animals who dwell in rivers and on hills am found.
4.36.6 I trouble the Pisachas as the tiger plagues men rich in kine. They, even as dogs when they have seen a lion, find no hiding- place.
4.36.7 Naught with Pisachas can I do, with thieves, with roamers of the wood. Pisachas flee and vanish from each village as I enter it.
4.36.8 Into whatever village this mine awful power penetrates, Thence the Pisachas flee away, and plot no further mischief there.
4.36.9 Those who enrage me with their prate, as flies torment an elephant, I deem unhappy creatures, like small insects troublesome to man.
4.36.10 Destruction seize upon the man, as with a cord they hold a horse, The fool who is enraged with me! He is not rescued from the noose.
;;; XXXVII A charm against Gandharvas and Apsarases
4.37.1 With thee, O Plant, in olden time Atharvans smote and slew the fiends. Kasyapa smote with thee, with thee did Kanava and Agastya smite.
4.37.2 With thee we scare and drive away Gandharvas and Apsarases. O Ajasringi, chase the fiends. Cause all to vanish with thy smell.
4.37.3 Let the Apsarases, puffed away, go to the river, to the ford,-- Guggulu, Pila, Naladi, Aukshagandhi, Pramandini. Ye have become attentive since the Apsarases have past away.
4.37.4 Where great trees are, Asvatthas and Nyagrodhas with their leafy crests, There where your swings are green and bright, and lutes and cymbals sound in tune, 'Ye have become attentive since the Apsarases have past away.
4.37.5 Hither hath come this one, the most effectual of herbs and plants.
4.37.6 Let Ajasringi penetrate, Ara4aki with sharpened horn.
4.37.7 From the Gandharva, dancing near, the lord of the Apsarases, Wearing the tuft of hair, I take all manhood and virility.
4.37.8 With those dread hundred iron spears, the darts of Indra, let it pierce. The Blyxa-fed Gandharvas, those who bring no sacrificial gift.
4.37.9 With those dread hundred golden spears, the darts of Indra, let it pierce. The Blyxa-fed Gandharvas, those who bring no sacrificial gift.
4.37.10 O Plant, be thou victorious, crush the Pisachas, one and all, Blyxa-fed, shining in the floods, illumining the selfish ones.
4.37.11 Youthful, completely decked with hair, one monkey-like, one like a dog,-- So the Gandharva, putting on a lovely look, pursues a dame. Him with an efficacious charm we scare and cause to vanish hence.
4.37.12 Your wives are the Apsarases, and ye, Gandharvas, are their lords. Run ye, immortal ones, away: forbear to interfere with men!
;;; XXXVIII A charm for success in gambling
4.38.1 Hither I call the Apsaras, victorious, who plays with skill, Her who comes freely fort to view, who wins the stakes in games of dice.
4.38.2 Hither I call that Apsaras who scatters and who gathers up. The Apsaras who plays with skill and takes her winnings in the game.
4.38.3 Dancing around us with the dice, winning the wager by her play. May she obtain the stake for us and gain the victory with skill. May she approach us full of strength: let them not win this wealth of ours.
4.38.4 Hither I call that Apsaras, the joyous, the delightful one-- Those nymphs who revel in the dice, who suffer grief and yield to wrath.
4.38.5 Who follow in their course the rays of Surya, or as a particle of light attend him. Whose leader from afar, with store of riches, compasses quickly all the worlds and guards them. Pleased, may he come to this our burnt oblation, together with the Air, enriched with treasure.
4.38.6 Together with the Air, O rich in treasure, guard here the white cow and the calf, O mighty! Here are abundant drops for thee, come hither! Here is thy white calf, let thy mind be with us.
4.38.7 Together with the Air, O rich in treasure, keep the white calf in safety here, O mighty! Here is the grass, here is the stall, here do we bind the calf. We are your masters, name by name. All Hail!
;;; XXXIX A prayer to various deities for health, wealth, and prosperity
4.39.1 Agni no earth kath had mine homage. May he bless me. As I have bowed me down to Agni on the earth, so let the Favouring Graces bow them down to me.
4.39.2 Earth is the Cow, her calf is Agni. May she with her calf Agni yield me food, strength, all my wish, life first of all, and off- spring, plenty, wealth. All Hail!
4.39.3 Vayu in air hath had mine homage. May he bless me. As I have bowed me down to Vayu in the air, so let the Favour- ing Graces bow them down to me.
4.39.4 Air is the Cow, her calf is Vayu. May she with her calf Vayu yield me food, strength, all my wish, life first of all, and off- spring, plenty, wealth. All Hail!
4.39.5 The Sun in heaven hath had my homage. May he bless me. As I have bowed me down unto the Sun in heaven, so let the Favouring Graces bow them down to me.
4.39.6 Heaven is the Cow, her calf Aditya. May she yield with her calf the Sun food, strength, and all my wish, life first of all, and offspring, plenty, wealth. All Hail!
4.39.7 To Chandra in the quarters have I bowed me. May he bless me. As unto Chandra in the quarters I have bent, so let the Favour- ing Graces bow them down to me.
4.39.8 The quarters are the Cows, their calf is Chandra. May they yield with their calf the Moon food, strength and all my wish, life first of all, and offspring, plenty, wealth. All Hail!
4.39.9 Agni moves having entered into Agni, the Rishis' son, who guards from imprecations, I offer unto thee with reverent worship. Let me not mar the Gods' appointed service.
4.39.10 Skilled in all ways, O God, O Jatavedas, I offer what is cleansed by heart and spirit. To all thy seven mouths, O Jatavedas. Do thou accept with pleasure my libation.
;;; X A charm against rival worshippers
4.40.1 O Jatavedas, eastward sacrificers, as foes assail us from the eastern quarter. May they, turned back, be pained for harming Agni. I drive them backward with mine incantation.
4.40.2 O Jatavedas, southward sacrificers as foes assail us from the southern quarter. May they, turned back, be pained for harming Yama. I smite them backward with mine incantation.
4.40.3 O Jatavedas, westward sacrificers as foes assail us from the western quarter. For harming Varuna be they turned and troubled! I smite them backward with mine incantation.
4.40.4 Jatavedas, northward sacrificers as foes assail us from the northern quarter. For harming Soma be they turned and troubled! I smite them backward with mine incantation.
4.40.5 O Jatavedas, nether sacrificers, as foes assail us from the stead- fast quarter. For harming Earth let them be turned and troubled. I smite them backward with mine incantation.
4.40.6 Those who pay sacrifice, O Jatavedas, from air assail us from the midway quarter. For harming Vayu be they turned and troubled! I smite them backward with mine incantation.
4.40.7 The sacrificers from above assail us, O Jatavedas, from the lofty quarter. For wronging Surya be they turned and troubled! I smite them backward with mine incantation.
4.40.8 Those from all points assail us, Jatavedas, who sacrifice from intermediate regions. For wronging Prayer let them be turned and troubled, I smite them backward with mine incantation.
;;; I A glorification of Trita and Varuna
5.1.1 He who with special plans and deathless spirit, waxing, well- born, hath come unto his birth-place, As he who shines upholds the days, thus Trita, of pure life, bears the Three as their supporter.
5.1.2 He who, the first, approached the holy statutes makes, after, many beauteous forms and figures. Eager to drink, his birth-place first he entered who understands the word when yet unspoken.
5.1.3 He who--the fluid gold, with radiant kinsmen--to fervent glow delivered up thy body, On him both set names, that shall live for ever: to him the regions shall send robes to clothe him,
5.1.4 As these have gone to their primeval station, each gaining an imperishable dwelling, May kissing mothers of the bards' beloved bring the pole-draw- ing husband to the sister.
5.1.5 By holy wisdom I a sage, Far-Strider! offer to thee this lofty adoration. This worship both the mighty eddying rivers, coming together to this station, heighten.
5.1.6 Seven are the pathways which the wise have fashioned: to one of these may come the troubled mortal. On sure ground where the ways are parted standeth Life's Pillar in the dwelling of the Highest.
5.1.7 Working, I go my way with deathless spirit: life, spirit, bodies have gone gladly thither. Aye, Sakra also gives his gift of treasure as when the sacrificer meets with power.
5.1.8 Yea, the son asks dominion of his father: this they declared the noblest path to welfare. Varuna, let them see thy revelations: display the wondrous shapes of times to follow.
5.1.9 Halt with the milk, its other half, thou minglest and with that half, strong! unbeguiled! increasest. Let us exalt the gracious friend, the mighty, Varuna son of- Aditi, strength-giver. We have told him the marvels sung by poets. The utterance of Heaven and Earth is truthful.
;;; II A glorification of Indra
5.2.1 In all the worlds That was the best and highest whence sprang the Mighty One of splendid valour. As soon as born he overcomes his foemen, when those rejoice in him who bring him succour.
5.2.2 Grown mighty in his strength, with ample vigour, he as a foe strikes fear into the Dasa, Eager to win the breathing and the breathless: All sang thy praise at banquet and oblation.
5.2.3 All concentrate on thee their mental vigour what time these, twice or thrice, are thine assistants, Blend what is sweeter than the sweet with sweetness win quickly with our meath that meath in battle.
5.2.4 If verily in every war the sages joy and exult in thee who win- nest treasures, With mightier power, strong God, extend thy firmness: let not malevolent Kaokas harm thee.
5.2.5 Proudly we put our trust in thee in battles, when we behold great wealth the prize of combat. I with my words impel thy weapons onward, and sharpen with my prayer thy vital vigour.
5.2.6 Thou in that house, the highest or the lowest, which thy protec- tion guards, bestowest riches. Establish ye the ever-wandering mother, and bring full many deeds to their completion.
5.2.7 Praise in the height Him who hath many pathways, courageous, strongest, Aptya of the Aptyas Through strength he shows himself of ample power: pattern of Prithivi, he fights and conquers.
5.2.8 Brihaddiva, the foremost of light-winners, hath made these holy prayers, this strength for Indra. Free Lord, he rules the mighty fold of cattle, winning, aglow, even all the billowy waters.
5.2.9 Thus hath Brihaddiva, the great Atharvan, spoken to Indra as himself in person. Two sisters free from stain, the Matarivans, with power impel him onward and exalt him.
;;; III A prayer to Agni, Indra, and other deities for victory and prosperity
5.3.1 Let strength be mine while I invoke thee, Agni! enkindling thee may we support our bodies. May the four regions bend and bow before me: with thee for guardian may we win the combat.
5.3.2 Baffling the range of our opponents, Agni! guard us as our protector round about us. Down the steep slope go they who hate us, backward, and let their thought who watch at home be ruined.
5.3.3 May all the Gods be on my side in battle, the Maruts led by Indra, Vishnu, Agni. Mine be the middle air's extended region, and may the Wind blow favouring these my wishes.
5.3.4 For me let them present all mine oblations, and let my mind's intention be accomplished. May I be guiltless of the least transgression: may all the Gods come hither and protect me.
5.3.5 May the Gods grant me riches, may the blessing and invocation of the Gods assist me. This boon shall the celestial Hotars win us: may we, unwound- ed, have brave heroes round us.
5.3.6 Ye six divine Expanses, give us freedom. Here, all ye Gods, acquit yourselves like heroes. Let not calamity or curse o'ertake us, nor deeds of wickedness that merit hatred.
5.3.7 Do ye three Goddesses give ample shelter and all success to us ourselves and children. Let us not lose our children or our bodies: let us not benefit the foe, King Soma!
5.3.8 Foodful and much-invoked, at this our calling may the far- reaching Bull grant us wide shelter. Lord of bay coursers, Indra, bless our children: harm us not, give us not as prey to others.
5.3.9 Lord of the world, Creator and Disposer, may the God Savitar who quells assailants, May the Adityas, Rudras, both the Asvins, Gods, guard the sacrificer from destruction.
5.3.10 Let those who are our foemen stay afar from us: with Indra and with Agni we will drive them off. The Adityas and the Rudras, over us on high, have made me strong, a thinker, and a sovran lord.
5.3.11 Yea, we call Indra hitherward, the winner of wealth in battle and of kine and horses. May he mark this our worship when we call him, Lord of bay steeds, thou art our friend and comrade.
;;; IV A charm against fever and other ailments
5.4.1 Thou who wast born on mountains, thou most mighty of all plants that grow. Thou Banisher of Fever, come, Kushtha! make Fever pass away.
5.4.2 Brought from the Snowy Mountain, born on the high hill where eagles breed, Men seek to buy thee when they hear: for Fever's Banisher they know.
5.4.3 In the third heaven above us stands the Asvattha tree, the seat of Gods. There the Gods sought the Kushtha Plant, embodiment of end- less life.
5.4.4 There moved through heaven a golden ship, a ship with cordage wrought of Gold. There the Gods won the Kushtha Plant, the blossom of eternal life.
5.4.5 They sailed on pathways paved with gold, the oars they piled were wrought of gold: All golden were the ships wherein they carried Kushtha down to earth.
5.4.6 O Kushtha, bring thou hitherward this man of mine, restore his health, Yes, free him from disease for me.
5.4.7 Thou art descended from thee Gods, Soma's benignant friend art thou, Befriend my breath and vital air be gracious unto this mine eye.
5.4.8 Sprung, northward, from the Snowy Hill thou art conveyed to eastern men. There they deal out among themselves Kushtha's most noble qualities.
5.4.9 Most excellent, indeed, art thou, Kushtha! most noble is thy sire. Make all Consumption pass away and render Fever powerless.
5.4.10 Malady that affects the head, eye-weakness, bodily defect-- All this let Kushtha heal and cure: aye, godlike is the vigorous power.
;;; V A charm to mend a broken bone
5.5.1 Aryaman is thy grandsire, Night thy mother, and the Cloud thy sire. Thy name is called Silachi. Thou, thyself, art sister of the Gods.
5.5.2 Whoever drinketh thee hath life: thou savest and protectest man. As nursing mother of mankind, thou takest all upon thy lap.
5.5.3 Thou clingest close to every tree, as a fond damsel clasps her love. Thy name is called The Conqueror, She who Stands Fast, The Rescuer.
5.5.4 Whatever wound the arrow, or the staff, or violence inflicts, Thereof thou art the remedy: as such restore this man to health.
5.5.5 Thou springest from blest Plaxa, or Asvattha, Dhava, Khadira, Parna, or blest Nyagrodha, so come thou to use, Arundhati!
5.5.6 Gold-coloured, bringing happy fate, most lovely, brilliant as the Sun, Mayst thou, O Healing! come unto the fracture: Healing is thy name.
5.5.7 Gold-coloured, bringing happy fate, odorous, hairy-bodied one, The sister of the Waters art thou, Laksha! and thy soul is Wind.
5.5.8 Silachi is thy name: thy sire, O goat-brown! is a damsel's son. Thou hast been sprinkled by the mouth of Yama's tawny- coloured horse.
5.5.9 Issuing from the horse's blood away she glided to the trees. Become a winged water-brook, and come to us, Arundhati!
;;; VI A prayer for protection and prosperity
5.6.1 Eastward at first the prayer was generated: Vena disclosed bright flashes from the summit, Disclosed his deepest nearest revelations, womb of the non- existent and existent.
5.6.2 None have attained to those of old, those who wrought holy acts for you, Let them not harm our heroes here. Therefore I set before you this.
5.6.3 Sweet-tongued, exhaustless, they have sent their voices down together in heaven's vault that pours a thousand streams. His wildly-restless warders never close an eye: in every place the snarers stand to bind men fast.
5.6.4 Speed forward, conquering all foes, to win the spoil, Thou comest on thy haters with a surging sea. Thy name is Fragile. The thirteenth month is Indra's home.
5.6.5 Through this now hast thou sent thy gifts. All hail! With sharpened arms and missiles, kind and friendly, be gracious unto us, Soma and Rudra!
5.6.6 Through this hast thou been left in want. All hail! With sharpened arms and missiles, kind and friendly, be gracious unto us, Soma and Rudra!
5.6.7 Through this hast thou committed faults. All hail! With sharpened arms and missiles, kind and friendly, be gracious unto us, Soma and Rudra!
5.6.8 Free us from trouble, free us from dishonour, accept our wor- ship, give us life immortal.
5.6.9 O missile of the eye, missile of spirit, thou missile of devotion and of fervour! Thou art the weapon shot against the weapon. Let those be weaponless who sin against us.
5.6.10 Make with thy weapon weaponless, O Agni, all wicked men who deal with us as foemen with eye, with thought, with spirit, or intention.
5.6.11 Thou art the house of Indra. I betake me to thee, I enter thee with all my cattle, With all my people and with all my body, with all my soul, with mine entire possessions.
5.6.12 Thou art the guard of Indra. I betake me to thee, etc.
5.6.13 Thou art the shield of Indra. I betake me to thee, etc.
5.6.14 Indra's protection art thou. I betake me to thee, I enter thee with all my cattle. With all my people and with all my body, with all my soul, with mine entire possessions.
;;; VII A charm to deprecate Arati or Malignity
5.7.1 Bring thou to us, bar not the way, Arati! Stay not the guerdon that is being brought us. Homage be paid to Failure, to Misfortune, and Malignity.
5.7.2 The man whom thou preferrest, O Arati, he who prates to us-- This man of thine, we reverence. Baffle not thou my heart's desire,
5.7.3 May our desire which Gods have roused fulfil itself by day and night. We seek to win Arati: to Arati be our homage paid.
5.7.4 We, suppliant, call on Bhaga, on Sarasvati, Anumati, Pleasant words have I spoken, sweet as honey is, at invocations of the Gods.
5.7.5 The portion that I crave with speech intelligent and full of power, May faith, presented with the gift of tawny Soma, find to-day.
5.7.6 Do not thou make our words or wishes fruitless. Let the twain Indra Agni, bring us treasures. All, fain to-day to give us gifts, welcome Arati with your love.
5.7.7 Misfortune! go thou far away: we turn thy harmful dart aside. I know thee well, Arati! as oppressor, one who penetrates.
5.7.8 Oft, coming as a naked girl thou hauntest people in their sleep, Baffling the thought, Arati! and the firm intention of a man.
5.7.9 To her the mighty vast in size, who penetrates all points of space, To her mine homage have I paid, Nirriti with her golden hair.
5.7.10 Auspicious, with her golden hue, pillowed on gold, the mighty one To this Arati clad in robes of gold mine homage have I paid.
;;; VIII A charm for the discomfiture and destruction of hostile priests
5.8.1 With fuel of Vikankata bring molten butter to the Gods. O Agni, make them joyful here: let them all come unto my call.
5.8.2 O Indra, come unto my call, This will I do. So hear it thou. Let these exertions for the sake of Indra guide my wish aright. Therewith, O Jatavedas, Lord of Bodies! may we win us strength.
5.8.3 Whatever plot from yonder, O ye Gods, that godless man would frame, Let not the Gods come to his call, nor Agni bear his offering up. Come, ye, come hither to my call.
