5.8.4 Run, ye Fxertions, farther on By Indra's order smite and slay. As a wolf worrieth a sheep, so let not him escape from you while life remains. Stop fast his breath.
5.8.5 The Brahman whom those yonder have appointed priest, for injury, He, Indra! is beneath thy feet. I cast him to the God of Death.
5.8.6 If they have issued forth, strongholds of Gods, and made their shield of prayer, Gaining protection for their lives, protection round about, make all their instigation powerless.
5.8.7 Exertions which that man hath made, Exertions which he yet will make Turn them, O Indra, back again, O Vritra-slayer, back again on him that they may kill that man.
5.8.8 As Indra, having seized him, set his foot upon Udvachana, Even so for all the coming years I cast those men beneath my feet.
5.8.9 Here, Indra Vritra-slayer, in thy strength pierce thou their vital. parts. Here, even here, attack them, O Indra. Thine own dear friend am I. Indra, we closely cling to thee. May we be in thy favouring grace.
;;; IX A prayer to Heaven and Earth for protection and assistance
5.9.1 All hail to Heaven!
5.9.2 All hail to Earth!
5.9.3 All hail to Air!
5.9.4 All hail to Air!
5.9.5 All hail to Heaven!
5.9.6 All hail to Eartht!
5.9.7 Mine eye is Siirya and my breath is Vata, Air is my soul and Prithivi my body. I verily who never have been conquered give up my life toe Heaven and Earth for keeping.
5.9.8 Exalt my life, my strength, my deed and action; increase my understanding and my vigour. Be ye my powerful keepers, watch and guard me, ye mistresses of life and life's creators! Dwell ye within me, and forbear to harm me.
;;; X A prayer to the presiding deities of the four quarters for protection
5.10.1 Thou art my wall of stone against the sinner who fights against me from the eastern quarter. May he encounter it!
5.10.2 Thou art my wall of stone against the sinner who fights against me from the southern quarter. May he encounter it!
5.10.3 Thou art my wall of stone against the sinner who fights against me from the western quarter. May he encounter it!
5.10.4 Thou art my wall of stone against the sinner who fights against me from northern quarter. May he encounter it!
5.10.5 Thou art my wall of stone against the sinner who fights against me from the stedfast region. May he encounter it! r 6.Thou art my wall of stone against the sinner who fights against Lme from the lofty region! M iy he encounter it!
5.10.7 Thou art my wall of stone against the sinner who from points intermediate fights against me. May he encounter it!
5.10.8 With Brihat I invoke the mind, with Matarisvan both the breaths, The eye from Surya, and the ear from Air, the body from the Earth. We, with Sarasvati who suits the mind, call Speech to come to us.
;;; XI A dialogue between Atharvan and Varuna
5.11.1 How, terrible in might, hast thou here spoken to the great God, how to the gold-hued Father! Thy mind watched, greedy Varuna! to recover the brindled cow thou hadst bestowed as guerdon.
5.11.2 Not through desire do I revoke my present: I bring this brind- led cow to contemplate her. Now by what lore, by what inherent nature, knowest thou all things that exist, Atharvan?
5.11.3 Truly I am profound in wisdom, truly I know by nature all existing creatures. No Dasa by his greatness, not an Arya, may violate the law that I will stablish.
5.11.4 None, self-dependent Varuna! existeth wiser than thou or sager by his wisdom. Thou knowest well all these created beings: even the man of wondrous powers fears thee.
5.11.5 O self-dependent Varuna, wise director, thou knowest verily all generations. What is, unerring one! beyond this region? What more remote than that which is most distant?
5.11.6 One thing there is beyond this air, and something beyond that one, most hard to reach, remotest. I, Varuna, who know, to thee declare it. Let churls be mighty in the lower regions. Let Dasas sink into the earth beneath them.
5.11.7 Many reproaches, Varuna, dost thou utter against the misers. who revoke their presents. Be not thou added to that crowd of niggards: let not men call thee an illiberal giver.
5.11.8 Let not men call me an illiberal giver. I give thee back the brindled cow, O singer. Attend in every place where men inhabit, with all thy powers, the hymn that tells my praises.
5.11.9 Let hymns of praise ascend to thee, uplifted in every place of human habitation. But give me now the gift thou hast not given. Thou art my friend for ever firm and faithful.
5.11.10 One origin, Varuna! one bond unites us I know the nature of that common kinship. I give thee now the gift that I retracted. I am thy friend for ever firm and faithful.
5.11.11 God, giving life unto the god who lauds me, Sage strengthener of the sage who sings my praises. Thou, self-dependent Varuna! hast begotten the kinsman of the Gods, our sire Atharvan. On him bestow most highly-lauded riches. Thou art our friend, high over all, our kinsman.
;;; XII An Apri or propitiatory hymn
5.12.1 Thou in the house of man this day enkindled worshippest Gods as God, O Jatavedas. Observant, bright as Mitra, bring them hither. Thou art a sapient and foreknowing envoy.
5.12.2 Tanunapat, fair-tongued! with sweet meath balming the baths and ways of Order, make them pleasant. Bear to the Gods our sacrifice, exalting with holy thoughts our hymns of praise and worship.
5.12.3 Invoked, deserving prayer and adoration, O Agni, come accor dant with the Vasus. Thou art, O youthful Lord, the Gods' Invoker, so, best of sacri- ficers, bring them quickly.
5.12.4 By rule the Sacred Grass is scattered eastward, a robe to clothe this earth when dawns are breaking. Widely it spreads around and far extended, fair for the Gods and bringing peace and freedom,
5.12.5 Let the expansive Doors be widely opened, like wives who deck their beauty for their husbands. Lofty, celestial, all-impelling Portals, admit the Gods and give them easy entrance!
5.12.6 Pouring sweet dews let holy Night and Morning, each close to each, be seated at their station,-- Lofty, celestial Dames with gold to deck them, assuming all their fair and radiant beauty.
5.12.7 Come the first two celestial sweet-voiced Hotars, arranging sacrifice for man to worship, As singers who inspire us in assemblies, showing the eastern light with their direction!
5.12.8 Let Bharati come quickly to our worship and Ila showing like a human being. So let Sarasvati and both her fellows, deft Goddesses, on this fair grass be seated.
5.12.9 Hotar more skilled in sacrifice, bring hither with speed to-day God Tvashar, thou who knowest, Even him who formed these two, the Earth and Heaven, the Parents, with their forms, and every creature.
5.12.10 Bring thou to our oblations which thou balmest the companies of Gods in ordered season. Agni, Vanaspati, the Immolator sweeten our offered gifts with meath and butter!
5.12.11 Agni as soon as he was born made ready the sacrifice and was the Gods' preceder. May the Gods eat our offering consecrated according to this true Priest's voice and guidance.
;;; XIII A charm against snakes
5.13.1 Varuna, Sage of heaven, hath given me the gift: with spells of mighty power I draw thy poison out. Dug up, not dug, adherent, I have seized it fast: low hath thy venom sunk like water in the sands.
5.13.2 All the non-fluid portion of thy venom, I receive in these. I take thy middlemost, thy highest, lowest juice: may it be spent and lest by reason of thy fear.
5.13.3 Strong is my cry like thunder with the rainy cloud: with power- ful incantation let thy strength be stayed. I, with the men to aid, have seized that juice of his; as light from out the gloom, let Surya rise on high
5.13.4 I with this eye destroy thine eye, and with this poison conquer thine. Live not, O Snake, but die the death: back go thy venom on thyself.
5.13.5 Listen to me, Black Snakes and hateful creatures, Lurker-in- Grass, Karait, and Brown, and Spotty, Approach not near the house my friend inhabits: give warning, and rest quiet with your poison.
5.13.6 Even as the cord that strings the bow, I slacken, as it were, the cars. Of the All-conquering serpent's wrath, of the fierce rage of Black, and Brown, Taimata, and Apodaka.
5.13.7 And Aligi and Viligi, their father and the mother too,-- What will ye do? Your venomed sap, we know, is utterly powerless.
5.13.8 Daughter of Urugula, she-fiend whom the black, skinned mother bare-- All female serpents poison who crept swiftly near is impotent.
5.13.9 Dwelling beside the mountain's slope, the quick-eared porcupine exclaimed: Of all these she-snakes homed in earth the poison is most powerless.
5.13.10 Tabuva or not Tabuva, thou verily art not Tabuva: poison is killed by Tabuva. Tastuva or not Tastuva, thou verily art not Tastuva: poison is killed by Tastuva.
;;; XIV A charm against witchcraft
5.14.1 An eagle found thee: with his snout a wild boar dug thee from the earth. Harm thou, O Plant, the mischievous, and drive the sorcerer away.
5.14.2 Beat thou the Yatudhanas back, drive thou away the sorcerer; And chase afar, O Plant, the man who fain would do us injury.
5.14.3 As 'twere a strip cut round from skin of a white-footed an- telope, Bind, like a golden chain, O God, his witchcraft on the sorcerer.
5.14.4 Take thou his sorcery by the hand, and to the sorcerer lead it back. Lay it before him, face to face, that it may kill the sorcerer.
5.14.5 Back on the wizard fall his craft, upon the curser light his curse! Let witchcraft, like a well-naved car, roll back upon the sorcerer.
5.14.6 Whoso, for other's harm hath dealt-woman or man-in magic arts, To him we lead the sorcery back, even as a courser with a rope.
5.14.7 Now whether thou hast been prepared by Gods or been pre- pared by men, We, with our Indra at our side to aid us, lead thee back again.
5.14.8 Agni, victorious in fight, subdue the armies of our foes! Back on the sorcerer we cast his sorcery, and beat it home.
5.14.9 Thou who hast piercing weapons, pierce him who hath wrought it; conquer him. We do not sharpen thee to slay the man who hath not practised it.
5.14.10 Go as a son goes to his sire: bite as a trampled viper bites. As one who flies from bonds, go back, O Witchcraft, to the sorcerer.
5.14.11 Even as the timid antelope or hind from her assailant flees, So swiftly let the sorcery o'ertake and reach the sorcerer.
5.14.12 Straighter than any arrow let it fly against him, Heaven and Earth. So let that witchcraft seize again the wizard like a beast of chase.
5.14.13 Let it go contrary like flame, like water following its course. Let witchcraft, like a well-naved car, roll back upon the sorcerer.
;;; XV A charm for general prosperity
5.15.1 Plant! I have those who shall avert the threatened danger, ten and one. O sacred Plant, produced aright! make sweetness, sweet thy self, for me.
5.15.2 Twenty and two, O Plant, have I who shall avert the threatened ill. O sacred Plant, produced aright! make sweetness, sweet thyself, for me.
;;; XVI A charm for the increase of cattle
5.16.1 Bull! if thou art the single bull, beget. Thou hast no vital sap.
;;; XVII The abduction and restoration of a Brahman's wife
5.17.1 These first, the boundless Sea, and Matarisvan, fierce glowing Fire, the Strong, the Bliss-bestower, And heavenly Floods, first-born by holy Order, exclaimed against the outrage on a Brahman.
5.17.2 King Soma first of all, without reluctance, made restitution of the Brahman's consort. Mitra and Varuna were the inviters: Agni as Hotar took her hand and led her.
5.17.3 The man, her pledge, must by the hand be taken when he hath cried, She is a Brahman's consort. She stayed not for a herald to conduct her: thus is the kingdom of a ruler guarded.
5.17.4 She whom they call the star with loosened tresses, descending as. misfortune on the village, The Brahman's consort, she disturbs the kingdom where hath appeared the hare with fiery flashing.
5.17.5 Active in duty serves the Brahmachari: he is a member of the Gods' own body. Through him Brihaspati obtained his consort, as the Gods gained the ladle brought by Soma.
5.17.6 Thus spake of her those Gods of old, Seven Rishis, who sate them down to their austere devotion: Dire is a Brahman's wife led home by others: in the supremest heaven she plants confusion.
5.17.7 When infants die, untimely born, when herds of cattle waste away, When heroes strike each other dead, the Brahman's wife destroyeth them.
5.17.8 Even if ten former husbands--none a Brahman--had espoused a dame, And then a Brahman took her hand, he is her husband, only he,
5.17.9 Not Vaisya, not Rajanya, no, the Brahman is indeed her lord: This Surya in his course proclaims to the Five Races of man- kind.
5.17.10 So then the Gods restored her, so men gave the woman back again. Princes who kept their promises restored the Brahman's wedded wife.
5.17.11 Having restored the Brahman's wife, and freed them, with Gods' aid, from sin, They shared the fulness of the earth and worn themselves ex- tended sway.
5.17.12 No lovely wife who brings her dower in hundreds rests upon his bed, Within whose kingdom is detained, through want of sense, a Brahman's dame.
5.17.13 No broad-browed calf with wide-set ears is ever in his homestead born. Within whose kingdom is detained, through want of sense, a Brahman's dame.
5.17.14 No steward, golden-necklaced, goes before the meat-trays of the man. Within whose kingdom is detained, through want of sense, a Brahman's dame.
5.17.15 No black-eared courser, white of hue, moves proudly, harnessed to his car, In whose dominion is detained, through want of sense, a Brahman's dame.
5.17.16 No lily grows with oval bulbs, no lotus-pool is in his field, In whose dominion is detained, through senseless love, a Brahman's dame.
5.17.17 The men whose task it is to milk drain not the brindled cow for him, In whose dominion is detained, through senseless love, a Brahman's dame.
5.17.18 His milch-cow doth not profit one, his draught-ox masters not the yoke, Wherever, severed from his wife, a Brahman spends the mourn- ful night.
;;; XVIII The wickedness of oppressing and robbing Brahmans
5.18.1 The Gods, O Prince, have not bestowed this cow on thee to eat thereof. Seek not, Rajanya, to devour the Brahman's cow which none may eat.
5.18.2 A base Rajanya, spoiled at dice, and ruined by himself, may eat. The Brahman's cow and think, To-day and not tomorrow, let me live!
5.18.3 The Brahman's cow is like a snake, charged with due poison, clothed with skin. Rajanya! bitter to the taste is she, and none may eat of her.
5.18.4 She takes away his strength, she mars his splendour, she ruins everything like fire enkindled. That man drinks poison of the deadly serpent who counts the Brahman as mere food to feed him.
5.18.5 Whoever smites him, deeming him a weakling-blasphemer, coveting his wealth through folly Indra sets fire alight within his bosom. He who acts thus is loathed by Earth and Heaven.
5.18.6 No Brahman must be injured, safe as fire from him who loves himself. For Soma is akin to him and Indra guards him from the curse.
5.18.7 The fool who eats the Brahmans' food and thinks it pleasant to the taste, Eats, but can ne'er digest, the cow that bristles with a hundred barbs,
5.18.8 His voice an arrow's neck, his tongue a bowstring, his windpipes fire-enveloped heads of arrows, With these the Brahman pierces through blasphemers, with God-sped bows that quell the hearts within them.
5.18.9 Keen arrows have the Brahmans, armed with missiles: the shaft, when they discharge it, never faileth. Pursuing him with fiery zeal and anger, they pierce the foeman even from a distance.
5.18.10 They who, themselves ten hundred, were the rulers of a thousand men, The Vaitahavyas, were destroyed for that they ate a Brahman's cow.
5.18.11 The cow, indeed, when she was slain o'erthrew those Vaitahavyas, who Cooked the last she-goat that remained of Kesaraprabandha's flock.
5.18.12 One and a hundred were the folk, those whom the earth shook off from her: When they had wronged the Brahman race they perished incon- ceivably.
5.18.13 Among mankind the Gods' despiser moveth: he hath drunk poison, naught but bone is left him. Who wrongs the kinsman of the Gods, the Brahman, gains not the sphere to which the Fathers travelled.
5.18.14 Agni, in sooth, is called our guide, Soma is called our next of kin. Indra quells him who curses us. Sages know well that this is so.
5.18.15 Prince! like a poisoned arrow, like a deadly snake, O lord of kine! Dire is the Brahman's arrow: he pierces his enemies therewith.
;;; XIX The wickedness of robbing or insulting Brahmans
5.19.1 The sons of Vitahavya, the Srinjayas, waxed exceeding strong. They well-nigh touched the heavens, but they wronged Bhrigu and were overthrown.
5.19.2 When men pierced Brihatsaman through, the Brahman, son of Angiras, The ram with teeth in both his jaws, the sheep, devoured their progeny.
5.19.3 If men have spat upon, or shot their rheum upon a Brahman, they. Sit in the middle of a stream running with blood, devouring hair.
5.19.4 While yet the Brahman's cow which men are dressing quivers in her throe: She mars the kingdom's splendour: there no vigorous hero springs to life.
5.19.5 Terrible is her cutting-up: her bitter flesh is cast away, And it is counted sin among the Fathers if her milk is drunk.
5.19.6 If any King who deems himself mighty would eat a Brahman up, Rent and disrupted is that realm wherein a Brahman is oppres- sed.
5.19.7 She grows eight-footed, and four-eyed, four-eared, four-jawed, two-faced, two-tongued, And shatters down the kingdom of the man who doth the Brahman wrong.
5.19.8 As water swamps a leaky ship so ruin overflows that realm. Misfortune smites the realm wherein a Brahman suffers scath and harm.
5.19.9 The very trees repel the man, and drive him from their sheltering shade, Whoever claims, O Narada, the treasure that a Brahman owns.
5.19.10 That wealth, King Varuna hath said, is poison by the Gods prepared. None hath kept watch to guard his realm who hath devoured a Brahman's cow.
5.19.11 Those nine-and-ninety people whom Earth shook and cast away from her, When they had wronged the Brahman race were ruined incon- ceivably.
5.19.12 Oppressor of the Brahmans! thus the Gods have spoken and declared, The step-effacing wisp they bind upon the dead shall be thy couch.
5.19.13 Oppressor of the Brahmans! tears wept by the man who suffers wrong, These are the share of water which the Gods have destined to be thine.
5.19.14 The share of water which the Gods have destined to be thine, is that, Oppressor of the priest! wherewith men lave the corpse and wet the beard.
5.19.15 The rain of Mitra-Varuna falls not on him who wrongs the priest. To him no counsel brings success: he wins, no friend to do his will.
;;; XX A hymn to the War-drum to secure victory
5.20.1 Formed out of wood, compact with straps of leather, loud is the: War-drum as he plays the hero. Whetting thy voice and vanquishing opponents, roar at them like a lion fain to conquer!
5.20.2 The fastened frame hath roared as 'twere a lion, like a bull bel- lowing to meet the heifer. Thou art a bull, thine enemies are weaklings: thine is the foe- subduing strength of Indra.
5.20.3 Like a bull marked by strength among the cattle, roar seeking kine and gathering up the booty. Pierce through our adversaries' heart with sorrow, and let our routed foes desert their hamlets.
5.20.4 Victorious in the battle, loudly roaring, seizing what may be seized, look all around thee. Utter, O Drum, thy heavenly voice with triumph. Bring, as a priest, our enemies' possessions.
5.20.5 Hearing the Drum's far-reaching voice resounding, let the foe's dame, waked by the roar, afflicted, Grasping her son, run forward in her terror amid the conflict of the deadly weapons.
5.20.6 Thou, first of all, O Drum, thy voice shalt utter: over the ridge of earth speak forth exultant. Crunching with might the army of the foemen, declare thy message pleasantly and clearly.
5.20.7 Loud be thy roar between the earth and heaven. Swift let thy sounds go forth in all directions. Neigh at them, thunder, set in opposition, song-maker, good ally that friends may conquer.
5.20.8 He shall send forth his voice whom art hath fashioned. Make thou the weapons of our warriors bristle. With Indra for ally call out our heroes, and with thy friends scatter and chase the foemen
5.20.9 Resonant, roaring, with thy powerful weapons, warning, and heard by troops in many places, Knowing all rules and winning us advantage, deal fame to many where two kings are fighting.
5.20.10 Bent on advantage, mightier, gaining treasures, victor in war, the spell hath made thee keener. As, in the press, the stone to stalks of Soma, thus, Drum! go dancing to our foes' possessions.
5.20.11 Foe-conqueror, victor, vanquishing opponents, seeker of booty, mastering, destroying. Speak out as a skilled speaker tells his counsel, speak strength to us that we may win the battle.
5.20.12 Shaker of things unshaken, readiest corner to battles; conquer- ing foes, resistless leader, Guarded by Indra, watching our assemblies, go quickly, breaker of their hearts who hate us.
;;; XXI A hymn to the War-drum and various deities for victory
5.21.1 Speak to our enemies, O Drum, discouragement and wild dismay. We bring upon our foemen fear and discord and discomfiture. Drum! drive these enemies away.
5.21.2 When sacrificial butter hath been offered, let our foemen flee. Through consternation, terrified, trembling in mind and eye and heart.
5.21.3 Wrought out of wood, compact with straps of leather, dear to all the clan, Bedewed with sacrificial oil, speak terror to our enemies.
5.21.4 As the wild creatures of the wood flee in their terror from a man, Even so do thou, O Drum, roar out against our foes to frighten them, and then bewilder thou their thoughts.
5.21.5 As, when the wolf approaches, goats and sheep run sorely terrified, Even so do thou, O Drum, roar out against our foes to frighten them, and then bewilder thou their thoughts.
5.21.6 As birds of air, day after day, fly in wild terror from the hawk, as from a roaring lion's voice, Even so do thou, O Drum, roar out against our foes to frighten them, and then bewilder thou their thoughts.
5.21.7 May all the deities whose might controls the fortune of the fray Frighten away our enemies with Drum and skin of antelope.
5.21.8 Let those our enemies who go yonder in their battalions shake. In fear at shadows and the sounds of feet which Indra sporteth with.
5.21.9 To all the quarters of the sky let clang of bowstrings and our Drums. Cry out to hosts of foes that go discomfited in serried ranks.
5.21.10 Aditya, take their sight away! Follow them close, ye motes of light. Let them cleave fast to foot-bound hosts when strength of arm hath past away.
5.21.11 Do ye, O mighty Maruts, sons of Prisni, crush down, with Indra for ally, our foemen. King Soma. Varuna, great God and sovran, Indra too, aye, Death,--
5.21.12 May these embattled Gods, brilliant as Surya--All hail!--one- minded conquer those who hate us.
;;; XXII A charm against fever
5.22.1 Hence, filled with holy strength let Agni, Soma, and Varuna, the Press-stone, and the Altar. And Grass, and glowing Fuel banish Fever. Let hateful things stay at a distance yonder.
5.22.2 And thou thyself who makest all men yellow, consuming them with burning heat like Agni, Thou, Fever! then be weak and ineffective. Pass hence into the realms below or vanish.
5.22.3 Endowed with universal power! send Fever down-ward, far away, The spotty, like red-coloured dust, sprung from a spotty ancestor.
5.22.4 When I have paid obeisance to Fever I send him downward forth. So let Sakambhara's boxer go again to the Mahavrishas.
5.22.5 His mansions are the Mujavans, and the Mahavrishas his home, Thou, Fever, ever since thy birth hast lived among the Bahlikas.
5.22.6 Fever, snake, limbless one, speak out! Keep thyself far away fi om us. Seek thou a wanton Dast girl and strike her with thy thunder- bolt.
5.22.7 Go, Fever, to the Mujavans, or, farther, to the Bahlikas. Seek a lascivious Sara girl and seem to shake her through and through.
5.22.8 Go hence and eat thy kinsmen the Mahavrishas and Mujavans. These or those foreign regions we proclaim to Fever for his home.
5.22.9 In a strange land thou joyest not; subdued, thou wilt be kind to us. Fever is eager to depart, and to the Bahlikas will go,
5.22.10 Since thou now cold, now burning hot, with cough besides, hast made us shake, Terrible, Fever, are thy darts: forbear to injure us with these.
5.22.11 Take none of these to be thy friends, Cough, or Consumption or Decline: Never come thence again to us! O Fever, thus I counsel thee.
5.22.12 Go, Fever, with Consumption, thy brother, and with thy sister, Cough. And with thy nephew Herpes, go away unto that alien folk.
5.22.13 Chase Fever whether cold or hot, brought by the summer or the rains, Tertian, intermittent, or autumnal, or continual.
5.22.14 We to Gandharis, Mujavans, to Angas and to Magadhas. Hand over Fever as it were a servant and a thing of price.
;;; XXIII A charm against parasitic worms
5.23.1 I have called Heaven and Earth to aid, have called divine Sarasvati, Indra and Agni have I called: Let these destroy the worm, I prayed.
5.23.2 O Indra, Lord of Treasures, kill the worms that prey upon this boy. All the malignant spirits have been smitten by my potent spell. We utterly destroy the worm, the worm that creeps around the eyes. The worm that crawls about the nose, the worm that gets bet- ween the teeth.
5.23.3 Two of like colour, two unlike, two coloured black, two coloured red. The tawny and the tawny-eared, Vulture and Wolf, all these are killed.
5.23.4 Worms that are white about the sides, those that are black with black-hued arms, All that show various tints and hues, these worms we utterly destroy.
5.23.5 Eastward the Sun is mounting, seen of all, destroying thing unseen, Crushing and killing all the worms invisible and visible.
5.23.6 Let the Yevashas, Kaskashas, Ejatkas, Sipavitnukas, Let both the worm that we can see, and that we see not, be destroyed.
5.23.7 Slain the Yevasha of the worms, slain too is the Nadaniman. I have reduced them all to dust like vetches with the pounding- stone.
5.23.8 The worm Saranga, white of hue, three-headed, with a triple hump, I split and tear his ribs away, I wrench off every head he has.
5.23.9 I kill you, worms, as Atri, as Kanva and Jamadagni killed. I crush the worms to pieces with a spell that erst Agastya used.
5.23.10 The King of worms hath been destroyed, he who was lord of these is slain. Slain is the worm whose mother, whose brother and sister have been slain.
5.23.11 Destroyed are his dependants, who those dwell around him are destroyed, And all the worms that seem to be the little ones are done to death
5.23.12 Of every worm and insect, of the female and the male alike, I crush the head to pieces with a stone and burn the face with fire.
;;; XXIV A priest's prayer for protection and assistance
5.24.1 Savitar, Lord of furthering aids, protect me, in this my prayer, in this mine act, in this my sacerdotal charge, in this perfor- mance, in this thought, in this my plan and wish, in this my calling on the Gods! All hail!
5.24.2 May Agni, Lord of forest trees, protect, me, in, etc.
5.24.3 May Heaven and Earth, the Queens of bounties, save me.
5.24.4 May Varuna, the Lord of waters, save me.
5.24.5 May Mitra-Varuna, Lords of rain, preserve me.
5.24.6 Lords of the mountains, may the Maruts save me.
5.24.7 May, Soma, Lord of plants and herbs, protect me.
5.24.8 May Vayu, Lord of middle air, protect me.
5.24.9 May Surya, sovran Lord of eyes, protect me.
5.24.10 May the Moon, Lord of constellations, save me.
5.24.11 May Indra who is Lord of heaven protect me.
5.24.12 The Maruts' father, Lord of cattle, save me.
5.24.13 May Mrityu, Lord of living creatures, save me.
5.24.14 May Yama, Regent of the Fathers, save me.
5.24.15 May the Forefathers of old time protect me.
5.24.16 May Fathers of succeeding ages save me.
5.24.17 Next may the Fathers of our fathers save me, in this my prayer,. in this mine act, in this my sacerdotal charge, in this perfor- mance, in this thought, in this my plan and wish, in this my calling on the Gods! All hail!
;;; XXV A charm to facilitate conception
5.25.1 Let the man, sower of the germ, lay, as a feather on a shaft. Limb drawn from limb, whate'er is culled from cloud and from the womb of heaven.
5.25.2 Even as this broad earth received the germ of all the things that be, Thus within thee I lay the germ. I call thee, Earth, to strengthen it.
5.25.3 O Sinivali, set the germ, set thou the germ, Sarasvati! In thee let both the Asvins, crowned with lotuses, bestow the germ.
5.25.4 Let Mitra-Varuna and God Brihaspati lay the germ in thee. Indra and Agni lay the germ, Dhatar bestow the germ in thee.
5.25.5 Let Vishnu form and mould the womb, let Tvashtar duly shape the forms, Prajapati infuse the stream, and Dhatar lay for thee the germ.
5.25.6 Drink thou the procreative draught well-known to Varuna the King, Known to divine Sarasvati, and Indra slayer of the foe.
5.25.7 Thou art the germ of plants and herbs, thou art the germ of forest trees, The germ of each existing thing, so here, O Agni, lay the germ.
5.25.8 Rise up, put forth thy manly strength, and lay thy germ within the womb. A bull art thou with vigorous strength: for progeny we bring thee near.
5.25.9 Prepare thee, Barhatsama, let the germ be laid within thy side. The Soma-drinking Gods have given a son to thee, thy son and mine.
5.25.10 O Dhatar, thou Disposer, lay within the body of this dame. A male germ with the noblest form, for her, in the tenth month, to bear.
5.25.11 Tvashtar, celestial artist, lay within the body of this dame. A male germ with the noblest form for her in the tenth month to bear.
5.25.12 Savitar, vivifier, lay within the body of this dame A male germ with the noblest form for her in the tenth month to bear.
5.25.13 O Lord of Life, Prajapati, within this woman's body lay A male germ with the noblest form for her in the tenth month to bear.
;;; XXVI A hymn of invitation to the gods
5.26.1 In sacrifice for you may sapient Agni--All hail!--use Yajus texts and fuel.
5.26.2 May Savitar the God--All hail!--foreknowing, chief in this sacrifice, employ them.
5.26.3 In this great rite--All hail!--may sapient Indra use lauds, rejoicings, well-yoked coursers.
5.26.4 Bring Praishas in the rite--All hail!--and Nivids, learned, con- nected, with the Consorts.
5.26.5 As a dame brings her son--All hail! O Maruts, connected, in the rite bring measures.
5.26.6 Here Aditi is come--All hail!--preparing the rite with grass and lustral waters.
5.26.7 Let Vishnu in this rite in varied manner--All hail! use well- yoked steeds, his fervours.
5.26.8 Let Tvashtar in this rite in varied manner--All hail!--use forms, his well-yoked coursers.
5.26.9 Let Bhaga in this rite use prayers, foreknowing--All hail! for this use well-yoked coursers.
5.26.10 Let Soma in this rite in varied manner--All hail!--use milk- streams, well-yoked coursers.
5.26.11 Let Indra in this rite in varied manner--All hail!--use powers,. his well-yoked coursers.
5.26.12 Hitherward come ye with the prayer, O Asvins, exalting sacrifice with cry of Vashat! Brihaspati!--All hail!--with prayer come hither. Here is the rite, here heaven for him who worships.
;;; XXVII An Apri or Propitiatory hymn
5.27.1 Uplifted be this sacrificer's fuel: lofty and brilliant be the flames of Agni! Splendidly bright, fair-faced, with all his offspring, Tanunapat the Asura, many-handed.
5.27.2 God among Gods, the God bedews the paths with fatness and' with mead.
5.27.3 With store of mead to sacrifice comes Agni, comes Narasansa Agni, friendly-minded, comes Savitar, righteous God who brings all blessings.
5.27.4 Hither he comes with power and fatness also, the luminous,. implored with adoration.
5.27.5 At holy rites and offerings Agni loveth the scoops: let this man worship Agni's greatness.
5.27.6 He is the furtherer at glad oblations: there stood the Vasus and the treasure-givers.
5.27.7 Ever the Doors divine, and all protect this worshipper's holy work.
5.27.8 Far-reaching, ruling by the Law of Agni, May Dawn and Night, the holy, speeding near us, aid this our sacrificial ceremony.
5.27.9 Celestial Hotars, with the tongues of Agni praise and extol our lofty ceremony, so that our sacrifice be well conducted!
5.27.10 Three Goddesses upon this grass, be seated, Ida, Sarasvati, Mahi, and Bharati adored with praise.
5.27.11 This our nutritious genial flow, God Tvashtar! and growth of wealth, pour down on this man's kindred.
5.27.12 Vanaspati, rejoicing, of thyself send God-ward! Let Agni, Im- molator, sweeten our libation.
5.27.13 Pay sacrifice to Indra, Jatavedas Agni, with Hail! Let all the Gods accept the gifts we offer.
;;; XXVIII A charm to ensure general protection and prosperity
5.28.1 For lengthened life, to last through hundred autumns, they equalize with nine the nine aspirations. Three in gold, three in silver, three in iron by heat are stablished in their several places.
5.28.2 May Agni, Sun, and Moon, and Earth, and Waters, Sky, Air, the Quarters and the Points between them, And Parts of Years accordant with the Seasons by this three- threaded Amulet preserve me.
5.28.3 In three-threaded Charm rest triple fulness! Let Pushan cover it with milk and butter. Here rest abundant store of food and people, may ample store of cattle rest within it.
5.28.4 Enrich this charm, Adityas, with your treasure; magnify this, when magnified, O Agni. Endow it with heroic strength, O Indra: therein be lodged a triple power of increase.
5.28.5 With gold let Earth protect thee, and with iron, accordant, all- sustaining Agni save thee! And in accordance with the plants may silver, regarding thee with favour, grant thee vigour.
5.28.6 This gold, born threefold at its first production, grew the one thing that Agni loved most dearly: it fell away, one part of injured Soma. One part they call seed of the sapient Waters. This gold bring thee long life when triply threaded!
5.28.7 Three lives of Jamadagni, thrice the vital force of Kasyapa, Three sights of immortality, three lives have I prepared for thee.
5.28.8 When with the three-stringed charm came three strong eagles, sharing the Sacred Syllable and mighty, With immortality they drove off Mrityu, obscuring and conceal- ing all distresses.
5.28.9 The golden guard thee from the sky, the silvern guard thee from the air, The iron guard thee from the earth! This man hath reached the forts of Gods.
5.28.10 May these three castles of the Gods keep thee secure on every side. Endowed with strength, possessing these, be thou the master of thy foes,
5.28.11 The God who first bound on in the beginning the deities' im- mortal golden castle,-- Him I salute with ten extended fingers. Blest be the three- stringed charm I bind upon thee.
5.28.12 Aryaman be thy binder-on, and Pushan and Brihaspati: Whatever name the brood of day possess, therewith we fasten thee.
5.28.13 With Seasons and with Lengths of Time, for vigour and exten- ded life, With all the splendour of the Sun we fasten thee about the neck.
5.28.14 Drawn forth from butter and with meath besprinkled, firm as the earth, unshakable, triumphant. Breaking down foes and casting them beneath me, be fastened on me for exalted fortune!
;;; XXIX A charm for the destruction of malignant goblins
5.29.1 Made ready in the east drive forth, take notice of what is hap- pening here, omniscient Agni! Thou bringest medicine and healest sickness: through thee may we win horses, kine, and people.
5.29.2 Accordant with all Gods, O Jatavedas Agni, perform this work as we beseech thee, That this defence of his may fall, whoever hath caused us pain, whoever hath consumed us.
5.29.3 Unanimous, with all the Gods together, so do this thing O Agni Jatavedas, that this defence of his may fall and fail him.
5.29.4 Pierce both his eyes, pierce thou the heart within him, crush thou his teeth and cleave his tongue asunder. Rend thou, most youthful Agni, that Pisacha whoso amid them all of this hath eaten.
5.29.5 Whatever of his body hath been taken, plundered, borne off, or eaten by Pisachas, This, Agni, knowing it, again bring hither! We give back flesh and spirit to his body.
5.29.6 If some Pisacha in my food raw, ready, thoroughly cooked, or, spotty, hath deceived me, Let the Pisachas with their lives and offspring atone for this, and let this man be healthy.
5.29.7 If one hath cheated me in milk or porridge, in food from grain or plants that need no culture. Let the Pisachas, etc.
5.29.8 If one, flesh eater, in a draught of water have wronged me lying in the bed of goblins, Let the Pisachas, etc.
5.29.9 If one, flesh-eater, in the day or night-time have wronged me lying in the bed of goblins, Let the Pisachas, etc.
5.29.10 O Agni Jatavedas, slay the bloody Pisacha, flesh-devourer, mind- destroyer, Strong Indra strike him with his bolt of thunder, courageous Soma cut his head to pieces!
5.29.11 Thou, Agni, ever slayest Yatudhanas, the fiends have never con- quered thee in battles. Consume thou from the root the flesh-devourers, let none of them escape thy heavenly weapon
5.29.12 Collect, O Jatavedas, what hath been removed and borne away. Let this man's members grow, let him swell like the tendril of a plant.
5.29.13 Like as the Soma's tendril, thus, O Jatavedas let him swell, Let him live, Agni I Make him fat, free from consumption, full of sap.
5.29.14 Here, Agni, is the fuel, here are logs that crush Pisachas down. O Jatavedas, willingly accept them and be pleased therewith.
5.29.15 Accept, O Agni, with thy flame the billets of Tarshtagha wood. Let the flesh-eater who would take the flesh of this man lose his form.
;;; XXX A charm to restore life and health
5.30.1 From thy vicinity I call, from near, from far, from night at hand. Stay here: depart not: follow not the Fathers of the olden time. I bind thy vital spirit fast.
5.30.2 If any man, a stranger or akin, hath cast a spell on thee, I with my voice to thee declare thy freedom and release there- from.
5.30.3 If in thy folly thou hast lied or cursed a woman or a man, I with my voice declare to thee thy freedom and release there- from.
5.30.4 If thou art lying there because of mother's or of father's sin, I with my voice declare to thee thy freedom and release there- from.
5.30.5 Accept the healing medicine, the balm thy mother and thy sire, Thy sister and thy brother bring. I make thee live through lengthened years.
5.30.6 O man, stay here among us; stay with all thy spirit: follow not Yama's two messengers. Approach the castles where the living dwell.
5.30.7 Come back as thou art called to come, knowing the outlet of the path, And the Approach and its ascent, the way of every living man.
5.30.8 Be not alarmed: thou wilt not die. I give thee lengthened years of life. Forth from thy members have I charmed Decline that caused the fever there.
5.30.9 Gone is the pain that racked thee, gone thy fever, gone thy heart's disease. Consumption, conquered by my voice, hath, like a hawk, fled far away.
5.30.10 Two sages, Sense and Vigilance, the sleepless and the watchful one, These, the protectors of thy life, shall be awake both day and night.
5.30.11 This Agni must be waited on. Here let the Sun mount up for thee. Rise from deep death and come away, yea, from black darkness rise thou up!
5.30.12 Homage be paid to Yama, to Mrityu, and to the Fathers, and to those who guide us! I honour first, for this man's preservation, that Agni who well knoweth how to save him.
5.30.13 Let breath and mind return to him, let sight and vigour come again Let all his body be restored and firmly stand upon its feet.
5.30.14 Provide this man with breath and sight, O Agni, and with his body and his strength unite him. Thou knowest Amrit: let him not go hence, nor dwell in house of clay.
5.30.15 Let not thine inward breathing fail, let not thine outward breath be lost. Let Surya who is Lord Supreme raise thee from death with beams of light.
5.30.16 Tied, tremulously moving, here the tongue is speaking in the mouth. With thee I charmed Decline away and Fever's hundred ago- nies.
5.30.17 This living world, unconquered of the Gods, is most beloved of all. To whatsoever death thou wast destined when thou wast born,. O man, This death and we call after thee. Die not before decrepit age!
;;; XXXI A counter-charm against the incantations of an enemy
5.31.1 The spell that they have cast for thee on unbaked dish or ming- led meal, The witchcraft wrought on undressed meat, this I strike back again on them.
5.31.2 The spell that they have cast for thee on jungle-cock, goat, horned ram, The witchcraft wrought upon thy ewe, this I strike back again on them.
5.31.3 The spell that they have cast upon thy beast that hath uncloven hooves, The ass with teeth in both his jaws, this I strike back again on them.
5.31.4 The secret spell upon thy plants Amula or Narachi, spell That they have cast upon thy field, this I strike back again on them.
5.31.5 The spell that wicked men have cast on thine original household- fire, And on thy sacrificial hall, this I strike back again on them.
5.31.6 The spell that they have cast upon thy public room thy gambl- ing-board, Spell they have cast upon thy dice, this I strike back again on them.
5.31.7 The spell that they have cast upon thine army or thy shafts and arms, Spell they have cast upon the drum, this I throw back again on them.
5.31.8 Charm they have laid within thy well or buried in the burning- ground, Charm they have laid within thy home, this I throw back again on them.
5.31.9 The spell that they have wrought for thee in flickering fire of human bones,-- Mroka, consuming, cannibal, this I throw back again on them.
5.31.10 He brought this by no proper path, by the right path we drive it back. The fool in folly brought it to those who observe established bounds.
5.31.11 No power had he who wrought the spell: he hurt his foot, he broke his toe. Unlucky for his wealthy lords, he hath wrought happiness for us.
5.31.12 May Indra slay with mighty bolt, may Agni with his missible pierce. The sorcerer who brings the curse, who deals with roots and secret spells.
;;; I In praise of Savitar
6.1.1 Sing, Atharvana, at eve, sing loudly, bring a splendid present: hymn God Savitar with praises.
6.1.2 Yea, praise him whose home is in the river, Son of Truth, the youthful, gracious friend whose word is guileless.
6.1.3 Savitar our God shall send us many everlasting treasures, that both paths may well be travelled.
;;; II In praise of Indra
6.2.1 For Indra, ministering priests! run ye and press the Soma juice, That he may hear his praiser's word, and this my call.
6.2.2 Thou into whom the drops find way as sap pours life into a tree, Drive off in thine abundant might our demon foes.
6.2.3 For Indra, thunder-armed, who drinks the Soma press the Soma out: He, youthful, conqueror, and Lord is praised by all.
;;; III A prayer to various deities for protection and prosperity
6.3.1 Guard us the Maruts! Guard us well, O Indra, Piishan, Aditi. Guard us, O Waters' Child, and Rivers Seven. May Vishnu guard us, and the Sky.
6.3.2 May Heaven and Earth take care of us for victory, may Pressing- Stone and Soma save us from distress. Sarasvati, auspicious Goddess, guard us well: preserve us Agni and his kind protecting powers.
6.3.3 Preserve us both the Asvins, Gods and Lords of Light, and let the Dawns and Night bring us deliverance. The Waters' Child protect our house from every harm. Do thou, God Tvashtar, make us strong for health and wealth.
;;; IV A hymn to various deities for protection
6.4.1 May Tvashtar, Brahmanaspati, Parjanya hear my holy prayer. May Aditi with all her sons, the brothers, guard us, invincible, protecting power.
6.4.2 May Ansa, Bhaga, Varuna, and Mitra, Aryaman, Aditi, and Maruts guard us. May we be freed from that oppressor's hatred. May he keep off that foeman who is near us.
6.4.3 May both the Asvins further our devotion. With ceaseless care deliver us, Wide-Ranger! O Father Heaven, keep from us all misfortunes.
;;; V A prayer to Agni and Indra for the well being of a princely patron
6.5.1 Agni, adored with sacred oil, lift up this man to high estate. Endow him with full store of strength and make him rich in progeny.
6.5.2 Advance him, Indra! Let him be ruler of all akin to him. Grant him sufficiency of wealth: guide him to life and length of days.
6.5.3 Prosper this man, O Agni, in whose house we offer sacrifice. May Soma bless him, and the God here present, Brahmanaspati.
;;; VI A prayer to Brahmanaspati for protection from wicked men
6.6.1 The godless man whoever plots against us, Brahmanaspati, Thou shalt give up as prey to me the worshipper who pour the juice.
6.6.2 If, Soma, any spiteful man hath aimed at us whose thoughts are kind, Smite with thy bolt upon his face: he, crushed to pieces, vani- sheth.
6.6.3 Soma, whoever troubleth us, be he a stranger or akin, Deprive him of the strength he hath: slay him thy-self like mighty Dyaus!
;;; VI A prayer to Aditi for help and protection
7.6.1 Aditi is sky, and air's mid-region, Aditi is the father, son, and mother, Aditi all the Gods and the Five Nations, Aditi what is now and what is future.
7.6.2 We call for help the Queen of Law and Order, great mother of all those whose ways are righteous, Far-spread, unwasting strong in her dominion, Aditi wisely lead- ing, well protecting.
7.6.3 Sinless may we ascend, for weal, the vessel, rowed with good oars, divine, that never leaketh, Earth, our strong guard, incomparable Heaven, Aditi wisely lead- ing, well protecting.
7.6.4 Let us bring hither, in pursuit of riches, Aditi with our word, the mighty mother, Her in whose lap the spacious air is lying: may she afford us triply-guarding shelter!
;;; VIII A man's love-charm
6.8.1 Like as the creeper throws, her arms on every side around the tree, So hold thou me in thine embrace that thou mayst be in love with me, my darling, never to depart.
6.8.2 As, when he mounts, the eagle strikes his pinions downward on the earth, So do I strike thy spirit down that thou mayst be in love with me, my darling, never to depart.
6.8.3 As in his rapid course the Sun encompasses the heaven and: earth, So do I compass round thy mind that thou mayst be in love with. me, my darling, never to depart.
;;; IX A man's love-charm
6.9.1 Desire my body, love my feet, love thou mine eyes, and love my legs. Let both thine eyes and hair, fond girl! be dried and parched. through love of me.
6.9.2 I make thee hang upon mine arm, I make thee lie upon my heart. Thou yieldest to my wish, that thou mayst be submissive to my will.
6.9.3 May they whose kisses are a bond, a love-charm laid within the heart, Mothers of butter, may the cows incline that maid to love of me.
;;; X A thanksgiving for life, hearing, and sight
6.10.1 All hail for hearing to the Earth, to Trees, to Agni, sovran Lord!
6.10.2 All hail for breath to Air, for power to life to Vayu, sovran Lord!
6.10.3 All hail for vision to the Stars, to Heaven, to Surya, sovran Lord!
;;; XI An epithalamian charm to ensure the birth of a boy
6.11.1 Asvattha on the Sami-tree. There a male birth is certified. There is the finding of a son: this bring we to the women-folk.
6.11.2 The father sows the genial seed, the woman tends and fosters it. This is the finding of a son: thus hath Prajapati declared.
6.11.3 Prajapati, Anumati, Sinivali have ordered it. Elsewhere may he effect the birth of maids, but here prepare a boy.
;;; XII A charm against venomous serpents
6.12.1 I, As the Sun goes round the heaven, have travelled round the Serpents' race. I ward thy poison off, as Night parts all else living from the Sun.
6.12.2 With this, discovered in the days of old by Brahmans, Rishis, Gods, With this I ward thy poison off, thou Biter! formed and form- ing now.
6.12.3 With mead I mingle flowing streams: the hills and mountains shall be mead. Parushni and Sipala mead. May it be well with mouth and heart.
;;; XIII Homage to death
6.13.1 Worship to weapons of the Gods! worship to weapons of the Kings! Then worship to the people's arms! worship, O Death, be paid to thee!
6.13.2 Let worship be to thy defence and to thine accusation paid. Death! be this worship paid to thy good-will and thy malevo- lence!
6.13.3 Worship to thy physicians, to thy sorcerers be worship paid! Death! let this reverence be done unto thy Brahmans and thy roots.
;;; XIV A charm against consumption
6.14.1 Remove thou all Decline that lurks within the members and the joints, The firmly-settled heart-disease that racks the bones and rends the limbs.
6.14.2 From the consumptive man I pluck Decline as 'twere a severed part. I cut the bond that fetters him, even as a root of cucumber.
6.14.3 Begone, Consumption, hence away, like a young foal that runs. at speed. Then, not pernicious to our men, flee, yearly visitant like grass!
;;; XV A charm for power and preeminence
6.15.1 Most excellent of all the plants art thou: thy vassals are the trees. Let him be subject to our power, the man who seeks to injure us.
6.15.2 Whoever seeks to injure us, with kinsmen or no kin to aid, May I be uppermost of all, even as this Plant is queen of trees.
6.15.3 As Soma hath been made the best of all oblations 'mid the plants, So, as Talasa is the queen of trees, may I be chief of all.
;;; XVI A medical charm
6.16.1 O Abayu, non-Abayu, dire is thy juice, O Abayu; we eat the gruel made of thee.
6.16.2 Vihalha is thy father's name, thy mother's is Madavati. Yea, verily thou art not he, thou who hast well protected life.
6.16.3 Go thou to rest, Tauvilika! This noisy cry hath sunk to rest. Go hence, depart, Nirala, thou! the tawny and the tawny- eared.
;;; XVII A charm to ensure conception
6.17.1 Even as this mighty Earth conceived the germ of all the things that be, So may the germ of life be laid in thee that thou mayst bear a son.
6.17.2 Even as this mighty Earth hath borne and bears the stately forest trees, So may the germ of life be borne in thee that thou mayst bear a son.
6.17.3 Even as this mighty Earth hath borne and bears the mountains and the hills, So may the germ of life be borne in thee that thou mayst bear a son.
6.17.4 Even as this mighty Earth supports the moving world that dwells thereon, So may the germ of life be borne in thee that thou mayst bear a son.
;;; XVIII A charm to banish jealousy
6.18.1 The first approach of Jealousy, and that which followeth the first, The pain, the fire that burns within thy heart we quench and drive away.
6.18.2 Even as the earth is dead to sense, yea, more unconscious than the dead, Even as a corpse's spirit is the spirit of the jealous man.
6.18.3 The thought that harbours in thy heart, the fluttering doubt that dwells therein. Yea, all thy jealousy, like heat born of the dance, I banish thence.
;;; XIX A prayer for purification
6.19.1 Let the Gods purify me, let men purify me with a prayer. Cleanse me all creatures that exist! may Pavamana make me pure.
6.19.2 May Pavamana make me pure for wisdom and for power and life, and unassailed security.
6.19.3 God Savitar, byboth of these, filter and pressing out this juice, purify us that we may see.
;;; XX A charm against fever
6.20.1 He goes away as 'twere from this fierce burning fire, inebriated and lamenting he departs. Let him, the lawless, seek another and not us. Worship be paid to Fever armed with fiery heat.
6.20.2 To Rudra and to Fever be our worship paid: worship be paid to Varuna the splendid King! Worship to Dyaus, to Earth, worship be paid to Plants!
6.20.3 Thou who, aglow with heat, makest all bodies green, to thee, red, brown, I bow, the Fever of the wood.
;;; XXI A charm to strengthen hair and promote its growth
6.21.1 Of all the three terrestrial realms the ground is verily the best. I from the skin that covers these gather a healing medicine.
6.21.2 Thou art the best of medicines, most excellent of Plants art thou, As Soma 'mid the wandering stars, as Varuna among the Gods.
6.21.3 Endowed with wealth, denying not, give freely fain to give your gifts! Ye stay the hair from falling off: ye strengthen and increase its growth.
;;; XXII To the Maruts or Storm-Gods
6.22.1 Dark the descent; the strong-winged birds are golden: they fly aloft to heaven, enrobed in waters. They have come hither from the seat of Order, and inundated earth with streams of fatness.
6.22.2 Ye make floods rich in milk, make plants propitious, what time ye stir, O golden-breasted Maruts! Pour down your showers of vigorous strength and favour there where ye sprinkle mead, O Maruts, heroes!
6.22.3 O Maruts, send ye down, streaming with water rain which, may, filling all the sloping valleys, Leap like a bold girl in a man's embraces, or like a matron tumbled by her husband.
;;; XXIII To the Waters
6.23.1 Here flow the restless ones, they flow unceasing through the day and night, Most excellently wise I call the Goddess Waters hitherward.
6.23.2 Let the deft Waters, summoned, give permission that we bear them off, And quickly set us on our way.
6.23.3 Let all the people celebrate the rite of Savitar the God. Sweet unto us be Waters, Plants propitious!
;;; XXIV To the Rivers
6.24.1 Forth from the Hills of Snow they stream, and meet in Sindhu here or there. To me the sacred Waters gave the balm that heals the heart's disease.
6.24.2 Whatever rupture I have had that injured eyes or heels or toes. All this the Waters, skilfullest physicians, shall make well again,
6.24.3 All Rivers who have Sindhu for your Lady, Sindhu for your Queen, Give us the balm that heals this ill: this boon let us enjoy from you.
;;; XXV A charm to remove pustules or scrofulous swellings (apachitas)
6.25.1 May all the five-and-fifty which meet round the tendons of the neck. Depart and vanish hence away like plaguing insects buzz and hum!
6.25.2 Those seventy-and-seven which meet round the upper vertebrae, Let them all vanish hence away like plaguing insects' buzz and hum!
6.25.3 Those nine-and-ninety which, combined, attack the shoulder round about, Let them all vanish hence away like plaguing insects' buzz and hum!
;;; XXVI To Affliction
6.26.1 Let me go free, O Misery: do thou, the mighty, pity us. Set me uninjured in the world of happiness, O Misery.
6.26.2 From thee, from thee who fliest not from us, O Misery, we fly. Then at the turning of the paths let Misery fall on someone else.
6.26.3 May the immortal, thousand eyed, dwell otherwhere apart from us. Let him afflict the man we hate: smite only him who is our foe.
;;; XXVII A charm to avert misfortune foreshown by the coming of a dove
6.27.1 Gods! whatsoe'er the Dove came hither seeking, sent to us as the envoy of Destruction, For that let us sing hymns and make atonement, Well be it with our quadrupeds and bipeds!
6.27.2 Auspicious be the Dove that hath been sent us, a harmless bird, O Gods, that seeks our dwelling! May Agni, Sage, be pleased with our oblation, and may the missile borne on wings avoid us.
6.27.3 Let not the arrow that hath wings distract us. Beside the fire- place, on the hearth it settles. May it bring welfare to our men and cattle: here let the Dove, ye Gods, forbear to harm us.
;;; XXVIII A charm to avert misfortune foreshown by the coming of a dove
6.28.1 Drive forth the Dove, chase it with holy verses: rejoicing bring we hither food and cattle, Obliterating traces of misfortune. Most fleet may it fly forth and leave us vigour.
6.28.2 These men have strengthened Agni's might, these men have brought the kine to us. They have sung glory to the Gods. Who is the man that con- quers them?
6.28.3 Be reverence paid to him who, while exploring the path for many, first approached the river, Lord of this world of quadrupeds and bipeds; to him be rever- ence paid, to Death, to Yama!
;;; XXIX A charm to avert misfortune foreshown by the coming of a dove and an owl
6.29.1 On these men yonder fall the winged missile: the screeching of the Owl is ineffective, And that the Dove beside the fire hath settled.
6.29.2 Thine envoys who came hither, O Destruction, sent or not sent by thee unto our dwelling, The Dove and Owl, effectless be their visit!
6.29.3 Oft may it fly to us to save our heroes from slaughter, oft perch here to bring fair offspring, Turn thee and send thy voice afar: cry to the region far away; That I may see thee in the home of Yama reft of all thy power, that I may see thee impotent.
;;; XXX A charm to promote the growth of hair
6.30.1 Over a magic stone, beside Sarasvati, the Gods Ploughed in this barley that was blent with mead. Lord of the plough was Indra, strong with hundred powers: the ploughers were the Maruts they who give rich gifts.
6.30.2 Thy joy in hair that falleth or is scattered, wherewith thou sub- jectest a man to laughter To other trees, far from thee will I drive it. Grow up, thou Sami, with a hundred branches.
6.30.3 Auspicious, bearing mighty leaves, holy one, nurtured by the rain, Even as a mother to her sons, be gracious, Sami to our hair.
;;; XXXI To Surya the Sun-God
6.31.1 This spotted Bull hath come and sat before his mother in the east. Advancing to his father Heaven.
6.31.2 As expiration from his breath his radiance penetrates within. The Bull shines out through all the sky.
6.31.3 He rules supreme through thirty realms--One winged with song hath made him mount Throughout the days at break of morn.
;;; XXXII A charm against fiends and goblins
6.32.1 With butter, in his hall v4here fire is burning, perform that sacri- fice which quells the goblins. Burn from afar against the demons Agni! Afflict not in thy fury us who praise thee.
6.32.2 Let Rudra break your necks, O ye Pisachas, and split your ribs asunder, Yatudhanas! Your herb of universal power with Yama hath allied itself.
6.32.3 Here, Mitra-Varuna! may we dwell safely: with splendour drive the greedy demons backward, Let them not find a surety or a refuge, but torn away go down to Death together.
;;; XXXIII A prayer to Indra for riches
6.33.1 He who controls this air and men who aid his strength, and wood, and heaven, the lofty seat which Indra loves.
6.33.2 The bold whose overpowering might the boldest never hath defied,-- As erst still, unassailable is Indra's wrath, and fame, and force.
6.33.3 May he bestow on us that wealth, far-spreading, bright with yellow hue. Indra is mightiest Lord among the folk.
;;; XXXIV To Agni for protection from enemies
6.34.1 Send forth thy voice to Agni, to the manly hero of our homes, So may he bear us past our foes.
6.34.2 That Agni who with sharpened flame of fire consumes the Rakshasas, So may he bear us past our foes.
6.34.3 He who from distance far remote shineth across the tracts of land, May he transport us past our foes.
6.34.4 He who beholds all creatures, who observes them with a careful eye, May he transport us past our foes.
6.34.5 That brilliant Agni who was born beyond this region of the air, May he transport us past our foes!
;;; XXXV To Agni Vaisvanara
6.35.1 Forth from the distance far away Vaisvanara come to succour us! Agni approach our eulogies!
6.35.2 Vaisvanara with friendly thoughts hath come to this our sacrifice, Agni who saves from woe, to lauds.
6.35.3 Vaisvanara hath formed the hymn and laud of the Angirases. To these may he bring glorious right.
;;; XXXVI In praise of Agni Vaisvanara
6.36.1 Holy Vaisvanara we seek, the Lord of light and endless life, the burning One who fadeth not.
6.36.2 He hath directed all things; he sends forth the Seasons in his might, furthering sacrifice's power.
6.36.3 Agni Kama in other homes shines forth the sole imperial Lord of all that is and is to be.
;;; XXXVII A charm to divert Imprecation personified
6.37.1 Hitherward, having yoked his steeds, came Imprecation, thousand-eyed, Seeking my curser, as a wolf the home of one who owneth sheep.
6.37.2 Avoid us, Imprecation! as consuming fire avoids the lake. Smite thou the man who curses us, as the sky's lightning strikes the tree.
6.37.3 Who curses us, himself uncursed, or, cursed, who curses us again, Him cast I as a sop to Death, as to a dog one throws a bone.
;;; XXXVIII A prayer for surpassing strength and energy
6.38.1 What energy the lion hath, the tiger, adder, and burning fire, Brahman, or Surya, And the blest Goddess who gave birth to Indra, come unto us conjoined with strength and vigour!
6.38.2 All energy of elephant and panther, all energy of gold, men, kine, and waters, And the blest Goddess who gave birth to Indra come unto us conjoined with strength and vigour.
6.38.3 Might in car, axles, in the strong bull's courage, in Varuna's breath, in Vata, in Parjanya, In Warrior, in the war-drum stretched for battle, in the man's roar and in the horse's mettle, May the blest Goddess who gave birth to Indra come unto us conjoined with strength and vigour.
;;; XXXIX A priest's prayer for power and glory
6.39.1 Let sacrifice, like fame, thrive sped by Indra, inspired, well- ordered, with a thousand powers. To highest rank raise me who bring oblation, me who move forth to far-extended vision.
6.39.2 We will pay sacrifice and serve with worship our glorious Indra, famous for his glories. Give thou us sway which Indra hath promoted, and in this boon of thine may we be famous.
6.39.3 Indra was glorious at his birth; Agni, Soma were born renowned. And glorious am I, the most illustrious of all that is.
;;; XL A prayer for peace and security
6.40.1 Here may we dwell, O Heaven and Earth, in safety. May Savitar and Soma send us safety. Our safety be the wide air: ours be safety through the oblation of the Seven Rishis.
6.40.2 May the Four Quarters give this hamlet power: Savitar favour us and make us happy! May Indra make us free from foes and danger: may wrath of Kings be turned to other places.
6.40.3 Make thou us free from enemies both from below and from above. O Indra, give us perfect peace, peace from behind and from be- fore.
;;; XLI A prayer for protection, long life, and various blessings
6.41.1 For mind, for intellect, for thought, for purpose, for intelligence,. For sense, for hearing, and for sight, let us adore with sacrifice.
6.41.2 For expiration, vital air, and breath that amply nourishes, Let us with sacrifice adore Sarasvati whose reach is wide.
6.41.3 Let not the Rishis, the divine, forsake us, our own, our very selves, our lives' protectors. Do ye, immortal, still attend us mortals, and give us vital power to live the longer.
;;; XLII A charm to reconcile estranged friends
6.42.1 I loose the anger from thy heart as 'twere the bowstring from a bow, That we, one-minded now, may walk together as familiar friends.
6.42.2 Together let us walk as friends: thy wrathful feeling I remove. Beneath a heavy stone we cast thy wrath away and bury it.
6.42.3 I trample on thine anger thus, I tread it down with heel and toe: So dost thou yield thee to my will, to speak no more rebelliously.
;;; XLIII The same
6.43.1 For stranger and for friend alike this Darbha-grass removeth wrath. Soother of Anger is it called because it calms the angry man.
6.43.2 This Plant that hath abundant roots spreads to the place where waters meet. Soother of anger is the name Darbha-grass that springs from earth.
6.43.3 We draw thine obstinacy forth, set in thy mouth and in thy jaw: So dost thou yield thee to my will. to speak no more rebelli- ously.
;;; XLIV A charm to remove disease
6.44.1 Firm stood the heaven, firm stood the earth, firm stood this universal world. Firm stood the trees that sleep erect: let this thy malady be still.
6.44.2 Of all thy hundred remedies, a thousand remedies combined. This is the surest cure for flux, most excellent to heal disease.
6.44.3 Thou art the stream that Rudra pours, the closest kin of Amrita. Thy name is called Vishanaka: thou sprangest from the Fathers' root, removing illness caused by wind.
;;; XLV A prayer for preservation from mental sin and evil promptings
6.45.1 Sin of the Mind, avaunt! begone! Why sayest thou what none should say? Go hence away, I love thee not. Go to the forests and the trees. My heart is in our homes and cows.
6.45.2 Whatever wrong we have committed, sleeping or waking, by ill-wish, dislike, or slander, All these offences, which deserve displeasure, may Agni take from us and keep them distant.
6.45.3 Indra and Brahmanaspati! whatever foolish deed we plan, May provident Angirasa preserve us from the sin and woe.
;;; XLVI A charm against evil dreams
6.46.1 Thou, neither quick nor dead, O Sleep, art fraught with Amrit of the Gods. Thy name is Araru: thy sire is Yama; Varunani bare thee.
6.46.2 We know thy birth, O Sleep, thou art son of the sisters of the Gods; the minister of Yama thou, thou art Antaka, thou art Death. So well we know thee who thou art. Sleep, guard us from the evil dream.
6.46.3 As men discharge a debt, as they pay up an eighth and half-an- eighth, So the whole evil dream do we pay and assign unto our foe.
;;; XLVII To accompany the three daily libations
6.47.1 Dear to all men, all-prosperer, all-creating, may Agni, guard us* at the morn's libation. May he, the brightly pure one, give us riches: may we have life enjoying food together.
6.47.2 At this our second offering may Indra, Maruts, and Visve Devas never fail us. Still may the favour of the Gods be with us, blest with long life and speaking words that please them.
6.47.3 We pour this third libation of the Sages who fashioned forth the cup in proper order. Winners of heaven, may they, Sudhanvan's children, lead our fair sacrifice to happy fortune.
;;; XLVIII Formulas to be used at the three daily libations
6.48.1 Thou art the Hawk, Gayatri's lord: I hold thee fast. Happily bear me to the goal of this my sacrifice. All hail!
6.48.2 Thou art the Ribhu, lord of Jagati: I hold thee fast. Happily bear me to the goal of this my sacrifice. Al I hail!
6.48.3 Thou art the Bull, the Trishtup's lord: I hold thee fast. Happily bear me to the goal of this my sacrifice. All hail!
;;; XLIX In praise of Agni
6.49.1 O Agni, in thy body man hath never found a wounded part. The Ape devours the arrow's shaft as a cow eats her after- birth.
6.49.2 Thou like a fleece contractest and expandest thee what time the upper stone and that below devour. Closely compressing head with head and breast with breast he crunches up the tendrils with his yellow jaws.
6.49.3 The Eagles have sent forth their voice aloud to heaven: in the sky's vault the dark impetuous ones have danced. When they come downward to repair the lower stone, they, dwellers with the Sun, have gained abundant seed.
;;; L A charm for the destruction of vermin
6.50.1 Destroy the rat, the mole, the boring beetle, cut off their heads and crush their ribs, O Asvins. Bind fast their mouths; let them not eat our barley: so guard, ye twain, our growing corn from danger.
6.50.2 Ho! boring beetle, ho! thou worm, ho! noxious grub and grasshopper! As a priest leaves the unfinished sacrifice, go hence devouring not, injuring not this corn.
6.50.3 Hearken to me, lord of the female borer, lord of the female grub! ye rough-toothed vermin! Whate'er ye be, dwelling in woods, and piercing, we crush and mangle all those piercing insects.
;;; LI A prayer for purification and forgiveness of sins
6.51.1 Cleansed by the filter of the Wind comes Soma past all our enemies, meet friend of Indra.
6.51.2 May the maternal Waters make us ready: cleanse us with fat- ness they who cleanse with fatness! The Goddesses bear off each blot and tarnish: I come forth from the waters cleansed and stainless.
6.51.3 O Varuna, whatever the offence may be, the sin which men commit against the heavenly folk-- When, through our want of thought we violate thy laws, punish us not, O God, for that iniquity.
;;; LII A charm against noxious reptiles and insects
6.52.1 Slaying the Rakshasas, the Sun mounts upward in the front of heaven, Aditya, from the mountains, seen of all, destroying things unseen.
6.52.2 The kine had settled in their pen, wild animals sought their lairs The wavelets of the brooks had passed away, and were beheld no more.
6.52.3 I have brought Kanva's famous Plant, life-giving, and itself inspired, The medicine that healeth all: may it suppress my hidden foes.
;;; LIII A prayer for recovery and preservation of health and security
6.53.1 May Heaven and Earth, wise pair, may lofty Sukra grant me this thing by reason of the guerdon. May Agni, Soma mark through this libation: may Vayu, Savitar, and Bhaga guard us.
6.53.2 Again return to us our breath and spirit, again come back to us our life and vision! Vaisvanara, unscathed, our bodies' guardian, stand between us and every woe and danger!
6.53.3 We are again united with our bodies, with happy mind, with spirit, strength, and splendour. May Tvashtar here make room for us, and freedom and smooth whate'er is injured in our bodies.
;;; LIV A benediction on a newly elected King
6.54.1 Win the love of Indra that his friend may reach yet higher state. Increase, as rain the grass, this man's dominion and his lofty fame.
6.54.2 Confirm the princely power in him, Agni and Soma! grant him wealth. In all the circuit of his rule make him yet higher for your friend.
6.54.3 The man who shows us enmity, whether a stranger or akin, Thou wilt give up entire to me who sacrifice and press the juice.
;;; LV A prayer for general protection and prosperity
6.55.1 Of all the many God-frequented pathways that traverse realms between the earth and heaven, Consign me, all ye Gods to that which leadeth to perfect and inviolable safety.
6.55.2 Maintain us in well-being Summer, Winter Dew-time and Spring, Autumn, and Rainy Season Give us our share of cattle and of Children. May we enjoy your unassailed protection.
6.55.3 Pay to the Year your lofty adoration, to the first Year, the second, and the present. Many we abide in the auspicious favour and gracious love of these who claim our worship.
;;; LVI A charm against snakes
6.56.1 Let not the serpent slay us, O Gods, with our children and our folk. Let it not close the opened mouth nor open that which now is closed.
6.56.2 Be worship paid unto the black, worship to that with stripes across! To the brown viper reverence, reverence to the demon brood!
6.56.3 I close together fangs with fang, I close together jaws with jaw. I close together tongue with tongue, I close together mouth with mouth.
;;; LVII A charm for a wound or bruise
6.57.1 This is a medicine indeed, Rudra's own medicine is this, Wherewith he warns the arrow off one-shafted, with a hundred tips.
6.57.2 Besprinkle it with anodyne, bedew it with relieving balm: Strong, soothing is the medicine: bless us therewith that we may live.
6.57.3 Let it be health and joy to us. Let nothing vex or injure us. Down with the wound! Let all to us be balm, the whole be medicine.
;;; LVIII A priest's prayer for power and glory
6.58.1 May Indra Maghavan give me name and glory. May Heaven and Earth, this couple, make me famous. May Savitar the deity make me honoured. Here may the man who gives the guerdon love me.
6.58.2 Indra from Heaven and Earth receiveth glory among the plants the Waters have their glory; Even so may we be glorious'mid all the Universal Gods.
6.58.3 Indra and Agni were renowned, famous was Soma at his birth; So too am I illustrious, most glorious of all that is.
;;; LIX A charm to protect cattle and men
6.59.1 First, O Arundhati, protect our oxen and milky kine: Protect each one that is infirm, each quadruped that yields no milk.
6.59.2 Let the Plant give us sheltering aid, Arundhati allied with Gods; Avert Consumption from our men and make our cow-pen rich in milk.
6.59.3 I welcome the auspicious Plant, life-giving, wearing every hue. Far from our cattle may it turn the deadly dart which Rudra casts.
;;; LX The wooing of a bride
6.60.1 With forelock loosened o'er his brow here comes the wooer of the bride, Seeking a husband for this maid, a wife for this unmarried man.
6.60.2 Wooer! this girl hath toiled in vain, going to others' marriages. Now to her wedding, verily, wooer! another maid shall come.
6.60.3 Dhatar upholds the spacious earth, upholds the sky, upholds the Sun. Dhatar bestow upon this maid a husband suited to her wish!
;;; LXI A prayer for prosperity and greatness
6.61.1 The Waters send me what is sweet and pleasant, Sura bring all I need for light and vision! The deities, and all of pious nature, and Savitar the God afford me freedom!
6.61.2 I set the heaven and the earth asunder, I brought all seven sea- sons into being. My word is truth, what I deny is falsehood, above celestial Vak, above the nations.
6.61.3 I gave existence to the earth and heaven, I made the seasons and the seven rivers. My word is truth; what I deny is falsehood, I who rejoice in Agni's, Soma's friendship.
;;; LXII A prayer for purification and riches
6.62.1 Cleanse us Vaisvanara with rays of splendour! With breath and clouds let quickening Vayu cleanse us. And, rich in milky rain, let Earth and Heaven, worshipful, holy, cleanse us with their water.
6.62.2 Lay hold on Sunrita whose forms and regions have fair smooth backs, her who is all men's treasure. Through her may we, in sacrificial banquets singing her glory, be the lords of riches.
6.62.3 For splendour, seize on her whom all men worship, becoming pure yourselves, and bright, and brilliant. Here, through our prayer rejoicing in the banquet, long may we look upon the Sun ascending.
;;; LXIII The symbolical liberation of a sacrificial victim
6.63.1 That collar round thy neck, not to be loosened, which Nirriti the Goddess bound and fastened, I loose for thy long life and strength and vigour. Eat, liberated, food that brings no sorrow.
6.63.2 To thee, sharp-pointed Nirriti, be homage! Loose thou the binding fetters wrought of iron. To me, in truth, again doth Yama give thee. To him, to Yama, yea, to Death, be homage!
6.63.3 Compassed by death which comes in thousand manners, here art thou fastened to the iron pillar. Unanimous with Yama and the Fathers, make this man rise and reach the loftiest heaven.
6.63.4 Thou, mighty Agni, good and true, gatherest up all precious things. Bring us all treasures as thou art enkindled at libation's place.
;;; LXIV To promote unanimity in an assembly
6.64.1 Agree and be united: let your minds be all of one accord, Even as the Gods of ancient days, unanimous, await their share.
6.64.2 The rede is common, common the assembly, common the law, so be their thoughts united. I offer up your general oblation: together entertain one common purpose.
6.64.3 One and the same be your resolve, be all your hearts in har- mony: One and the same be all your minds that all may happily con- sent.
;;; LXV A sacrificial charm against enemies
6.65.1 The angry spirit hath relaxed: loose are the arms that act with mind. Do thou, destroyer, overcome and drive these foemen's might away, and then bring opulence to us.
6.65.2 The shaft for handless fiends which, Gods! ye cast against the handless ones, With this, in shape of sacrifice, I rend the arms of enemies.
6.65.3 Indra made first for Asuras the shaft designed for handless foes: Victorious shall my heroes be with Indra as their constant friend.
;;; LXVI A charm for the destruction and plunder of enemies
6.66.1 Handless be every foeman who assaileth, they who with missiles come to fight against us! Dash them together with great slaughter, Indra! and let their robber chief run pierced with arrows.
6.66.2 Ye who run hither bending bows, brandishing swords and cast- ing darts. Handless be ye, O enemies! Let Indra mangle you to-day.
6.66.3 Handless be these our enemies! We enervate their languid limbs. So let us part among ourselves, in hundreds, Indra! all their wealth.
;;; LXVII A charm for the destruction and plunder of enemies
6.67.1 Indra and Pushan have gone forth along the ways on every side. To-day those hosts of enemies must flee bewildered far away.
6.67.2 Ye foes, come hitherward dismayed like serpents when their heads are gone. Let Indra slay each bravest one of you whom Agni hath con- fused.
6.67.3 Gird thou a bullock's hide on these, make those as timid as the deer. Let the foe flee away, and let his kine come hither-ward to us.
;;; LXVIII A charm to accompany the shaving of the beard
6.68.1 Savitar hath come hither with the razor: come thou, O Vayu, with the heated water. One-minded let Adityas, Rudras, Vasus moisten the hair: shave ye who know King Soma.
6.68.2 Let Aditi shave the beard, and let the Waters bathe it with their strength: Prajapati restore his health for sight and days of lengthened life!
6.68.3 The razor used by Savitar, for shaving, who knoweth Varuna and royal Soma, Even with this shave ye this man, O Brahman. Let him be rich in horses, kine, and children.
;;; LXIX A priest's prayer for power and glory
6.69.1 Mine be the glory in the hill, in vales, in cattle, and in gold, Mine be the sweetness that is found in nectar and in flowing wine!
6.69.2 With your delicious honey balm me, Asvins, Lords of splendid light! That clear and resonant may be the voice I utter to mankind.
6.69.3 In me be strength, in me be fame, in me the power of sacrifice: Prajapati establish this in me as firm as light in heaven!
;;; LXX A benediction on cow and calf
6.70.1 As wine associates with flesh, as dice attend the gaming-board, As an enamoured man's desire is firmly set upon a dame, So let thy heart and soul, O Cow, be firmly set upou thy calf.
6.70.2 As the male elephant pursues with eager step his female's track, As an enamoured man's desire is firmly set upon a dame, So let thy heart and soul, O Cow, be firmly set upon the calf.
6.70.3 Close as the felly and the spoke, fixt as the wheel-rim on the nave, As an enamoured man's desire is firmly set upon a dame, So let thy heart and soul, O Cow, be firmly set upon thy calf.
;;; LXXI A priest's benediction after meat
6.71.1 What food I eat of varied form and nature, food whether gold, or horse, sheep, goat, or bullock, Whatever gift I have received, may Agni the Hotar make it sacrifice well-offered.
6.71.2 Whatever, sacrificed or not, hath reached me, bestowed by men and sanctioned by the Fathers, Whereby my heart seems to leap up, may Agni the Hotar make that sacrifice well-offered.
6.71.3 What food I eat unjustly, Gods! or, doubtful between bestow- ing and refusing, swallow, Through greatness of Vaisvanara the mighty may that same food be sweet to me and blessed!
;;; LXXII A charm to restore or increase virile power
6.72.1 Sicut anguis niger ad voluntatem se extendit, Asurarum arte magica formas novas efficiens, sic fascinum tuum, partem cum parte, conjunctum, hic hymnus efficiat.
6.72.2 Velut penis (tayadarus quem ventus permagnum fecit, quantus. est onagri penis, tantus penis tuus increscat.
6.72.3 Quantum estonagri membrum masculinum, elephanti, asinique, quantum est fortis equi, tantus penis tuus increscat.
;;; LXXIII A King's charm to conciliate his discontented kinsmen
6.73.1 Let Varuna come hither, Soma, Agni, Brihaspati come hither with the Vasus! Unanimous, ye kinsmen, come united, come to the glory of this mighty guardian.
6.73.2 The inclination which your hearts have harboured, the purpose which hath occupied your spirits, This I annul with sacrifice and butter. In me be your sweet resting-place, O kinsmen.
6.73.3 Stand even here; forsake me not. Before us may Pushan make your path unfit to travel. Vastoshpati incessantly recall you! In me be your sweet resting- place, O kinsmen!
;;; LXXIV A King's charm to secure the fidelity of his people
6.74.1 Close gathered be your bodies: be your minds and vows in. unison! Here present Brahmanaspati and Bhaga have assembled you.
6.74.2 Let there be union of your minds, let there be union of your hearts: All that is troubled in your lot with this I mend and harmonize.
6.74.3 As, free from jealousy, the strong Adityas have been the Vasus' and the Rudras' fellows. So free from jealousy, Lord of Three Titles! cause thou these people here to be one-minded.
