;;; LXXV A charm to effect the removal of an enemy
6.75.1 Forth from his dwelling drive that man, the foeman who assaileth us: Through the Expellent sacrifice hath Indra rent and mangled him.
6.75.2 Indra, Foe-Slayer, drive him forth into the distance most remote, Whence never more shall be return in all the years that are to come.
6.75.3 To the three distances, beyond mankind's Five Races, let him go, Beyond the three skies let him go, whence he shall never come- again In all the years that are to be, long as the Sun is in the heaven.
;;; LXXVI A benediction on a new-born Kshatriya child
6.76.1 Those who are sitting round this babe prepare him to be looked upon. Let Agni thoroughly inflamed with all his tongues rise from his- heart.
6.76.2 For length of life I use the name of Agni the Consuming God, Whose smoke the sage who knows the truth beholds proceeding. from his mouth.
6.76.3 The man who knows his fuel laid in order by the Kshatriya Sets not his foot upon the steep declivity that leads to Death.
6.76.4 Those who encompass slay him not: he goes not near his lurk-- ing foes The Kshatriya who, knowing well, takes Agni's name for length of life.
;;; LXXVII A charm to bring the cattle home
6.77.1 Firm stands the heaven, firm stands the earth, firm stands this universal world, Firm stand the rooted mountains. I have put the horses in the stall.
6.77.2 I call the Herdsman, him who knows the way to drive the cattle forth, Who knows the way to drive them home, to drive them back and drive them in.
6.77.3 O Jatavedas turn them back: a hundred homeward ways be thine! Thou hast a thousand avenues: by these restore our kine to us.
;;; LXXVIII A nuptial benediction
6.78.1 Let this man be again bedewed with this presented sacrifice. And comfort with the sap of life the bride whom they have brought to him.
6.78.2 With life's sap let him comfort her, and raise her high with princely sway. In wealth that hath a thousand powers, this pair be inexhausti- ble!
6.78.3 Tvashtar formed her to be thy dame, Tvashtar made thee to be her lord. Long life let Tvashtar give you both. Let Tvashtar give a thousand lives.
;;; LXXIX A prayer for seasonable rain and prosperity
6.79.1 May this our Lord of Cloudy Sky, bedewed with liquid drops preserve unequalled riches in our homes.
6.79.2 Lord of the Cloudy Sky, bestow vigour and strength on our abodes. Let wealth and treasure come to us.
6.79.3 Thou, God bedewed with drops, art Lord of infinite prosperity. Grant us thereof, give us thereof: may we enjoy this boon of thine.
;;; LXXX A prayer for help and protection
6.80.1 He flieth in the firmament observing all the things that be: We with this offering will adore the greatness of the Heavenly Hound.
6.80.2 The three, the Kalakanjas, set aloft in heaven as they were Gods All these I call to be our help and keep this man secure from harm.
6.80.3 In waters is thy birth, in heaven thy station, thy majesty on earth and in the ocean. We with this offering will adore the greatness of the Heavenly Hound.
;;; LXXXI A charm to facilitate child-birth
6.81.1 Thou art a grasper, holding fast both hands: drivest fiends away. A holder both of progeny and riches hath this Ring become.
6.81.2 Prepare accordantly, O Ring, the mother for the infant's birth. On the right way bring forth the boy. Make him come hither. I am here.
6.81.3 The Amulet which Aditi wore when desirous of a son, Tvashtar hath bound upon this dame and said, Be mother of a boy.
;;; LXXXII A charm to win a bride
6.82.1 I call the name of him who comes, hath come, and still draws- nigh to us. Foe-slaying Indra's name I love, the Vasus' friend with hundred powers.
6.82.2 Thus Bhaga spake to me: Let him bring thee a consort by the path. Whereon the Asvins brought the bride Surya the child of Savitar.
6.82.3 Great, Indra. is that hook of thine, bestowing treasure, wrought of gold: Therewith, O Lord of Might, bestow a wife on me who long to wed.
;;; LXXXIII A charm against sores and pustules (apachitas)
6.83.1 Hence, Sores and Pustules, fly away even as the eagle from his home. Let Surya bring a remedy, the Moon shine forth and banish you.
6.83.2 One bright with variegated tints, one white, one black, a couple red:-- The'names of all have I declared. Begone, and injure not our men.
6.83.3 Hence, childless, shall the Pustule flee, grand-daughter of the dusky one. The Boil shall fly away from us, the morbid growth shall vanish hence. Taste, happy in thy mind, thine own oblation, as I with Svaha with my heart present it.
;;; LXXXIV A charm to accompany the symbolical loosing of sacrificial victims
6.84.1 Thou in whose dread mouth I present oblation, that these bound victims may obtain their freedom, The people deem that thou art Earth: I know thee thoroughly, and I say thou art Destruction.
6.84.2 Be thou enriched, O Welfare, with oblations, here among us is thine allotted portion. Free--Hail to thee!--from sin those here and yonder.
6.84.3 Do thou, Destruction, thus, without a rival, release us from the iron bonds that hind us. To me doth Yama verily restore thee. To him, to Yama, yea, to Death be worship!
6.84.4 Thou hast been fastened to an iron pillar, here compassed with a thousand deaths around thee. In full accord with Yama and the Fathers, send this man up- ward to the loftiest heaven.
;;; LXXXV A charm against Consumption
6.85.1 Let Varana the heavenly tree here present keep disease away. The Gods have driven off Decline that entered and possessed this man.
6.85.2 We with the speech of Indra and of Mitra and of Varuna. We with the speech of all the Gods will drive Decline away from thee.
6.85.3 Even as Vritra checked and stayed these waters flowing every way, With Agni, God of all mankind. I check and banish thy Decline.
;;; LXXXVI A glorification of a newly consecrated King
6.86.1 This is the Lord of Indra, this the Lord of Heaven, the Lord of Earth, The Lord of all existing things: the one and only Lord be thou,
6.86.2 The Sea is regent of the floods, Agni is ruler of the land, The Moon is regent of the stars: the one and only Lord be thou.
6.86.3 Thou art the King of Asuras, the crown and summit of man- kind: Thou art the partner of the Gods: the one and only Lord be thou.
;;; LXXXVII A benediction addressed to a newly elected King
6.87.1 Here art thou: I have chosen thee. Stand stedfast and immov- able. Let all the clans desire thee: let not thy kingdom fall away.
6.87.2 Be even here: fall not away: be like a mountain unremoved. Stand stedfast here like Indra's self, and hold the kingship in the grasp.
6.87.3 This man hath Indra stablished, made secure by constant sacri- fice. Soma, and Brahmanaspati here present bless and comfort him!
;;; LXXXVIII A benediction addressed to a newly elected King
6.88.1 Firm is the sky, firm is the earth, and firm is all this living world; Firm are these mountains on their base, and stedfast is this King of men.
6.88.2 Stedfast may Varuna the King, stedfast the God Brihaspati, Stedfast may Indra stedfast, too, may Agni keep thy stedfast reign.
6.88.3 Firm, never to be shaken, crush thy foemen, under thy feet lay those who strive against thee. One-minded, true to thee be all the regions: faithful to thee, the firm, be this assembly!
;;; LXXXIX A man's love charm
6.89.1 This strength that Soma hath bestowed, the head of her who gladdeneth,-- With that which thence hath been produced we make thy spirit sorrowful.
6.89.2 We make thy spirit sorrowful, we fill thy mind with pain and grief. As smoke accompanies the wind, so let thy fancy follow me.
6.89.3 May Varuna and Mitra, may Sarasvati the Goddess, May the centre of the earth, and both her limits bring thee close to me.
;;; XC A charm to cure a poisoned man
6.90.1 The shaft that Rudra hath shot forth against thy members and thy heart, Here do we draw from thee to-day, and turn it hence to every side.
6.90.2 From all the hundred vessels spread throughout the members of thy frame. From all those vessels and canals we call the poisonous matter forth.
6.90.3 Worship to thee, the archer, and O Rudra, to thy levelled shaft! Yea, worship to thine arrow when it left the bow, and when it fell!
;;; XCI A charm against disease
6.91.1 They made this barley ready with a team of eight, a team of six. With this I drive to westward, far away, thy bodily disease.
6.91.2 Vita breathes downward from above, and downward Surya sends his heat: Downward is drawn the milch-cow's milk: so downward go thy malady!
6.91.3 The Waters verily bring health, the Waters drive disease away. The Waters cure all malady: may they bring medicine for thee.
;;; XCII A charm to strengthen and inspirit a war-horse
6.92.1 Be fleet as wind, Strong Steed, when thou art harnessed; go forth as swift as thought at lndra's sending. Let the possessors of all wealth, the Maruts, yoke thee, and Tvashtar in thy feet lay swiftness.
6.92.2 That speed, that lies concealed in thee, O Charger, speed granted to the hawk or wind that wandered, Therewith, Strong Steed, saving in shock of battle endowed with might by might win thou the contest.
6.92.3 Bearing thy body, Charger, may thy body run blessing us and winning thee protection. May he, unswerving, to uphold the mighty, stablish his lustre as a God in heaven.
;;; XCIII A prayer for protection from poison
6.93.1 Yama, Death direly fatal, the Destroyer, with his black crest, Sarva the tawny archer, And all the Gods uprisen with their army, may these on every side avoid our heroes.
6.93.2 With mind, burnt offerings, butter, and libation, to royal Bhava and the archer Sarva, To these the worshipful I pay my worship: may they turn else- where things with deadly venom.
6.93.3 Save us, All-Gods and all-possessing Maruts, from murderous stroke and things that slay with poison. Pure is the might of Varuna, Agni, Soma. May Vata's and Parjanya's favour bless us.
;;; XCIV A charm to reconcile a King's discontented people
6.94.1 We bend your minds in union, bend in harmony your hopes and plans: You there, who turn to sundered ways, we bend and bow in unison.
6.94.2 I with my spirit make your spirits captive: these with their thoughts follow my thought and wishes. I make your hearts submissive to mine order closely attending go where I precede you.
6.94.3 I have invoked both Heaven and Earth, invoked divine Sarasvati, Indra and Agni have I called: Sarasvati, so may we thrive!
;;; XCV A charm to remove disease
6.95.1 In the third heaven above us stands the Asvattha tree, the seat of Gods. There the Gods gained the Kushtha plant, embodiment of end- less life.
6.95.2 There moved through heaven a golden ship, a ship with cordage wrought of gold. There Gods obtained the Kushtha plant, the flower of immor- tality.
6.95.3 Thou art the infant of the plants, the infant of the Snowy Hills: The germ of every thing that is: free this my friend from his disease.
;;; XCVI A prayer for deliverance from sin and sorrow
6.96.1 The many plants of hundred shapes and forms that Soma rules as King, Commanded by Brihaspati, deliver us from grief and woe!
6.96.2 Let them release me from the curse and from the noose of Varupa, Free me from Yama's fetter, and from every sin against the Gods!
6.96.3 From every fault in look, in word, in spirit that we, awake or sleeping, have committed, May Soma, with his godlike nature, cleanse us.
;;; XCVII A prayer for the success and prosperity of a King
6.97.1 The sacrifice is victor, Agni victor, victorious is Soma, Indra conquers: So will we bring oblation unto Agni, this sacrifice that I may win all battles.
6.97.9 Praise to you, Mitra-Varupa, hymn-singers! Here swell with meath dominion blest with children. Far into distant regions drive Destruction, and even from committed sin absolve us.
6.97.3 In this strong hero be ye glad and joyful: cleave ye to him even as ye cleave to Indra. Victorious, kine-winner, thunder-wielder, who quells a host and with his might destroys it.
;;; XCVIII Praise of Indra
6.98.1 Indra be victor, never to be vanquished, to reign among the Kings as sovran ruler! Here be thou meet for praise and supplication, to be revered and waited on and worshipped.
6.98.2 Thou fain for glory, an imperial ruler, hast won dominion over men, O Indra, Of these celestial tribes be thou the sovran: long-lasting be thy sway and undecaying!
6.98.3 Thou governest the north and eastern regions, Indra! fiend- slayer! thou destroycst foemen. Thou hast won all, far as the rivers wander. Bull, called to help, on our right hand thou goest.
;;; XCIX A prayer for protection in battle
6.99.1 Indra, before affliction comes, I call thee from the wide expanse. The mighty guardian, born alone, wearer of many names, I call.
6.99.2 Whatever deadly missile launched to-day flies forth to slaughter us. We take both arms of Indra to encompass us on every side.
6.99.3 We draw about us both the arms of Indra, our deliverer. May they protect us thoroughly. O Savitar, thou God, O royal Soma, make thou me pious- minded for my welfare.
;;; C A charm against poison
6.100.1 The Gods and Surya gave the gift, the Earth and Heaven best- owed the boon. The three Sarasvatis in full accord bestowed the antidote.
6.100.2 That water, Upajikas! which Gods poured for you on thirsty land, With that same water sent by Gods, drive ye away this poison here.
6.98.3 The daughter of the Asuras art thou, and sister of the Gods. Thou who hast sprung from heaven and earth hast robbed the poison of its power.
;;; CI A charm to promote virile vigour
6.101.1 Taurum age, palpita, incresce et teipsum extende: per totum membrum increscat penis: hoc tu caede feminam.
6.101.2 Quo debilem stimulant, quo aegrum excitant (homines), hoc, O Brahmanaspatis, hujus penem in arcus modum extende.
6.101.3 Velut nervum in arcu ego tuum fascinum extendo. Aggredere (mulierem) semper indefessus velut cervus damam.
;;; CII A man's love charm
6.102.1 Even as this ox, O Asvins, steps and turns together with his mate, So let thy fancy turn itself, come nearer, and unite with me.
6.102.2 I, as the shaft-horse draws the mare beside him, draw thee to myself. Like grass that storm and wind have rent, so be thy mind at- tached to me!
6.102.3 Swiftly from Bhaga's hands I bear away a love-compelling charm Of ointment and of sugar-cane, of Spikenard and the Kushtha plant.
;;; CIII A charm to check the approach of a hostile army
6.103.1 Brihaspati and Savitar prepare a rope to bind you fast! Let Bhaga, Mitra, Aryaman, and both the Asvins make the bond.
6.103.2 I bind together all of them, the first, the last, the middlemost. Indra hath girded these with cord: bind them together, Agni, thou!
6.103.3 Those yonder who approach to fight, with banners raised along their ranks, Indra hath girded these with cord: bind them together, Agni, thou!
;;; CIV The same
6.104.1 We bind our foemen with a bond that binds them close and holds them fast. Their breath and respiration I dissever, and their lives from life.
6.104.2 This bond, made keen by Indra, I have formed with heat of holy zeal. Securely bind our enemies, O Agni, who are standing here.
6.104.3 Indra and Agni bind them fast, Soma the King, and both the Friends! May Indra, girt by Maruts, make a bond to bind our enemies.
;;; CV A charm to cure cough
6.105.1 Rapidly as the fancy flies forth with conceptions of the mind. So following the fancy's flight, O Cough, flee rapidly away.
6.105.2 Rapidly as an arrow flies away with keenly-sharpened point, So swiftly flee away, O Cough, over the region of the earth!
6.105.3 Rapidly as the beams of light, the rays of Surya, fly away, So, Cough! fly rapidly away over the current of the sea!
;;; CVI A charm to protect a house from fire
6.106.1 Let flowery Durva grass grow up about thine exit and approach. There let a spring of water rise, or lake with blooming lotuses.
6.106.2 This is the place where waters meet, here is the gathering of the flood. Our home is set amid the lake: turn thou thy jaws away from it.
6.106.3 O House, we compass thee about with coolness to envelop thee. Cool as a lake be thou to us. Let Agni bring us healing balm!
;;; CVII A charm to protect men and cattle
6.107.1 Entrust me, Visvajit, to Trayamana. Guard, Trayamana, all our men, guard all our wealth of quadrupeds.
6.107.2 To Visvajit entrust me, Trayamana. O Visvajit, guard all our men, etc.
6.107.3 To Visvajit entrust me, O Kalyani. Guard, O Kalyani, all our men, etc.
6.107.4 To Sarvavid entrust me, O Kalyani. O Sarvavid, guard all our men, guard all our wealth of quadrupeds.
;;; CVIII A prayer for wisdom
6.108.1 Intelligence, come first to us with store of horses and of kine! Thou with the rays of Surya art our worshipful and holy one.
6.108.2 The first, devout Intelligence, lauded by sages, sped by prayer, Drunk by Brahmacharis, for the favour of the Gods I call.
6.108.3 That excellent Intelligence which Ribhus know, and Asuras, Intelligence which sages know, we cause to enter into me.
6.108.4 Do thou, O Agni, make me wise this day with that Intelligence. Which the creative ishis, which the men endowed with wisdom knew.
6.108.5 Intelligence at eve, at morn, Intelligence at noon of day, With the Sun's beams, and by our speech we plant in us Intelligence.
;;; CIX A charm to heal punctured wounds
6.109.1 The Berry heals the missile's rent, it heals the deeply-piercing wound. The Gods prepared and fashioned it. This hath sufficient power for life.
6.109.2 When from their origin they came, the Berries spake among themselves: The man whom we shall find alive shall never suffer injury.
6.109.3 Asuras buried thee in earth: the Gods again uplifted thee. Healer of sickness caused by wounds and healer of the missile's rent.
;;; CX A benediction on a new-born child
6.110.1 Yea, ancient, meet for praise at sacrifices, ever and now thou sittest down as Hotar. And now, O Agni, make thy person friendly, and win felicity for us by worship.
6.110.2 Neath Jyaishthaghni and Yama's Two Releasers this child was born: preserve him from uprooting. He shall conduct him safe past all misfortunes to lengthened life that lasts a hundred autumns.
6.110.3 Born on the Tiger's day was he, a hero, the Constellations' child, born brave and manly. Let him not wound, when grown in strength, his father, nor disregard his mother, her who bare him.
;;; CXI A charm for insanity
6.111.1 Unbind and loose for me this man, O Agni, who bound and well restrained is chattering folly. Afterward he will offer thee thy portion when he hath been delivered from his madness.
6.111.2 Let Agni gently soothe thy mind when fierce excitement troubles it. Well-skilled I make a medicine that thou no larger mayst be mad.
6.111.3 Insane through sin against the Gods, or maddened by a demon's power-- Well-skilled I make a medicine to free thee from insanity.
6.111.4 May the Apsarases release, Indra and Bhaga let thee go. May all the Gods deliver thee that thou no longer mayst be mad.
;;; CXII A health-charm for man, woman, and son
6.112.1 Let not this one, O Agni, wound the highest of these: preserve thou him from utter ruin. Knowing the way do thou untie the nooses of the she-fiend: let all the Gods approve thee.
6.112.2 Rend thou the; bonds of these asunder, Agni! the, threefold noose whereby the three were fastened. Knowing the way untie the she-fiend's nooses: free all, the son, the father, and the mother.
6.112.3 The elder brother's bonds, still left unwedded, fettered in every limb and bound securely, Loose these, for they are bonds for loosing: Pushan, turn woes away upon the babe-destroyer.
;;; CXIII A charm to banish the fiend Grahi
6.113.1 This sin the Gods wiped off and laid on Trita, and Trita wiped it off on human beings. Thence if the female fiend hath made thee captive, the Gods by prayer shall banish her and free thee.
6.113.2 Enter the particles of light and vapours, go to the rising fogs or mists, O Evil! Hence! vanish in the foams of rivers. Pushan, wipe woes away upon the babe-destroyer!
6.113.3 Stored in twelve separate places lies what Trita hath wiped away, the sins of human beings. Thence if the female fiend hath made thee captive, the Gods by prayer shall banish her and free thee.
;;; CXIV A prayer for pardon of faults and errors in sacrificing
6.114.1 Whatever God-provoking wrong we priests have done, O Deities. Therefrom do ye deliver us, Adityas! by the right of Law.
6.114.2 Here set us free, O holy ones, Adityas, by the right of Law. When striving, bringing sacrifice, we failed to offer it aright.
6.114.3 With ladle full of fatness we, worshippers, pouring holy oil, Striving, have failed, O all ye Gods, against our will, to offer it.
;;; CXV A prayer for forgiveness of sins
6.115.1 Whatever wrong we wittingly or in our ignorance have done, Do ye deliver us therefrom, O all ye Gods, of one accord.
6.115.2 If I, a sinner, when awake or sleeping have committed sin, Free me therefrom as from a stake, from present and from future guilt.
6.115.3 As one unfastened from a stake, or cleansed by bathing after toil, As butter which the sieve hath cleansed, so all shall purge me from the sin.
;;; CXVI A prayer for pardon of sin against mother, father, son, or brother
6.116.1 The wealth which husbandmen aforetime, digging, like men who find their food with knowledge, buried, This to the King, Vivasvan's son, I offer, Sweet be our food and fit for sacrificing!
6.116.2 May he, Vaivasvata, prepare our portion; May he whose share is mead with mead besprinkle. Our sin in hasty mood against our mother, or guilt whereby a sire is wronged and angered.
6.116.3 Whether this sin into our heart hath entered regarding mother, father, son or brother, Auspicious be to us the zeal and spirit of all the fathers who are here among us.
;;; CXVII A prayer for freedom from debt
6.117.1 That which I eat, a debt which still is owing, the tribute due to Yama, which supports me, Thereby may I be free from debt, O Agni. Thou knowest how to rend all bonds asunder.
6.117.2 Still dwelling here we give again this present; we send it forth, the living from the living. Throwing away the grain whence I have eaten, thereby shall I be free from debt, O Agni.
6.117.3 May we be free in this world and that yonder, in the third world may we be unindebted. May we, debt-free, abide in all the pathways, in all the worlds which Gods and Fathers visit.
;;; CXVIII A prayer for pardon of cheating at play
6.118.1 If we have sinned with both our hands, desiring to take the host of dice for our possession, May both Apsarases to-day forgive us that debt, the fiercely- conquering, fiercely-looking.
6.118.2 Stern viewers of their sins who rule the people, forgive us what hash happened as we gambled. Not urging us to pay the debt we owed him, he with a cord hath gone to Yama's kingdom.
6.118.3 My creditor, the man whose wife I visit, he, Gods! whom I approach with supplication, Let not these men dominate me in speaking. Mind this, ye two Apsarases, Gods' Consorts!
;;; CXIX A prayer for release from debts incurred without intention of payment
6.119.1 The debt which I incur, not gaming, Agni! and, not intending to repay, acknowledge, That may Vaisvanara, the best, our sovran, carry away into the world of virtue.
6.119.2 I cause Vaisvanara to know, confessing the debt whose payment to the Gods is promised. He knows to tear asunder all these nooses: so may we dwell with him the gentle-minded.
6.119.3 Vaisvanara the Purifier purge me when I oppose their hope and break my promise, Unknowing in my heart. With supplication, whatever guilt there is in that, I banish.
;;; CXX A prayer for pardon of sins and felicity hereafter
6.120.1 If we have injured Air, or Earth, or Heaven, if we have wronged our Mother or our Father, May Agni Garhapatya here absolve us, and bear us up into the world of virtue.
6.120.2 Earth is our Mother, Aditi our birth-place: our brother Air save us from imprecation! Dyaus, Father, save us, from the world of Fathers! My world not lost, may I approach my kindred.
6.120.3 There where our virtuous friends, who left behind them their bodily infirmities, are happy, Free from distortion of the limbs and lameness, may we behold, in heaven, our sons and parents.
;;; CXXI A prayer for happiness in heaven
6.121.1 Spreading them out, untie the snares that hold us, Varuna's bonds, the upper and the lower. Drive from us evil dream, drive off misfortune; then let us go in- to the world of virtue.
6.121.2 If thou art bound with cord or tied to timber, fixt in the earth, or by a word imprisoned, Our Agni Garhapatya here shall free thee, and lead thee up into the world of virtue.
6.121.3 The two auspicious stars whose name is called Releasers have gone up. Send Amrit hither, let it come freeing the captive from his bonds!
6.121.4 Open thyself, make room: from bonds thou shalt release the prisoner. Freed, like an infant newly born, dwell in all pathways where thou wilt.
;;; CXXII A prayer for happiness in heaven
6.122.1 This portion I who understand deliver to Visvakarman first-born son of Order. So may we follow to the end, unbroken, beyond old age, the thread which we have given.
6.122.2 This long-drawn thread some follow who have offered in order- ed course oblation to the Fathers: Some, offering and giving to the friendless, if they can give: herein they find their heaven. 3, Stand on my side and range yourselves in order, ye two! The faithful reach this world of Svarga. When your dressed food hath been bestowed on Agni, to guard it, wife and husband, come together!
6.122.4 Dwelling with zeal I mount in spirit after the lofty sacrifice as it departeth. Agni, may we, beyond decay, invited, in the third heaven, feast and enjoy the banquet.
6.122.5 These women here, cleansed, purified, and holy, I place at rest singly, in hands of Brahmans. May Indra, Marut-girt, grant me the blessing I long for as I pour you this libation.
;;; CXXIII A prayer for happiness in heaven
6.123.1 Ye who are present, unto you I offer this treasure brought to us by Jatavedas Happily will the sacrificer follow: do ye acknowledge him in highest heaven.
6.123.2 Do ye acknowledge him in highest heaven: ye know the world here present in assembly. In peace will he who sacrifices follow: show him the joy which comes from pious actions.
6.123.3 Gods are the Fathers, and the Fathers Gods. I am the very man I am.
6.123.4 I cook, I give, I offer up oblation. From what I gave let me not be disparted.
6.123.5 O King, take thou thy stand in heaven, there also let that gift be placed. Recognize, King, the gift which we have given, and be gracious, God!
;;; CXXIV An Omen from the sky
6.124.1 From the high firmament, yea, out of heaven a water-drop with dew on me hath fallen. I, Agni! share the merit of the pious, with vigour, milk, and hymns and sacrifices.
6.124.2 If from a tree that fruit hath fallen downward if, aught from air that is vayu. Where it hath touched my body or my garment, thence may the Waters drive Destruction backward.
6.124.3 It is a fragrant ointment, happy fortune, sheen all of gold, yea, purified from blemish. Spread over us are all purifications. Death and Malignity shall not subdue us.
;;; CXXV Glorification of a war-chariot
6.125.1 Mayst thou, O Tree, be firm indeed in body, our friend that furthers us, a goodly hero. Put forth thy strength, compact with thongs of leather, and let thy rider win all spoils of battle.
6.125.2 Its mighty strength was borrowed from the heaven and earth: its conquering force was brought from sovrans of the wood. Honour with sacrifice the Car like Indra's bolt, the Car girt round with straps, the vigour of the floods.
6.125.3 Thou bolt of Indra, vanguard of the Maruts, close knit to Varuna and child of Mitra, As such, accepting gifts which here we offer, receive, O godlike Chariot, these oblations.
;;; CXXVI Glorification of the war drum
6.126.1 Send forth thy voice aloud through earth and heaven, and let the world in all its breadth regard thee. O Drum, accordant with the Gods and Indra, drive thou afar, yea, very far, our foemen.
6.126.2 Thunder out strength and fill us full of vigour, yea, thunder forth and drive away misfortunes. Drive hence, O Drum, drive thou away mischances. Thou art the fist of Indra, show thy firmness.
6.126.3 Conquer those yonder and let these be victors. Let the Drum speak aloud as battle's signal. Let our men, winged with horses, fly together. Let our car- warriors, Indra! be triumphant.
;;; CXXVII A charm to banish various diseases
6.127.1 Of abscess, of decline, of inflammation of the eyes. O Plant, Of penetrating pain, thou Herb, let not a particle remain.
6.127.2 Those nerves of thine, Consumption! which stand closely hidden in thy groin I know the balm for that disease: the magic cure is Sipudru.
6.127.3 We draw from thee piercing pain that penetrates and racks thy limbs, That pierces ears, that pierces eyes, the abscess, and the heart's disease. Downward and far away from thee we banish that unknown. decline.
;;; CXXVIII A charm for fair weather
6.128.1 What time the heavenly bodies chose the Weather Prophet as their King, They brought him favouring weather, and, Let this be his do- main, they said.
6.128.2 May we have weather fair at noon, May we have weather fair at eve, Fair weather when the morning breaks, fair weather when the night is come.
6.128.3 Fair weather to the day and night, and to the stars and sun and moon. Give favourable weather thou, King, Weather Prophet, unto us.
6.128.4 Be worship ever paid to thee, O Weather Prophet, King of Star s, Who gavest us oo weather in the evening and by night and day!
;;; CXXIX A charm for success and happiness
6.129.1 With fortune of the Sisu tree--with Indra as my friend to aid I give myself a happy fate. Fly and begone, Malignities!
6.129.2 That splendour and felicity wherewith thou hast excelled the trees Give me therewith a happy fate. Fly and begone, Malignities
6.129.3 Blind fortune, with reverted leaves that is deposited in trees-- Give me therewith a happy fate. Fly and begone, Malignities.
;;; CXXX A woman's love-charm
6.130.1 This is the Apsarases' love-spell, the conquering, resistless ones'. Send the spell forth, ye Deities! Let him consume with love of me.
6.130.2 I pray, may he remember me, think of me, loving and beloved. Send forth the spell, ye Deities! Let him consume with love of me.
6.130.3 That he may think of me, that I may never, never think of him,. Send forth the spell, ye Deities! Let him consume with love of me.
6.130.4 Madden him, Maruts, madden him. Madden him, madden him, O Air. Madden him, Agni, madden him. Let him consume with love of me.
;;; CXXXI A woman's love-charm
6.131.1 Down upon thee, from head to foot, I draw the pangs of long- ing love. Send forth the charm, ye Deities! Let him consume with love of me.
6.131.2 Assent to this, O Heavenly Grace! Celestial Purpose, guide it well! Send forth the charm, ye Deities! Let him consume with love of me.
6.131.3 If thou shouldst run three leagues away, five leagues, a horse's daily stage, Thence thou shalt come to me again and be the father of our sons.
;;; CXXXII The same
6.132.1 The Philter, burning with the pangs of yearning love, which Gods have poured within the bosom of the floods, That spell for thee I heat by Varuna's decree.
6.132.2 The charm which, burning with the pangs of love, the General Gods have poured within the bosom of the floods, That spell for thee I heat by Varuna's decree.
6.132.3 The Philter, burning with the pangs of longing, which Indrani hath effused within the waters' depth, That spell for thee I heat by Varuna's decree.
6.132.4 The charm, aglow with longing, which Indra and Agni have effused within the bosom of the floods, That spell for thee I heat by Varuna's decree.
6.132.5 The charm aglow with longing which Mitra and Varuna have poured within the bosom of the floods, That spell for thee I heat by Varuna's decree.
;;; CXXXIII A glorification of the sacred girdle
6.133.1 By the direction of that God we journey, he will seek means to save and he will free us; The God who hath engirt us with this Girdle, he who hath fast- ened it, and made us ready.
6.133.2 Thou, weapon of the Rishis, art adored and served with sacrifice. First tasting of the votive milk, Zone, be a hero-slayer thou!
6.133.3 As I am now Death's Brahmachari claiming out of the living world a man for Yama, So with Austerity and Prayer and Fervour I bind this Girdle round the man before me.
6.133.4 She hath become, Faith's daughter, sprung from Fervour, the sister of the world-creating Rishis; As such, O Girdle, give us thought and wisdom, give us religious zeal and mental vigour.
6.133.5 Thou whom primeval Rishis girt about them, they who made the world, As such do thou encircle me, O Girdle, for long days of life.
;;; CXXXIV A priest's prayer for power to punish wrong-doers
6.134.1 This Thunderbolt shall take its fill of Order, scare life away and overthrow the kingdom. Tear necks in pieces. rend napes asunder, even as the Lord of Might the neck of Vritra.
6.134.2 Down, down beneath the conquerors, let him not rise, concealed in earth, but lie down-smitten with the bolt.
6.134.3 Seek out the fierce oppressor, yea, strike only the oppressor dead. Down on the fierce oppressor's head strike at full length, O Thunderbolt!
;;; CXXXV A priest's fulmination against an enemy
6.135.1 Whate'er I eat I turn to strength, and thus I grasp the Thunder- bolt, Rending the shoulders of that man as Indra shattered Vritra's neck.
6.135.2 I drink together what I drink, even as the sea that swallows all. Drinking the life-breath of that man, we drink that man and swallow him.
6.135.3 Whate'er I eat I swallow up, even as the sea that swallows all. Swallowing that man's vital breath, we swallow him completely up.
;;; CXXXVI A charm to promote the growth of hair
6.136.1 Born from the bosom of wide Earth the Goddess, godlike Plant, art thou: So we, Nitatni! dig thee up to strengthen and fix fast the hair.
6.136.2 Make the old firm, make new hair spring, lengthen what has already grown.
6.136.3 Thy hair where it is falling off, and with the roots is torn away, I wet and sprinkle with the Plant, the remedy for all disease.
;;; CXXXVII A charm to promote the growth of hair
6.137.1 The Plant which Jamadagni dug to make his daughter's locks. grow long, This same hath Vitahavya brought to us from Asita's abode.
6.137.2 They might be measured with a rein, meted with both extended arms. Let the black locks spring thick and strong and grow like reeds upon thy head.
6.137.3 Strengthen the roots, prolong the points, lengthen the middle part, O Plant. Let the black locks spring thick and strong and grow like reeds upon thy head.
;;; CXXXVIII A woman's imprecation on her unfaithful lover
6.138.1 O Plant, thy fame is spread abroad as best of all the herbs that grow. Unman for me to-day this man that he may wear the horn of hair.
6.138.2 Make him a eunuch with a horn, set thou the crest upon his- head. Let Indra with two pressing-stones deprive him of his manly strength.
6.138.3 I have unmanned thee, eunuch! yea, impotent! made thee- impotent, and robbed thee, weakling! of thy strength. Upon his head we set the horn, we set the branching ornament.
6.138.4 Duas tuas venas, a Diis factas, in quibus stat vigor virilis, paxillo ligneo in testiculis ob istam mulierem tibi findo.
6.138.5 Ut mulieres mattam (tegetem) facturae arundinem lapide findunt, sic fascinum tuum cum testiculis ob istam mulierem findo.
;;; CXXXIX A woman's love-charm
6.139.1 Thou hast grown up, a source of joy to bless me with pros- perity. A hundred are thy tendrils, three-and-thirty thy descending shoots. With this that bears a thousand leaves I dry thy heart and wither it.
6.139.2 Let thy heart wither for my love and let thy month be dry for me. Parch and dry up with longing, go with lips that love of me hath dried.
6.139.3 Drive us together, tawny! fair! a go-between who wakens love. Drive us together, him and me, and give us both one heart and mind.
6.139.4 Even as his mouth is parched who finds no water for his burn- ing thirst, So parch and burn with longing, go with lips that love of me hath dried.
6.139.5 Even as the Mungoose bites and rends and then restores the wounded snake, So do thou, Mighty one, restore the fracture of our severed love.
;;; CXL A blessing on a child's first two teeth
6.140.1 Two tigers have grown up who long to eat the mother and the sire: Soothe, Brahmanaspati, and thou, O Jatavedas, both these teeth.
6.140.2 Let rice and barley be your food, eat also beans and sesamum. This is the share allotted you, to be your portion, ye two Teeth. Harm not your mother and your sire.
6.140.3 Both fellow teeth have been invoked, gentle and bringing happi- ness. Else whither let the fierceness of your nature turn away, O Teeth! Harm not your mother or your sire.
;;; CXLI A blessing on cattle
6.141.1 Vayu collected these: to find their sustenance be Tvashtar's care: May Indra bless and comfort them, and Rudra look that they increase.
6.141.2 Take thou the iron axe and make a pair by marks upon their ears. This sign the Asvins have impressed: let these increase and multiply.
6.141.3 Even as Gods and Asuras, even as mortal men have done, Do ye, that these may multiply in thousands, Asvins! make the mark.
;;; CXLI A blessing on cattle
6.142.1 Spring high, O Barley, and become much through thine own magnificence: Burst all the vessels; let the bolt from heaven forbear to strike thee down.
6.142.2 As we invite and call to thee, Barley, a God who heareth us, Raise thyself up like heaven on high and be exhaustless as the sea.
6.142.3 Exhaustless let thine out-turns be, exhaustless be thy gathered heaps, Exhaustless be thy givers, and exhaustless those who eat of thee.
;;; I Glorification of the power of prayer and to Agni
7.1.1 They who by thought have guided all that Speech hath best, or they who with their heart have uttered words of truth, Made stronger by the strength which the third prayer bestows, have by the fourth prayer learned the nature of the Cow.
7.1.2 Well knows this son his sire, he knows his mother well: he hath been son, and he hath been illiberal. He hath encompassed heaven, and air's mid-realm, and sky; he hath become this All; he hath come nigh to us.
;;; II Praise of Atharvan
7.2.1 Invoke for us, proclaim in sundry places, the kinsman of the Gods, our sire Atharvan, His mother's germ, his father's breath, the youthful, who with his mind hath noticed this oblation.
;;; IV To Vayu God of the Wind
7.4.1 With thine eleven teams, to aid our wishes, yea, with thy two- and-twenty teams, O Vayu, With all thy three-and-thirty teams for drawing, here loose these teams, thou who art prompt to listen!
;;; IV To Vayu God of the Wind
7.4.1 With thine eleven teams, to aid our wishes, yea, with thy two- and-twenty teams, O Vayu, With all thy three-and-thirty teams for drawing, here loose these teams, thou who art prompt to listen!
;;; V A glorification of sacrifice
7.5.1 The Gods adored the Sacrifice with worship: these were the statutes of primeval ages. Those mighty ones attained the cope of heaven, there where the Sadhyas, Gods of old, are dwelling.
7.5.2 Sacrifice was, was manifest among us: it sprang to life and then in time grew stronger. Then it became thedeities' lord and ruler: may it bestow on us abundant riches.
7.5.3 Where the Gods worshipped Gods with their oblation, worship- ped immortals with immortal spirit, There in the loftiest heaven may we be happy, and look upon that light when Surya rises.
7.5.4 With their oblation, Purusha, the Gods performed a sacrifice. A sacrifice more potent still they paid with the invoking hymn.
7.5.5 With dog the Gods, perplexed, have paid oblation, and with cow's limbs in sundry sacrifices. Invoke for us, in many a place declare him who with his mind. hath noticed this our worship.
;;; VI A prayer to Aditi for help and protection
7.6.1 Aditi is sky, and air's mid-region, Aditi is the father, son, and mother, Aditi all the Gods and the Five Nations, Aditi what is now and what is future.
7.6.2 We call for help the Queen of Law and Order, great mother of all those whose ways are righteous, Far-spread, unwasting strong in her dominion, Aditi wisely lead- ing, well protecting.
7.6.3 Sinless may we ascend, for weal, the vessel, rowed with good oars, divine, that never leaketh, Earth, our strong guard, incomparable Heaven, Aditi wisely lead- ing, well protecting.
7.6.4 Let us bring hither, in pursuit of riches, Aditi with our word, the mighty mother, Her in whose lap the spacious air is lying: may she afford us triply-guarding shelter!
;;; VII Praise of the Adityas
7.7.1 I have sung praise to Diti's sons and Aditi's, those very lofty and invulnerable Gods. For far within the depths of ocean is their home and in the wor- ship paid them none excelleth these.
;;; VIII Godspeed to a departing traveller
7.8.1 Go forward on thy way from good to better: Brihaspati pre- cede thy steps and guide thee! Place this man here, within this earth's enclosure, afar from foes with all his men about him.
;;; IX A prayer to Pushan for protection and the recovery of lost property
7.9.1 Pushan was born to move on distant pathways, on roads remote from earth, remote from heaven. To both most lovely places of assembly he travels and returns with perfect knowledge.
7.9.2 Pushan knows all these realms: may he conduct us by ways that are most free from fear and danger. Giver of blessings, glowing, all heroic, may he the wise and watchful go before us.
7.9.3 We are thy praisers here, O Pushan: never let us be injured under thy protection.
7.9.4 From out the distance, far and wide, may Pushan stretch his right hand forth. Let him drive back our lost to us, let us return with what is lost.
;;; X A prayer for the favour of Sarasvati
7.10.1 That breast of thine, exhaustless and delightful, good to invoke, beneficent, free giver. Wherewith thou feedest all things that are choicest, bring that, Sarasvati, that we may drain it.
;;; XI A prayer to protect corn from lightning and drought
7.11.1 That far-spread thunder, sent from thee, which cometh on all this world, a high celestial signal Strike not, O God, our growing corn with lightning, not kill it with the burning rays of Surya.
;;; XII A prayer for influence at deliberative and religious meetings
7.12.1 In concord may Prajapati's two daughters, Gathering and As- sembly, both protect me. May every man I meet respect and aid me. Fair be my words, O Fathers, at the meetings.
7.12.2 We know thy name, O Conference: thy name is interchange of talk. Let all the company who join the Conference agree with me.
7.12.3 Of these men seated here I make the splendour and the lore mine own. Indra, make me conspicuous in all this gathered company.
7.12.4 Whether your thoughts are turned away, or bound and fastened here or there, We draw them hitherward again: let your mind firmly rest on me.
;;; XIII A charm to win superiority over foes and rivals
7.13.1 As the Sun, rising, taketh to himself the brightness of the stars,. So I assume the glory of women and men mine enemies. All ye amang my rivals who behold me as I come to you, I seize the glory of my foes as the Sun, rising, theirs who sleep.
;;; XIV A prayer to Savitar for prosperity
7.14.1 I praise this God, parent of heaven and earth, exceeding wiser possessed of real energy, giver of treasure, thinker dear to all,.
7.14.2 Whose splendour is sublime, whose light shone brilliant in crea- tion, who, wise, and golden-handed, in his beauty made the sky.
7.14.3 As thou, God! quickening, for our ancient father, sentest him height above and room about him, So unto us, O Savitar, send treasures, abundant, day by day, in shape of cattle.
7.14.4 Savitar, God, our household friend, most precious, hath sent our fathers life and power and riches. Let him drink Soma and rejoice when worshipped. Under his law even the Wanderer travels.
;;; XV A charm to win divine favour and felicity
7.15.1 I choose, O Savitar, that glorious favour, with fruitful energy and every blessing, Even this one's teeming cow, erst milked by Kanva, thousand- streamed, milked for happiness by the mighty.
;;; XVI A prayer for prosperity
7.16.1 Increase this man Brihaspati! Illume him, O Savitar, for high and happy fortune. Sharpen him thoroughly though already sharpened: with glad acclaim let all the Gods receive him.
;;; XVII A prayer for wealth and children
7.17.1 May the Ordainer give us wealth, Lord, ruler of the world of life: with full hand may he give to us.
7.17.2 May Dhatar grant the worshipper henceforth imperishable life. May we obtain the favour of the God who giveth every boon.
7.17.3 To him may Dhatar grant all kinds of blessings who, craving children, serves him in his dwelling. Him may the Gods invest with life eternal, yea, all the Gods and Aditi accordant.
7.17.4 May this our gift please Savitar, Rati, Dhatar, Prajapati, and Agni Lord of Treasures. May Tvashtar, Vishnu, blessing him with children, give store ot riches to the sacrificer.
;;; XVIII A prayer for rain
7.18.1 Burst open, Prithvi, and cleave asunder this celestial cloud. Untie, O Dhatar--for thou canst--the bottle of the breast of heaven.
7.18.2 Let not the Sun's heat burn, nor cold destroy her. Let Earth with all her quickening drops burst open. Even for her the waters flow, and fatness: where Soma is even there is bliss for ever.
;;; XIX A prayer for prosperity
7.19.1 Prajapati engenders earthly creatures: may the benevolent Ordainer form them, Having one common womb, and mind, and spirit. He who is. Lord of Plenty give me plenty!
;;; XX A prayer for prosperity and happiness
7.20.1 Anumati approve to-day our sacrifice among the Gods! May Agni bear mine offerings away for me the worshipper.
7.20.2 Do thou, Anumati! approve, and grant us health and happiness. Accept the offered sacrifice, and, Goddess, give us progeny.
7.20.3 May he approving in return accord us wealth inexhaustible with store of children. Never may we be subject to his anger, but rest in his benevo- lence and mercy.
7.20.4 Thy name is easy to invoke, good leader! approved, Anumati and rich in bounty. Source of all bonds! fill up therewith our worship, and, Blest One! grant us wealth with goodly heroes.
7.20.5 Anumati hath come to this our worship well-formed to give good lands and valiant heroes: For her kind care hath blessed us. God-protected, may she assist the sacrifice we offer.
7.20.6 Anumati became this All, whatever standeth or walketh, every- thing that moveth. May we enjoy thy gracious love, O Goddess. Regard us, O Anu- mati, with favour.
;;; XXI A funeral stanza
7.21.1 With prayer come all together to the Lord of Heaven: he is the peerless one, far-reaching, guest of men. He, God of ancient time, hath gained a recent thrall; to him alone is turned the path which all must tread.
;;; XXII To Savitar, or Yama invested with Savitar's attributes
7.22.1 Unto a thousand sages he hath given sight: thought, light is he in ranging all.
7.22.2 The Bright One hath sent forth the Dawns, a closely gathered band, Immaculate, unanimous, brightly refulgent in their homes.
;;; XXIII A charm to banish fiends and troubles
7.23.1 The fearful dream, and indigence, the monster, the malignant hags. All female fiends of evil name and wicked tongue we drive afar.
;;; XXIV A prayer for riches
7.24.1 What treasure hath been dug for us by Indra, by Agni, Visve- devas, tuneful Maruts, On us may Savitar whose laws are faithful, Prajapati, and Heavenly Grace bestow it.
;;; XXV Praise of Vishnu and Varuna
7.25.1 The early morning prayer hath come to Vishnu and Varuna, Lords through might, whom none hath equalled, Gods by whose power the realms of air were stablished, strongest and most heroic in their vigour.
7.25.2 The early prayer hath ever come to Vishnu and Varuna by that God's high power and statute. In whose control is all this world that shineth, all that hath powers to see and all that breatheth.
;;; XXVI Praise of Vishnu
7.26.1 I will declare the mighty deeds of Vishnu, of him who measured out the earthly regions, Who propped the highest place of congregation, thrice setting down his footstep, widely striding.
7.26.2 Loud boast doth Vishnu make of this achievement, like some wild beast, dread, prowling, mountain-roaming. May he approach us from the farthest distance.
7.26.3 Thou within whose three wide-extended paces all worlds and creatures have their habitation, Drink oil, thou homed in oil! promote the sacrificer more and more.
7.26.4 Through all this world strode Vishnu: thrice his foot he planted, and the whole Was gathered in his footstep's dust.
7.26.5 Vishnu the guardian, he whom none deceiveth, made three steps, thenceforth. Establishing these high decrees.
7.26.6 Look ye on Vishnu's works, whereby the friend of Indra, close- allied, Hath let his holy ways be seen.
7.26.7 The princes evermore behold that loftiest place where Vishnu is, Like an extended eye in heaven,
7.26.8 From heaven, O Vishnu, or from earth, O Vishnu, or from the great far-spreading air's mid-region, Fill both thy hands full of abundant treasures, and from the right and left bestow them freely.
;;; XXVII A prayer to Ida, Goddess of devotion
7.27.1 May Ida with her statute dwell beside us, she in whose place the pious purge and cleanse them. She, mighty, Soma-decked, whose foot drops fatness, meet for All-Gods, hath come to aid our worship.
;;; XXVIII Praise of the sacrificial utensils
7.28.1 Blest be the Broom, may the Mace bring a blessing, and may the Altar and the Hatchet bless us. Worshipful Gods, may they accept this worship, lovers of sacri- fice, and sacrificers.
;;; XXIX To Agni and Vishnu
7.29.1 This is your glorious might, Agni and Vishnu! Ye drink the essence of the mystic butter. Placing in every home seven costly treasures. Let your tongue stretch to take the offered fatness.
7.29.2 Ye love the great law, Agni Vishnu! joying, ye feast on mystic essences of butter, Exalted in each house with fair laudation. Let your tongue stretch to take the offered fatness.
;;; XXX A charm to be used when the eyes are anointed
7.30.1 Heaven, Earth, and Mitra here have caused mine eyes to be- anointed well, Savitar, Brahmanaspati take care that they be duly balmed!
;;; XXXI A prayer for the overthrow of enemies
7.31.1 Rouse us to-day O Indra, Maghavan, hero, with thy best pos- sible and varied succours, May he who hateth us fall low beneath us, and him whom we detest let life abandon.
;;; XXXII A prayer to Agni for long life
7.32.1 We bringing homage have approached the friend who seeks our wondering praise, Young, strengthener of the sacrifice. May he bestow long life on me.
;;; XXXIII A prayer for long life, children, and riches
7.33.1 Let Pushan, let the Maruts, let Brihaspati pour forth on me; This present Agni pour on me children and riches in a stream! May he bestow long life on me.
;;; XXXIV A prayer for freedom from sin and the overthrow of enemies
7.34.1 Agni, drive off my rivals born and living, repel those yet unborn, O Jatavedas. Cast down beneath my feet mine adversaries. In Aditi's regard may we be sinless.
;;; XXXV A prayer for the prosperity of a King and his kingdom
7.35.1 Subdue with conquering might his other rivals, those yet unborn repel, O Jatavedas. For great felicity protect this kingdom, and in this man let all the Gods be joyful.
7.35.2 Hae quot tibi sunt venae atque arteriae harum omnium os tibi lapide occlusi.
7.35.3 Uteri tui summam partem inferam facio: ne tibi soboles neque filius eveniat. Sterilem et infecundam te facio: lapidem tuum, operimentum facio.
;;; XXXVI A charm to be pronounced by bride and bridegroom
7.36.1 Sweet are the glances of our eyes, our faces are as smooth as balm, Within thy bosom harbour me; one spirit dwell in both of us!
;;; XXXVII A nuptial charm to be spoken by the bride
7.37.1 With this my robe, inherited from Manu, I envelop thee, So that thou mayst be all mine own and give no thought to other dames.
;;; XXXVIII A maiden's love-charm
7.38.1 I dig this Healing Herb that makes my lover look on me and weep; That bids the parting friend return and kindly greets him as he comes.
7.38.2 This Herb wherewith the Asuri drew Indra downward from the Gods, With this same Herb I draw thee close that I may be most dear to thee.
7.38.3 Thou art the peer of Soma, yea, thou art the equal of the Sun, The peer of all the Gods art thou: therefore we call thee hither-- ward.
7.38.4 I am the speaker here, not thou: speak thou where the assembly meets. Thou shalt be mine and only mine, and never mention other dames.
7.38.5 If thou art far away beyond the rivers, far away from men, This Herb shall seem to bind thee fast and bring thee back my prisoner.
;;; XXXIX A sacrificial charm for rain and prosperity
7.39.1 May he establish in our home the master of riches, gladdening with rain in season, Mighty, strong-winged, celestial, dropping moisture, Bull of the plants and embryo of waters.
;;; XL A prayer for prosperity
7.40.1 We call Sarasvan, under whose protection all cattle wander, to preserve and aid us, Him in whose ordinance abide the waters, to whose command the Lord of Plenty listens.
7.40.2 Abiding here let us invoke Sarasvan, the seat of riches, glorious, wealth-increaser, Him who inclines and gives to him who worships, the rich pos- sessor and the Lord of Fulness.
;;; XLI A prayer for prosperity
7.41.1 Observing men, and viewing home, the Falcon hath cleft his swift way over wastes and waters. May he, with Indra for a friend, auspicious, traversing all air's lower realms, come hither.
7.41.2 The heavenly Falcon, viewing men, well-pinioned, strength-giver, hundred-footed, hundred-nested, Shall give us treasure which was taken from us. May it be rich in food among our Fathers.
;;; XLII A prayer for delivery from sin and sickness
7.42.1 Scatter and drive away, Soma and Rudra, the sickness that hath come within our dwelling, Afar into the distance chase Destruction, and even from commit- ted sin release us.
7.42.2 Lay on our bodies, O ye twain, O Soma and Rudra, all those balms that heal diseases. Set free and draw away the sin committed, which we have still inherent in our persons.
;;; XLIII A charm against lightning
7.43.1 Some of thy words bode weal and some misfortune: thou scat- terest them all with friendly feeling. Deep within this three words are laid: among them one hath flown off even as the sound was uttered.
;;; XLIV In praise of Indra and Vishnu
7.44.1 Ye twain have conquered, and have not been vanquished: not either of the pair hath been defeated. Ye, Indra Vishnu, when ye fought your battle; produced this infinite with three divisions.
;;; XLV A charm against jealousy
7.45.1 Brought hitherward from Sindhu, from a folk of every mingled race, Fetched from afar, thou art I deem, a balm that cureth. jealousy.
7.45.2 As one with water quencheth fire, so calm this lover's jealousy, Like heat of fire that burneth here, or flame that rageth through the wood.
;;; XLVI A charm for offspring and prosperity
7.46.1 O broad-tressed Sinivali, thou who art the sister of the Gods, Accept the offered sacrifice, and, Goddess, grant us progeny.
7.46.2 Present the sacrifice to her, to Sinivali, Queen of men, Beauti- ful-fingered, lovely-armed, prolific, bearing many a child.
7.46.3 Thou who as Queen of men art Indra's equal, a Goddess coming with a thousand tresses, To thee our sacrifices are performed, O Consort of Vishnu Goddess, urge thy Lord to bounty!
;;; XLVII A prayer for wealth and birth of a son
7.47.1 Oft in this sacrifice with favoured cry I call Kuhu, beneficent Goddess, skilled in all her works. May she vouchsafe us wealth with every boon, and give a, hero meet for praise who gives a hundred gifts.
7.47.2 Kuhl), the Queen of Gods and immortality, called to assist, enjoy this sacrifice of' ours! Let her, desirous of our worship, hear to-day: may she, intelligent, give increase of our wealth.
;;; XLVIII A prayer for prosperity and the birth of a son
7.48.1 I call on Raka with hair laud and reverent cry: may she, auspicious, hear us and herself observe. With never-breaking needle may she sew her work, and send a glorious man who gives a hundred gifts.
7.48.2 All thy kind favours, Raka! lovely in their form, wherewith thou grantest treasures to the man who gives, With these come thou to us this day benevolent, O blessed one, bestowing wealth of thousand sorts.
;;; XLIX A prayer for children and booty
7.49.1 May the Gods' Consorts aid us of their own free will, help us to offspring and the winning of the spoil. May Goddesses who quickly listen shelter us, both those on earth and they within the waters' realm.
7.49.2 May the Dames, wives of Gods, enjoy our presents, Rat, Asvini Indrani and Agnayi; May Rodasi and Varunani hear us, and Goddesses come at the matrons' season.
;;; L A gambler's prayer for success in gaming
7.50.1 As evermore the lightning flash strikes, irresistible, the tree, So, irresistible, may I conquer the gamblers with the dice.
7.50.2 From every side, from hale and sick, impotent to defend them- selves, May all the fortune of the folk as winnings pass into my hands.
7.50.3 I pray to Agni, him who guards his treasure: here, won by homage, may he pile our winnings. As 'twere with racing cars I bring my presents: duly with reverence, let me laud the Maruts.
7.50.4 With thee to aid us may we win the treasure: do thou assist our side in every battle. Give us wide room and easy way, O Indra; break down, O Maghavan, the foemen's valour.
7.50.5 I have completely cleaned thee out, won from thee what thou keptest back. As a wolf tears and rends a sheep, so do I tear thy stake away.
7.50.6 Yea, by superior play one gains advantage: in time he piles his spoil as doth a gambler. He overwhelms with wealth's inherent powers the devotee who keeps not back his riches.
7.50.7 May we all, much-invoked! repel with cattle want that brings sin, hunger with store of barley. May we uninjured, first among the princes, obtain possessions by our own exertions.
7.50.8 My right hand holds my winnings fast, and in my left is victory. I would that I were winner of cattle and horses, wealth and gold.
7.50.9 Dice, give me play that bringeth fruit as 'twere a cow with flowing milk! And, as the bowstring binds, the bow, unite me with a stream of gains.
;;; LI A prayer for Brihaspati's and Indra's protection
7.51.1 Brihaspati protect us from the sinner, from rearward, from above, and from below us! May Indra from the front and from the centre, as friend to friends, vouchsafe us room and freedom.
;;; LII A prayer for peace and concord
7.52.1 Give us agreement with our own, with strangers give us unity: Do ye, O Asvins, in this place join us in sympathy and love.
7.52.2 May we agree in mind, agree in purpose: let us not fight against the heavenly spirit. Around us rise no din of frequent slaughter, nor Indra's arrow fly, for day is present!
;;; LIII A charm to recover a sick man at the point of death
7.53.1 As thou, Brihaspati, from the curse hast saved us, from dwel- ling yonder in the realm of Yama, The Asvins, leeches of the Gods, O Agni, have chased Death far from us with mighty powers.
7.53.2 Move both together; do not leave the body. Let both the breathings stay for thee united. Waxing in strength live thou a hundred autumns. Thy noblest guardian and thy lord is Agni.
7.53.3 Return, thy life now vanished into distance! Return, the breath thou drawest and exhalest! Agni hath snatched it from Destruction's bosom: into thyself again I introduce it.
7.53.4 Let not the vital breath he draws forsake him, let not his expiration part and leave him. I give him over to the Seven Rishis: let them conduct him to old age in safety.
7.53.5 Enter him, both ye breaths, like two draught-oxen entering their stall. Let him, the treasure of old age, still wax in strength, uninjured,. here.
7.53.6 I send thee back thy vital breath; I drive Consumption far from thee, May Agni here, most excellent, sustain our life on every side.
7.53.7 From out the depth of darkness, we, ascending to the highest heaven, Have come to the sublimest light, to Surya, God among the. Gods.
;;; LIV A charm to obtain knowledge of the Veda
7.54.1 We worship holy Verse and Song, by which they carry out their acts, Shining in order's seat these twain present the sacrifice to Gods.
7.54.2 As I have asked about Verse, Song, Sacrifice, strength, force,. Yajus-text, So never let this lore that I have sought forsake me, Lord of Might!
;;; LV A charm to ensure a prosperous journey
7.55.1 Thy downward paths from heaven, whereby thou hast raised all the world to life, Give us in gracious love, good Lord!
;;; LVI A charm against poisonous bites and stings
7.56.1 Whether it came from viper, from black snake or snake with transverse stripes, Or Kankaparvan's bite, this herb hath made the poison power- less.
7.56.2 Honey-born, honey-dropping, rich in honey, honeysweet, this herb, Is medicine that heals the wound and kills the gnat that bites and stings.
7.56.3 Whatever bit, or sucked thy blood, we summon thence away from thee The ineffectual poison of the little sharply-stinging gnat.
7.56.4 Thou here who crookest wicked jaws, thou tortuous, jointless, limbless thing, These jaws thou, Brahmanaspati! shalt bend together like a reed.
7.56.5 This scorpion here that creeps along, low on the ground and powerless-- I have removed his poison and then utterly demolished him.
7.56.6 No strength in thy two arms hast thou, nor in thy head, nor in thy waist: Then what is that small thing thou so viciously bearest in thy tail?
7.56.7 The emmets make a meal of thee and peahens tear and mangle thee: All ye are crying out, In sooth the scorpion's poison hath no strength.
7.56.8 Thou creature who inflictest wounds both with thy mouth and with thy tail, No poison in thy mouth hast thou: what at thy tail's root will there be?
;;; LVII A charm for some physical disorder
7.57.1 Whatever trouble hath disturbed and shaken me--I speak with hope, I move, imploring, 'mid the folk What harm my body in myself hath suffered, now let Sarasvati relieve with fatness.
7.57.2 Seven flow for him, the youth on whom the Maruts wait: the sons have taught the Father everlasting laws. Both worlds are his: both shine belonging unto him. Both move together: both, as his possession thrive.
;;; LVIII An invitation to Indra and Varuna
7.58.1 True to laws, Indra Varuna, drinkers of the juice, quaff this pressed Soma which shall give you rapturous joy! Let sacrifice, your car, to entertain the Gods, approach its rest- ing-place that they may drink thereof.
7.58.2 O Indra Varuna, drink your fill, ye heroes, of this effectual and sweetest Soma. This juice was shed by us that ye might quaff it. On this trimmed grass be seated and rejoice you.
;;; LIX An imprecation
7.59.1 Like a tree struck by lightning may the man be withered from the root. Who curseth us who curse not him, or, when we curse him. curseth us.
;;; LX A parting traveller's address to the houses of his village
7.60.1 I, prudent, bringing power, a treasure-winner, with amicable eye that strikes no terror, Come, praising and kind-thoughted, to these houses: be not afraid of me, be glad and joyful.
7.60.2 Let these delightful Houses that are rich in power and store of milk, Replete with wealth and standing firm, become aware of our approach.
7.60.3 These Houses we invoke, whereon the distant exile sets his thought, Wherein dwells many a friendly heart: let them beware of our approach.
7.60.4 Thus greeted, ye of ample wealth, friends who enjoy delightful sweets. Be ever free from hunger, free from thirst! Ye Houses, fear us not.
7.60.5 Kind greeting to the cattle here, kind greeting to the goats and sheep! Then, of the food within our homes, kind greeting to the plea- sant drink!
7.60.6 Full of refreshment, full of charms, of laughter and felicity, Be ever free from hunger, free from thirst! Ye Houses, fear us not. Stay here, and come not after me: prosper in every form and shape. With happy fortune will I come! Grow more abundant still through me!
;;; LXI A prayer for sacred knowledge and its fruits
7.61.1 Since, Agni, with our fervent zeal we undergo austerity, May we be dear to Sacred Lore, may we be wise and live long lives.
7.61.2 Agni, we practise acts austere, we undergo austerity. So listening to Holy Lore may we grow wise and full of days.
;;; LXII A prayer for the overthrow of enemies
7.62.6 Like a car-warrior, Agni here, grown mighty, Lord of the brave, Chief Priest, hath conquered footmen. Laid on earth's centre he hath flashed and glittered. Low may he lay our enemies beneath us.
;;; LXIII A prayer for deliverance from affliction
7.63.1 We call with lauds from his most lofty dwelling victorious Agni, conqueror in battles. May he conveyus over all distresses, may the God Agni bear us past our troubles.
;;; LXIV A charm to avert an evil omen
7.64.1 From all that woe and trouble may the Waters save and rescue me, Whate'er the Raven, black of hue, flying out hither ward, hath dropped.
7.64.2 May Agni Garhapatya save and set me free from all this guilt. Which the black Raven with thy mouth, O Nirriti, hath wiped away.
;;; LXV A charm against imprecation and threatened evils
7.65.1 With retroverted fruit hast thou, O Apamarga, sprung and grown. Hence into distance most remote drive every curse away from, me.
7.65.2 Whatever evil we have done, whatever vile or sinful act, With thee, O Apamarga, who lookest all ways, we wipe it off.
7.65.3 If with the cripple we have lived, whose teeth are black and nails deformed, With thee, O Apamarga, we wipe all that ill away from us.
;;; LXVI A prayer to Vak
7.66.1 If it was in the wind or air's mid-region, if it was in the trees or in the bushes, To meet whose utterance forth streamed the cattle, may that. Celestial Power again approach us.
;;; LXVII A priest's prayer to the Agnayo Dhishnyah
7.67.1 May sense return to me again, and spirit, return my Sacred Power and my possessions! Again let fires, aflame on lesser altars, each duly stationed, here succeed and prosper.
;;; LXVIII A prayer for children and prosperity
7.68.1 Sarasvati, in thy decrees, Goddess, in thy celestial laws, Accept the offered sacrifice, and, Goddess, grant us progeny.
7.68.2 Here is, Sarasvati, thy fat libation, this sacrifice passing to the mouth of Fathers. These most auspicious offerings have ascended to thee: through, these may we be full of sweetness.
7.68.3 Be kind and most auspicious, be gracious to us, Sarasvati, May we be ever in thy sight.
;;; LXIX A prayer for prosperity
7.69.1 May the wind kindly breathe on us, may the Sun warm us. pleasantly. May days pass happily for us, may night draw near delightfully, may dawn break joyfully for us!
;;; LXX A charm to frustrate an enemy's sacrifice
7.70.1 Whatever sacrifice that man performeth with voice, mind, sacred formula, oblation, May, in accord with Death, Destruction ruin his offering before it gain fulfilment.
7.70.2 For him may sorcerers, Destruction, demons strike and prevent fulfilment through their falsehood. Let Gods, by Indra sent, destroy his butter, and let his sacrifice be ineffective.
7.70.3 Let the two Sovrans, swift to come, like falcons swooping on their prey, Destroy the butter of the foe whoever plots to injure us.
7.70.4 I seize thine arms and draw them back, I bind a bandage on thy mouth. I with the anger of the God Agni have killed thy sacrifice.
7.70.5 Behind thy back I tie thine arms, I bind a bandage on thy mouth: With the terrific Agni's wrath have I destroyed thy sacrifice.
;;; LXXI In praise of Agni
7.71.1 We set thee round us as a fort, victorious Agni! thee a sage, Bold in thy colour day by day, destroyer of the treacherous foe.
;;; LXXII An invitation to Indra
7.72.1 Rise up and look upon the share of Indra fixt by ritual use. Whether ye poured libation dressed or took delight in it un- cooked.
7.72.2 Libation is prepared. Come to us, Indra: the Sun hath travelled over half his journey. Friends with their treasures sit around thee, waiting like heads of houses for their wandering chieftain.
7.72.3 Dressed in the udder and on fire, I fancy; well dressed, I fancy, is this new oblation. Quaff thickened milk of noon's libation, Indra, well pleased, O Thunderer, famed for many an exploit!
;;; LXXIII An invitation to the Asvins
7.73.1 Inflamed is Agni, Heroes! charioteer of heaven. The caldron boils: the meath is drained to be your food. For we, O Asvins, singers sprung from many a house, invite you to be present at our banquetings.
7.73.2 Asvins, the fire is all aglow: your caldron hath been heated;. come! Here, even now, O Heroes, are the milch-kine milked. The priests, ye mighty ones! rejoice.
7.73.3 Pure with the Gods is sacrifice with cry of Hail! That is the Asvins' cup whence Gods are wont to drink. Yea, the Immortal Ones accept it, one and all, and come to kiss that cup with the Gandharva's mouth.
7.73.4 Milk, molten butter offered when the mornings break,--this is your portion, Asvins! Come ye hitherward. Lords of the brave, balm-lovers, guards of sacrifice, drink ye the warm libation in the light of heaven.
7.73.5 Let the warm drink approach you with its Hotar-priest: let the Adhvaryu come to you with store of milk. Come, O ye Asvins, taste the meath that hath been drained, drink of the milk provided by this radiant cow.
7.73.6 Come hither, quickly come, thou milker of the kine; into the caldron pour milk of the radiant cow. Most precious Savitar hath looked upon the heaven. After Dawn's going-forth he sends his light abroad.
7.73.7 I invocate this milch-cow good for milking, so that the milker, deft of hand, may milk her. May Savitar give goodliest stimulation. The caldron hath been warmed. Let him proclaim it.
7.73.8 She, sovran of all treasures, is come hither yearning in spirit for her calf, and lowing. May this cow yield her milk for both the Asvins, and may she prosper to our great advantage.
7.73.9 As dear house-friend, guest welcome in the dwelling, to this our sacrifice come thou who knowest. And, Agni, having scattered all assailants, bring to us the posses- sions of our foemen.
7.73.10 Show thyself strong for mighty bliss, O Agni! Most excellent be thine effulgent splendours! Make easy to maintain our household lordship, and overcome the might of those who hate us.
7.73.11 Fortunate mayst thou be with goodly pasture, and may we also be exceeding wealthy. Feed on the grass, O Cow, at every season, and, coming hither, drink the limpid water.
;;; LXXIV A charm to cure pustules, sores, or scrofulous swellings (apachitas)
7.74.1 Black is the mother, we have heard, from whom the red-hued Pustules sprang. With the divine ascetic's root I pierce and penetrate them all.
7.74.2 I pierce the foremost one of these, I perforate the middlemost, And here I cut the hindermost asunder like a lock of hair.
7.74.3 With spell that Tvashtar sent to us I have dispelled thy jealousy. We mitigate and pacify the anger that thou feltest, Lord!
7.74.4 Lord of religious rites, by law, anointed, shine thou forth here for ever friendly-minded. So may we all with children, Jatavedas! worship and humbly wait on thee enkindled.
;;; LXXV A blessing on cows
7.75.1 Let not a thief or wicked man possess you: let not the dart of Rudra come anear you, Prolific, shining in the goodly pasture, drinking at pleasant pools the limpid water.
7.75.2 Ye know the place and rest content, close-gathered, called by many a name. Come to me, Goddesses, with Gods Bedew with streams of fatness us, this cattle-pen, and all this place.
;;; LXXVI A charm to cure scrofulous pustules and scrofula
7.76.1 Rapidly dropping, quick to drop, more evil than the evil ones, More sapless than a dried-up bone, swifter than salt to melt away.
7.76.2 Pustules that rise upon the neck, Pustules upon the shoulder- joints, Pustules that, falling of themselves, spring up on every twofold limb:
7.76.3 I have expelled and banished all Scrofula harboured in the head, And that which bores the breast-bone through, and that which settles in the sole.
7.76.4 Scrofula flies borne on by wings: it penerates and holds the man. Here is the cure of either kind, the chronic and the transient.
7.76.5 We know thine origin, Scrofula! know whence thou, Scrofula, art born. How hast thou then struck this man here, him in whose house we sacrifice?
7.76.6 Boldly drink Soma from the beaker, Indra! hero in war for treasure! Vritra-slayer. Fill thyself full at the mid-day libation: thyself possessing riches grant us riches.
;;; LXXVII An incantation against an enemy
7.77.1 Ye Maruts, full of fiery heat, accept this offering brought for you To help us, ye who slay the foe.
7.77.2 Maruts, the man who filled with rage against us beyond our thoughts would harm us, O ye Vasus, May he be tangled in the toils of Mischief: smite ye him down with your most flaming weapon.
7.77.3 Each year come, friends to man, the tuneful Maruts, dwelling in spacious mansions, trooped together. Exhilarating, gladdening full of fiery heat, may they deliver us from binding bonds of sin.
;;; LXXVIII A charm for a prince's prosperity
7.78.1 I free thee from the cord, I loose the bond, I loose the fastening. Even here, perpetual, Agni, wax thou strong.
7.78.2 I with celestial prayer appoint thee, Agni, maintainer of this man in princely powers. Here brightly shine for us with wealth: declare thou to Gods this favoured giver of oblations.
;;; LXXIX A hymn to the New Moon
7.79.1 Night of the New-born Moon, whatever fortune the Gods who dwell with greatness have assigned thee, Therewith fulfil our sacrifice, all-baunteous! Blessed One, grant us wealth with manly offspring.
7.79.2 I am the New Moon's Night, the good and pious are my in- habitants, these dwell within me. In me have Gods of both the spheres, and Sadhyas, with Indra as their chief, all met together.
7.79.3 The Night hath come, the gatherer of treasures, bestowing strength, prosperity, and riches. To New Moon's Night let us present oblation: pouring out strength, with milk hath she come hither.
7.79.4 Night of New Moon! ne'er hath been born another than thou embracing all these forms and natures, May we have what we longed for when we brought thee obla- tions: may we be the lords of riches.
;;; LXXX A hymn to the Full Moon
7.80.1 Full in the front, full rearward, from the middle the Full Moon's Night hath conquered in the battle. In her: may we, dwelling with Gods and greatness, feast in the height of heaven, on strengthening viands.
7.80.2 To him, the Full Moon's mighty Bull, we pay our solemn sacri- fice. May he bestow upon us wealth unwasting, inexhaustible.
7.80.3 No one but thou, Prajapati, none beside thee, pervading, gave to all these forms their being. Grant us our hearts' desire when we invoke thee: may we have store of riches in possession.
7.80.4 First was the Full Moon meet for adoration among the days and in the nights' deep darkness. Into thy heaven, O Holy One, have entered those pious men who honour thee with worship.
;;; LXXXI A hymn to the New Moon
7.81.1 Forward and backward by their wondrous power move these two youths, disporting, round the ocean. One views all living things, and thou, the other, art born again arranging times and seasons.
7.81.2 Thou art re-born for ever new: thou marchest, ensign of days, in forefront of the mornings. Marching thou dealest to the Gods their portion. Thou lengthe- nest, Moon! the days of man's existence.
7.81.3 O spray of Soma, Lord of Wars! all-perfect verily art thou. Make me all-perfect, Beauteous One! in riches and in progeny.
7.81.4 Thou art the New Moon, fair to see, thou art complete in every part. May I be perfect, fully blest in every way in steeds and kine, in children, cattle, home, and wealth.
7.81.5 Inflate thee with his vital breath who hathes us and whom we detest. May we grow rich in steeds and kine, in children, cattle, houses, wealth.
7.81.45 With that unwasting stalk which Gods, unwasting Gods, in- crease and eat, May Varuna, Brihaspati, and Indra, the Lords and Guardians of the world, increase us.
;;; LXXXII In praise of Agni
7.82.1 Sing with fair laud the combat for the cattle. Bestow upon us excellent possessions. Lead to the Gods the sacrifice we offer: let streams of oil flow pure and full of sweetness.
7.82.2 Agni I first appropriate with power, with splendour, and with might. I give myself children and lengthened life, with Hail! take Agni to myself.
7.82.3 Even here do thou, O Agni, stablish wealth: let not oppressors injure thee by thinking of thee first. Light be thy task of ruling, Agni, with, thy power: may he who worships thee wax strong, invincible.
7.82.4 Agni hath looked upon the spring of Morning, looked on the days, the earliest Jatavedas. So, following the gleams of Morning, Surya hath entered heaven and earth as his possession.
7.82.5 Agni hath looked upon the spring of Mornings, looked on the days, the earliest Jatavedas. So he in countless places hath extended, full against heaven and earth, the beams of Surya.
7.82.6 Butter to thee in heaven thy home, O Agni! Manu this day hath kindled thee with butter. Let the Celestial Daughters bring thee butter: Let cows pour butter forth for thee, O Agni.
;;; LXXXIII A prayer for deliverance from sin and other evils
7.83.1 Stablished amid the waters is, King Varuna, thy golden home. Thence let the Sovran who maintains the statutes loose all bind- ing cords.
7.83.2 Hence free thou us, King Varuna, from each successive bond and tie. As we have cried, O Varuna! have said, The Waters, they are kine, thence set us free, O Varuna.
7.83.3 Loosen the bonds, O Varuna, that hold us, loosen the bond. above, between, and under. So before Aditi may we be sinless under thy favouring auspices, Aditya!
7.83.4 Varuna, free us from all snares that bind us, Varuna's bonds, the upper and the lower. Drive from us evil dream, drive off misfortune: then let us pass into the world of virtue.
;;; LXXXIV A prayer for protection
7.84.1 Holder of sway, shine here refulgent, Agni! invincible immortal Jatavedas. With succours friendly to mankind, auspicious, driving away all maladies, guard our dwelling.
7.84.2 Thou, Indra, lord and leader of the people, wast born for lovely strength and high dominion. Thou dravest off the folk who were unfriendly, and madest for the Gods wide room and freedom.
7.84.3 Like a dread wild beast roaming on the mountain, may he. approach us from the farthest distance. Whetting thy bolt and thy sharp blade, O Indra, crush down our foes and scatter those who hate us.
;;; LXXXV A charm to ensure victory in battle
7.85.1 This very mighty one whom Gods urge onward, the conqueror of cars, ever triumphant, Swift, fleet to battle, with uninjured fellies, even Tarkshya for our weal will we call hither.
;;; LXXXVI The same
7.86.1 Indra the rescuer, Indra the helper, Indra the brave who hears each invocation, Sakra I call, Indra invoked of many. May Indra Maghavan pros- per and bless us.
;;; LXXXVII A prayer to Rudra as Agni
7.87.1 To Rudra in the fire, to him who dwells in floods, to Rudra who hath entered into herbs and plants, To him who formed and fashioned all these worlds, to him this Rudra, yea, to Agni, reverence be paid!
;;; LXXXVIII A charm to cure a snake-bite
7.88.1 Depart! thou art a foe, a foe. Poison with poison hast thou mixt, yea, verily poison hast thou mixt. Go to the serpent: strike him dead.
;;; LXXXIX A prayer for purification and prosperity
7.89.1 The heavenly Waters have I ranged: we have been sated with their dew. Here, Agni, bearing milk, am I. Endow me with the gift of strength.
7.89.2 Endow me with the gift of strength, with children, and a length- ened life. May the Gods mark this prayer of mine, may Indra with the Rishis mark.
7.89.3 Ye Waters, wash away this stain and whatsoever taint be here, Each sinful wrong that I have done and every harmless curse of mine.
7.89.4 Thou art the wood, may I succeed! fuel, may I be glorified! splendour, give splendour unto me.
;;; XC A charm against a rival in love
