7.90.1 Tear thou asunder, as of old, like tangles of a creeping plant. Demolish thou the Dasa's might.
7.90.2 May we with Indra's help divide the gathered treasure of the foe. I, by the law of Varuna, bring down thy pride and wantonness.
7.90.3 Ut virga abeat et feminis innocua fiat, (virga) membri humidi, membri quod verberat penetratque, id quod tentum est laxa, id quod sursum tentum est deorsum tende.
;;; XCI A Prayer for protection
7.91.1 May Indra with his help, Lord of all treasures, be unto us a careful protector. Drive off our foes and give us peace and safety. May we be lords of goodly store of heroes.
;;; XCII A Prayer for protection
7.92.1 May this rich Indra as our good protector keep even far away the men who hate us. May we enjoy his favour, his the holy: may we enjoy his blessed loving-kindness.
;;; XCIII A prayer for success in battle
7.93.1 With Indra's and with Manyu's aid may we subdue our enemies, resistlessly destroying foes.
;;; XCIV A charm to ensure the obedience of subjects
7.94.1 We laid the constant Soma on with constant sacrificial gift, That Indra may make all the tribes unanimous and only ours.
;;; XCV An incantation against an undetected thief
7.95.1 To heaven, as 'twere, have soared this man's two vultures, staggering, dusky hued. The Parcher and the Drier-up, the pair who parch and dry his heart.
7.95.2 I verily have stirred them up like oxen resting after toil. Like two loud-snarling curs, or like two wolves who watch to make their spring:
7.95.3 Like two that thrust, like two that pierce, like two that strike with mutual blows. I bind the conduit of the man or dame who hence hath taken aught.
;;; XCVI An incantation against an undetected thief
7.96.1 The kine are resting in the stall, home to her nest hath flown the bird, The hills are firmly rooted: I have fixed the kidneys in their place.
;;; XCVII Sacrificial formulas
7.97.1 As we have here elected thee, skilled Hotar! to-day as this our sacrifice proceedeth, Come to the firm place, mightiest! yea, come firmly. Knowing the sacrifice, approach the Soma.
7.97.2 With kine connect us, and with spirit, Indra! Lord of Bay Steeds, with princes and with favour, With the God-destined portion of the Brahmans, and the good-will of Gods who merit worship.
7.97.3 The willing Gods whom, God, thou hast brought hither, send thou to their own dwelling-place, O Agni. When ye have eaten and have drunk sweet juices, endow this man with precious wealth, ye Vasus.
7.97.4 Gods, we have made your seats of easy access, who, pleased with me, have come to my libation. Bearing and bringing hitherward your treasures, after the rich warm beverage mount to heaven.
7.97.5 Go to the sacrifiee, go to its master, Sacrifice! To thy birth- place go with Svaha.
7.97.6 This is thy sacrifice with hole hymnal, Lord of the Rite, Svaha! and fraught with vigour.
7.97.7 Vashat to paid and yet unpaid oblations! Ye Gods who know the way, find and pursue it!
7.97.8 Lord of the Mind, lay this our sacrifice in heaven among the Gods. Svaha in heaven! Svaha on earth! Svaha in air! In wind have I paid offerings. Hail!
;;; XCVIII Anointing the sacred grass
7.98.1 Balmed is the Grass with butter and libation, with Indra. gracious Lord, and with the Maruts. Hail! let the sacrifice go forth anointed to Indra with the Gods and Visve Devas.
;;; XCIX The preparation of the altar
7.99.1 Strew thou the Grass, and spread it on the Altar: rob not the sister who is lying yonder. The Hotar's seat is green and golden: these are gold necklets. in the plaee of him who worships.
;;; C A charm against nightmare
7.100.1 I turn away from evil dream, from dream of sin, from indigence. I make the prayer mine inmost friend. Hence! torturing. dreamy phantasies!
;;; CI The same
7.101.1 The food that in a dream I eat is not perceived at early morn. May all that food be blest to me because it is not seen by day.
;;; CII A charm to obtain pardon for an indecent act
7.102.1 When I have worshipped Heaven and Earth, reverenced Firma- ment and Death, I will make water standing up. Let not the Sovrans injure me.
;;; CIII The cry of an unemployed priest
7.103.1 What princely warrior, seeking higher fortune, will free us from this shameful fiend of mischief? What friend of sacrifice? What guerdon-lover? Who winneth: 'mid the Gods a long existence?
;;; CIV A prayer for prosperity
7.104.1 Who will prepare the dappled Cow, good milker, ne'er without calf, whom Varuna gave Atharvan, And, joying in Brihaspati's alliance, arrange according to his will her body?
;;; CV An initiation formula
7.105.1 Leaving humanity behind, making the heavenly word thy choice, With all thy friends address thyself to furthering and guiding men.
;;; CVI A prayer for pardon of sin
7.106.1 Each thoughtless ill that we have done, O Agni, all error in our conduct, Jatavedas! Therefrom do thou, O sapient God, preserve us. May we thy friends, for bliss, have life eternal.
;;; CVII A charm against Cough
7.107.1 The seven bright beams of Surya bring the waters downward from the sky, The streams of ocean: these have made the sting that pained thee drop away.
;;; CVIII A prayer for protection
7.108.1 Whoso by stealth or openly would harm us, a friend who knows us, or a stranger, Agni! May the strange she-fiend armed with teeth attack them: O Agni, theirs be neither home nor children!
7.108.2 Whoso oppresseth us O Jatavedas, asleep or waking, standing still or moving. Accordant with Vaisvanara thy comrade, O Jatavedas, meet them and consume them.
;;; CIX A prayer for success in gambling
7.109.1 My homage to the strong, the brown, the sovran lord among the dice! Butter on Kali I bestow: may he be kind to one like me.
7.109.2 Bear butter to the Apsarases, O Agni, and to the Dice bear dust and sand and water. The Gods delight in both oblations, joying in sacrificial gifts apportioned duly.
7.109.3 The Apsarases take pleasure in the banquet between the Sun and. the libation-holder. With butter let them fill my hands, and give me, to be my prey, the man who plays against me.
7.109.4 Evil be mine opponent's luck! Sprinkle thou butter over us. Strike, as a tree with lightning flash, mine adversary in the game.
7.109.5 The God who found for us this wealth for gambling, to cast the dice and count the winning number, May he accept the sacrifice we offer, and with Gandharvas revel in the banquet.
7.109.6 Fellow-inhabitants, such is your title, for Dice with looks of power support dominion. As such with offerings may we serve you, Indus! May we have riches in our own possession.
7.109.7 As I invoke the Gods at need, as I have lived in chastity, May these, when I have grasped the Dice, the brown, be kind to one like me.
;;; CX A prayer for success in battle
7.110.1 Resistless, Agni, Indra, smite his foemen for the worshipper, For best foe-slayers are ye both.
7.110.2 Agni I call, and Indra, foe-destroyers, swift moving, heroes, Gods who wield the thunder, Through whom they won the light in the beginning, these who have made all worlds their habitation.
7.110.3 The God Brihaspati hath won thy friendly favour with the cup. With hymns, O Indra, enter us for the juice-pouring worshipper.
;;; CXI A prayer for offspring
7.111.1 Belly of Indra art thou, Soma-holder! the very soul of Gods and human beings. Here be the sire of offspring, thine here present! Here be they glad in thee who now are elsewhere.
;;; CXII A prayer for protection and freedom from sin
7.112.1 Radiant with light are Heaven and Earth, whose grace is nigh, whose sway is vast. Seven Goddesses have flowed to us: may they deliver us from woe;
7.112.2 Release me from the curse's bond and plague that comes from Varuna; Free me from Yama's fetter and from every sin against the Gods.
;;; CXIII A woman's incantation against a rival
7.113.1 Rough Plant, thou rough rude parasite, cut thou that man, O Rough and Rude, That thou mayst hinder from his act that man in all his manly strength.
7.113.2 Thou, rugged Plant, art rude and rough, Visha, Vishataki art thou. That thou mayest be cast off by him, as by a bull a barren cow.
;;; CXIV A woman's incantation against a rival
7.114.1 I have extracted from thy sides, I have extracted from thy heart, I have extracted from thy face the strength and splendour that were thine.
7.114.2 Let pain and suffering pass away, let cares and curses vanish. hence. Let Agni slay the fiendish hags, Soma kill bags who trouble us.
;;; CXV A charm against Misfortune
7.115.1 Hence. Evil Fortune! fly away, vanish from this place and from that. We fix thee with an iron hook unto the man who hateth us.
7.115.2 Granting us riches, Savitar! golden-banded, send thou away from us to other regions That Fortune who, flying, abominable, hath, as a creeper climbs* a tree, assailed me.
7.115.3 One and a hundred Fortunes all together are at his birth born with a mortal's body. Of these we send away the most unlucky: keep lucky ones for us, O Jatavedas.
7.115.4 I have disparted these and those like cows who stray on common land. Here let auspicious Fortunes stay: hence have I banished evil ones.
;;; CXVI A charm against Fever
7.116.1 Homage to him the burning one, shaker, exciter, violent! Homage to him the cold who acts according to his ancient will!
7.116.2 May he, the lawless one, who comes alternate or two following days, pass over and possess the frog.
;;; CXVII A charm to ensure prosperity
7.117.1 Come hither, Indra, with bay steeds, joyous, with tails like pea- cock plumes. Let none impede thy way as fowlers stay the bird: pass o'er them as o'er desert lands.
;;; CXVIII A benediction on a warrior
7.118.1 Thy vital parts I cover with thine armour: with immortality King Soma clothe thee! Varuna give thee what is more than ample, and in thy triumph let the Gods be joyful.
;;; I A charm to recover a dying man
8.1.1 Homage to Death the Ender! May thy breathings, inward and outward, still remain within thee. Here stay this man united with his spirit in the Sun's realm, the world of life eternal!
8.1.2 Bhaga hath lifted up this man, and Soma with his filaments, Indra and Agni, and the Gods the Maruts, raised him up to health.
8.1.3 Here is thy spirit, here thy breath, here is thy life, here is thy soul: By a celestial utterance we raise thee from Destruction's bonds.
8.1.4 Up from this place, O man, rise! sink not downward, casting away the bonds of Death that hold thee. Be not thou parted from this world, from sight of Agni and the Sun.
8.1.5 Purely for thee breathe Wind and Matarisvan, and let the Waters rain on thee their nectar. The Sun shall shine with healing on thy body; Death shall have mercy on thee: do not leave us!
8.1.6 Upward must be thy way, O man, not downward: with life and mental vigour I endow thee. Ascend this car eternal, lightly rolling; then full of years shalt thou address the meeting.
8.1.7 Let not thy soul go thither, nor be lost to us: slight not the living, go not where the Fathers are. Let all the Gods retain thee here in safety.
8.1.8 Yearn not for the departed ones, for those who lead men far away. Rise up from darkness into light: come, both thy hands we clasp in ours.
8.1.9 Let not the black dog and the brindled seize thee, two warders of the way sent forth by Yama. Come hither; do not hesitate: with mind averted stay not there.
8.1.10 Forbear to tread this path, for it is awful: that path I speak of which thou hast not travelled. Enter it not, O man; this way is darkness: forward is danger, hitherward is safety.
8.1.11 Thy guardians be the Fires within the Waters, thy guardian be the Fire which men enkindle. Thy guardian be Vaisvanara Jatavedas; let not celestial Fire with lightning burn thee.
8.1.12 Let not the Flesh-Consumer plot against thee: depart thou far away from the Destroyer. Be Heaven and Earth and Sun and Moon thy keepers, and from the dart of Gods may Air protect thee.
8.1.13 May Vigilance and Watchfulness protect thee, Sleepless and Slumberless keep guard above thee! Let Guardian and let Wakeful be thy warders.
8.1.14 Let these be thy preservers, these thy keepers. All hail to these, to these be lowly worship!
8.1.15 May saving Savitar, Vayu, Indra, Dhatar restore thee to com- munion with the living. Let not thy vigour or thy breath forsake thee: we recall thy life.
8.1.16 Let not the fiend with snapping jaws, nor darkness find thee: tongue, holy grass: how shouldst thou perish? May the Adityas and the Vasus, Indra and Agni raise thee and to health restore thee.
8.1.17 The Sky hath raised thee, and the Earth, Prajapati hath raised thee up. The Plants and Herbs with Soma as their King have rescued thee from Death.
8.1.18 Here let this man, O Gods, remain: let him not go to yonder world. We rescue him from Mrityu with a charm that hath a thousand powers.
8.1.19 I have delivered thee from Death. Strength-givers smelt and fashion thee! Let not she-fiends with wild loose locks, or fearful howlers yell at thee.
8.1.20 I have attained and captured thee: thou hast returned restored to youth. Perfect in body: so have I found all thy sight and all thy life.
8.1.21 Life hath breathed on thee; light hath come: darkness hath past away from thee. Far from thee we have buried Death, buried Destruction and: Decline.
;;; II The same
8.2.1 Seize to thyself this trust of life for ever: thine be longevity which nothing shortens. Thy spirit and thy life again I bring thee: die not, nor vanish into mist and darkness.
8.2.2 Come to the light of living men, come hither: I draw thee to a life of hundred autumns. Loosing the bonds of Death, the curse that holds thee, I give thee age of very long duration.
8.2.3 Thy breath have I recovered from the Wind, thy vision from the Sun. Thy mind I stablish and secure within thee: feel in thy members,. use thy tongue, conversing.
8.2.4 I blow upon thee with the breath of bipeds and quadrupeds, as on a fire new-kindled. To thee, O Death, and to thy sight and breath have I paid reverence.
8.2.5 Let this man live, let him not die: we raise him, we recover him. I make for him a healing balm. O Death, forbear to slay this man.
8.2.6 Here for sound health I invocate a living animating plant, Preserving, queller of disease, victorious, full of power and might.
8.2.7 Seize him not, but encourage and release him: here let him stay, though thine, in all his vigour. Bhava and Sarva, pity and protect him: give him full life and drive away misfortunes.
8.2.8 Comfort him, Death, and pity him: let him arise and pass away, Unharmed, with all his members, hearing well, with old, may he through hundred years win profit with his soul.
8.2.9 May the Gods' missile pass thee by. I bring thee safe from the mist: from death have I preserved thee. Far have I banished flesh-consuming Agni: I place a rampart for thy life's protection.
8.2.10 Saving him from that misty path of thine which cannot be defined. From that descent of thine, O Death, we make for him a shield of prayer.
8.2.11 I give thee both the acts of breath, health, lengthened life, and death by age. All Yama's messengers who roam around, sent by Vaivasvata, I chase away.
8.2.12 Far off we drive Malignity, Destruction, Pisachas banqueters on flesh, and Grahi. And all the demon kind, the brood of sin, like darkness, we dispel.
8.2.13 I win thy life from Agni, from the living everlasting Jatavedas. This I procure for thee, that thou, undying, mayst not suffer harm, that thou mayst be content, that all be well with thee.
8.2.14 Gracious to thee be Heaven and Earth, bringing no grief, and drawing nigh! Pleasantly shine the Sun for thee, the Wind blow sweetly to thy heart! Let the celestial Waters full of milk flow happily for thee.
8.2.15 Auspicious be the Plants to thee! I have upraised thee, borne thee from the lower to the upper earth: Let the two Sons of Aditi, the Sun and Moon, protect thee there.
8.2.16 Whatever robe to cover thee or zone thou makest for thyself, We make it pleasant to thy frame: may it be soft and smooth to touch.
8.2.17 When, with a very keen and cleasing razor, our hair and beards thou shavest as a barber, Smoothing our face steal not our vital forces.
8.2.18 Auspicious unto thee be rice and barley, causing no painful sick- ness or consumption, these deliver from calamity.
8.2.19 Thy food, thy drink, whate'er they be corn grown by cultivation, milk, Food eatable, uneatable, I make all poisonless for thee.
8.2.20 We give thee over as a charge to Day and Night, in trust to both. Keep him for me from stingy fiends, from those who fain would feed on him.
8.2.21 A hundred, yea, ten thousand years we give thee, ages two, three, four. May Indra, Agni, all the Gods, with willing favour look on thee.
8.2.22 To Autumn we deliver thee, to Winter, Spring and Summer's care. We trust thee with auspicious years wherein the plants and herbs grow up.
8.2.23 Death is the lord of bipeds, Death is sovran lord of quadrupeds. Away I bear thee from that: Death the ruler: be not thou afraid.
8.2.24 Thou, still uninjured, shalt not die: be not afraid; thou shalt not die. Here where I am men do not die or go to lowest depths of gloom.
8.2.25 Here verily all creatures live, the cow, the horse, the man, the beast, Here where this holy prayer is used, a rampart that protecteth life. Let it preserve thee from thy peers, from incantation, from thy friends.
8.2.26 Live very long, be healthy, be immortal: let not the vital breath forsake thy body.
8.2.27 One and a hundred modes of death, dangers that may be over- come, May Gods deliver thee from this when Agni, dear to all men, bids.
8.2.28 Body of Agni prompt to save, slayer of fiends and foes art thou, Yea, banisher of malady, the healing balm called Putudru.
;;; III A prayer for the destruction of demons
8.3.1 I balm with oil the mighty demon-slayer, to the most famous friend I come for shelter. Enkindled, sharpened by our rites, may Agni protect us in the day and night from evil.
8.3.2 O Jatavedas, armed with teeth of iron, enkindled with thy flame, attack the demons. Seize with thy tongue the foolish gods' adorers: rend, put with- in thy mouth the raw-flesh-eaters.
8.3.3 Apply thy teeth, the upper and the lower, thou who hast both, enkindled and destroying. Roam also in the air, O King, around us, and with thy jaws assail the wicked spirits.
8.3.4 Pierce through the Yatudhana's skin, O Agni; let the destroying dart with fire consume him. Rend his joints, Jatavedas! let the eater of raw flesh, seeking flesh, tear and destroy him.
8.3.5 Where now thou seest, Agni Jatavedas! a Yatudhana, standing still or roaming. Or one that flieth through the air's mid-region, kindled to fury as an archer pierce him.
8.3.6 Bending thy shafts through sacrifices, Agni! dipping thine arrows in the hymn to point them, Pierce to the heart therewith the Yatudhanas, and break their arms uplifted to attack thee.
8.3.7 Rescue the captives also, Jatavedas! yea, those whom Yatudha- nas' spears have captured. Strike down that fiend, blazing before him, Agni! Let spotted carrion-eating kites devour him.
8.3.8 Here tell this forth, O Agni: whosoever is, he himself, or acteth as, a demon, Grasp him, O thou most youthful, with thy fuel: to the Man- Seer's eye give him as booty.
8.3.9 With keen glance guard the sacrifice, O Agni: thou Sage, con- duct it onward to the Vasus. Let not the fiends, O Man-Beholder, harm thee burning against the Rakshasas to slay them.
8.3.10 Look on the fiend, 'mid men, as Man-Beholder: rend thou his three extremities in pieces. Demolish with thy flame his ribs, O Agni: the Yatudhana's root destroy thou triply.
8.3.11 Thrice, Agni, let thy noose surround the demon who with his falsehood injures holy Order. Loud roaring with thy flame, Jatavedas, fetter him in the pre- sense of the singer.
8.3.12 Agni, what curse the pair this day may utter, what rude rough word the worshippers have spoken, Each arrowy taunt sped from the angry spirit,--pierce to the heart therewith the Yatudhanas.
8.3.13 With fervent heat exterminate the demons: destroy the fiends with glow and flame, O Agni. Destroy with fire the foolish gods' adorers: destroy the insatiate fiercely-burning creatures.
8.3.14 May Gods destroy to-day the evil-doer: may uttered curses turn again and strike him. Let arrows pierce the liar in his vitals, and Visva's net enclose the Yatudhana.
8.3.15 The fiend who smears himself with flesh of cattle, with flesh of horses and of human bodies, Who steals the milch-cow's milk away, O Agni,--tear off the heads of such with fiery fury.
8.3.16 Let the fiends steal the poison of the cattle: may Aditi cast off the evil-doers. May the God Savitar give them up to ruin, and be their share of herbs and plants denied them.
8.3.17 The cow gives milk each year, O Man-Beholder: let not the Yatudhana ever taste it. Agni, if one should glut him with the biestings, pierce with thy flame his vitals as he meets thee.
8.3.18 Agni, from days of old thou slayest demons: never have Rakshasas in fight o'ercome thee. Burn up the foolish ones, the flesh-devourers: let none of them escape thy heavenly arrow.
8.3.19 Guard us, O Agni, from above and under, protect us from be- hind and from before us; And may thy flames, most fierce and never wasting, glowing with fervent heat, consume the sinner.
8.3.20 From rear, from front, from under, from above us, Agni, pro- tect us as a sage with wisdom. Guard to old age thy friend as friend eternal: O Agni, as im- mortal, guard us mortals.
8.3.21 Lend thou the worshipper that eye, O Agni, where with thou lookest on the hoof-armed demons. With light celestial in Atharvan's manner burn up the fool who ruins truth with falsehood.
8.3.22 We set thee round us as a fort, victorious Agni! thee, a sage, In conquering colour day by day, destroyer of the treacherous foe.
8.3.23 With deadly poison strike thou back the treacherous brood of Rakshasas, O Agni, with thy sharpened glow, with rays that flash with points of flame.
8.3.24 Agni shines far and wide with lofty splendour, and by his great- ness makes all things apparent. He conquers godless and malign enchantments, and sharpens both his horns to gore the ogres.
8.3.25 Thy two unwasting horns, O Jatavedas, keen-pointed weapons, sharpened by devotion With these transfix the wicked-souled Kimidin, with fierce flame, Jatavedas! when he meets thee.
8.3.26 Bright, radiant, meet to be adored, immortal with refulgent glow, Agni drives Rakshasas away.
;;; IV Imprecations on demons
8.4.1 Indra and Soma, burn, destroy the demon foe! Send downward, O ye Bulls, those who add gloom to gloom. Annihilate the fools, slay them and burn them up: chase them away from us, pierce the voracious fiends.
8.4.2 Let sin, Indra and Soma! round the wicked boil, like as a cald- ron set amid the flames of fire. Against the foe of prayer, eater of gory flesh, the fearful-eyed Kimidin, keep perpetual hate.
8.4.3 Indra and Soma, plunge the wicked in the depth, yea, cast them into darkness that hath no support, So that not one of them may ever thence return: so may your wrathful might prevail and conquer them.
8.4.4 Indra and Soma, hurl your deadly crushing bolt down on the wicked fiend from heaven and from the earth. Yea, fashion from the big clouds your celestial dart wherewith ye burn to death the waxing demon race.
8.4.5 Indra and Soma, cast ye downward from the sky your deadly bolts of stone burning with fiery flame, Eternal, scorching darts. Plunge the voracious fiends within the depth, and let them pass without a sound.
8.4.6 Indra and Soma, let this hymn control you both, even as the girth encompasses two vigorous steeds The song of praise which I with wisdom offer you. Do ye, as Lords of men, animate these my prayers.
8.4.7 In your impetuous manner think ye both thereon: destroy those evil spirits, kill the treacherous fiends. Indra and Soma, let the wicked have no bliss whoso at any time- attacks and injures us.
8.4.8 Whoso accuses me with words of falsehood when I pursue my way with guileless spirit, May he, the speaker of untruth, be, Indra! like water which the hollowed hand compresses.
8.4.9 Those who destroy, as is their wont, the simple, and with their evil natures harm the righteous, May Soma give them over to the serpent, or to the lap of Nirriti consign them.
8.4.10 O Agni, whosoever seeks to injure the essence of our food, kine, steeds, or bodies, May he, the adversary, thief, and robber, sink to destruction,. both himself and offspring.
8.4.11 May he be swept away, himself and children; may all the three earths press him down beneath them. May his fair glory, O ye Gods, be blighted, who in the day or night would fain destroy us.
8.4.12 The prudent finds it easy to distinguish the true and false: their words oppose each other. Of these two that which is the true and honest Soma protects, and brings the false to nothing.
8.4.13 Never doth Soma aid and guide the wicked or him who falsely claims the Warrior's title. He slays the fiend and him who speaks untruly: both lie entan- gled in the noose of Indra.
8.4.14 As if I worshipped deities of falsehood, or thought vain thoughts about the Gods, O Agni! Why art thou angry with us, Jatavedas? Destruction fall on those who lie against thee!
8.4.15 So may I die this day if I have harassed any man's life, or if I be a demon. Yea, may he lose all his ten sons together who with false tongue hath called me Yatudhana.
8.4.16 May Indra slay him with a mighty weapon, and let the vilest of all creatures perish, The fiend who says that he is pure, who calls me a demon though devoid of demon nature.
8.4.17 She too who wanders like an owl at night-time, hiding her body in her guile and malice, May she fall downward into endless caverns. May press-stones with loud ring destroy the demons.
8.4.18 Spread out, ye Maruts, search among the people: seize ye and grind the Rakshasas to pieces, Who fly abroad, transformed to birds, at night-time, and sully and pollute our holy worship.
8.4.19 Hurl down from heaven thy bolt of stone, O Indra: sharpen it, Maghavan, made keen by Soma. Forward, behind, and from above and under, smite down the demons with thy rocky weapon.
8.4.20 They fly, the demon dogs, and, bent on mischief, fain would they harm indomitable Indra. Sakra makes sharp his weapon for the wicked: now let him cast his bolt at fiendish wizards.
8.4.21 Indra hath ever been the fiends' destroyer who spoil oblations of the Gods' invokers. Yea, Sakra, like an axe that splits the timber, assails and sma- shes them like earthen vessels.
8.4.22 Destroy the fiend shaped like an owl or owlet, destroy him in. the form of dog or cuckoo. Destroy him shaped as eagle or as vulture: as with a stone, O Indra, crush the demon.
8.4.23 Let not the fiend of witchcraft-workers reach us: may Dawn. drive off the couples of Kimidins. Earth keep us safe from earthly woe and trouble! From grief that comes from heaven Mid-air preserve us!
8.4.24 Indra destroy the demon, male and female, joying and triumph- ing in arts of magic! Let the fools' gods with bent necks fall and perish, and see no. more the Sun when he arises.
8.4.25 Look, each one, hither, look around. Indra and Soma, watch ye well. Cast forth your weapon at the fiends: against the sorcerers hurl your bolt.
;;; V A charm accompanying investiture with an amulet
8.5.1 Upon the strong is bound the strong, this magic cord, this Amu- let, Potent, foe-slayer, served by valiant heroes, happy and fortu- nate defence.
8.5.2 This Charm, foe-slayer, served by many heroes, strong, power- ful, victorious, and mighty, goes bravely forth to meet and ruin witchcraft.
8.5.3 With this same Amulet wise Indra routed the Asuras, with this he slaughtered Vritra, With this he won this pair, both Earth and Heaven, and made the sky's four regions his possession.
8.5.4 May this encircling magic cord, this Amulet of Sraktya wood, Mighty, subduing enemies, keep us secure on every side.
8.5.5 This Agni hath declared, Soma declared it, Brihaspati, and Savitar, and Indra. So may these Gods whom I have set before me oppose with saving charms and banish witchcraft.
8.5.6 I have obscured the heaven and earth, yea, and the daylight and the sun. So may these Gods whom I have set before me oppose with saving charms and banish witchcraft.
8.5.7 Whoever for his armour takes an amulet of the Sraktya tree, Like the Sun risen up to heaven, quells witchcraft with superior might.
8.5.8 With Amulet of Sraktya wood, as with a thoughtful Rishi's aid, In every fight have I prevailed; I smite the foes and Rakshasas.
8.5.9 All witchcraft of Angirases,"all witchcraft wrought by Asuras, All witchcraft self-originate, and all that others have prepared, May these depart to both remotest spaces, past ninety ample water-floods.
8.5.10 May the Gods bind the Charm on him for armour, Indra, and Vishnu, Savitar Rudra, Agni, Prajapati, sublimest Parameshlhin, Viraj, Vaisvanara, and all the Rishis.
8.5.11 Thou art the chief of all the plants, even as a bull among the beasts. A tiger of the beasts of prey. Him whom we sought for have we found, him lying near in wait for us.
8.5.12 A tiger verily is he, he is a lion, and a bull, Subduer of his foes is he, the man who wears this Amulet.
8.5.13 No mortal beings slay him, no Gandharvas, no Apsarases; O'er all the regions he is king, the man who wears this Amulet.
8.5.14 Kasyapa formed and fashioned thee, Kasyapa raised and sent thee forth. Indra wore thee, and, wearing thee, won in the wrestling-match with man. The Amulet of boundless might the Gods have made a coat of mail.
8.5.15 Whoever would destroy thee with Diksha-rites, sacrifices, spells, Meet him and smite him, Indra! with thy hundred-knotted thunderbolt.
8.5.16 Verily let this Amulet, circular, potent, conquering, Happy and fortunate defence, preserve thy children and thy wealth.
8.5.17 Brave Indra, set before us light, peace and security from below, Peace and security from above, peace and security from behind.
8.5.18 My coat of mail is Heaven and Earth, my coat of mail is Day and Sun: A coat of mail may Indra and Agni and Dhatar grant to me.
8.5.19 Not all the Gods may pierce, all leagued together, the vast strong shield which Indra gives, and Agni. May that great shield on all sides guard my body, that to full old my life may be extended.
8.5.20 Let the Gods' Charm be bound on me to keep me safe from every ill. Come ye and enter all within this pillar, the safe-guard of the body, thrice-defended.
8.5.21 In this let Indra lay a store of valour: approach ye Gods, and enter it together, For his long life, to last a hundred autumns, that to full age his days may be extended.
8.5.22 Lord of the clan who brings, us bliss, fiend-slayer, queller of the foe, May he, the conqueror, ne'er subdued, may Indra bind the Charm on thee, Bull, Soma-drinker, he who gives us peace. May he protect thee round about, by night and day on every, side.
;;; VI A charm to exercise evil spirits who beset women
8.6.1 Let neither fiend of evil name, Alinsa, Vatsapa, desire Thy pair of husband-wooers which thy mother cleansed when, thou wast born.
8.6.2 Palala, Anupalala, Sarku, Koka, Malimlucha, Palijaka Vavri- vasas and Asresha, Rikshagriva and Pramilin.
8.6.3 Approach not, come not hitherward: creep not thou in-between her thighs. I set, to guard her, Baja, that which chases him of evil name.
8.6.4 Durnama and Sunama both are eager to converse with her. We drive away Arayas: let Sunama seek the women-folk,
8.6.5 The black and hairy Asura, and Stambaja and Tundika, Arayas from this girl we drive, from bosom, waist, and parts below.
8.6.6 Sniffer, and Feeler, him who eats raw flesh, and him who licks his lips, Arayas with the tails of dogs, the yellow Baja hath destroyed.
8.6.7 Whoever, in thy brother's shape or father's comes to thee in sleep, Let Baja rout and chase them like eunuchs with woman's head- dress on.
8.6.8 Whoever steals to thee asleep or thinks to harm thee when awake,-- These hath it banished, as the Sun travelling round drives shade away.
8.6.9 Whoever causeth her to lose her child or bear untimely fruit,-- Destroy him, O thou Plant, destroy the slippery fiend who lusts for her.
8.6.10 Those who at evening, with the bray of asses, dance around the house, Kukshilas, and Kusfilas, and Kakubhas, Srimas, Karumas, These with thine odour, O thou Plant, drive far away to every side.
8.6.11 Kukundhas and Kukurabhas who dress themselves in hides and skins, Who dance about like eunuchs, who raise a wild clamour in the wood, all these we banish far away.
8.6.12 All those who cannot bear the Sun who warms us yonder from the sky, Arayas with the smell of goats, malodorous, with bloody mouths, the Makakas we drive afar.
8.6.13 All those who on their shoulders bear a head of monstrous magnitude, Who pierce the women's loins with pain,--those demons, Indra drive away!
8.6.14 Those, bearing horns upon their hands, who first of all approach the brides; Standing in ovens, laughing loud, those who in bushes flash forth light, all these we banish hence away.
8.6.15 Those who have retroverted toes, and heels and faces in the front, Khalajas, Sakadhumajas, Urundas, all the Matmatas, impotent Kumbhamushkas, these, Drive thou, O Brahmanaspati, far from this girl with vigilance.
8.6.16 Sightless and with distorted eyes, impotent. woman less be they. O Healing Plant, cast each away who, not her husband, would approach this woman wedded to her lord.
8.6.17 The Bristly-haired, the Maniac-haired, the Biter, and the Groper-fiend, The Creeper-near, the Copper-hued, the Snouty, and the Saluda, With foot and heel kick over, as a hasty cow her milking-pan.
8.6.18 If one should touch thy coming babe or kill thine infant newly born, The yellow Plant with mighty bow shall pierce him even to the heart.
8.6.19 Those who kill infants unawares, and near the new-made mothers lie, Let Pinga chase the amorous Gandharvas as wind chases cloud.
8.6.20 Let it maintain the genial seed: let the laid embryo rest secure. Let both strong Healers, to be worn within the girdle, guard the babe.
8.6.21 From the Kimidin, for thy lord and children, Pinga shield thee well, From Sayaka, and Nagnaka, Tangalva, and Pavinasa.
8.6.22 From the five-footed, fingerless, from the four-eyed, the double- faced, From the Close-creeper, from the Worm, from the Quick-roller guard her well.
8.6.23 Those who eat flesh uncooked, and those who eat the bleeding flesh of men, Feeders on babes unborn, long-haired, far from this place we banish these.
8.6.24 Shy slinkers from the Sun, as slinks a woman from her husband's sire, Deep down into the heart of these let Baja and let Pinga pierce.
8.6.25 Pinga, preserve the babe at birth, make not the boy a female child. Let not Egg-eaters mar the germs: drive the Kimidins far away.
8.6.26 Sterility, and infants' death, and weeping that announceth woe, Dear! lay them on the fiend as thou wouldst pluck a garland from a tree.
;;; VII A charm to restore a sick man to health
8.7.1 The tawny-coloured, and the pale, the variegated and the red, The dusky-tinted, and the black,--all Plants we summon hither- ward.
8.7.2 This man let them deliver from Consumption which the Gods have sent. The father of these Herbs was Heaven, their mother Earth, the Sea their root.
8.7.3 The Waters are the best, and heavenly Plants. From every limb of thine have they removed Consumption caused by sin.
8.7.4 I speak to Healing Herbs spreading, and bushy, to creepers, and to those whose sheath is single, I call for thee the fibrous and the reed-like, and branching. Plants, dear to the Visve Devas, powerful, giving life to men.
8.7.5 The conquering strength, the power and might which ye, victo- rious Plants, possess, Therewith deliver this man here from this Consumption, O ye Plants: so I prepare the remedy.
8.7.6 The living Plant that giveth life, that driveth malady away, Arundhatr, the rescuer, strengthening, rich a sweets I call, to free this man from scath and harm.
8.7.7 Hitherward let the sapient come, the friendly sharers o f my speech. That we may give this man relief and raise him from his evil plight.
8.7.8 Germ of the Waters, Agni's food, Plants ever growing fresh and new, Sure, healing, bearing thousand names, let them be all collected here.
8.7.9 Let Plants whose soul is water, girt with Avakas, piercing with their sharp horns expel the malady.
8.7.10 Strong, antidotes of poison, those releasers, free from Varuna, And those that drive away Catarrh, and those that frustrate magic arts, let all those Plants come hitherward.
8.7.11 Let purchased Plants of mightier power, Plants that are praised for excellence. Here in this village safely keep cattle and horses, man and beast.
8.7.12 Sweet is their root, sweet are these Plants' top branches, sweet also is their intermediate portion; Sweet is their foliage, and sweet their blossom, combined with sweetness is their taste of Amrit: food, fatness let them yield, with kine preceding.
8.7.13 These Plants that grow upon the earth, whate'er their number and their size, Let these with all their thousand leaves free me from Death and misery.
8.7.14 May the Plants' Tiger-amulet, protective, guardian from the curse, Beat off the brood of demons, drive all maladies afar from us.
8.7.15 Before the gathered Plants they fly and scatter, as though a lion's roar or fire dismayed them. Expelled by Plants, let men's and kine's Consumption pass from us to the navigable rivers.
8.7.16 Emancipated from the sway of Agni, of Vaisvanara, go, covering the earth, ye Plants whose ruler is Vanaspati.
8.7.17 May these be pleasant to our heart, auspicious, rich in store of milk, These Plants of the Angirases which grow on mountains and on plains.
8.7.18 The Plants I know myself, the plants that with mine eye I look upon, Plants yet unknown, and those we know, wherein we find that power is stored,
8.7.19 Let all the congregated Plants attend and mark mine utterance, That we may rescue this man here and save him from severe distress.
8.7.20 Asvattha, Darbha, King of Plants, is Soma, deathless sacrifice Barley and Rice are healing balms, the sons of Heaven who never die.
8.7.21 Lift yourselves up, ye Healing Plants, loud is the thunder's crash and roar. When with full flow Parjanya, ye Children of Prisni! blesseth; you.
8.7.22 We give the essence of that stream of nectar of this man to drink: So I prepare a remedy that he may live a hundred years.
8.7.23 Well doth the wild boar know a Plant, the mungoose knows the Healing Herb. I call, to aid this man, the Plants which Serpents and Gandhar- vas know.
8.7.24 Plants of Angirases which hawks, celestial Plants which eagles. know; Plants known to swans and lesser fowl, Plants known to all the birds that fly. Plants that are known to sylvan beasts,--I call them all to aid this man.
8.7.25 The multitude of herbs whereon the Cows whom none may slaughter feed, all that are food for goats and sheep, So many Plants, brought hitherward, give shelter and defence to thee!
8.7.26 Hitherward unto thee I bring the Plants that cure all maladies, All Plants wherein physicians have discovered health-bestowing power.
8.7.27 Let Plants with flower and Plants with bud, the fruitful and the fruitless, all, Like children of one mother, yield their stores for this man's perfeet health.
8.7.28 From the Five-arrowed, from the Ten-arrowed have I delivered thee, Freed thee from Yama's fetter and from all offence against the Gods,
;;; VIII Imprecations directed against a hostile army
8.8.1 Indra the Shaker shake them up, brave, hero, fortdemolisher, That into thousand fragments we may strike the armies of our foes!
8.8.2 Let Putirajju with her breath corrupt and putrefy that host, And terror smite our foemen's heart when fire and smoke are seen afar.
8.8.3 Asvattha, rend those men; do thou devour them quickly, Khadira! Like reeds let them be broken through, down-smitten by a lifted rush.
8.8.4 Let Parushahva make them reeds, and let the bulrush strike them down: Bound in a mighty net let them break quickly like an arrow's shaft.
8.8.5 Air was the net; the poles thereof were the great quarters of the sky: Sakra therewith enveloped and cast on the ground the Dasyus' host.
8.8.6 Verily mighty is the net of mighty Sakra rich in wealth: Therewith press all the foemen down so that not one of them escape!
8.8.7 Great is thy net, brave Indra, thine the mighty match for a thousand, Lord of Hundred Powers! Holding them, with his host, therewith hath Indra slaughtered Dasyus a hundred, thousand, myriad, hundred millions.
8.8.8 This world so mighty was the net of Sakra, of the Mighty One: With this, the net of Indra, I envelop all those men with gloom.
8.8.9 Great weakness and misfortune, pain which words can never charm away, Languor, fatigue, bewilderment, with these I compass all the foes.
8.8.10 I give those foemen up to Death: bound in the bonds of Death are they. I bind and carry them away to meet Death's wicked messengers.
8.8.11 Bear them away, Death's messengers! envoys of Yama! bind them fast. More than a thousand be their slain: the club of Bhava pierce them through!
8.8.12 Forth go the Sadhyas in their might bearing one netpole raised aloft. One pole the Rudras carry, one the Vasus, and the Adityas one.
8.8.13 The Visve Devas from above shall come depressing it with might, And in the midst the Angirases, slaying the mighty host, shall go.
8.8.14 Trees of the forest, trees that bear flower and fruit, and herbs and plants, Quadruped, biped send I forth that they may strike this army dead,
8.8.15 Gandharvas, and Apsarases, Gods, Serpents, Fathers, Holy Men, Seen and unseen, I send them forth that they may strike this army dead.
8.8.16 Here spread are snares of Death wherefrom thou, once within them, ne'er art freed: Full many a thousand of the host yonder this horn shall smite and slay.
8.8.17 The Gharma hath been warmed with fire: this Homa slays a thousand men. Let Bhava, Prisnibahu, and Sarva destroy that armament.
8.8.18 Their portion be the fire of Death, hunger, exhaustion, slaughter, fear. With your entangling snares and nets, Sarva and Indra! slay that host.
8.8.19 Fly, conquered, in alarm, ye foes, run driven by the spell away! Let not one man escape of those when routed by Brihaspati.
8.8.20 Down fall their weapons on the ground: no strength be theirs to point a shaft: Then in their dreadful terror let their arrows wound their vital parts.
8.8.21 Let Heaven and Earth roar out in wrath against them, and Air with all the Deities in concert, Let them not find a surety or a refuge, but torn away go down to Death together.
8.8.22 The mules of the Gods' car are heaven's four quarters; their hooves are sacred cakes, the air its body. Its sides are Heaven and Earth, its reins the Seasons, Voice is its hood, its grooms are sky's mid-regions.
8.8.23 Year is the car, Full Year the seat for driving, Viraj the pole, the chariot's front is Agni, Indra the warrior, and the Moon the driver.
8.8.24 Hence conquer, conquer, Hail! be thou the victor! Let these be conquerors and those be conquered. Good luck to these, ill luck to those men yonder! With the dark-blue-and-red our foes I cover.
;;; IX An enunciation of cosmogonical, ritual, and metrical doctrine
8.9.1 Whence were these two produced? which was that region?' From what world, from which earth had they their being? Calves of Viraj, these two arose from water. I ask thee of these twain, who was their milker.
8.9.2 He who prepared a threefold home, and lying there made the water bellow through his greatness, Calf of Viraj, giving each wish fulfilment, made bodies for him- self far off, in secret.
8.9.3 Which are the three, the mighty three, whereof the fourth divides the voice, This may the Brahman know by prayer and fervour, whereto belongs the one, whereto the other.
8.9.4 Out of the Brihat as the sixth five Salmons have been fashioned forth: From Brihati was Brihat formed: whence was the Brihati com- posed?
8.9.5 On measure Brihati is based, and measure on the measurer: From magic might came magic might, from magic might came Matali.
8.9.6 Vaisvanara's image is the sky above us, so far as Agni forced both spheres asunder. Thence from that region as the sixth come praise-songs, and every sixth day hence again go upward.
8.9.7 We, Kagyapa! six present Rishis, ask thee--for thou hast prov- ed things tried and meet for trial They call Viraj the Father of Devotion: tell her to us thy friends in all her figures.
8.9.8 She whom, advancing, sacrifices follow, and when she takes her station stand beside her, By whose control and hest the spirit moveth, she is Viraj, in highest heaven, O Rishis.
8.9.9 Breathless, she moves by breath of living creatures, Svaraj pre- cedes, Viraj comes closely after. Some men behold her not, and some behold her, Viraj meet- shaped, who thinks of all existence.
8.9.10 Who hath perceived Viraj's duplication, perceived her seasons and her rule and practice? Who knows her steps, how oft, how far extended, who knows her home and number of her dawnings?
8.9.11 She here who first of all sent forth her lustre moves onward resting on these lower creatures. Exalted power and might are stored within her: the woman hath prevailed, the new-come mother.
8.9.12 Both Dawns on wings of song, with rich adornment, move on together to their common dwelling. Surya's two wives, unwasting, most prolific, knowing their way, move, rich in light, together.
8.9.13 The three have passed along the path of Order--three warm libations have regarded offspring One quickens progeny, one strengthens vigour, and one protects the kingdom of the pious.
8.9.14 She who was fourth was made by Agni, Soma, and Rishis as. they formed both halves of worship, Gayatri, Trishtup, Jagati, Anushtup, Brihadarki lightening the sacrificer.
8.9.15 Five milkings answer to the fivefold dawning, five seasons to the cow who bears five titles. The five sky-regions made fifteen in number, one head have these to one sole world directed.
8.9.16 Six Elements arose, first-born of Order: the six-day time is carried by six Samans. Six-yoked the plough is, as each trace is numbered: they call both broad ones six; six, Earth and Heaven.
8.9.17 They call the cold months six, and six the hot ones. Which, tell us, of the seasons is redundant? Seven sages, eagles, have sat down together: seven metres match the seven Consecrations.
8.9.18 Seven are the Homas, seven the logs for burning, seven are the streams of mead, and seven the seasons. Into the world have come seven streams of butter; those we have heard of as the Seven Vultures.
8.9.19 Seven metres, by four syllables increasing, each of the seven founded upon another How are the hymns of praise on these supported, and how are these imposed upon the praise-songs?
8.9.20 How hath the Gayatri filled out three triads? On the fifteen how is the Trishtup moulded, Jagati fashioned on the three-and-thirty? How is Anushtup formed? how Ekavinsa?
8.9.21 Eight Elements sprang up, first born of Order: the Priests divine are eight in number, Indra! Eight are the wombs of Aditi, eight her children; for the eighth night is the libation destined.
8.9.22 So planning bliss for you have I come hither to win your friendship: kind am I, and gracious. Born from one source, propitious is your wisdom: knowing full well to all of you it cometh.
8.9.23 To Indra eight, to Yama six, seven to the Rishis, seven to each: The number five accompanies waters and men and healing herbs.
8.9.24 The Heifer, all his own, poured forth for Indra control and milk at her first time of milking; And he then satisfied the four divisions, the Gods and men and Asuras and Rishis.
8.9.25 Who is the Cow? Who is the Single Rishi? What is the law, what are the benedictions? What on the earth is the one only Spirit? Which of the number is the Single Season?
8.9.26 One is the Cow, one is the Single Spirit, one is the law, single are benedictions. The Spirit dwelling on the earth is single: the Single Season never is transcended.
;;; X A glorification of the mystical abstraction Viraj
8.10.1 Viraj at first was This. At birth all feared her; the thought, She will become this All, struck terror.
8.10.2 She rose, the Garhapatya fire she entered. He who knows this becomes lord of a household, performer of domestic sacri- fices.
8.10.3 She mounted up, the Eastward fire she entered. He who knows this becomes the Gods' beloved, and to his call they come when she invokes them.
8.10.4 She mounted up, the Southward fire she entered. He who knows this becomes a fit performer of sacrifice, meet for honour, shelter-giver.
8.10.5 She mounted up, she entered the Assembly. He who knows this becomes polite and courtly, and people come as guests to his assembly.
8.10.6 She mounted up, she passed within the meeting. He who knows this becomes fit for the meeting, and to his hall of meeting come the people.
8.10.7 She mounted up, she entered Consultation. Whoso knows this is fit to be consulted, and to his consultation come the people.
8.10.8 She mounted up, and, into four divided, she took her station in the air's mid-region.
8.10.9 Of her the Gods and men said, This she knoweth. That we may both have life let us invoke her.
8.10.10 Thus did they cry to her:
8.10.11 Come, Strength! come, Food! come, Charmer! come, Free- giver!
8.10.12 Her calf, her well-beloved calf, was Indra: Gayatri was her rope, the cloud her udder.
8.10.13 Two teats she had, Rathantara and Brihat, two, Yajnayajniya and Vamadevya.
8.10.14 With the Rathantara the Gods milked from her the Plants, and all the wide expanse with Brihat.
8.10.15 They drew the Waters forth with Vamadevya, with Yajnayaj- niya they milked out worship.
8.10.16 For him who knoweth this, Rathantara poureth out Plants, and Brihat yieldeth wide expansion.
8.10.17 Waters from Vamdevya come, from Yajnayajniya sacrifice.
8.10.18 She rose, she came unto the tress: they killed her. A year went by and she again existed. Hence in a year the wounds of trees heal over. He who knows this sees his loathed rival wounded.
8.10.19 She mounted up, she came unto the Fathers: they killed her: in a month she re-existed. Hence men give monthly offerings to the Fathers: who knows this, knows the path which they have trodden.
8.10.20 She rose, she came unto the Gods: they killed her: but in a fortnight she again was living. Fortnightly, hence, men serve the Gods with Vasat! Who knows this knows the way which Gods pass over.
8.10.21 She mounted up, she came to men: they killed her Presently she regained her life and being. Hence on both days to men they bring and offer--who knows this--near-seated in the dwelling.
8.10.22 She rose, approached the Asuras: they called her: their cry was, Come, O Maya, come thou hither. Her dear calf was Virochana Prahradi: her milking vessel was a. pan of iron. Dvimurdha Artvya milked her, yea, this Maya, The Asuras depend for life on Maya. He who knows this becomes a fit supporter.
8.10.23 She mounted up, she came unto the Fathers. The Fathers called. to her, O Food, come hither. King Yama was her calf, her pail was silvern. Antaka, Mrityu's. son, milked her, this Svadha. This Food the Fathers make their lives' sustainer. He who* knows this becomes a meet supporter.
8.10.24 She mounted up, she came to men. They called her, Come unto- us, come hither thou Free-giver! Earth was her milking-pail, the calf beside her Manu Vaivasvata, Vivasvan's offspring. Prithi the son of Vena was her milker: he milked forth hus- bandry and grain for sowing. These men depend for life on corn and tillage. He who knows this becomes a meet supporter, successful in the culture of his_ corn-land.
8.10.25 She rose, she came unto the Seven Rishis. They called her,. Come, Rich in Devotion! hither. King Soma was her calf. the Moon her milk-pail. Brihaspati. Angirasa, her milker, Drew from her udder Prayer and Holy Fervour. Fervour and Prayer maintain the Seven Rishis. He who knows this becomes a meet supporter, a priest illustri- ous for his sacred knowledge.
8.10.26 She rose, she came unto the Gods. They called her, crying, O Vigour, come to us, come hither! God Savitar milked her, he milked forth Vigour. The Gods depend for life upon that Vigour. He who knows this becomes a meet supporter.
8.10.27 She rose approached the Apsarases and Gandharvas. They called her, Come to us, O Fragrant-scented! The son of Suryavarchas, Chitraratha, was her dear calf, her pail. a lotus-petal. The son of Suryavarchas, Vasuruchi, milked and drew from her most delightful fragrance. That scent supports Apsarases and Gandharvas. He who knows this becomes a meet supporter, and round him ever breathes delicious odour.
8.10.28 She mounted up, she came to Other People. They called her, crying, Come, Concealment! hither. Her dear calf was Vaisravana Kubera, a vessel never tempered was her milk-pail. Rajatanabhi, offspring of Kubera, milked her, and from her udder drew concealment. By that concealment live the Other People. He who knows this becomes a meet supporter, and makes all evil disappear and vanish.
8.10.29 She mounted up, she came unto the Serpents. The Serpents called her, Venomous! come hither. Her calf was Takshaka, Visala's offspring: a bottlegourd suppli- ed a milking-vessel. Iravan's offspring, Dhritarashtra milked her, and from her udder drew forth only poison. That poison quickens and supports the Serpents: He who knows this becomes a meet supporter.
8.10.30 One would ward off, for him who hath this knowledge, if with a bottle-gourd he sprinkled water.
8.10.31 And did he not repel, if in his spirit he said, I drive thee back, he would repel it.
8.10.32 The poison that it drives away, that poison verily repels.
8.10.33 The man who hath this knowledge pours its venom on his hated foe.
;;; I A glorification of the Asvins' whip and a prayer for blessings
9.1.1 The Asvins' Honey-whip was born from heaven and earth, from middle air, and ocean, and from fire and wind. All living creatures welcome it with joyful hearts, fraught with the store of Amrit it hath gathered up.
9.1.2 They call thee earth's great strength in every form, they call thee too the ocean's genial seed. Whence comes the Honey-whip bestowing bounty, there Vital Spirit is, and Amrit treasured.
9.1.3 In sundry spots, repeatedly reflecting, men view upon the earth: her course and action; For she, the first-born daughter of the Maruts, derives her origin from Wind and Agni.
9.1.4 Daughter of Vasus, mother of Adityas, centre of Amrit breath of living creatures. The Honey-whip, gold-coloured, dropping fatness, moves as a mighty embryo 'mid mortals.
9.1.5 The deities begat the Whip of Honey: her embryo assumed all forms and fashions. The mother nourishes that tender infant which at its birth looks on all worlds and beings.
9.1.6 Who understandeth well, who hath perceived it, her heart's un- injured Soma-holding beaker? Let the wise Brahman priest therein be joyful.
9.1.7 He understandeth them, he hath perceived them, her breasts that pour a thousand streams, uninjured. They unreluctantly yield strength and vigour.
9.1.8 She who with voice upraised in constant clamour, mighty, life- giving, goes unto her function, Bellowing to the heated three libations, suckles with streams of milk, and still is lowing.
9.1.9 On whom, well-fed, the Waters wait in worship, and steers and self-refulgent bulls attend her. For thee, for one like thee down pour the Waters, and cause desire and strength to rain upon thee.
9.1.10 The thunder is thy voice, O Lord of Creatures: a Bull, thou castest on the earth thy vigour. The Honey-whip, the Manus' first-born daughter, derives her origin from Wind and Agni.
9.1.11 As at the morning sacrifice the Asvins twain love Soma well, Even so may both the Asvins lay splendour and strength within my soul.
9.1.12 As at the second sacrifice Indra and Agni love him well, Let the pair, Indra Agni, lay splendour and strength within my soul.
9.1.13 As at third sacrifice Soma is the Ribhus' well-beloved one, Even so may they, the Ribhus, store splendour and strength within my soul.
9.1.14 Fain would I bring forth sweetness, fain would make it mine. Bringing milk, Agni! have I come: splendour and strength bestow on me!
9.1.15 Grant me, O Agni, splendid strength, and progeny, and length- ened life. May the Gods know me as I am, may Indra with the Rishis know.
9.1.16 As honey-bees collect and add fresh honey to their honey store, Even so may both the Asvins lay splendour and strength within my soul.
9.1.17 As over honey flies besmear this honey which the bees have made, So may both Asvins lay in me splendour and strength and power and might.
9.1.18 May all the sweetness that is found in hills and mountains, steeds and kine, And wine that floweth from the cup,--may all that sweetness be in me.
9.1.19 May both the Asvins, Lords of Light, balm me with honey of the bees, That I may speak among the folk words full of splendour and of strength.
9.1.20 The thunder is thy voice, O Lord of Creatures: a Bull, thou castest strength on earth and heaven. To that all cattle look for their existence: with this she nourishes their force and vigour.
9.1.21 The Whip itself is Heaven, Earth is the handle, the point of juncture is the Air's mid-region. The lash is lightning, and the tip is golden.
9.1.22 Whoever knows the Whip's seven kinds of honey, becomes himself a man endowed with sweetness. Brahman and King, the draught-ox and the milch-cow, barley and rice, and honey is the seventh.
9.1.23 Sweet is the man, sweet are his goods and chattels: he who knows this conquers the worlds of sweetness.
9.1.24 The thundering of Prajapati in heaven is verily manifest to living creatures. Therefore I stand from right to left invested, and, O Prajapati, I cry, regard me! The man who hath this knowledge is regarded by living beings and the Lord of Creatures.
;;; II A glorification of Kama as God of desire of all that is good
9.2.1 Kama the Bull, slayer of foes, I worship with molten butter, sacrifice, oblation. Beneath my feet cast down mine adversaries with thy great manly power, when I have praised thee.
9.2.2 That which is hateful to mine eye and spirit, that harasses and robs me of enjoyment, The evil dream I loose upon my foemen. May I rend him when I have lauded Kama.
9.2.3 Kama, do thou, a mighty Lord and Ruler, let loose ill dream, misfortune, want of children, Homelessness, Kama! utter destitution, upon the sinner who designs my ruin.
9.2.4 Drive them away, drive them afar, O Kama; indigence fall on those who are my foemen! When they have been cast down to deepest darkness, consume their dwellings with thy fire, O Agni.
9.2.5 She, Kama! she is called the Cow, thy daughter, she who is named Vak and Viraj by sages. By her drive thou my foemen to a distance. May cattle, vital breath, and life forsake them.
9.2.6 By Kama's might, King Varuna's and Indra's, by Vishnu's strength, and Savitar's instigation, I chase my foes with sacrifice to Agni, as a deft steersman drives his boat through waters.
9.2.7 May Kama, mighty one, my potent warder, give me full free- dom from mine adversaries. May all the Deities be my protection, all Gods come nigh to this mine invocation.
9.2.8 Accepting this oblation rich with fatness, be joyful here, ye Gods whose chief is Kama, Giving me freedom from mine adversaries.
9.2.9 Ye, Indra, Agni, Kama! come together and cast mine adver- saries down beneath me. When they have sunk into the deepest darkness, O Agni, with thy fire consume their dwellings.
9.2.10 Slay those who are mine enemies, O Kama: headlong to depth of blinding darkness hurl them. Reft be they all of manly strength and vigour! Let them not have a single day's existence.
9.2.11 Kama hath slain those who were mine opponents, and given me ample room to grow and prosper. Let the four regions bow them down before me, and let the six expanses bring me fatness.
9.2.12 Let them drift downward like a boat torn from the rope that held it fast. There is no turning back for those whom our keen arrows have repelled.
9.2.13 Agni averts, Indra averts, and Soma: may the averting Gods avert this foeman.
9.2.14 To be avoided by his friends, detested, repelled, with few men round him, let him wander. Yea, on the earth descend the lightning-flashes: may the strong God destroy your adversaries.
9.2.15 This potent lightning nourishes things shaken, and things un- shaken yet, and all the thunders. May the Sun, rising with his wealth and splendour, drive in victorious might my foemen downward.
9.2.16 Thy firm and triply-barred protection, Kama! thy spell, made weapon-proof extended armour With that drive thou my foemen to a distance. May cattle, vital breath, and life forsake them.
9.2.17 Far from the world wherein we live, O Kama, drive thou my foemen with that selfsame weapon Wherewith the Gods repelled the fiends, and Indra cast down the Dasyus into deepest darkness.
9.2.18 As Gods repelled the Asuras, and Indra down to the lowest darkness drove the demons, So, Kama, from this world, to distant places, drive thou the men who are mine adversaries.
9.2.19 First before all sprang Kama into being. Gods, Fathers, mortal men have never matched him. Stronger than these art thou, and great for ever. Kama, to thee, to thee I offer worship.
9.2.20 Wide as the space which heaven and earth encompass, far as the flow of waters, far as Agni, Stronger than these art thou, and great for ever. Kama, to thee, to thee I offer worship.
9.2.21 Vast as the quarters of the sky and regions that lie between them spread in all directions, vast as celestial tracts and views of heaven, Stronger than these art thou, and great for ever. Kama, to thee, to thee I offer worship.
9.2.22 Many as are the bees, and bats, and reptiles, and female serpents of the trees, and beetles, Stronger art thou than these, and great for ever. Kama, to thee, to thee I offer worship.
9.2.23 Stronger art thou than aught that stands or twinkles, stronger art thou than ocean, Kama! Manyu! Stronger than these art thou, and great for ever. Kama, to thee, to thee I offer worship.
9.2.24 Not even Vata is the peer of Kama, not Agni, Chandramas the Moon, nor Surya. Stronger than these art thou, and great for ever. Kama, to thee, to thee I offer worship.
9.2.25 Thy lovely and auspicious forms, O Kama, whereby the thing thou wilt becometh real, With these come thou and make thy home among us, and make malignant thoughts inhabit elsewhere.
;;; III On the consecration of a newly built house
9.3.1 We loose the ties and fastenings of the house that holds all precious things, The bands of pillars and of stays, the ties of beams that form the roof.
9.3.2 All-wealthy House! each knot and band, each cord that is attached to thee I with my spell untie, as erst Brihaspati disclosed the cave.
9.3.3 He drew them close, he pressed them fast, he made thy knotted. bands secure: With Indra's help we loose them as a skilful Slaughterer severs joints.
9.3.4 We loose the bands of thy bamboos, of bolts, of fastening, of thatch, We loose the ties of thy side-posts, O House that holdest all we prize.
9.3.5 We loosen here the ties and bands of straw in bundles, and of clamps, Of all that compasses and binds the Lady Genius of the Home.
9.3.6 We loose the loops which men have bound within thee, loops to tie and hold. Be gracious, when erected, to our bodies, Lady of the Home.
9.3.7 Store-house of Soma, Agni's hall, the ladies' bower, the resi- dence, The seat of Gods art thou, O Goddess House.
9.3.8 We with our incantation loose the net that hath a thousand. eyes. The diadem, securely tied and laid upon the central beam.
9.3.9 The man who takes thee as his own, and he who was thy builder,. House! Both these, O Lady of the Home, shall live to long-extended' years.
9.3.10 There let her come to meet this man. Firm, strongly fastened,. and prepared Art thou whose several limbs and joints we part and loosen one by one.
9.3.11 He who collected timber for the work and built thee up, O House, Made thee for coming progeny, Prajapati, the Lord Supreme.
9.3.12 Homage to him! We worship too the giver and the Mansion's lord: Homage to Agni! to the man who serves at holy rites for thee.
9.3.13 Homage to kine and steeds! to all that shall be born within the house We loose the bonds that fasten thee, mother of multitudes to come!
9.3.14 Agni thou shelterest within, and people with domestic beasts. We loose the bonds that fasten thee, mother of multitudes to come!
9.3.15 All space that lies between the earth and heaven, therewith I take this house for thy possession, And all that measures out the air's mid-region I make a hollow to contain thy treasures. Therewith I take the house for his possession.
9.3.16 Rich in prosperity, rich in milk, founded and built upon the earth, Injure not thy receivers, House who holdest food of every sort!'
9.3.17 Grass-covered, clad with straw, the house, like Night, gives rest to man and beast. Thou standest, built upon the earth, like a she-elephant, borne on feet.
9.3.18 I loosen and remove from thee thy covering formed by mats of reed. What Varuna hath firmly closed Mitra shall ope at early morn.
9.3.19 May Indra, Agni, deathless Gods, protect the house where Soma dwells, House that was founded with the prayer, built and erected by the wise.
9.3.20 Nest upon nest hath been imposed, compartment on compart- ment laid: There man shall propagate his kind, and there shall everything born.
9.3.21 Within the house constructed with two side-posts, or with four, or six. Built with eight side-posts, or with ten, lies Agni like a babe unborn.
9.3.22 Turned to thee, House! I come to thee, innocent, turned to welcome me: For Fire and Water are within, the first chief door of sacrifice.
9.3.23 Water that kills Consumption, free from all Consumption, here I bring. With Agni, the immortal one, I enter and possess the house.
9.3.24 Lay thou no cord or noose on us: a weighty burthen, still be light! Withersoever be our will, O House, we bear thee like a bride.
9.3.25 Now from the east side of the house to the Great Power be homage paid! Hail to the Gods whose due is Hail!
9.3.26 Now from the south side of the house, etc.
9.3.27 Now from the west side of the house, etc.
9.3.28 Now from the north side of the house, etc.
9.3.29 So from the mansion's every side to the Great Power be homage paid! Hail to the Gods whose due is Hail!
;;; IV A glorification of the typical sacrificial bull
9.4.1 The Bull, fierce, thousandfold, filled full of vigour, bearing within his flanks all forms and natures, Brihaspati's Steer, hath stretched the thread, bestowing bliss on the worshipper, the liberal giver.
9.4.2 He who at first became the Waters' model, a match for everyone, like Earth the Goddess; The husband of the cows, the young calves' father, may be secure us thousandfold abundance.
9.4.3 Masculine, pregnant, stedfast. full of vigour, the Bull sustains a trunk of goodly treasure. May Agni Jatavedas bear him offered, on pathways traversed by the Gods, to Indra.
9.4.4 The husband of the cows, the young calves' father, father is he of mighty water-eddies. Calf, after-birth, new milk drawn hot, and biestings, curds, butter, that is his best genial humour.
9.4.5 He is the Gods' allotted share and bundle, essence of waters, and of plants, and butter. Sakra elected him, the draught of Soma. What was his body was a lofty mountain.
9.4.0 6. A beaker filled with Soma juice thou bearest. framer of forms, begetter of the cattle. Kindly to us be these thy wombs here present, and stay for us, O Axe, those that are yonder.
9.4.7 He bears oblation, and his seed is butter. Thousand-fold plenty; sacrifice they call him. May he, the Bull, wearing the shape of Indra, come unto us, O Gods, bestowed, with blessing.
9.4.8 Both arms of Varuna, and Indra's vigour, the Maruts' hump is he, the Asvins' shoulders. They who are sages, bards endowed with wisdom, call him Brihaspati compact and heightened.
9.4.9 Thou, vigorous, reachest to the tribes of heaven. Thee they call Indra, thee they call Sarasvan. Turned to one aim, that Brahman gives a thousand who offers up the Bull as his oblation.
9.4.10 Brihaspati, Savitar gave thee vital vigour: thy breath was brought from Tvashtar and from Vayu. In thought I offer thee in air's mid-region. Thy sacrificial grass be Earth and Heaven!
9.4.11 Let the priest joyfully extol the limbs and members of the Bull Who moved and roared among the kine as Indra moves among the Gods.
9.4.12 The sides must be Anumati's, and both rib-pieces Bhaga's share, Of the knee-bones hath Mitra said, Both these are mine, and only mine.
9.4.13 The Adityas claim the hinder parts, the loins must be Brihas- pati's. Vata, the God, receives the tail: he stirs the plants and herbs therewith,
9.4.14 To Surya they assigned the skin, to Sinivali inward parts. The Slaughterer hath the feet, they said, when they distributed the Bull.
9.4.15 They made a jest of kindred's curse: a jar of Soma juice was set, What time the deities, convened, assigned the Bull's divided parts.
9.4.16 They gave the hooves to tortoises, to Sarama scraps of the feet: His undigested food they gave to worms and things that creep and crawl.
9.4.17 That Bull, the husband of the kine, pierces the demons with his horns, Banishes famine with his eye, and hears good tidings with his ears.
9.4.18 With hundred sacrifices he worships: the fires consume him not: All Gods promote the Braman who offers the Bull in sacrifice.
9.4.19 He who hath given away the Bull to Brahmans frees and cheers his soul. In his own cattle-pen he sees the growth and increase of his cows.
9.4.20 Let there be cattle, let there be bodily strength and progeny: All this may the Gods kindly grant to him who gives away the Bull.
9.4.21 Indra here verily hath rejoiced: let him bestow conspicuous wealth. May he draw forth at will from yonder side of heaven a deft cow, good to milk, whose calf is never wanting.
9.4.22 With close connexion mingle with the cows in this our cattle- pen: Mingle, the Bull's prolific flow, and, Indra! thine heroic strength!
9.4.23 Here we restore this Bull, your youthful leader: sporting with him, go, wander at your pleasure. Ne'er, wealthy ones! may he be reft of offspring; and do ye favour us with growth of riches.
;;; V A glorification of a sacrificial goat
9.5.1 Seize him and bring him hither. Let him travel. foreknowing, to the regions of the pious. Crossing in many a place the mighty darkness, let the Goat mount to the third heaven above us.
9.5.2 I bring thee hither as a share for Indra; prince, at this sacrifice,. for him who worships. Grasp firmly from behind all those who hate us: so let the sacri- ficer's men be sinless.
9.5.3 Wash from his feet all trace of evil-doing: foreknowing, with cleansed hooves let him go upward. Gazing on many a spot, crossing the darkness, let the Goat mount to the third heaven above us.
9.5.4 Cut up this skin with the grey knife, Dissector! dividing joint from joint, and mangle nothing Do him no injury: limb by limb arrange him, and send him up to the third cope of heaven.
9.5.5 With verse upon the fire I set the caldron: pour in the water; lay him down within it! Encompass him with fire, ye Immolators. Cooked, let him reach the world where dwell the righteous.
9.5.6 Hence come thou forth, vexed by no pain or torment. Mount to the third heaven from the heated vessel. As fire out of the fire hast thou arisen. Conquer and win this lucid world of splendour.
9.5.7 The Goat is Agni: light they call him, saying that living man must give him to the Brahman. Given in this world by a devout believer, the Goat dispels and drives afar the darkness.
9.5.8 Let the Panchaudana Goat, about to visit the three lights, pass away in five divisions. Go midst the pious who have paid their worship, and parted, dwell on the third cope of heaven.
9.5.9 Rise to that world, O Goat, where dwell the righteous: pass, like a Sarabha veiled, all difficult places. The Goat Panchaudana, given to a Brahman, shall with all ful- ness satisfy the giver.
9.5.10 The Goat Panchaudana, given to a Brahman, sets the bestower on the pitch of heaven, In the third vault, third sky, third ridge. One only Cow omni- form art thou, that yields all wishes.
9.5.11 That is the third light that is yours, ye Fathers. He gives the Goat Panchaudana to the Brahman. Given in this world by the devout believer, the Goat dispels and drives afar the darkness.
9.5.12 Seeking the world of good men who have worshipped, he gives the Goat Panchaudana to the Brahman. Win thou this world as thy complete possession. Auspicious unto us be he, accepted!
9.5.13 Truly the Goat sprang from the glow of Agni, inspired as sage with all a sage's power. Sacrifice, filled, filled full, offered with Vashat--this let the Gods arrange.at proper seasons.
9.5.14 Home-woven raiment let him give, and gold as guerdon to the priests. So he obtains completely all celestial and terrestrial worlds.
9.5.15 Near to thee, Goat! approach these streams of Soma, divine, distilling meath, bedecked with butter! Stay thou the earth and sky and fix them firmly up on the seven- rayed pitch and height of heaven.
9.5.16 Unborn art thou, O Goat: to heaven thou goest. Though thee Angirases knew that radiant region. So may I know that holy world.
9.5.17 Convey our sacrifice to heaven, that it may reach the Gods, with that Whereby thou, Agni, bearest wealth in thousands, and all pre- cious things.
9.5.18 The Goat Panchaudana, when cooked, transporteth, repelling Nirriti, to the world of Svarga. By him may we win worlds which Surya brightens.
9.5.19 The droppings of the Odanas attending the Goat which I have lodged with priest or people May all this know us in the world of virtue, O Agni, at the meeting of the pathways.
9.5.20 This Unborn cleft apart in the beginning: his breast became the earth, his back was heaven. His middle was the air, his sides the regions; the hollows of his belly formed both oceans.
9.5.21 His eyes were Truth and Right. The whole together was Truth: Viraj his head and Faith his breathing. This Goat Panchaudana was indeed a sacrifice unlimited.
9.5.22 A boundless sacrifice he performs, he wins himself a boundless world: Who gives the Goat Panchaudana illumined with a priestly fee.
9.5.23 Let him not break the victim's bones, let him not suck the marrow out. Let the man, taking him entire, here, even here deposit him.
9.5.24 This, even this is his true form: the man uniteth him therewith. Food, greatness, strength he bringeth him who giveth the Goat Panchaudana illumed with guerdon.
9.5.25 The five gold pieces, and the five new garments, and the five milch-kine yield him all his wishes. Who gives the Goat Panchaudana illumined with a priestly fee.
9.5.26 The five gold pieces, area light to light him, robes become armour to defend his body; He winneth Svarga as his home who giveth the Goat Panchaud- ana illumed with bountry.
9.5.27 When she who hath been wedded finds a second husband after- ward, The twain shall not be parted if they give the Goat Panchaud- ana.
9.5.28 One world with the re-wedded wife becomes the second hus- band's home. Who gives the Goat Panchaudana illumined with the priestly fee.
9.5.29 They who have given a cow who drops a calf each season, or an ox, A coverlet, a robe, or gold, go to the loftiest sphere of heaven.
9.5.30 Himself, the father and the son, the grandson, and the father's sire, Mother, wife, her who bore his babes, all the beloved ones I call.
9.5.31 The man who knows the season named the Scorching--the Goat Pafichaudana is this scorching season He lives himself, he verily burns up his hated rival's fame, Who gives the Goat Panchaudana illumined with the priestly fee.
9.5.32 The man who knows the season called the Working takes to himself the active fame, his hated rival's active fame. The Goat Panchaudana is this Working season. He lives himself, etc.
9.5.33 The man who knows the season called the Meeting takes to him- self the gathering fame, his hated rival's gathering fame. The Goat Panchaudana is this Meeting season.
9.5.34 The man who knows the called the Swelling takes to himself the swelling fame, his hated rival's swelling fame. The Goat Panchaudana is this Swelling season. He lives himself, etc.
9.5.35 The man who knows the season called the Rising takes to him- self the rising fame, his hated rival's rising fame. The Goat Panchaudana in this Rising season.
9.5.36 The man who knows the season called Surpassing takes to him- self the conquering fame, his hated rival's conquering fame. The Goat Panchaudana is this Conquering season. He lives himself, he verily burns up his hated rival's fame Who gives the Goat Panchaudana illumined with a priestly fee.
9.5.37 He cooks the Goat and the five boiled rice messes. May the uni- ted Quarters, all accordant, and intermediate points, accept him from thee.
9.5.38 May these preserve him for thee. Here I offer t o these the molten butter as oblation.
;;; VI A glorification of hospitable reception of guests
9.6.1 Whoso will know Prayer with immediate knowledge, whose mem- bers are the stuff, whose spine the verses:
9.6.2 Whose hairs are psalms, whose heart is called the Yajus, whose coverlet is verily oblation--
9.6.3 Verily when a host looks at his guests he looks at the place of sacrifice to the Gods.
9.6.4 When he salutes them reverently he undergoes preparation for a religious ceremony: when he calls for water, he solemnly brings sacrificial water.
9.6.5 The water that is solemnly brought at a sacrifice is this same water.
9.6.6 The libation which they bring; the sacrificial victim dedicated to Agni and Soma which is tied to the post, that, verily, is this man.
9.6.7 When they arrange dwelling-rooms they arrange the sacred chamber and the shed for housing the Soma cars.
9.6.8 What they spread upon the floor is just Sacrificial Grass.
9.6.9 With the couch that the men bring, he wins for himself the world of Svarga.
9.6.10 The pillow-coverings that they bring are the green sticks that surround the sacrificial altar.
9.6.11 The ointment that they bring for injunction is just clarified liquid butter.
9.6.12 The food they bring before the general distribution represents the two sacrificial cakes of rice meal.
9.6.13 When they call the man who prepares food they summon the preparer of oblation.
9.6.14 The grains of rice and barley that are selected are just filaments of the Soma plant.
9.6.15 The pestle and mortar are really the stones of the Soma press.
9.6.16 The winnowing-basket is the filter, the chaff the Soma dregs, the water, the pressing-gear.
9.6.17 Spoon, ladle, fork, stirring-prong are the wooden Soma tubs; the earthen cooking-pots are the mortar-shaped Soma vessels; this earth is just the black-antelope's skin.
9.6.18 Or the host acts in this way to a Yajamana's Brahman: when he looks at the furniture and utensils he says, More here t yet more here.
9.6.19 When he says, Bring out more, he lengthens his life thereby.
9.6.20 He brings oblations: he makes the men sit down.
9.6.21 As the guest of the seated company he himself offers up sacrifice.
9.6.22 With ladle, with hand, in life, at the sacrificial post, with cry of Ladle! with exclamation of Vashat!
9.6.23 Now these guests, as priests beloved or not beloved, bring one to the world of Svarga.
9.6.24 He who hath this knowledge should not eat hating, should not eat the food of one who hates him, nor of one who is doubt- ful, nor of one who is undecided.
9.6.25 This man whose food they eat hath all his wickedness blotted out.
9.6.26 All that man's sin whose food they do not eat remains unblot- ted out.
9.6.27 The man who supplies food hath always pressing stones adjusted, a wet Soma filter, well prepared religious rites, and mental power to complete the arranged sacrifice.
9.6.28 The arranged sacrifice of the man who offers food is a sacrifice to Prajapati.
9.6.29 The man who offers food follows the steps of Prajapati.
