12.5.40 Homelessness is she when denied her rights.
12.5.41 Having become Flesh-eating Agni the Brahman's cow entereth into and devoureth the oppressor of Brahmans.
12.5.42 She sunders all his members, joints, and roots.
12.5.43 She cuts off relationship on the father's side and destroys mater- nal kinship.
12.5.44 The Brahman's cow, not restored by a Kshatriya, ruins the marriages and all the kinsmen of the Brahman's oppressor.
12.5.45 She makes him houseless, homeless, childless: he is extinguished without posterity to succeed him.
12.5.0 46. So shall it be with the Kshatriya who takes to himself the cow of the Braman who hath this knowledge.
12.5.47 Quickly, when he is smitten down by death, the clamorous vul- tures cry:
12.5.48 Quickly around his funeral fire dance women with dishevelled locks, Striking the hand upon the breast and uttering their evil shriek.
12.5.49 Quickly the wolves are howling in the habitation where he lived:
12.5.50 Quickly they ask about him, What is this? What thing hath happened here?
12.5.51 Rend, rend to pieces, rend away, destroy, destroy him utterly.
12.5.52 Destroy Angirasi! the wretch who robs and wrongs the Brah- mans, born.
12.5.53 Of evil womb, thou witchcraft hid, for Vaisvadevi is thy name,
12.5.54 Consuming, burning all things up, the thunderbolt of spell and charm.
12.5.55 Go thou, becoming Mrityu sharp as razor's edge pursue thy course:
12.5.56 Thou bearest off the tyrants' strength, their store of merit, and their prayers.
12.5.57 Bearing off wrong, thou givest in that world to him who hath been wronged.
12.5.58 O Cow, become a tracker through the curse the Brahman hath pronounced,
12.5.59 Become a bolt, an arrow through his sin, be terribly venomous.
12.5.60 O Cow, break thou the head of him who wrongs the Brahmans, criminal, niggard, blasphemer of the Gods.
12.5.61 Let Agni burn the spiteful wretch when crushed to death and slain by thee.
12.5.62 Rend, rend to bits, rend through and through, scorch and con- sume and burn to dust,
12.5.63 Consume thou, even from the root, the Brahmans' tyrant, god- like Cow!
12.5.64 That he may go from Yama's home afar into the worlds of sin. its
12.5.65 So, Goddess Cow, do thou from him, the Brahmans' tyrant, criminal, niggard, blasphemer of the Gods,
12.5.66 With hundred-knotted thunderbolt, sharpened and edged with razor-blades,
12.5.67 Strike off the shoulders and the head.
12.5.68 Snatch thou the hair from off his head, and from his body strip the skin:
12.5.69 Tear out his sinews, cause his flesh to fall in pieces from his frame.
12.5.70 Crush thou his bones together, strike and beat the marrow out of him.
12.5.71 Dislocate all his limbs and joints.
12.5.72 From earth let the Carnivorous Agni drive him, let Vayu burn. him from mid-air's broad region.
12.5.73 From heaven let Surya drive him and consume him.
;;; I The glorification of Rohita, a form of Fire and of the Sun
13.1.1 Rise, Mighty One, who liest in the waters, and enter this thy fair and glorious kingdom. Let Rohita who made this All uphold thee carefully nurtured for supreme dominion.
13.1.2 The strength that was in waters hath ascended. Mount o'er the tribes which thou hast generated. Creating Soma, waters, plants and cattle, bring hitherward both quadrupeds and bipeds.
13.1.3 Ye Maruts, strong and mighty, sons of Prisni, with Indra for ally crush down our foemen. Let Rohita, ye bounteous givers, hear you, thrice-seven Maruts who delight in sweetness!
13.1.4 Up to the lap of births, to lofty places, hath Rohita, the germ of Dames, ascended. Conjoined with these he found the six realms: seeing his way in front here he received the kingship.
13.1.5 For thee hath Rohita obtained dominion, scattered thine ene- mies, become thy safeguard. So by the potent Sakvaris let Heaven and Earth be milked to- yield thee all thy wishes.
13.1.6 Rohita gave the Earth and Heavens their being. There Para- meshthin held the cord extended. Thereon reposeth Aja Ekapada. He with his might hath stab- lished Earth and Heaven.
13.1.7 Rohita firmly stablished Earth and Heaven: by him was ether fixt by him the welkin. He measured out mid air and all the regions: by him the Gods found life that lasts for ever.
13.1.8 Arranging shoots, springs, Rohita considered this Universe in all its forms and phases. May he, gone up to heaven with mighty glory, anoint thy sov- ranty with milk and fatness.
13.1.9 Thy risings up, thy mountings and ascensions wherewith thou fillest heaven and air's mid-region-- By prayer for these, by milk of these, increasing, in Rohita's kingdom watch, among his people.
13.1.10 The tribes thy heat produced have followed hither the Calf and Gayatri, the strain that lauds him. With friendly heart let them approach to serve thee, and the Calf Rohita come with his mother.
13.1.11 Erected, Rohita hath reached the welkin, wise, young, creating every form and figure. Agni, refulgent with his heightened lustre, in the third realm hath brought us joy and gladness.
13.1.12 Thousand-horned Bull, may Jatavedas, worshipped with butter, balmed with Soma, rich in heroes, Besought, ne'er quit me; may I ne'er forsake thee. Give me abundant men and herds of cattle.
13.1.13 Rohita is the sire and mouth of worship: to him with voice, ear, heart I pay oblation. To Rohita come Gods with joyful spirit. May he by risings raise me till I join him.
13.1.14 Rohita ordered sacrifice for Visvakarman: thence have I obta- ined this strength and energy. May I proclaim thee as my kin over the greatness of the world.
13.1.15 On thee have mounted Brihati and Pankti. and Kakup with great splendour, Jatavedas! The cry of Vashat with the voice uplifted and Rohita with seed on thee have mounted.
13.1.16 He goes into the womb of earth, he robes himself in heaven and air. He on the Bright One's station hath reached heavenly light and all the worlds.
13.1.17 To us, Vachaspati, may Earth be pleasant, pleasant our dwelling, pleasant be our couches. Even here may Prana be our friend: may Agni, O Parameshthin give thee life and splendour.
13.1.18 And those, Vachaspati, our own five seasons, sacred to Visva- karman their creator. Even here our friend be Prana: Parameshthin, may Rohita vouchsafe the life and splendour.
13.1.19 Breed, O Vachaspati, joy and understanding, kine i n our stall and children in our consorts. Even here may Prana be our friend: may Agni, O Parameshthin, give thee life and splendour.
13.1.20 With splendour let God Savitar, and Agni, with splendour Mitra, Varuna invest thee. Treading down all Malignities, come hither. Pleasant and' glorious hast thou made this kingdom.
13.1.21 Rohita, car-borne by a speckled leader, thou, pouring water,. goest on in triumph.
13.1.22 Golden, refulgent, lofty is the Lady, Rohini, Rohita's devoted Consort. Through her may we win various spoil and booty, through her be conquerors in every battle.
13.1.23 Rohita's seat is Rohini before us: that is the path the speckled Mare pursueth. Kasyapas and Gandharvas lead her upward, and heavenly sages ever watch and guard her,
13.1.24 Surya's bay steeds refulgent and immortal draw the light-rolling. chariot on for ever. Drinker of fatness, Rohita, resplendent, hath entered into various-coloured heaven,
13.1.25 Rohita, Bull whose horns are sharply pointed, superior of Agni and of Surya, He who supports the sundered earth and heaven,--from him the Gods effect their own creations.
13.1.26 Rohita rose to heaven from mighty ocean, Rohita rose and clomb all steeps and rises.
13.1.27 Prepare the Milky One who teems with fatness: she is the Gods' never-reluctant milch-cow. Indra drink Soma: ours be peace and safety. Let Agni lead the laud, and chase our foemen.
13.1.28 Both kindling and inflamed, adored with butter and enhanced thereby. May conquering Agni, conqueror of all, destroy mine enemies.
13.1.29 Let him smite down in death and burn the foeman who attacketh me. Our adversaries we consume through Agni the Carnivorous.
13.1.30 Beat them down, Indra, with thy bolt, beat them down, mighty with thine arm. I through the energy and force of Agni have secured my foes.
13.1.31 Cast down our foes beneath our feet, O Agni. Brihaspati, oppress our rebel kinsman. Low let them fall, O Indra-Agni. Mitra-Varuna, powerless to show their anger.
13.1.32 Ascending up on high, O God. O Surya, drive my foes away. Yea, beat them backward with the stone: to deepest darkness let them go.
13.1.33 Calf of Viraj, the Bull of prayers and worship, whitebacked, he hath gone up to air's mid-region. Singing, they hymn the Calf, with gifts of butter: him who is Brahma they exalt with Brahma.
13.1.34 Rise up to earth, rise up to heaven above it; rise up to opulence, rise up to kingship. Rise up to offspring, rise to life immortal; rise, and with Rohita unite thy body.
13.1.35 With all the Gods who circle round the Sun, upholding royal sway, With all of these may Rohita accordant, give sovranty to thee with friendly spirit.
13.1.36 Cleansed by prayer, sacrifices bear thee upward: bay coursers, ever travelling, convey thee. Thy light shines over sea and billowy ocean.
13.1.37 Rohita, conqueror of cows and riches and gathered spoil, is heaven's and earth's upholder. Over earth's greatness would I tell my kinship with thee who hast a thousand births and seven.
13.1.38 A glorious sight to beasts and men, thou goest glorious to the regions and mid-regions. On earth's, on Aditi's bosom, bright with glory. Fain would I equal Savitar in beauty.
13.1.39 Thou, yonder, knowest all things here, when here thou knowest what is there. From here men see the sphere of light, Surya profoundly wise in heaven.
13.1.40 A God, thou injurest the Gods: thou movest in the ocean's depth. Men kindle common Agni: him only the higher sages know.
13.1.41 Beneath the upper realm, above this lower, bearing her Calf at foot, the Cow hath risen Whitherward, to what place hath she departed? Where doth she calve? Not in this herd of cattle.
13.1.42 She hath become one-footed or two-footed, four-footed, or eight-footed or nine-footed, This universe's thousand-syllabled Pankti Oceans flow forth from her in all directions.
13.1.43 Rising to heaven, immortal, hear my calling. Cleansed by prayer, sacrifices bear thee upward. Bay coursers, ever on the road, convey thee.
13.1.44 This, O Immortal One, I know of thee, thy progress to the sky thy dwelling-place in loftiest heaven.
13.1.45 Beyond the sky, beyond the Earth looks Surya, and beyond the floods. The single eye of all that is; to mighty heaven hath he arisen.
13.1.46 The earth was made his altar, and the wide expanses were the fence. There Rohita established both these Agnis, fervent heat and cold.
13.1.47 He stablished heat and cold, he made the mountains sacrificial posts. Then both the Agnis, Rohita's who found celestial light, with rain for molten butter, sacrificed.
13.1.48 Rohita's Agni-his who found heaven's light-is kindled with the prayer. From him the heat, from him the cold, from him the sacrifice was born.
13.1.49 Both Agins-Rohita's who found the light of heaven--made strong by prayer, Waxing by prayer, adored with prayer, by prayer enkindled, sacrificed.
13.1.50 One is deposited in Truth, one kindled in the waters: both Agnis of Rohita who found the light are set aflame with prayer.
13.1.51 That decked by Wind, and that prepared by Indra Brahman- aspati, Agnis of Rohita who found light, prayer-enkindled, sacrificed.
13.1.52 Rohita made the earth to be his altar, heaven his Dakshina. Then heat he took for Agni, and with rain for molten butter he created every living thing.
13.1.53 The earth became an altar, heat was Agni, and the butter rain. There Agni made, by song and hymn, these mountains rise and stand erect.
13.1.54 Then, having made the hills stand up, Rohita spake to Earth, and said: In thee let every thing be born, what is and what is yet to be.
13.1.55 This sacrifice, the first of all, the past, the present, had its birth. From that arose this universe, yea, all this world of brightness, brought by Rohita the heavenly Sage.
13.1.56 If thou should kick a cow, or by indecent act offend the Sun, Thy root I sever; nevermore mayst thou cast shadow on the ground.
13.1.57 Thou who, between the fire and me, passest across the line of shade. Thy root I sever: nevermore mayst thou cast shadow on the ground.
13.1.58 Whoe'er he be who, Surya, God! comes between thee and me to-day, On him we wipe away ill-dream, and troubles, and impurity.
13.1.59 Let us not, Indra, leave the path, the Soma-presser's sacrifice. Let not malignities dwell with us.
13.1.60 May we obtain, completely wrought, the thread spun out tc reach the Gods, That perfecteth our sacrifice.
;;; II The glorification of the Sun as Aditya, Surya and Rohita
13.2.1 Radiant, refulgent in the sky are reared the banners of his light, Aditya's, who beholdeth man, mighty in act and bountiful.
13.2.2 Let us laud him, the whole world's Herdsman, Surya, who with his rays illumines all the regions, Mark of the quarters, brightening them with lustre, swift, mighty-pinioned, flying in the ocean.
13.2.3 From west to east thou speedest freely, making by magic day and night of diverse colours. This is Aditya, thy transcendent glory, that thou alone art born through all creation.
13.2.4 Victorious, inspired, and brightly shining, whom seven strong tawny-coloured coursers carry, Whom Atri lifted from the flood to heaven, thus men behold thee as thy course thou runnest.
13.2.5 Let them not snare thee speeding on thy journey: pass safely, swiftly places hard to traverse, While measuring out the day and night thou movest--O Surya, even Heaven and Earth the Goddess.
13.2.6 Hail to thy rapid car whereon, O Surya, thou circlest in a moment both the limits, Whirled by thy bay steeds, best of all at drawing, thy hundred horses or seven goodly coursers!
13.2.7 Mount thy strong car, O Surya, lightly rolling, drawn by good steeds, propitious, brightly gleaming, Whirled by thy bays, most excellent at drawing, thy hundred horses or seven goodly coursers.
13.2.8 Surya hath harnessed to his car to draw him seven stately bay steeds gay with wolden housings. The Bright One started from the distant region: dispelling gloom the God hath climbed the heavens.
13.2.9 With lofty banner hath the God gone upward, and introduced the light, expelling darkness. He hath looked round on all the worlds, the Hero, the son of Aditi, Celestial Eagle.
13.2.10 Rising, thou spreadest out thy rays, thou nourishest all shapes and forms. Thou with thy power illumest both the oceans, encompassing all spheres with thy refulgence.
13.2.11 Moving by magic power to east and westward, these two young creatures, sporting, circle ocean. One of the pair beholds all living creatures: with wheels of gold the bay steeds bear the other.
13.2.12 Atri established thee in heaven. O Surya, to create the month. So on thou goest, firmly held, heating, beholding all that is.
13.2.13 As the Calf both his parents so thou joinest both the distant bounds, Surely the Gods up yonder knew this sacred mystery long ago.
13.2.14 Surya is eager to obtain all wealth that lies along the sea, Great is the course spread out for him, his eastward and his westward path.
13.2.15 He finishes his race with speed and never turns his thought aside, Thereby he keeps not from the Gods enjoyment of the Drink of Life.
13.2.16 His heralds bear him up aloft, the God who knoweth all that live, Surya, that all may look on him.
13.2.17 The Constellations pass away, like thieves, departing in the night. Before the all-beholding Sun.
13.2.18 His herald rays are seen afar refulgent o'er the world of men, Like flames of fire that burn and blaze.
13.2.19 Swift and all-beautiful art thou, O Surya, maker of the light, Illuming all the radiant realm.
13.2.20 Thou goest to the hosts of Gods, thou comest hither to mankind, Hither, all light to behold.
13.2.21 With that same eye of thine wherewith thou seest, brilliant Varuna. The active one among mankind,
13.2.22 Traversing sky and wide mid-air, thou metest with thy beams our days, Sun, seeing all things that have life.
13.2.23 Seven bay steeds harnessed to thy car bear thee, O thou far- seeing One, God, Surya, with the radiant hair.
13.2.24 Surya, hath yoked the pure bright seven, the daughters of the car, with these, His own dear team, he travelleth.
13.2.25 Devout, aflame with fervent heat, Rohita hath gone up to heaven. He is re-born, returning to his birthplace, and hath become the Gods' imperial ruler.
13.2.26 Dear unto all men, facing all directions, with hands and palms on every side extended, He, the sole God, engendering earth and heaven, beareth them with his wings and arms together.
13.2.27 The single-footed hath outstepped the biped, the biped overtakes the triple-footed. The biped hath outstridden the six-footed: these sit around the single-footed's body.
13.2.28 When he, unwearied, fain to go, hath mounted his bays, he makes two colours, brightly shining. Rising with banners, conquering the regions, thou sendest light through all the floods, Aditya.
13.2.29 Verily, Surya, thou art great: truly, Aditya, thou art great. Great is thy grandeur, Mighty One: thou, O Aditya, thou art great.
13.2.30 In heaven, O Bird, and in mid-air thou shinest: thou shinest on the earth and in the waters. Thou hast pervaded both the seas with splendour: a God art thou, O God, light-winner, mighty.
13.2.31 Soaring in mid-course hither from the distance, fleet and ins- pired, the Bird that flies above us, With might advancing Vishnu manifested, he conquers all that moves with radiant banner:
13.2.32 Brilliant, observant, mighty Lord, an Eagle illuming both the spheres and air between them. Day and the Night, clad in the robes of Surya, spread forth more widely all his hero powers.
13.2.33 Flaming and radiant, strengthening his body, bestowing floods that promptly come to meet us, He, luminous, winged, mighty, strength-bestower, hath mounted all the regions as he forms them.
13.2.34 Bright presence of the Gods, the luminous herald Surya hath mounted the celestial regions. Day's maker, he hath shone away the darkness, and radiant, passed o'er places hard to traverse.
13.2.35 He hath gone up on high, the Gods' bright presence, the eye of Mitra, Varuna and Agni. The soul of all that moveth not or moveth, Surya hath filled the earth and air and heaven,
13.2.36 High in the midst of heaven may we behold thee whom men call Savitar, the bright red Eagle, Soaring and speeding on thy way, refulgent, unwasting light which Atri erst discovered.
13.2.37 Him, Son of Aditi, an Eagle hasting along heaven's height, I supplicate in terror, As such prolong our lengthened life, O Surya: may we, unha- rmed, enjoy thy gracious favour.
13.2.38 This gold-hued Hansa's wings, soaring to heaven, spread o'er a thousand days' continued journey Supporting all the Gods upon his bosom, he goes his way behold- ing every creature.
13.2.39 Rohita, in primeval days Prajapati, was, after, Time, Mouth of all sacrifices, he, Rohita, brought celestial light.
13.2.40 He, Rohita, became the world: Rohita gave the heaven its heat. Rohita with his beams of light travelled along the earth and sea.
13.2.41 To all the regions Rohita came, the imperial Lord of heaven. He watches over ocean, heaven, and earth and all existing things.
13.2.42 Mounting the lofty ones, he, bright, unwearied, splendidly shining, makes two separate colours, While through all worlds that are he sends his lustre, radiant, observant, mighty, wind-approacher.
13.2.43 One form comes on, the other is reverted: to day and night the Strong One shapes and fits him. With humble prayer for aid we call on Surya, who knows the way, whose home is in the region.
13.2.44 The suppliant's way, filling the earth, the Mighty circleth the world with eye that none deceiveth. May he, all-seeing, well-disposed and holy, give ear and listen to the word I utter.
13.2.45 Blazing with light his majesty hath compassed ocean and earth and heaven and air's mid-region. May he, all-seeing, well-disposed and holy, give ear and listen to the word I utter.
13.2.46 Agni is weakened by the people's fuel to meet the Dawn who cometh like a milch-cow, Like young trees shooting up on high their branches, his flames are mounting to the vault of heaven.
;;; III A glorification of Rohita. with a malediction on the man who wrongs a Brahman
13.3.1 He who engendered these, the earth and heaven, who made the worlds the mantle that he weareth, In whom abide the six wide-spreading regions through which the Bird's keen vision penetrateth, This God is wroth offended by the sinner who wrongs the Brahman who hath gained this knowledge Agitate him, O Rohita; destroy him: entangle in thy snares the Braman's tyrant.
13.3.2 He from whom winds blow pure in ordered season, from whom the seas flow forth in all directions, This God, etc.
13.3.3 He who takes life away, he who bestows it; from whom comes breath to every living creature, This God, etc.
13.3.4 Who with the breath he draws sates earth and heaven, with expiration fills the ocean's belly, This God, etc.
13.3.5 In whom Viraj, Prajapati, Parameshthin, Agni Vaisvanara abide with Pankti, He who hath taken to himself the breathing of the Supreme, the vigour of the Highest, This God, etc.
13.3.6 On whom rest six expenses and five regions, four waters, and three syllables of worship, He who hath looked between both spheres in anger, This God, etc.
13.3.7 He who, consuming food, became its master, the Lord of Prayer, the Regent of Devotion, The world's Lord, present and to be hereafter, This God, etc.
13.3.8 He who metes out the thirteenth month, constructed with days and nights, containing thirty members, This God, etc.
13.3.9 Dark the descent; the strong-winged birds are golden: they fly aloft to heaven, enrobed in waters. They have come hither from the seat of Order, This God, etc.
13.3.10 What silver. Kasyapa, thou hast refulgent, what brightly-shining lotus-flower collected, Wherein are gathered seven Suns together, This God, etc.
13.3.11 In front the Brihat-Saman is his mantle, and from behind Rathantara enfolds him, Ever with care robing themselves in splendour. This God, etc.
13.3.12 One of his wings was Brihat, and the other Rathantarr., vigorous with one same purpose, What time the Gods gave Rohita his being. This God, etc.
13.3.13 At evening he is Varuna and Agni, ascending in the morning he is Mitra. As Savitar, he moves through air's mid region, as Indra warms- the heavens from the centre. This God, etc.
13.3.14 This gold-hued Harisa's wings, soaring to heaven spread o'er a thousand days' continued journey. Supporting all the Gods upon his bosom, he goes his way behol- ding every creature. This God, etc.
13.3.15 This is the God who dwells-within the waters, the thousand- rooted, many-powered Atri, He who brought all this world into existence. This God; etc.
13.3.16 With flying feet his tawny coursers carry the bright God through, the sky, aglow with splendour. Whose limbs uplifted fire and heat the heavens: hither he shines- with beams of golden colour. This God, etc.
13.3.17 He beside whom his bay steeds bear the Adityas, by whom as sacrifice go many knowing. The sole light shining spread through various places. This God, etc.
13.3.18 This seven make the one-wheeled chariot ready: bearing seven names the single courser draws it. The wheel, three-naved, is sound and undecaying: thereon these worlds of life are all dependent. This God, etc.
13.3.19 Eight times attached the potent Courser draws it, Sire of the Gods, father of hymns and praises. So Matarisvan, measuring in spirit the thread of Order, purifies all regions. This God, etc.
13.3.20 The thread that goes through all celestial quarters within the Gayatri, womb of life eternal. This God, etc.
13.3.21 There are the settings, three the upward risings, three are the- spaces, yea, and three the heavens. We know thy triple place of birth, O Agni, we know the deities'' triple generations.
13.3.22 He who, as soon as born, laid broad earth open, and set the ocean in the air's mid-region, This God, etc.
13.3.23 Thou, Agni, kind with lights and mental powers, hast up in heaven shone as the Sun, enkindled. The Maruts, sons of Prisni, sang his praises what time the Gods gave Rohita his being. This God, etc.
13.3.24 Giver of breath, giver of strength and vigour, he whose com- mandment all the Gods acknowledge, He who is Lord of this, of man and cattle, This God, etc.
13.3.25 The single-footed hath outstepped the biped, the biped overtakes the triple-footed. The quadruped hath wrought when bipeds called him, standing and looking on the five collected. This God is wroth offended by the sinner that wrongs the Brahman who hath gained this knowledge. Agitate him, O Rohita; destroy him: entangle in thy snares the Brahman's tyrant.
13.3.26 Born is the darksome Mother's Son, the whitely shining Calf of Night. He, Rohita, ascendeth up to heaven, hath mounted to the heights.
;;; IV A glorification of the Sun as the only Deity
13.4.1 Down looking, on the ridge of sky Savitar goes to highest heaven.
13.4.2 To misty cloud filled with his rays Mahendra goes encompassed round.
13.4.3 Creator and Ordainer, he is Vayu, he is lifted cloud.
13.4.4 Rudra, and Mahadeva, he is Aryaman and Varuna.
13.4.5 Agni is he, and Siirya, he is verily Mahayama.
13.4.6 Calves, joined, stand close beside him, ten in number, with one single head.
13.4.7 From west to east they bend their way: when he mounts up he shines afar.
13.4.8 His are these banded Maruts: they move gathered close like porters' thongs.
13.4.9 To misty cloud filled with his rays Mahendra goes encompassed round,
13.4.10 His are the nine supports, the casks set in nine several places here.
13.4.11 He keeppeth watch o'er creatures, all that breatheth and that breatheth not.
13.4.12 This conquering might hath entered him, He is the sole the simple One, the One alone.
13.4.13 In him these Deities become simple and One
13.4.14 Renown and glory, and force and cloud, the Brahman's splendour, and food, and nourishment,
13.4.15 To him who knoweth this God as simple and one.
13.4.16 Neither second, nor third, nor yet fourth is he called;
13.4.17 He is called neither fifth, nor sixth, nor yet seventh
13.4.18 He is called neither eighth, nor ninth, nor yet tenth.
13.4.19 He watcheth over creatures, all that breatheth and that breatheth not.
13.4.20 This conquering might hath entered him. He is the sole, the simple One, the One alone,
13.4.21 In him these Deities become simple and One
13.4.22 Devotion and Religious Fervour, and renown and glory, and force and cloud, the Brahman's splendour, and food and nourishment.
13.4.23 And past and future, and Faith and lustre, and heaven and sweet oblation,
13.4.24 To him who knoweth this God as simple and One.
13.4.25 He, verily, is death, he is immortality, he is the monster, he is the fiend.
13.4.26 He is Rudra, winner of wealth in the giving of wealth; in uttering homage he is the sacrificial exclamation Vashat duly employed.
13.4.27 All sorcerers on earth obey with reverence his high behest.
13.4.28 All constellations yonder, with the Moon, are subject to his will.
13.4.29 He was brought forth from Day: and Day derives his origin. from him.
13.4.30 He was brought forth from Night: and Night derives her origins from him.
13.4.31 He was produced from Air: and Air derives its origin from him.
13.4.32 He was produced from Wind: and Wind derives his origin from. him.
13.4.33 From Heaven was he produced: and Heaven derives his origin from him.
13.4.34 He sprang from regions of the sky: from him the heavenly regions sprang.
13.4.35 He is the offspring of the Earth: Earth hath her origin from him.
13.4.36 He was produced from fire: and fire derives its origin from him.
13.4.37 He is the waters' offspring: and from him the waters were produced.
13.4.38 From holy verses was he born: from him the holy verses sprang.
13.4.39 He is the son of sacrifice: and sacrifice was born from him.
13.4.40 Sacrifice, sacrifice's Lord, he was made head of sacrifice.
13.4.41 He thundereth, he lighteneth, he casteth down the thunder-stone
13.4.42 For misery or happiness, for mortal man or Asura.
13.4.43 Whether thou formest growing plants, or sendest rain for happiness, or hast increased the race of man,
13.4.44 Such is thy greatness, liberal Lord! A hundred bodily forms are thine.
13.4.45 Millions are in thy million, or thou art a billion in thyself.
13.4.46 Stronger than immortality is Indra: stronger thou than deaths;
13.4.47 Yea, stronger than Malignity art thou, O Indra, Lord of Might. Calling thee Master, Sovran Chief, we pay our reverence to thee.
13.4.48 Worship to thee whom all behold! Regard me, thou whom all regard,
13.4.49 With food, and fame, and vigour, with the splendour of a Brahman's rank
13.4.50 We pay thee reverence calling thee strength, power, and might, and conquering force.
13.4.51 We pay thee reverence calling thee red power, the silvery expanse.
13.4.52 We pay thee reverence calling thee vast, wide, the good, the universe.
13.4.53 We pay thee reverence, calling thee extension, compass, width, and world.
13.4.54 We pay thee reverence, calling thee rich, opulent in this and that, with wealth unceasing and secure
13.4.55 Worship to thee whom all behold! Regard me, thou whom all regard.
13.4.56 With food, and fame, and vigour, with the splendour of a Brahman's rank.
;;; I On the Bridal of Surya, marriage ceremonies in general
14.1.1 Truth is the base that bears the earth; by Surya are the heavens upheld. By Law the Adityas stand secure, and Soma holds his place in heaven.
14.1.2 By Soma are the Adityas strong, by Soma mighty is the earth: Thus Soma in the lap of all these constellations hath his home.
14.1.3 One thinks, when men have brayed the plant, that he hath drunk the Soma's juice. Of him whom Brahmans truly know as Soma never mortal eats.
14.1.4 When they begin to drink thee, then, O God, thou swellest out again. Vayu in Soma's sentinel. The month is that which shapes the years.
14.1.5 Soma, preserved by covering rules, guarded by hymns in Brihati, Thou standest listening to the stones; none tastes of thee who dwells on earth.
14.1.6 Thought was her coverlet, the power of sight was unguent for her eyes: Her treasure-chest was earth and heaven, when Surya went unto her lord.
14.1.7 Raibhi was her dear bridal friend, and Narasatisi led her home. Lovely to see was Surya's robe: by Gatha beautified she moves
14.1.8 Songs were the cross-bars of the pole, Kurira metre docked her head. Both Asvins were the paranymphs: Agni was leader of the train.
14.1.9 Soma was he who wooed the maid: the groomsmen were both. Asvins, when The Sun-God Savitar bestowed his willing Surya on her lord.
14.1.10 Her spirit was the bridal car, the canopy thereof was heaven: Two radiant oxen formed the team when Surya came unto her lord.
14.1.11 Steadily went the steers upheld by holy verse and song of praise, The chariot-wheels were listening ears: thy path was tremulous in the sky.
14.1.12 Pure, as thou wentest, were thy wheels, breath was the axle pier- cing them. Surya advancing to her lord rode on the chariot of her heart.
14.1.13 The bridal pomp of Surya, which Savitar started, moved along. In Magha days are oxen slain, in Phalgunis they wed the bride.
14.1.14 When on your three-wheeled chariot, O ye Asvins, ye came as suitors unto Surya's bridal, Where was one chariot-wheel of yours? Where stood ye for the sire's command?
14.1.15 Twin Lords of Lustre, at the time when ye to Surya's wooing came, Then all the Gods agreed to your proposal Pushan as son elected you as father.
14.1.16 Two wheels of thine the Brahmans know, Surya! according to their times. That which is hidden only those who know the highest truths have learned.
14.1.17 Worship we pay to Aryaman, finder of husbands, kindly friend. As from its stalk a cucumber, from here I loose thee, not from there
14.1.18 Hence and not thence I send her free. I make her softly fettered there. That, bounteous Indra! she may live blest in her fortune and her sons.
14.1.19 Now from the noose of Varuna I free thee, where with the bless- ed Savitar hath bound thee. May bless be thine together with thy wooer in Order's dwelling, in the world of virtue.
14.1.20 Let Bhaga take thy hand and hence conduct thee: let the two Asvins on their car transport thee. Go to the house to be the household's mistress, and speak as lady to thy gathered people.
14.1.21 Happy be thou and prosper with thy children here: be vigilant to rule the household in this home. Closely unite thy body with this man thy lord. So shalt thou, full of years, address thy company.
14.1.22 Be not divided; dwell ye here; reach the full time of human life. With sons and grandsons sport and play, rejoicing in your happy home.
14.1.23 Moving by magic power from east to westward, these children twain go sporting round the ocean. The one beholds all creatures: thou, the other, art born anew, duly arranging seasons.
14.1.24 Thou, born afresh, art new and new for ever; ensign of days, before the Dawns thou goest. Coming, thou orderest for Gods their portion. Thou lengthenest, Moon, the days of our existence.
14.1.25 Give thou the wollen robe away: deal treasure to the Brahman- priests. This Witchery hath got her feet: the wife attendeth on her lord.
14.1.26 It turneth dusky-red: the witch who clingeth close is driven off. Well thrive the kinsmen of this bride: the husband is bound fast in bonds.
14.1.27 Unlovely is his body when it glistens with that wicked fiend, What time the husband wraps about his limbs the garment of his wife.
14.1.28 The butchering, the cutting-up, the severing of limb and joint-- Behold the forms which Surya wears: yet these the Brahman purifies,
14.1.29 Pungent is this, bitter is this, filled as it were with arrow barbs, empoisoned and not fit for use. The Brahman who knows Surya well deserves the garment of the bride.
14.1.30 The Brahman takes away the robe as a fair thing that brings good luck. He knows the expiating rite whereby the wife is kept unharmed.
14.1.31 Prepare, ye twain, happy and prosperous fortune, speaking the truth in faithful utterances. Dear unto her, Brihaspati, make the husband, and pleasant be these words the wooer speaketh.
14.1.32 Remain ye even here and go no farther: strengthen this man, ye Cows, with plenteous offspring. May Dawns that come for glory, bright with Soma, here may all Gods fix and enchant your spirits.
14.1.33 Come, O ye Cows, with offspring dwell around him: he doth not stint the Gods' alloted portion. To him, your friend, may Pushan, all the Maruts, to him may Dhatar, Savitar send vigour.
14.1.34 Straight in direction be the paths, and thornless, whereby our fellows travel to the wooing. With Bhaga and with Aryaman Dhatar endue the pair with strength!
14.1.35 Whatever lustre is in dice, whatever lustre is in wine, Whatever lustre is in cows, Asvins, endue this dame therewith.
14.1.36 With all the sheen that balmeth wine, or thigh of female para- mour, With all the sheen that balmeth dice, even with this adorn the dame.
14.1.37 He who in water shines unfed with fuel, whom sages worship in their sacrifices. May he, the Waters' Child, send us sweet waters those that en- hanced the power of mighty Indra.
14.1.38 I cast away a handful here, hurtful, injurious to health. I lift another handful up, sparkling and bringing happiness.
14.1.39 Hither let Brahmans bring her bathing water; let them draw such as guards the lives of heroes. Aryaman's fire let her encircle, Pushan! Fathers-in-law stand, with their sons, expectant.
14.1.40 Blest be the gold to thee, and blest the water, blest the yoke's opening, and blest the pillar. Blest he the waters with their hundred cleansings: blest be thy body's union with thy husband.
14.1.41 Cleansing Apala, Indra! thrice, thou gavest sunbright skin to her Drawn, Satakratu! through the hole of car, of wagon, and of yoke.
14.1.42 Saying thy prayer for cheerfulness, children, prosperity, and wealth, Devoted to thy husband, gird thyself for immortality.
14.1.43 As vigorous Sindhu won himself imperial lordship of the streams, So be imperial queen when thou hast come within thy husband's home.
14.1.44 Over thy husband's fathers and his brothers be imperial queen. Over thy husband's sister and, his mother bear supreme control.
14.1.45 They who have spun, and woven, and extended Goddesses who have drawn the ends together, May they invest thee for full long existence. Heiress of lengthen- ed life, endue this garment,
14.1.46 They mourn the living, they arrange the sacred rite: the men have set their thoughts upon a distant cast: They who have brought the Fathers this delightful gift, when wives allowed their lords the joy of their embrace.
14.1.47 I place upon the lap of Earth the Goddess, a firm auspicious stone to bring thee children. Stand on it, thou, greeted with joy, resplendent: a long long life may Savitar vouchsafe thee.
14.1.48 As Agni in the olden time took the right hand of this our Earth. Even so I take and hold thy hand: be not disquieted, with me, with children and with store of wealth.
14.1.49 God Savitar shall take thy hand, and Soma the King shall make thee rich in goodly offspring, Let Agni, Lord Omniscient, make thee happy, till old old age a wife unto thy husband.
14.1.50 I take thy hand in mine for happy fortune that thou mayst reach old age with me thy consort, Gods, Aryaman, Bhaga, Savitar, Purandhi, have given thee to be my household's mistress.
14.1.51 Bhaga and Savitar the God have clasped that hand of thine in theirs, By rule and law thou art my wife: the master of thy house am I.
14.1.52 Be it my care to cherish her: Brihaspati hath made thee mine. A hundred autumns live with me thy husband, mother of my sons!
14.1.53 Tvashtar, by order of the holy sages, hath laid on her Brihas- pati's robe for glory, By means of this let Savitar and Bhaga surround this dame, like Surya, with her children.
14.1.54 May Indra-Agni, Heaven-Earth, Matarisvan, may Mitra-Varuna, Bhaga, both the Asvins, Brihaspati, the host of Maruts, Brahma, and Soma magnify this dame with offspring.
14.1.55 It was Brihaspati who first arranged the hair on Surya's head, And therefore, O ye Asvins, we adorn this woman for her lord.
14.1.56 This lovely form the maiden wears in spirit I long to look on as my wife approaching, Her will I follow with my nine companions. Who is the sage that loosed the bonds that held her?
14.1.57 I free her: he who sees, within my bosom, my heart's nest knows how her fair form hath struck me. I taste no stolen food: myself untying Varuna's nooses I am freed in spirit.
14.1.58 Now from the bond of Varuna I loose thee, wherein the blessed Savitar hath bound thee. O bride, I give thee here beside thy husband fair space and room and pleasant paths to travel.
14.1.59 Lift up your weapons. Drive away the demons. Transport this woman to the world of virtue. Dilator, most wise, hath found for her a husband. Let him who knows, King Bhaga, go before her.
14.1.60 Bhaga hath formed the four legs of the litter, wrought the four pieces that compose the frame-work. Tvashtar hath decked the straps that go across it, May it be blest, and bring us happy fortune.
14.1.61 Mount this, all-hued. gold tinted, strong wheeled, fashioned of Kinsuka, this chariot lightly rolling, Bound for the world of life immortal, Surya! Made for thy lord a happy bride's procession.
14.1.62 To us, O Varuna, bring her, kind to brothers; bring her, Brihas- pati, gentle to the cattle. Bring her, O Indra, gentle to her husband: bring her to us, O Savitar, blest with children.
14.1.63 Hurt not the girl, ye Pillars twain upon the path which Gods have made. The portal of the heavenly home we make the bride's auspicious road.
14.1.64 Let prayer he offered up before and after, prayer in the middle, lastly, all around her. Reaching the Gods' inviolable castle shine in thy lord's world gentle and auspicious.
;;; II On the Bridal of Surya, marriage ceremonies in general, continued
14.2.1 For thee with bridal train they first escorted Surya to her home, Give to the husband in return, Agni, the wife with future sons.
14.2.2 Agni hath given the bride again with splendour and a lengthened. life. Long-lived be he who is her lord: a hundred autumns let him live.
14.2.3 She was the wife of Soma first: next the Gandharva was thy lord. Agni was the third husband: now one born of woman is thy fourth.
14.2.4 Soma to the Gandharva, and to Agni the Gandharva gave. Now, Agni hath bestowed on me riches and sons and this my bride.
14.2.5 Your favouring grace hath come, ye who are rich in spoil! Asvins, your longings are stored up within your hearts. Ye, Lords of Splendour have become our twofold guard: may we as dear friends reach the dwelling of the friend.
14.2.6 Thou, Dame, rejoicing, take with kindly spirit wealth worthy to be famed, with all thy heroes. Give, Lords of Light a fair ford, good to drink at: remove the spiteful stump that blocks the pathway.
14.2.7 May all the Rivers, all the Plants, may all the Forests, all the Fields, O Bride, protect thee from the fiend, guard his sons' mother for her lord.
14.2.8 Our feet are on this pleasant path, easy to travel, bringing bliss, Whereon no hero suffers harm, which wins the wealth of other men.
14.2.9 Here these my words, ye men, the benediction through which the wedded pair have found high fortune. May the divine Apsarases, Gandharvas, all they who are these fruitful trees' protectors, Regard this bride with their auspicious, favour, nor harm the nuptial pomp as it advances.
14.2.10 Consumptions, which, through various folk, attack the bride's resplendent train, These let the holy Gods again bear to the place from which they sprang.
14.2.11 Let not the highway thieves who lie in ambush find the wedded pair. Let wicked men's malignities go elsewhere by an easy path.
14.2.12 I look upon the house and bride's procession with prayer and with the gentle eye of friendship. All that is covered there in perfect beauty may Savitar make pleasant to the husband.
14.2.13 She hath come home this dame come home to bless us: this her appointed world hath Dhatar shown her. So may Prajapati, and both the Asvins, Aryaman, Bhaga gladden her with offspring.
14.2.14 This dame hath come, an animated corn-field: there sow, thou man, the seed of future harvest. She from her teeming side shall bear thee children, and feed them from the fountain of her bosom.
14.2.15 Take thou thy stand, a Queen art thou, like Vishnu here, Sarasvati! O Sinivali, let her bear children, and live in Bhaga's grace.
14.2.16 So let your wave bear up the pins, and ye, O Waters, spare the thongs; And never may the holy pair, sinless and innocent, suffer harm.
14.2.17 Not evil-eyed no slayer of thy husband, be strong, mild, kind, and gentle to thy household. Mother of heroes, love thy husband's father: be happy, and through thee may we too prosper.
14.2.18 No slayer of thy husband or his father, gentle and bright, bring blessing on the cattle. Loving thy husband's father, bring forth heroes. Tend well this household fire: be soft and pleasant.
14.2.19 Up and begone! What wish hath brought thee hither from thine own house? Thy mightier, I conjure thee. Vain is the hope, O Nirriti, that brought thee. Fly off, Malignity; stay here no longer.
14.2.20 As first of all this woman hath adored the sacred household fire. So do thou, Dame, pay homage to the Fathers and Sarasvati.
14.2.21 Take thou this wrapper as a screen, to be a covering for the bride O Sinivali, let her bear children, and live in Bhaga's grace.
14.2.22 Let her who shall be blest with sons, the maid who finds a. husband, step Upon the rough grass that ye spread and on the skin ye lay beneath.
14.2.23 Over the ruddy-coloured skin strew thou the grass, the Balbuja. Let her, the mother of good sons, sit there and serve this Agni here.
14.2.24 Step on the skin and wait upon this Agni: he is the God who drives away all demons. Here bear thou children to this man thy husband: let this thy boy be happy in his birthnight.
14.2.25 Let many babes of varied form and nature spring in succession from this fruitful mother. Wait on this fire, thou bringer of good fortune. Here with thy husband serve the Gods with worship.
14.2.26 Bliss-bringer, furthering thy household's welfare, dear gladdening thy husband and his father, enter this home, mild to thy hus- band's mother.
14.2.27 Be pleasant to the husband's sire, sweet to thy household and thy lord, To all this clan be gentle, and favour these men's prosperity.
14.2.28 Signs of good fortune mark the bride. Come all of you and look at her. Wish her prosperity: take on you her evil lucks and go your way.
14.2.29 Ye youthful maidens, ill-disposed, and all ye ancient woman here, Give all your brilliance to the bride, then to your several homes depart!
14.2.30 Surya the child of Savitar mounted for high felicity Her litter with its cloth of gold, wearing all forms of loveliness.
14.2.31 Rise, mount the bridal bed with cheerful spirit. Here bring forth children to this man thy husband. Watchful and understanding like Indrani wake thou before the earliest light of Morning.
14.2.32 The Gods at first lay down beside their consorts; body with body met in close embracement. O Dame, like Surya perfect in her grandeur, here rich in future children, meet thy husband.
14.2.33 Rise and go hence, Visvavasu: with reverence we worship thee. Steal to her sister dwelling with her father: this is the share-- mark this--of old assigned thee.
14.2.34 Apsarases rejoice and feast together between the sun and place of sacrificing. These are thy kith and kin: go thou and join them: I in due season worship thee Gandharva.
14.2.35 Homage we pay to the Gandharva's favour, obeisance to his eye and fiery anger. Visvavasu, with prayer we pay thee homage. Go hence to those Apsarases thy consorts.
14.2.36 May we be happy with abundant riches. We from this place have banished the Gandharva. The God is gone to the remotest region, and we have come where men prolong existence.
14.2.37 In your due season, Parents! come together. Mother and sire be ye of future children. Embrace this woman like a happy lover. Raise ye up offspring here: increase your riches.
14.2.38 Send her most rich in every charm, O Pushan, her who shall be the sharer of my pleasures; Her who shall twine her eager arms about me, and welcome all my love and soft embraces.
14.2.39 Up, happy bridegroom! with a joyous spirit caress thy wife and throw thine arm around her. Here take your pleasure, procreate your offspring. May Savitar bestow long life upon you.
14.2.40 So may the Lord of Life vouchsafe you children, Aryaman bind you, day and night, together. Enter thy husband's house with happy omens, bring blessing to our quadrupeds and bipeds.
14.2.41 Sent by the Gods associate with Manu, the vesture of the bride, the nuptial garment, He who bestows this on a thoughtful Brahman, drives from the marriage-bed all evil demons.
14.2.42 The priestly meed wherewith ye twain present me, the vesture of the bride, the nuptial garment, This do ye both, Brihaspati and Indra, bestow with loving-kind- ness on the Brahman.
14.2.43 On your soft couch awaking both together, revelling heartily with joy and laughter, Rich with brave sons, good cattle, goodly homestead, live long to look on many radiant mornings.
14.2.44 Clad in new garments, fragrant, well-apparelled, to meet reful- gent Dawn have I arisen. I, like a bird that quits the egg, am freed from sin and purified.
14.2.45 Splendid are Heaven and Earth, still near to bless us, mighty in their power; The seven streams have flowed: may they, Goddesses, free us from distress
14.2.46 To Surya and the Deities, to Mitra and to Varuna, Who know aright the thing that is, this adoration have I paid.
14.2.47 He without ligature, before making incision in the neck. Closed up the wound again, most wealthy Bounteous Lord who healeth the dissevered parts.
14.2.48 Let him flash gloom away from us, the blue, the yellow and the red. I fasten to this pillar here the burning pest Prishataki.
14.2.49 All witcheries that hang about this garment, all royal Varuna's entangling nooses. All failure of success and all misfortunes here I deposit fastened to the pillar.
14.2.50 My body that I hold most dear trembles in terror at this robe. Tree, make an apron at the top. Let no misfortune fall on us.
14.2.51 May all the hems and borders all the threads that form the web and woof. The garment woven by the bride, be soft and pleasant to our touch.
14.2.52 These maids who from their father's house have come with long- ing to their lord have let the preparation pass. All hail!
14.2.53 Her whom Brihaspati hath loosed the Visve Devas keep secure. With all the splendour that is stored in cows do we enrich this. girl.
14.2.54 Her whom Brihaspati hath loosed the Visve Devas keep secure. With all the vigour that is stored in cows do we enrich this girl.
14.2.55 Her whom Brihaspati, etc. With all good fortune, etc.
14.2.56 Her whom Brihaspati, etc. With all the glory, etc.
14.2.57 Her whom Brihaspati, etc. With all the milky store possessed by cows do we enrich this girl.
14.2.58 Her whom Brihaspati hath freed the Visve Devas keep secure. With all the store of sap that cows contain do we enrich this. girl.
14.2.59 If, wearing long loose hair, these men have danced together in thy house, committing sin with shout and cry, May Agni free thee from that guilt, may Savitar deliver thee,
14.2.60 If in thy house thy daughter here have wept, with wild dishevel- led locks, committing sin with her lament. May Agni, etc.
14.2.61 If the bride's sisters, if young maids have danced together in thy house, committing sin with shout and cry. May Agni free thee from that guilt, may Savitar deliver thee.
14.2.62 If any evil have been wrought by mischief-makers that affects thy cattle progeny or house, May Agni free thee from the woe, may Savitar deliver thee.
14.2.63 This woman utters wish and prayer, as down she casts the husks of corn: Long live my lord and master! yea, a hundred autumns let him live!
14.2.64 Join thou this couple, Indra! like the Chakravaka and his. mate: May they attain to full old age with children in their happy home.
14.2.65 Whatever magic hath been wrought on cushion, chair, or canopy. Each spell to mar the wedding rites, all this we throw into the bath.
14.2.66 Whatever fault or error was in marriage or in bridal pomp. This woe we wipe away upon the cloak the interceder wears.
14.2.67 We, having laid the stain and fault upon the interceder's cloak, Are pure and meet for sacrifice. May he prolong our lives for us.
14.2.68 Now let this artificial comb, wrought with a hundred teeth, remove Aught of impurity that dims the hair upon this woman's head.
14.2.69 We take away consumption from each limb and member of the bride. Let not this reach Earth, nor the Gods in heaven, let it not reach the sky or air's wide region. Let not this dust that sullies reach the Waters, nor Yama, Agni, nor the host of Fathers.
14.2.70 With all the milk that is in Earth I gird thee, with all the milk that Plants contain I dress thee. I gird thee round with children and with riches. Do thou, thus girt, receive the offered treasure.
14.2.71 I am this man, that dame art thou I am the psalm and thou the verse. I am the heaven and thou the earth. So will we dwell together here, parents of children yet to be.
14.2.72 Unmarried men desire to wed; bountiful givers wish for sons. Together may we dwell with strength unscathed for high pros- perity.
14.2.73 May they, the Fathers who, to view the bride, have joined this nuptial train, Grant to this lady and her lord children and peaceful happiness.
14.2.74 Her who first guided by a rein came hither, giving the bride, here offspring and possessions, Let them convey along the future's pathway. Splendid, with noble children, she hath conquered.
14.2.75 Wake to long life, watchful and understanding, yea, to a life shall last a hundred autumns Enter the house to be the household's mistress. A long long life let Savitar vouchsafe thee.
;;; I The hyperbolical glorification of the Vratya or Aryan Non-conformist
15.1.1 There was a roaming Vratya. He roused Prajapati to action.
15.1.2 Prajapati beheld gold in himself and engendered it.
15.1.3 That became unique, that became distinguished, that became great, that became excellent, that became Devotion, that be- came holy Fervour, that became Truth: through that he was born.
15.1.4 He grew, he became great, he became Mahadeva.
15.1.5 He gained the lordship of the Gods. He became Lord.
15.1.6 He became Chief Vratya. He held a bow, even that Bow of Indra.
15.1.7 His belly is dark-blue, his back is red.
15.1.8 With dark-blue he envelops a detested rival, with red he pierces the man who hates him: so the theologians say.
;;; II The same, continued
15.2.1 He arose and went his way to the eastern region. The Brihat, the Rathantara, the Adityas and all the Gods followed him. That man is alienated from the Brihat, the Rathantara, the Adityas, and all Gods who reviles the Vratya who possesses this knowledge. He who hath this knowledge becomes the beloved home of the Brihat, the Rathantara the Adityas, and all the Gods. In the eastern region Faith is his leman, the hymn his panegyrist, knowledge his vesture, day his turban, night his hair, Indra's two Bays his circular ornaments, the splendour of the stars his jewel. Present and Future are his running footmen, mind is his war-chariot, Matarisvan and Pavamana are they who draw it, Vita is his charioteer, Storm his goad, Fame and Glory are his harbingers. Fame and Glory come to him who hath this knowledge.
15.2.2 He arose and went away to the southern region. Yajnayajniya and Vamadevya and Sacrifice and Sacrificer and sacrificial victims followed him. The man who reviles the Vratya possessing this knowledge is alienated from Yajnayajniya and Vamadevya, Sacrifice, Sacrificer and sacrificial victims. He who hath this knowledge becomes the beloved home of Yajnayajniya,Vamadevya, Sacrifice, Sacrificer, and sacrificial victims. In the southern region Dawn is his leman, Mitra his panegyrist, knowledge his vesture, day his turban, night his hair, Indra's two Bays are his circular ornaments, New Moon Night and Full Moon Night are his running attendants, Mind, etc. as in stanza 1.
15.2.3 He arose and went away to the western region. Vairupa and Vairaja, the Waters, and King Varuna followed him. He who reviles the Vratya possessing this knowledge is alienated from Vairupa and Vairaja, the Waters and Varuna the King. He who possesses this knowledge becomes the dear home of Vairupa and Vairaja, the Waters and King Varuna. In the western region Ira is his leman, Laughter his panegyrist, knowledge, etc., as above. Day and Night are his running attendants, Mind, etc., as above.
15.2.4 He arose and went away to the northern region. Syaita and Naudhasa, the Seven Rishis, and King Soma followed him. He who reviles the Vratya possessing this knowledge is alienated from Syaita, etc. He who hath this knowledge be- comes the dear home of Syaita, etc. In the northern region Lightning is his leman, thunder his panegyrist, etc. as above. Revelation and Tradition are his running attendants, Mind, etc., as above.
;;; III Vratya
15.3.1 For a whole year he stood erect. The Gods said unto him, Why standest thou, O Vratya? He answered and said, Let them bring my couch.
15.3.3 They brought the couch for that Vratya.
15.3.4 Two of its feet were Summer and Spring, and two were Autumn and the Rains.
15.3.5 Brihat and Rathantara were the two long boards, Yajnayajniya and Vamadevya the two cross-boards.
15.3.6 Holy verses were the strings lengthwise, and Yajus formulas the cross-tapes.
15.3.7 Sacred lore was the blanket, Devotion the coverlet.
15.3.8 The Saman was the Cushion, and chanting the bolster.
15.3.9 The Vratya ascended that couch.
15.3.10 The hosts of Gods were his attendants, solemn vows his messengers, and all creatures his worshippers.
15.3.11 All creatures become the worshippers of him who possesses this knowledge.
;;; IV Vratya
15.4.1 For him they made the two Spring months protectors from the eastern region, and Brihat and Rathantara superintendents. The two Spring months protect from the eastern region, and Brihat and Rathantara superintend, the man who possesses this knowledge. For him they made the two Summer months pro- tectors from the southern region, and Yajnayajniya and Vamadevya superintendents. The two Summer months, etc. as in Verse 1,
15.4.3 They made the two Rain months, his protectors from the western region, and Vairupa and Vairaja superintendents. The two Rain months, etc. as above.
15.4.4 They made the two Autumn months his protectors from the northern region, and Syaita and Naudhasa superintendents. The two Autumn months. etc. as above.
15.4.5 They made the two Winter months his protectors from the region of the nadir, and earth and Agni superintendents. The two Winter months, etc.
15.4.6 They made the two Dewy months his protectors from the region of the zenith, and Heaven and the Adityas superintendents. The two Dewy months, etc.
;;; V Vratya
15.5.1 For him they made the Archer Bhava a deliverer from the inter- mediate space of the eastern region. Bhava the Archer, a deliverer, delivers him from the intermediate space of the eastern region. Neither Sarva nor Bhava nor Isana slays him who possesses this knowledge, or his cattle, or his kinsmen.
15.5.2 They made Sarva the Archer his deliverer from the intermediate space of the southern region, etc, as in verse 1.
15.5.3 They made Pasupati the Archer his deliverer from the inter- mediate space of the western region, etc.
15.5.4 They made the Awful God, the Archer, his deliverer from the intermediate space of the northern region, etc, as above.
15.5.5 They made Rudra the Archer his deliverer from the intermediate space of the region of the nadir etc.
15.5.6 They made Mahadeva his deliverer from the intermediate space of the region of the zenith, etc.
15.5.7 They made Isana the Archer his deliverer from all the inter- mediate regions. Isana the Archer, a deliverer, delivers him from all the intermediate regions. Neither Sarva nor Bhava, nor Isana slays him who possesses this knowledge, or his cattle, or his kinsmen.
;;; VI Vratya
15.6.1 He went his way to the region of the nadir. Earth and Agni and herbs and trees and shrubs and plants followed him. He who possesses this knowledge becomes the dear home of Earth and Agni and herbs and trees and shrubs and plants.
15.6.2 He went his way to the region of the zenith. Right and Truth and Sun and Moon and Stars followed him. He who possesses this knowledge becomes, etc., as in verse 1. mutatis mutandis.
15.6.3 He went away to the last region. Richas, Samans Yajus formulas and Devotion followed him. He who, etc., as above.
15.6.4 He went away to the great region. Itihasa and Purana and Gathas and Narasansis followed him. He who, etc.
15.6.5 He went away to the supreme region. The Ehavaniya, Garha- patya, and Southern Fires, and Sacrifice, and Sacrificer, and sacrificial victims followed him. He who, etc.
15.6.6 He went away to the unindicated region. The Seasons, groups of seasons, the worlds and their inhabitants, the months and half-months, and Day and Night followed him. He who, etc.
15.6.7 He went away to the unfrequented region. Thence he thought that he should not return. Diti and Aditi and Ida and Indrani followed him. He who, etc.
15.6.8 He went away to the regions. Viraj and all the Gods and all the Deities followed him. He who, etc.
15.6.9 He went away to all the intermediate spaces. Prajapati and Parameshthin and the Father and the Great Father followed him. He who possesses this knowledge becomes the beloved home of Prajapati and Parameshthin and the Father and the Great Father.
;;; VII Vratya
15.7.1 He, having become moving majesty, went to the ends of the earth. He became the sea.
15.7.2 Prajapati and Parameshthin and the Father and the Great Father and the Waters and Faith, turned into rain, followed him.
15.7.3 The Waters, Faith, and rain approach him who possesses this knowledge.
15.7.4 Faith, and Sacrifice and the world, having become food and nourishment, turned toward him.
15.7.5 Faith Sacrifice, the world, food and nourishment approach him who possesses this knowledge.
;;; VIII Vratya
15.8.1 He was filled with passion: from him sprang the Rajanya.
15.8.2 He came to the people, to kinsmen, food and nourishment.
15.8.3 He who possesses this knowledge becomes the dear home of the people, kinsmen, food and nourishment.
;;; IX Vratya
15.9.1 He went away to the people.
15.9.2 Meeting and Assembly and Army and Wine followed him.
15.9.3 He who hath this knowledge becomes the dear home of Meeting, Assembly, Army, and Wine.
;;; X Vratya
15.10.1 So let the King, to whose house the Vratya who possesses this knowledge comes as a guest.
15.10.2 Honour him as superior to himself. So he Both not act against the interests of his princely rank or his kingdom.
15.10.3 From him, verily, sprang Priesthood and Royalty. They said, Into whom shall we enter?
15.10.4 Let Priesthood enter into Brihaspati, and Royalty into Indra, was the answer.
15.10.5 Hence Priesthood entered into Brihaspati and Royalty into Indra.
15.10.6 Now this Earth is Brihaspati, and Heaven is Indra.
15.10.7 Now this Agni is Priesthood, and yonder Sun is Royalty.
15.10.8 Priesthood comes to him, and he becomes endowed with priestly lustre.
15.10.9 Who knows that Earth is Brihaspati and Agni Priesthood.
15.10.10 Great power comes to him and he becomes endowed with great power.
15.10.11 Who knows that Aditya is Royalty and that Heaven is Indra.
;;; XI Vratya
15.11.1 Let him to whose house the Vratya who possesses this knowledge comes as a guest.
15.11.2 Rise up of his own accord to meet him, and say, Vratya, where didst thou pass the night? Vratya, here is water, Let them refresh thee. Vratya, let it be as thou pleasest. Vratya, as thy wish is so let it be. Vratya, as thy desire is so be it.
15.11.3 When he says to his guest, Where didst thou pass the night? he reserves for himself thereby the paths that lead to the Gods.
15.11.4 When he says to him, Here is water, he secures thereby water for himself.
15.11.5 When he says to him, Let them refresh thee, he thereby wins vital breath to exceeding old age.
15.11.6 When he says to him, Vratya, let it be as thou pleasest, he secures to himself thereby what is pleasant.
15.11.7 That which is pleasant comes to him, and he is the beloved of the beloved, who is possessed of this knowledge.
15.11.8 When he says to him, Vratya, as thy will is so let it be, he secures to himself thereby the fulfilment of his will.
15.11.9 Authority comes to him who possesses this knowledge, and he becomes the controller of the powerful.
15.11.10 When he says to him, Vratya, as thy desire is so be it, he secures to himself thereby the attainment of his desire.
15.11.11 His desire comes to him who possesses this knowledge and he gains the complete satisfaction of his wish.
;;; XII Vratya
15.12.1 The man, to whose house, when the fires have been taken up from the hearth and the oblation to Agni placed therein, the Vratya possessing this knowledge comes as a guest.
15.12.2 Should of his own accord rise to meet him and say, Vratya, give me permission. I will sacrifice.
15.12.3 And if he gives permission he should sacrifice, if he does not permit him he should not sacrifice.
15.12.4 He who sacrifices when permitted by the Vratya who possesses this knowledge.
15.12.5 Well knows the path that leads to the Fathers and the way that. leads to the Gods.
15.12.6 He does not act in opposition to the Gods. It becomes his sacrifice.
15.12.7 The abode of the man who sacrifices when permitted by the Vratya who possesses this knowledge is long left remaining in this world.
15.12.8 But he who sacrifices without the permission of the Vratya who- possesses this knowledge.
15.12.9 Knows not the path that leads to the Fathers nor the way that leads to the Gods.
15.12.10 He is at variance with the Gods. He hath offered no accepted. sacrifice.
15.12.11 The abode of the man who sacrifices without the permission of the Vratya who possesses this knowledge is not left remaining in this world.
;;; XIII Vratya
15.13.1 He in whose house the Vratya who possesses this knowledge abides one night secures for himself thereby the holy realms that are on earth.
15.13.2 A second night . . . . the holy realms that are in the firma- ment (the rest as in verse 1).
15.13.3 A third night . . . the holy realms that are in heaven.
15.13.4 A fourth night . . . . the holy realms of the Holy.
15.13.5 Unlimited nights . . . . unlimited holy realms.
15.13.6 Now he to whose house a non-Vratya, calling himself a Vratya, and one in name only, comes as a guest.
15.13.7 Should punish him and not punish him.
15.13.8 He should serve him with food saying to himself, To this Deity I offer water: I lodge this Deity; I wait upon this, this Deity.
15.13.9 To that Deity the sacrifice of him who has this knowledge is acceptable.
;;; XIV Vratya
15.14.1 He when he went away to the eastern region, went away having become the Marut host, and having made Mind an eater of food. He who hath this knowledge eats food with Mind as food-eater.
15.14.2 He, when he went away to the southern region, went away having become Indra, and having made Strength an eater of food. He who hath this knowledge eats food with strength as food-eater.
15.14.3 He, when he went away to the western region, went away having become King Varuna, and having made the Waters eaters of food. He who hath this knowledge eats food with the Waters as food-eaters.
15.14.4 He, when he went away to the northern region, went away having become King Soma and having made the Seven Rishis' oblation an eater of food. He who hath this knowledge eats food with oblation as food-eater.
15.14.5 He, when he went away to the stedfast region, went away having become Vishnu and having made Viraj an eater of food. He who hath this knowledge eats food with Viraj as food-eater.
15.14.6 He, when he went away to animals, went away having become Rudra and having made herbs eaters of food. He who hath this knowledge eats food with herbs as food-eaters.
15.14.7 He, when he went away to the Fathers, went away having be- come King Yama and having made the exclamation Svadha an eater of food. He who hath this knowledge eats food with the exclamation Svadha as food-eater.
15.14.8 He, when he went away to men, went away having become Agni and having made the exclamation Svaha an eater of food. He who hath this knowledge eats food with the exclamation Svaha as food-eater.
15.14.9 He, when he went away to the upper region, went away having become Brihaspati and having made the exclamation Vashat an eater of food. He who hath this knowledge eats food with the exclamation Vashat as food-eater.
15.14.10 He, when he went away to the Gods, went away having become Isana and having made Passion an eater of food. He who hath this knowledge eats food with Passion as food-eater.
15.14.11 He, when he went away to creatures, went away having become Prajapati and having made vital breath an eater of food. He who hath this knowledge eats food with vital breath as foodeater.
15.14.12 He, when he went away to all the intermediate spaces, went away having become Parameshthin and having made Devotion an eater of food. He who hath this knowledge eats food with Devotion as food-eater.
;;; XV Vratya
15.15.1 Of that Vratya.
15.15.2 There are seven vital airs, seven downward breaths, seven diff- used breaths.
15.15.3 His first vital breath, called Upward, is this Agni.
15.15.4 His second vital breath, called Mature, is that Aditya.
15.15.5 His third vital breath, called Approached, is that Moon.
15.15.6 His fourth vital breath, called Pervading is this Pavamana.
15.15.7 His fifth vital breath, called Source, are these Waters.
15.15.8 His sixth vital breath, called Dear, are these domestic animals.
15.15.9 His seventh vital breath, called Unlimited, are these creatures.
;;; XVI Vratya
15.16.1 His first downward breath is the time of Full Moon.
15.16.2 His second downward breath is the eighth day after Full Moon.
15.16.3 His third downward breath is the night of New Moon.
15.16.4 His fourth downward breath is Faith.
15.16.5 His fifth downward breath is Consecration.
15.16.6 His sixth downward breath is Sacrifice.
15.16.7 His seventh downward breath are these sacrificial fees.
;;; XVII Vratya
15.17.1 His first diffused breath is this Earth.
15.17.2 His second diffused breath is that Firmament.
15.17.3 His third diffused breath is that Heaven.
15.17.4 His fourth diffused breath are those Constellations.
15.17.5 His fifth diffused breath are the Seasons.
15.17.6 His sixth diffused breath are the Season-groups.
15.17.7 His seventh diffused breath is the year.
15.17.8 With one and the same object the Gods go round the Year and the Seasons follow round the Vratya.
15.17.9 When they surround the Sun on the day of New Moon, and that time of Full Moon.
15.17.10 That one immortality of theirs is just an oblation.
;;; XVIII Vratya
15.18.1 Of that Vratya.
15.18.2 The right eye is the Sun and the left eye is the Moon.
15.18.3 His right ear is Agni and his left ear is Pavamana.
15.18.4 Day and Night are his nostrils. Diti and Aditi are his head and skull.
15.18.5 By day the Vratya is turned westward, by night he is turned eastward. Worship to the Vratya!
;;; I On the preparation and use of holy water, with, a prayer for purification and freedom from sin
16.1.1 The Bull of the Waters hath been let go; the heavenly fires have been let go.
16.1.2 Breaking, breaking down, crushing, crushing to pieces,
16.1.3 Mroka, mind-destroying, rooting up, consuming, ruiner of the soul, ruiner of the body.
16.1.4 Here I let him go: thou washest me clean of him.
16.1.5 With this we let him loose who hates us and whom we hate.
16.1.6 Thou art in front of the waters. I let loose your sea.
16.1.7 I let loose the Agni who is within the waters, Mroka the up- rooter, the destroyer of the body.
16.1.8 Your Agni who entered into the waters, even he here is that very dread of yours.
16.1.9 May he anoint you with Indra's own mighty power!
16.1.10 May stainless waters cleanse us from defilement.
16.1.11 May they carry sin away from us, may they carry away from us the evil dream.
16.1.12 Look on me with a friendly eye, O, Waters, and touch my skin with your auspicious body.
16.1.13 We call the gracious Fires that dwell in waters. Goddesses, grant me princely power and splendour.
;;; II A charm to secure various blessings
16.2.1 Away from distasteful food, strength and sweet speech,
16.2.2 Are pleasant. May I obtain a pleasant voice.
16.2.3 I have invoked the Protector; I have invoked his protection.
16.2.4 Quick of hearing are mine ears; mine ears hear what is good- Fain would I hear a pleasant sound.
16.2.5 Let not good hearing and overhearing fail the Eagle's eye, the undecaying light.
16.2.6 Thou art the couch of the Rishis. Let worship be paid to the divine couch.
;;; III A charm to secure power and long life
16.3.1 I am the head of riches. Fain would I be the head of mine equals.
16.3.2 Let not Ruja and Vena desert me. Let not the Head and the Preserver forsake me.
16.3.3 Let not the Boiler and the Cup fail tme: let not the Supporter and the Sustainer abandon me.
16.3.4 Let not Unyoking and the Moist-fellied car desert me: let not the Sender of Moisture and Matarisvan forsake me.
16.3.5 Brihaspati is my soul, he who is called the Friend of man, dear to my heart.
16.3.6 My heart is free from sorrow; spacious is my dwelling-place. I am the sea in capacity.
;;; IV A charm to secure long life and success
16.4.1 I am the:centre of riches. Fain would I be the centre of mine equals.
16.4.2 Pleasant art thou to sit by one, a mother: immortal among mortals.
16.4.3 Let not inward breath desert me; let not outward breath depart and leave me.
16.4.4 Let Surya protect me from Day, Agni from Earth, Vayu from Firmament, Yama from men, Sarasvati from dwellers on the earth.
16.4.5 Let not outward and inward breath fail me. Be not thou destruc- tive among the men.
16.4.6 Propitious to-day be dawns and evenings. May I drink water with all my people safe around me.
16.4.7 Mighty are ye, domestic creatures. May Mitra-Varuna stand beside me. May Agni give me inward and outward breath. May,he give me ability.
;;; V A charm against evil dreams
16.5.1 We know thine origin, O Sleep. Thou art the son of Grahi, the minister of Yama. Thou art the Ender, thou art Death. As such, O Sleep, we know thee well. As such preserve us from the evil dream.
16.5.2 We know thine origin, O Sleep. Thou art the son of Destruction, the minister of Yama, etc. (as in verse 1).
16.5.3 We know thine origin, O Sleep. Thou art the son of Misery, etc.
16.5.4 We know thine origin, O Sleep. Thou art the son of Disappear- ance, etc.
16.5.5 We know thine origin, O Sleep. Thou art the son of Defeat etc.
16.5.6 We know thine origin, O Sleep. Thou art the son of the sisters of the Gods, the minister of Yama. Thou art the Ender, thou are Death. As such, O Sleep, we know thee well. As such, preserve us from the evil dream.
;;; VI A charm to avert evil dreams, and to transfer them to an enemy
16.6.1 Now have we conquered and obtained: we have been freed from sin to-day.
16.6.2 Let Morning with her light dispel that evil dream that frightened us.
16.6.3 Bear that away to him who hates, away to him who curses us.
16.6.4 To him whom we abhor, to him who hates us do we send it hence.
16.6.5 May the Goddess Dawn in accord with Speech, and the Goddess Speech in accord with Dawn,
16.6.6 The Lord of Dawn in accord with the Lord of Speech and the Lord of Speech in accord with the Lord of Dawn,
16.6.7 Carry away to Such-an-one niggard fiends, hostile demons, and Sadanvas,
16.6.8 Kumbhikas, Dushikas, and Piyakas,
16.6.9 Evil day-dream, evil dream in sleep,
16.6.10 Wishes for boons that will not come, thoughts of poverty, the snares of the Druh who never releases.
16.6.11 This, O Agni, let the Gods bear off to Such-an-one that he may be a fragile good-for-nothing eunuch.
;;; VII An imprecation on an enemy
16.7.1 Herewith I pierce this man. With poverty I pierce him. With disappearance I pierce him. With defeat I pierce him. With Grahi I pierce him. With darkness I pierce him.
16.7.2 I summon him with the awful cruel orders of the Gods.
16.7.3 I place him between Vaisvanara's jaws.
16.7.4 Thus or otherwise let her swallow him up.
16.7.5 Him who hates us may his soul hate, and may he whom we hate hate himself.
16.7.6 We scorch out of heaven and earth and firmament the man who hates us.
16.7.7 Suyaman son of Chakshus.
16.7.8 Here I wipe away the evil dream on the descendant of Such-an- one, son of Such-a-woman.
16.7.9 Whatsoever I have met with, whether at dusk or during early night,
16.7.10 Whether waking or sleeping, whether by day or by night.
16.7.11 Whether I meet with it day by day, from that do I bribe him away.
16.7.12 Slay him; rejoice in this; crush his ribs.
16.7.13 Let him not live. Let the breath of life forsake him.
;;; VIII An imprecation on an enemy
16.8.1 Whatever we have gained, whatever hath accrued to us, our Right, our energy, our Devotion, our heavenly light, our sacrifice, our domestic animals, our offspring, our men,--from all share herein we exclude Such-an-one, descendant of Such- an-one, son of Such-a-woman. Let him not be freed from the noose of Grahi. Here I bind up his splendour, his energy, his vital breath, his life, and cast him down beneath me.
16.8.2 Whatever we have gained, etc. (as in verse 1). Let him not be freed from the noose of Nirriti, etc.
16.8.3 Whatever we have gained, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of misery, etc.
16.8.4 Whatever we have gained, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of disappearance, etc.
16.8.5 Whatever we have gained, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of defeat, etc.
16.8.6 Whatever we have gained, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of the sisters of the Gods, etc.
16.8.7 Whatever we have gained, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of Brihaspati, etc.
16.8.8 Whatever we have gained, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of Prajapati, etc.
16.8.9 Whatever we have gained, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of the Rishis, etc.
16.8.10 Whatever we have gained, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of the Rishis' children, etc.
16.8.11 Whatever, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of the Angirases, etc.
16.8.12 Whatever, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of the Angirases, etc.
16.8.13 Whatever, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of the Atharvans, etc.
16.8.14 Whatever, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of the Atharvans, etc.
16.8.15 Whatever, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of the Trees, etc.
16.8.16 Whatever, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of Shrubs, etc.
16.8.17 Whatever, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of the Seasons, etc.
16.8.18 Whatever, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of the Season-groups, etc.
16.8.19 Whatever, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of the Months, etc.
16.8.20 Whatever, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of the Half- months, etc.
16.8.21 Whatever, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of Day and Night, etc.
16.8.22 Whatever, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of continued Day, etc.
16.8.23 Whatever, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of Heaven and Earth, etc.
16.8.24 Whatever, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of Indra- Agni, etc.
16.8.25 Whatever, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of Mitra- Varuna, etc.
16.8.26 Whatever, etc. Let him not be freed from the noose of King Varuna, etc.
16.8.27 Whatever we have gained, whatever hath accrued to us, our Right, our energy, our Devotion, our heavenly light, our sacrifice, our domestic animals, our offspring, our men,--from all share herein we exclude Such-as-one, descendant of Such- an-one, son of Such-a-woman. Let him not be freed from the fetter and noose of Death. Here I bind up his splendour, his energy, his vital breath, his life, and cast him down beneath me.
;;; IX A charm to secure wealth and felicity
16.9.1 Ours is superior place and ours is conquest: may I in all fights tread down spite and malice.
16.9.2 This word hath Agni, this hath Soma spoken. May Pushan set me in the world of virtue.
16.9.3 We have come to the light of heaven; to the light of heaven have we come: we have united with the light of Surya.
16.9.4 Sacrifice is fraught with wealth for the increase of prosperity. I would win riches; fain would I be wealthy. Do thou bestow wealth upon me.
;;; I A prayer to Indra, Identified with Vishnu and the Sun, for the love of Gods, men, and beasts, general protection and prosperity, and all earthly and heavenly blessings
17.1.1 Vanquishing, overpowering, a conqueror, exceeding strong, Victorious, winner of the light, winner of cattle and of spoil,. Indra by name, adorable, I call: a long, long life be mine!
17.1.2 Vanquishing etc. Indra by name, adorable I call: May I be dear to Gods.
17.1.3 Vanquishing, etc. Indra by name, adorable, I call: may creatures love me well.
17.1.4 Vanquishing, etc. Indra by name, adorable, I call: may cattle hold me dear.
17.1.5 Vanquishing, etc. Indra by name, adorable, I call: may equals love me well.
17.1.6 Rise up, O Surya, rise thou up; with strength and splendour rise on me. Let him who hates me be my thrall; let me not be a thrall to him. Manifold are thy great deeds, thine, O Vishnu. Sate us with cattle of all forms and colours: set me in happiness, in loftiest heaven.
