19.30.5 What time Parjanya roared to it with lightning flashes in the sea, Thence came the drop, the golden drop, thence Darbha into being sprang.
;;; XXXI A charm to ensure general prosperity, accompanying self-investiture with an amulet of Udumbara
19.31.1 Savitar make all cattle grow and prosper in my stable with. Amulet of Udumbara, helper of him who longs for wealth!
19.31.2 May he who was our Household Fire, the ruler of our cattle, strong. Amulet of Udumbara endow us with prosperity.
19.31.3 By power of the Udumbara Charm may Dhatar give me plenty, rich. In the kine's droppings and in fruit, and, in our dwelling, food, and drink.
19.31.4 I win great plenty, while I wear the Amulet of Udumbara. Of quadrupeds and bipeds, of juices and food of every sort.
19.31.5 I have obtained abundant wealth of cattle, bipeds and quad- rupeds, and corn in plenty. Savitar and Brihaspati vouchsafe me the milk of kine and herbs' refreshing juices!
19.31.6 Fain would I be the lord of herds of cattle: may he who rules o'er riches send me riches! May the Udumbara Amulet vouchsafe possessions unto me.
19.31.7 To me with wealth and children come the Amulet of Udumbara. With splendour come the Amulet hastened by Indra on its way!
19.31.8 Divine, foe-quelling Amulet, wealth-winner for the gain of wealth-- May it give store of beasts and food and cause our kine to multiply.
19.31.9 As thou, O Forest Tree, wast born with increase when thy life began, So let Sarasvati bestow abundant growth of wealth on me.
19.31.10 Sarasvati vouchsafe me wealth, household prosperity, and corn! Let Sinivali bring them, and this Amulet of Udumbara.
19.31.11 The Lord of amulets art thou, most mighty: in thee wealth's ruler hath engendered riches, These gains are lodged in thee, and all great treasures. Amulet, conquer thou: far from us banish malignity and indigence, and hunger.
19.31.12 Vigour art thou, in me do thou plant vigour: riches art thou, so do thou grant me riches. Plenty art thou, so prosper me with plenty: House-holder, hear" a householder's petition.
19.31.13 Amulet of Udumbara, enrich us: vouchsafe us wealth with all good men about us. I bind thee on for increase of possessions.
19.31.14 For hero is this hero bound, Amulet of Udumbara. So may he make our offering sweetly-savoured, and grant us wealth with all good men about us.
;;; XXXII A charm, with an amulet of Darbha grass, to subdue enemies and win the affection of others
19.32.1 For lengthened life I bind on thee the Darbha grass, the mighty plant. Excellent, hard to overthrow, with hundred stems and thousand blades.
19.32.2 They cut not off his hair, they strike blow upon the breast for' him. To whom one gives protection by Darbha that hath uninjured leaves.
19.32.3 O Plant, thy root is in the sky, and thou art stationed on the earth: With thee who hast a thousand stalks we strengthen all the powers of life.
19.32.4 Through all three skies the plant hath pierced, and the three regions of the earth; With thee I split in twain the tongue and words of the bad- hearted man.
19.32.5 Thou art victorious in thy might I am endowed with conquering strength: Possessed of overpowering force we two will quell our enemies.
19.32.6 Subdue our foeman, overcome the men who fain would fight: with us. Conquer all evil-hearted ones: make many well-disposed to me.
19.32.7 With Darbha that hath sprung from Gods, stationed in heaven, full many a time. With this have I won many men, have won and may I win them still.
19.32.8 Do thou, O Darbha, make me dear to Brahman and Rajanya, dear to Sudra, and to Arya dear, Yea, dear to every man we love, to every man with eyes to see.
19.32.9 He who first born fixed earth in her position, he who established heaven and air's mid-region, Whom sinner ne'er hath known as his supporter,--this Darbha be our shelter and protection!
19.32.10 First of all plants it sprang into existence, victorious, hundred- stemmed, the foe-subduer, So may this Darbha from all sides protect us: with this may I subdue our foes in battle.
;;; XXXIII A protective and benedictive charm
19.33.1 Hundred stemmed, succulent, and worth a thousand, the Royal Rite of plants, the Water's Agni, Let this same Darbha guard us from all quarters. This Godlike Amulet shall with life endow us.
19.33.2 Drawn forth from butter, juicy, sweetly-flavoured, firm as the earth, unshaken, overthrowing. Driving off foes and casting them beneath me, mount with the strength of mighty Ones, O Darbha.
19.33.3 Thou movest o'er the earth with vigour: lovely in sacrifice thou sittest on the altar. The Rishis bear thee as a purifier: cleanse thou us from all evil deeds' defilement.
19.33.4 A stern and all-victorious king, foe-queller, dear to every man-- That energy of Gods and mighty power, I bind this on thee for long life and welfare.
19.33.5 Achieve heroic deeds with Darbha, wearing this Darbha never let thy soul be troubled. In splendour and precedence over others illumine like the Sun the heaven's four regions.
;;; XXXIV A protective charm addressed to the panacea called A Jangida
19.34.1 Jangida, thou art Angiras: thou art a guardian, Jangida. Let Jangida, keep safely all our bipeds and our quadrupeds.
19.34.2 Dice-witcheries, the fifty-threes, the hundred witchcraft-practi- sers, All these may Jangida make weak, bereft of their effectual force.
19.34.3 Baffle the loud factitious howl, make impotent the seven decays. As when an archer speeds the shaft, drive away want, O Jangida,
19.34.4 This counteracts the sorceress, this banishes malignity: Then may victorious Jangida's prolong the days we have to live.
19.34.5 Let Jangida's protecting might encompass us on every side. Wherewith he quells Vishkandha and Sanskandha, might by greater might.
19.34.6 Three times the Gods engendered thee fixt on the surface of the earth; The Brahmans of the olden time knew that thy name was Angiras;
19.34.7 The ancient plants surpass thee not, nor any herbs of recent days. A potent charm is Jangida, a most felicitous defence.
19.34.8 Then when thou sprangest into life, Jangida of un-measured strength, Indra, O mighty One, bestowed great power upon thee from the first.
19.34.9 To thee in truth, O Forest Tree, Indra the mighty One gave strength. Driving away all maladies, strike thou the demons down, O Plant.
19.34.10 Lumbago and rheumatic pain, consumptive cough, and pleurisy, And fever which each Autumn brings, may Jangida make- powerless.
;;; XXXV A similar charm addressed to the same
19.35.1 While their lips uttered Indra's name the Rishis gave us Jangida.. Which in the earliest time Gods made a remedy, Vishkandha's- cure.
19.35.2 So may this Jangida guard us, even as a treasurer guards wealth,. Even this which Gods and Brahmans made a malice-quelling sure defence.
19.35.3 Hard-hearted men, the cruel eye, the sinner who hath come to- us, Destroy thou these with watchful care, O thou who hast a. thousand eyes. Thou, Jangida, art my defence.
19.35.4 Guard me from earth and guard me from the heavens, guard me from middle air, from plants protect me. Protect me from the present and the future. From every region Jangida preserve us!
19.35.5 All sorcerers made by the Gods, all that arise from mortal men,. These, one and all, let Jangida, healer of all, make impotent.
;;; XXXVI A charm against disease and evil spirits
19.36.1 The Hundred-haired hath banished hence fiends and Consump- tions by its might. With splendour hath the charm that scares demons of ill-name mounted up.
19.36.2 It drives off demons with its horns and sorceresses with its root, It stays Consumption with its waist: from this no wickedness escapes.
19.36.3 Consumptions, light and serious, and those which sounds accompany, All these the Amulet, Hundred-haired, scarer of fiends, hath banished hence.
19.36.4 A hundred men hath it produced, hundred Consumptions chased away, All fiends of evil-name it hath smitten, and shakes the Rakshasas.
19.36.5 The Bull that weareth horns of gold, this Amulet with hundred hairs, Hath cleft the demons of ill-name and overcome the Rakshasas.
19.36.6 Hundred she-fiends, a hundred of Gandharvas and Apsarasas, A hundred of dog-mated nymphs, I keep away with Hundred- Hair
;;; XXXVII A charm to secure long life and dominion to a prince
19.37.1 To me hath come this word given by Agni, fame, force and might, and strength, and life, and lustre. May Agni too bestow on me three-times a hundred manly powers.
19.37.2 For mighty strength, for action, I receive thee, for manly power, to last a hundred autumns.
19.37.3 For conquering strength and energy and vigour I fasten thee for chieftainship, for bearing royal dominion through a hundred autumns.
19.37.4 With Seasons and with Season-groups, for vigour and extended life. With splendour of the perfect year we fasten thee about the neck.
;;; XXXVIII A protective charm
19.38.1 Never Consumption, never curse touches the man, Arundhati! Whom the delicious odour of the healing Bdellium penetrates
19.38.2 Consumptions flee apart from it as from a wild beast fly the deer. If thou, O Bdellium, art produced from Sindhu or hast come from sea, The quality of both have I taken to keep this man unscathed.
;;; XXXIX A protective charm
19.39.1 Let Kushtha from the Hill of Snow come, a divine deliverer. Banish thou all Consumption, drive all sorceresses far away.
19.39.2 Kushtha, three several names hast thou, Naghamara, Nagharisha: let not mishap befall this man, For whom I make a charm of thee at eve, at morning, and by day.
19.39.3 Jivala is thy mother's name, thy father's name is Jivala; let not mishap, etc.
19.39.4 Thou art the best amid the plants, even as the ox is best of tame, the tiger of rapacious beasts: let not mishap, etc.
19.39.5 Born thrice from the Adityas, thrice from Bhrigus, thrice from Angiras' sons, born from the Visve Devas thrice, Healer of every malady, that Kushtha stands by Soma's side. Banish thou all Consumption, drive all sorceresses far away.
19.39.6 In the third heaven above us stands the Asvattha tree, the seat of Gods: There is embodiment of life that dies not: thence was Kushtha born.
19.39.7 There moved through heaven a golden ship, a ship with cordage wrought of gold: There is embodiment of life that dies not; thence was Kushtha born.
19.39.8 Where is the Sinking of the Ship, the summit of the Hill of Snow, There is embodiment of life that dies not: thence was Kustha born. Healer of every malady, that Kushtha stands by Soma's side. Banish thou all Consumption, drive all sorceresses far away.
19.39.9 Thou whom Ikshvaku's ancestor, whom he who well-loved Kushtha, knew, Whom Vayasa and Matsya knew, hence healer of all ills art thou.
19.39.10 O thou who hast all-reaching might drive away Fever, drive it down, racking Fever, tertian, continual, lasting for a year.
;;; XL A prayer for pardon of error in sacrifice, and for wisdom, strength, and life
19.40.1 For each defect of mine in voice and spirit I have approached One vehement and ardent. With all the Deities, fully approving, Brihaspati supply the want!
19.40.2 Disturb ye not our intellect, O Waters, nor the power of prayer_ Glide on your way, strength-giving, invocated: may I be vigor- ous and wise.
19.40.3 Mar not our consecrating rite, our intellect, or fervent zeal. Gracious to us for lengthened life, propitious let the Mothers be.
19.40.4 Vouchsafe to us, ye Asvins twain, such strength as, with atten- dant light, May through the darkness carry us.
;;; XLI A benediction on a newly elected king
19.41.1 Desiring bliss, at first, light-finding Rishis began religious rite and holy fervour. Thence energy was born, and might, and kingship: so to this man let gathered Gods incline them.
;;; XLII In praise of Brahma, Prayer, or Devotion
19.42.1 Brahma is Hotar, sacrifice: with Brahma are the stakes set up. From Brahma was the Adhvaryu born, from Brahma hidden offering.
19.42.2 Brahma is fatness-dropping scoops: with Brahma was the altar reared. Brahma is worship, lengthened rite, the Rishis who pay sacrifice, the victim's Immolators. Hail!
19.42.3 To him who frees from woe mine hymn I offer, to the Good Guardian, as I seek his favour. Accept this offering of mine, O Indra. Fulfilled be all the sacri- ficer's wishes!
19.42.4 With prayer I call on him who frees from trouble, Prince of Gods, Splendid, chief of sacrifices, I call the Waters' Child and both the Asvins, Vigour is mine, and strength bestowed by Indra.
;;; XLIII In praise of Brahma, Prayer, or Devotion
19.43.1 Whither men versed in Brahma go, with fervour and the cleans- ing rite, Thither let Agni lead me, let Agni give me intelligence, All hail to Agni!
19.43.2 Whither etc. Thither let Vayu lead me, let Vayu vouchsafe me vital breath. All hail to Vayu!
19.43.3 Whither, etc. Thither let Surya lead me, let Surya vouchsafe me power of sight. All hail to Surya
19.43.4 Whither, etc. Thither let Chandra lead me, let Chandra vouchsafe me intellect. All hail to Chandra!
19.43.5 Whither, etc. Thither let Soma lead me, let Soma vouchsafe me vital sap. All hail to Soma!
19.43.6 Whither, etc. Thither let Indra lead me, let Indra bestow upon me power. All hail to Indra!
19.43.7 Whither, etc. Thither, let Waters lead me, let the Waters give me deathless life. All hail to Waters!
19.43.8 Whither, etc. Thither let Brahma lead me, let Brahma give Brahma unto me. All hail to Brahma!
;;; XLIV A curative and protective charm
19.44.1 Thou art the lengthening of life, thy name is Universal Cure: Then, Ointment! send felicity; Waters, send happiness and peace.
19.44.2 The yellow hue, the feverish heat, the shooting pain that rends II the limbs, All the consumptive malady let the Ointment drive from out thy frame.
19.44.3 Let the Salve born upon the earth, benignant, giving life to man. Make the swift rider on the car sinless, exempt from sudden death.
19.44.4 Preserve our breath, O Vital Breath, have mercy on our life, O Life. From snares of Nirriti do thou, O Nirriti, deliver us.
19.44.5 Thou art the babe of Sindhu, thou art lightnings' flower, wind, breath, and Sun: thou art the eye and milk of heaven.
19.44.6 Gods' Ointment from the Three Peaked Hill, preserve thou me on every side. No plants of earth surpass thee, none from mountain or from cultured ground.
19.44.7 Now hath it gently crept within, fiend-slaying, chasing malady. And driving all diseases hence, and evil omens, banished them.
19.44.8 Full many a falsehood, O thou King Varuna, man hath uttered here: Do thou who hast a thousand powers preserve us from that misery.
19.44.9 If we have cried, O Waters! Cows! if we have cried, O Varuna! For this endowed with thousand powers! deliver us from misery.
19.44.10 Mitra and Varuna, O Salve have closely followed after thee May they, when they have followed thee afar, restore thee for our use.
;;; XLV A curative and protective charm
19.45.1 As debt from debt repay and send sorcery to the sorcerer's house. Split, Salve! the cruel villain's ribs whose evil eye bewitches us.
19.45.2 Whatever evil dream we have, what'er befall our kine or home, Be this that is salubrity, the evil-hearted's foe applied.
19.45.3 Increasing from the Waters' strength and vigour, sprung into life from Agni Jatavedas, Strong as four heroes, mountain born, this Ointment make for thee quarters and mind-points auspicious!
19.45.4 On thee is laid the Chaturvira Ointment: let all the regions give thee peace and safety. Secure like precious Savitar thou standest: to thee let all these regions bring their tribute.
19.45.5 Make one thy salve, thine amulet another, drink one, and with another bathe thy body. So let the Chaturvira keep us guarded from the four bonds of Nirriti and Grahi.
19.45.6 May Agni protect me with fire for inspiration and expiration, for strength, for energy, for vigour, for weal and prosperity. All Hail!
19.45.7 May Indra protect me with his Indra-power for inspiration, etc.
19.45.8 May Soma protect me with Soma-power, etc.
19.45.9 May Bhaga with good fortune protect me, etc.
19.45.10 May the Maruts protect me with their troops for inspiration and expiration, for strength, for energy, for vigour, for weal and prosperity. All Hail!
;;; XLVI A charm accompanying investiture with an amulet that ensures safety and victory
19.46.1 For manly strength Prajapati bound thee on first, invincible. This for long life on thee I bind for splendour, strength, and energy. Invincible, let it guard thee well.
19.46.2 Erect, invincible, be this man's watchful keeper: let not the Panis or the sorcerers harm thee. Shake off thy foes as Indra scattered Dasyus: quell all enemies. Invincible, let it guard thee well.
19.46.3 Indra hath lent the power of sight, and vital breath and strength to this. Whom even a hundred combatants, striking, have failed to over- come. Invincible, let it guard thee well.
19.46.4 Around thy limbs I place the mail of Indra who hath become the Gods' imperial Sovran. Again let all the Deities bring thee hither. Invincible let it guard thee well.
19.46.5 One and a hundred manly powers, a thousand lives hath this Amulet, unconquered ever. Go forth a tiger, strike down all thy foemen: let him who would oppose fall low beneath thee. Invincible, let it guard thee well.
19.46.6 Drawn forth from butter, rich in milk and sweetness, hundred- lived, thousand-homed, bestowing vigour, Kindly, delightsome, full of sap, and mighty, invincible let it guard thee well.
19.46.7 That thou mayst be pre-eminent, slayer of rivals, rivalless, May Savitar cause thee to be chief and controller of thy kin. Invincible, let it guard thee well.
;;; XLVII A hymn to Night for protection from fiends, robbers, snakes and wolves
19.47.1 Night! the terrestrial realm hath been filled with the Father's power and might. Thou spreadest forth on high unto the seats of Heaven: dark- ness that strikes with awe comes near.
19.47.2 Each moving thing finds rest in her whose yonder boundary is not seen, nor that which keeps her separate. O spacious, darksome Night, may we uninjured reach the end of thee, reach, O thou blessed One, thine end.
19.47.3 Thy ninety-nine examiners, O Night, who look upon mankind, Eighty-and-eight in number, or seven-and-seventy are they.
19.47.4 Sixty-and-six, O opulent, fifty-and-five, O happy One, Forty-and-four and thirty-three are they, O thou enriched with spoil.
19.47.5 Twenty-and-two hast thou, O Night, eleven, yea, and fewer still. With these protectors guard us well. O Daughter of the Sky, to- day.
19.47.6 Let not a fiends or spiteful man, let no ill-wisher master us. Let not the robber seize our cows, nor the wolf take our sheep today.
19.47.7 Let not the thief, O Blessed, seize our horses, nor she-fiends our men. Let thief and robber run away on pathways most remote from us.
19.47.8 Far from us let Rope with Fangs, far from us let the wicked flee. Do thou make blind and headless. Night, the serpent with his pungent breath.
19.47.9 Crush the wolf's jaws in pieces, strike the robber dead against a post. In thee, O Night, do we abide: we here will sleep. Be watchful thou.
19.47.10 Give thou protection to our kine; and to our horses, and our men.
;;; XLVIII A hymn to Night for protection
19.48.1 Then all that we accumulate, all that the treasure-chest contains,. All this do we entrust to thee.
19.48.2 Entrust thou us to Dawn, O Mother Night. May Dawn entrust us to the Day, and Day to thee, O splendid. One.
19.48.3 Whatever flying thing be here, whatever thing that creeps and. crawls. Whatever fastens on a joint, therefrom do thou protect us, Night.
19.48.4 So guard thou us from west and east, protect us from the north and south. O splendid One, preserve us: we, the singers of thy praise, are here.
19.48.5 They who are followers of Night, and they who watch o'er living things. They who protect all cattle, they keep watch and ward over our lives, over our herds keep watch and ward.
19.48.6 Verily, Night, I know thy name, Dropper of Fatness art thou called. Thee Bharadvaja knew as such: as such be watchful o'er our wealth.
;;; XLIX A hymn of Praise and prayer to Night
19.49.1 Friend of the home, the strong and youthful maiden, Night, dear to Savitar the God, and Bhaga, All-compassing, all-glorious, prompt to listen, hath with her greatness filled the earth and heaven.
19.49.2 Over all depths hath she gone up, and mounted, most mighty One, the sky's exalted summit. Over me now the loving Night is spreading with her auspicious. Godlike ways like Mitra.
19.49.3 Excellent, high-born, blissful, meet for worship, Night, thou hast come: stay here with friendly spirit. Guard us, the food for men that we have gotten, and all pro- sperity that comes of cattle.
19.49.4 With eager haste hath Night assumed the vigour of leopard,. tiger, or of tawny lion, The horse's neighing and the wild-man's bellow, Thou takest many a form when thou appearest.
19.49.5 Kind through the Night be absence of the sunshine: Mother of Frost, may she be swift to hear us. Take notice of the hymn, thou highly favoured, wherewith I worship thee in all the regions.
19.49.6 Even as a King, O splendid Night, thou takest pleasure in our hymn. May we through Mornings as they flush have all our good men, round us, and become possessors of all wealth.
19.49.7 Yes, Ramya is the name thou hast assumed. The men who fain. would spoil. My wealth do thou annoy, O Night, that not one robber may appear, none may a second time appear.
19.49.8 Thou like a well-wrought cup, O Night, art lovely: thou, a. young maid, art formed in perfect beauty. Thou lovingly, for me with eyes to se: them, hast bound on thee heaven's stars as thine adornment.
19.49.9 Whatever robber comes to-day, mischievous mortal enemy. Let Night go forth, encounter him, and smite away his neck and head;
19.49.10 His feet that he may walk no more, his hands that he may do no harm. The robber who comes hitherward goes crushed and mutilated hence, Goes hence, goes far away from us, goes hence and bears no spoil away.
;;; L A hymn to Night for protection and prosperity
19.50.1 Blind him and make him headless, Night! the serpent with the pungent breath. Strike from his head the wolf's two eyes, and dash the thief against a post.
19.50.2 Those oxen that are thine, O Night, with sharpened horns and rapid pace, With those transport us safe to-day o'er difficulties everywhere.
19.50.3 Uninjured in our bodies may we pass through each succeeding night, And let malignities fail to pass, as men without a boat the depth.
19.50.4 As millet hurried through the air before us is beheld no more. So cause the man to vanish, Night, who plans to do us injury.
19.50.5 The thief hast thou kept far away, the robber driver of our kine. Even him who having covered up the horse's head would lead him off.
19.50.6 If dealing treasure thou hast come to-day, O highly favoured Night. Cause thou us to enjoy it all so that this may not pass away.
19.50.7 Do thou entrust us to the Dawn, all of us free from sin, O Night. May Dawn deliver us to Day, and Day to thee, O glorious One.
;;; LI A sacrificial formula
19.51.1 Undisturbed am I, undisturbed is my soul, undisturbed mine eye, undisturbed mine ear, undisturbed is mine in-breathing, undisturbed mine out-breathing, undisturbed my diffusive- breath, undisturbed the whole of me.
19.51.2 Under the impulse of the God Savitar, sent forth from the arms- of the Asvins and both hands of Pushan I have taken thee.
;;; LII A hymn to Kama or Desire
19.52.1 Thereafter rose Desire in the beginning, Desire the primal seed and germ of Spirit. O Kama dwelling with the lofty Kama, give growth of riches to the sacrificer.
19.52.2 Thou, Kama, art victorious, famous, potent, splendid, a friend. to him who seeks thy friendship. Mighty and overpowering in battle, give strength and vigour to the sacrificer.
19.52.3 They heard his prayers, and they begot, by Kama, heavenly- light for him. Who from a distance longed for it, a dealer ready to exchange.
19.52.4 O Kama, with whatever wish we make this offering to thee, May it be all fulfilled to us. Then taste this sacrifice, All hail!
;;; LIII A hymn to Kama or Time
19.53.1 Prolific, thousand-eyed, and undecaying, a horse with seven reins Time bears us onward. Sages inspired with holy knowledge mount him: his chariot wheels are all the worlds of creatures.
19.53.2 This Time hath seven rolling wheels and seven naves immorality is the chariot's axle. This Time brings hitherward all worlds about us: as primal Deity is he entreated.
19.53.3 On Time is laid an overflowing beaker: this we behold in many a place appearing. He carries from us all these worlds of creatures. They call him Kala in the loftiest heaven.
19.53.4 He only made the worlds of life, he only gathered the worlds of living things together. Their son did he become who was their Father: no other higher power than he existeth.
19.53.5 Kala created yonder heaven, and Kala made these realms of earth. By Kala, stirred to motion, both what is and what shall be expand.
19.53.6 Kala created land; the Sun in Kala hath his light and heat. In Kala rest all things that be: in Kala doth the eye discern.
19.53.7 In Kala mind, in Kala breath, in Kala name are fixt and joined. These living creatures, one and all, rejoice when Kala hath approached.
19.53.8 Kala embraces Holy Fire, the Highest, Brahma in himself. Yea, Kala, who was father of Prajapati, is Lord of All.
19.53.9 He made, he stirred this universe to motion, and on him it rests. He, Kala, having now become Brahma, holds Parameshthin up.
19.52.10 Kala created living things and, first of all, Prajapati. From Kala self-made Kasyapa, from Kala Holy Fire was born.
;;; LIV A hymn to Kala; a continuation of the preceding hymn
19.54.1 From Kala sprang the Waters, sprang the regions, Brahma, Holy Fire. The Sun ascends by Kala, and in Kala sinks again to rest.
19.54.2 By Kala freshly blows the wind, mighty through Kala is the Earth: on Kala rests the mighty Sky.
19.54.3 In Kala erst the text produced what is and what is yet to be. From Kala sprang the Richas, and from Kala was the Yajus born.
19.54.4 They formed in Kala sacrifice, eternal portion for the Gods. In Kala the Gandharvas and Apsarasas and worlds abide.
19.54.5 Atharvan and this Angiras in Kala are supreme o'er heaven. Both this world and the world that is most lofty, the pure worlds and pure intermediate spaces,--
19.54.6 Yea, having conquered all the worlds by Brahma, Kala as God Supreme is supplicated.
;;; LV A hymn to Agni for protection and prosperity
19.55.1 Bringing, as 'twere, with care unceasing fodder night after night to feed this stabled Courser, Joying in food and in the growth of riches, may we thy neigh- bours, Agni, ne'er be injured.
19.55.2 Here is thine own desire for wealth: through this be gracious unto us. Joying in food and in the growth of riches, may we thy neigh- bours, Agni, ne'er be injured.
19.55.3 Each eve that comes our household's Lord is Agni, showing his. loving-kindness every morning. Bestow upon us treasure after treasure: enkindling thee may we increase thy body.
19.55.4 Each morn that comes our household's Lord is Agni, showing. his loving-kindness every evening. Vouchsafe us treasure after treasure: kindling thee may we prosper through a hundred winters.
19.55.5 Never may I come short of food to feed me. Glory to Agni, Rudra, the consumer and the Lord of food!
19.55.6 Protect my company, protect its courteous members, courteous. God! Only through thee, O much-invoked, may I be ever rich in kine.
19.55.7 Only to thee bringing our tribute, Agni, each day as fodder to a stabled courser, Joying in food and in the growth of riches, may we the neigh- bours, Agni ne'er be injured.
;;; LVI A hymn to Sleep
19.56.1 Thou art come hither from the world of Yama: thou, resolute, affectest men with rapture. Thou, Sleep, created in the Asura's dwelling, goest, well-know- ing, with the solitary.
19.56.2 At first the all-containing, depth beheld thee, ere Night was born, when only Day existed. Thence hast thou come, thence, Sleep, hast thou come hither, concealing, deep within, all form and figure.
19.56.3 Come from the Asuras in lofty, glory, he hath approached the Gods in search of greatness. Winners of heavenly light, the Three-and-Thirty endowed this Sleep with his supreme dominion.
19.56.4 Of him nor Fathers nor the Gods have knowledge, the Gods whose gentle talk is still about him. Urged by command of Varuna the Adityas, Heroes, transported Sleep to Trita Aptya.
19.56.5 Thou whose severity hath reached ill-doers, and whose reward the good have gained in slumber, Delightest heaven with thy most lofty kinship, born from his spirit who was worn and weary.
19.56.6 Of old we know all places whence thou comest. O Sleep, we know him who is here thy ruler. Protect us here illustrious with glory. Go, from afar, with poisons, into distance.
;;; LVII A charm against evil dreams
19.57.1 As men discharge the utmost debt, collect the eighth and sixteenth part, So to the foeman we transfer together all the evil dream.
19.57.2 Princes came together, debts came together, Kushthas came to- gether, Sixteenths came together. The whole evil dream that hath visited us we send away as a bad dream to the man who hates us.
19.57.3 Child of Gods' Consorts, minister of Yama is the good Dream: that which is my trouble we drive away to the enemy.
19.57.4 Thou whose name is Rough art the mouth of the Black Bird. As such we know thee, Dream, as such we know thee well. Like a horse art thou, O Dream. As they bind girth and surcingle on a horse, so bind the alien mischief-maker, the scorner of the Gods.
19.57.5 The evil dream that threatens us, threatens our cattle or our home. That let the scorner of the Gods, the alien mischief-maker bind as a gold jewel round his neck.
19.57.6 Having measured off nine cubits' distance from us we give away the whole of the evil dream to the man who hates us.
;;; LVIII A prayer for prosperity, accompanying a sacrifice
19.58.1 Still equal be the flow of butter ever causing the Year to prosper with oblation. Still be our hearing, sight, and breath uninjured: let us lose nothing of our life and vigour.
19.58.2 Let lively breath invite us: we call vital breath to visit us. Earth and air's middle realm have gathered, Soma, Brihaspati and Dhartar gathered vigour.
19.58.3 The earth and heaven have come to be two gatherers up of vigo- rous might. So let us gather vigour up and closely follow after Earth. With glory come the cows and stand beside the master of the herd. Let us when we have gathered fame and glory closely follow Earth.
19.58.4 Prepare the cow-stall, for there drink your heroes: stitch ye the coats of armour wide and many. Make iron forts defying all assailants: let not your pitcher leak; stay it securely.
19.58.5 The eye of sacrifice, source and beginning with voice, car, spirit unto him I offer. To this our sacrifice, wrought by Visvakarman, may the Gods come gracious and kindly-hearted.
19.58.6 Let the Gods' Priests and those who merit worship, to whom oblation as their share is offered, Come to this holy service with their Consorts, and all Gods revel in the food we bring them.
;;; LIX An expiatory hymn accompanying sacrifice
19.59.1 God among mortals, Agni, thou art guard of holy Law, thou art To be adored in sacred rites.
19.59.2 When, ignorant, we violate the statutes of you, O Deities, with whom is knowledge, Wise Agni shall correct our faults and failings, and Soma who hath entered into Brahmans.
19.59.3 To the Gods' pathway have we come desiring to execute what work we may accomplish. Let Agni--for he knows--complete the worship. He is the Priest: let him fix rites and seasons.
;;; LX A prayer for perfect bodily and mental health and vigour
19.60.1 May I have voice in my mouth, breath in my nostrils, sight in mine eyes, hearing in mine ears, hair that hath not turned gray, teeth free from yellowness, and much strength in mine arms.
19.60.2 May I have power in my thighs, swiftness in my legs, stedfast- ness in my feet. May all my members be uninjured and my soul unimpaired.
;;; LXI A prayer for long life prosperity and final happiness in heaven
19.61.1 May my self remain in my body: may I enjoy the full time of life, Rest thee pleasantly: pour forth abundance, purifying thyself in Svarga.
;;; LXII A prayer for the love of Gods and men
19.62.1 Make me beloved among the Gods, beloved among the Princes, make Me dear to everyone who sees, to Sudra and to Aryan man.
;;; LXIII A prayer, with sacrifice, for long life and prosperity
19.63.1 Rise up, O Brahmanaspati; awake the Gods with sacrifice. Strengthen the Sacrificer: aid life, breath, and off-spring, cattle, fame.
;;; LXIV A prayer to Agni for children, long life, and various blessings
19.64.1 For lofty Jatavedas I have brought the fuel hither first. May he who knoweth all bestow faith and intelligence on me.
19.64.2 With fuel and with flaming wood we, Jatavedas, strengthen thee; So do thou strengthen us in turn with children and with store of wealth.
19.64.3 Whatever even be the logs which, Agni, we lay down for thee, propitious be it all to me: accept it, O most youthful God.
19.64.4 Agni, these logs are thine: with these be, fain to burn! a flaming brand. Vouchsafe us length of life and give us hope of immortality.
;;; LXV A hymn to Agni identified with the Sun
19.65.1 A Golden Eagle thou hast soared with light to heaven. Those who would harm thee as thou fliest skyward. Beat down, O Jatavedas, with thy fury. The strong hath feared: to heaven mount up with light, O Surya.
;;; LXVI A hymn to Agni as the Sun
19.66.1 The Asuras with iron nets, magicians, who roam about with hooks and bonds of iron, With wrath I make thy thralls, O Jatavedas. Come as a bolt foe- quelling, thousand pointed.
;;; LXVII A prayer for long life
19.67.1 A hundred autumns may we see.
19.67.2 A hundred autumns may we live.
19.67.3 A hundred autumns may we know.
19.67.4 A hundred autumns may we grow.
19.67.5 A hundred autumns may we thrive.
19.67.6 A hundred autumns may we be.
19.67.7 A hundred autumns may we bide.
19.67.8 A hundred, yea, and even more.
;;; LXVIII A preliminary sacrificial formula
19.68.1 Both of broad and narrow I with magic power unclose the mouth. With these when we have raised the bunch of grass we pay the holy rites.
;;; LXIX A prayer or charm for long life
19.69.1 Ye are alive. I fain would live. I fain would live my complete term of life.
19.69.2 Ye live dependent. I fain would live dependent. I fain would live my complete term of life.
19.69.3 Ye remain alive. I fain would remain alive. I fain would live my complete term of life.
19.69.4 Ye are life-givers. I fain would live. I fain would live my com- plete term of life.
;;; LXX A charm for long life
19.70.1 Live, Indra. Live Surya. Live, ye Gods. I fain would live. Fain would I live my complete term of life.
;;; LXXI A hymn, accompanying libations, for wealth and prosperity
19.71.1 Let my libations, giving boons, adoring, further the Twice-born's song that honours Soma. Go ye to Brahma's world having enriched me with life and breath, with children and with cattle, with fame and wealth, and with a Brahman's lustre.
;;; LXXII A sacrificial formula
19.72.1 Within the chest whence we before extracted the bunch of grass, this do we now deposit. Wrought is the sacrifice by power of Brahma. Through this assist me here, ye God, with Fervour.
;;; I ???
20.1.1 Thee, Indra, we invoke, the Bull, what time the Soma hath been pressed. Drink of the sweetly-flavoured juice.
20.1.2 The best of guardian hath the man within whose dwelling-place ye drink, O Maruts, giants of the sky.
20.1.3 Let us serve Agni with our hyms, Sage who consumeth ox and cow, Who beareth Soma on his back.
;;; II ???
20.2.1 Let the Maruts drink Trishtups from the Potar's cup, according to the season Soma from heaven.
20.2.2 Let Agni from the Kindler's cup drink Trishtups, according to the season Soma from heaven.
20.2.3 Let Indra the Brahman from the Brahman's cup drink Trishtups, according to the season Soma from heaven.
20.2.4 Let the God, Granter of Wealth, from the Potar's cup drink Trishtups, according to the season Soma from heaven.
;;; III ???
20.3.1 Come, we have pressed the juice for thee: O Indra, drink this Soma here. Seat thee on this my sacred grass.
20.3.2 Let both thy bay steeds, yoked by prayer long-maned, O Indra, bring thee nigh.
20.3.3 We Soma-bearing Brahmans call thee Soma-drinker with thy friend, We, Indra, who have pressed the juice.
;;; IV ???
20.4.1 Come unto us who poured the juice, come hither to our eulogies. Drink of the juice, O fair of face.
20.4.2 I pour it down within thee, so through all thy members let it run. Take with thy tongue the pleasant drink.
20.4.3 Sweet to thy body let it be, delicious be the savoury juice. Sweet be the Soma to thy heart.
;;; V ???
20.5.1 Like women, let this Soma juice invested with its raiment, glide.. Most active Indra, close to thee.
20.5.2 Mighty in bulk, strong-necked, stout-armed in the wild rapture. of the juice Doth Indra smite the foemen dead.
20.5.3 Indra, advance, go forward thou who by thy might art Lord of all. Slay, Vritra-slayer slay thy foes.
20.5.4 Long be thy grasping-hook wherewith thou givest treasure unto- him Who pours the juice and worships thee.
20.5.5 Here, Indra, is thy Soma draught, made pure upon the sacred. grass. Run hither, come and drink thereof.
20.5.6 Famed for thy radiance, worshipped well! this juice is shed for thy delight: Thou art invoked, Akhandala!
20.5.7 To Kundapayya, grandson's son, grandson of Sringavrish, to thee, To him have I addressed my thought.
;;; VI ???
20.6.1 Thee, Indra, we invoke, the Bull, what time the Soma is ex- pressed. So drink thou of the savoury juice.
20.6.2 Indra, whom many laud, accept the strength-confering Soma juice. Quaff, pour down drink that satisfies.
20.6.3 Indra, with all the Gods promote our wealth-bestowing sacrifice, Thou highly-lauded Lord of men.
20.6.4 Lord of the brave, to thee proceed these drops of Soma juice expressed, The bright drops to thy dwelling-place.
20.6.5 Within thy belly, Indra take Soma the juice most excellent: The heavenly drops belong to thee.
20.6.6 Drink our libation, Lord of hymns: with streams of meath thou art bedewed: Our glory, Indra, is thy gift.
20.6.7 To Indra go the treasures of the worshipper which never fail: He drinks the Soma and is strong.
20.6.8 From far away, from near at hand, O Vritra-slayer, come to us: Accept the songs we sing to thee.
;;; VII ???
20.7.1 Surya, thou mountest up to meet the Hero famous for his wealth, Who hurls the bolt and works for man:
20.7.2 Him who with might of both his arms brake nine-and ninety castles down, Slew Vritra and smote Ahi dead.
20.7.3 This Indra is our gracious Friend. He sends us in a full broad stream Riches in horses, kine, and corn.
20.7.4 Indra, whom many laud, accept the strength-conferring Soma juice. Quaff, pour down drink that satisfies.
;;; VIII ???
20.8.1 Drink as of old, and let the draught delight thee: hear thou my prayer and let our songs exalt thee. Make the Sun visible, make food abundant: slaughter the foes,. pierce through and free the cattle.
20.8.2 Come to us; they have called thee Soma-lover. Here is the pressed juice: drink thereof for rapture. Widely-capacious, pour it down within thee, and invocated hear us like a father.
20.8.3 Full is his chalice. Blessing! Like a pourer I have filled up the vessel for his drinking. Presented on the right, dear Soma juices have brought us Indra,. to rejoice him, hither.
;;; IX ???
20.9.1 As cows low to their calves in stalls, so with our songs we glorify This Indra, even your wondrous God who checks attack, who joys in the delicious juice.
20.9.2 Celestial, bounteous Giver, girt about with might, rich, moun- tain-like, in precious things Him swift we seek for foodful booty rich in kine, brought hundredfold and thousandfold.
20.9.3 I crave of thee that hero strength, that thou mayst first regard this prayer, Wherewith thou helpest Bhrigu and the Yatis and Praskanva when the prize was staked.
20.9.4 Wherewith thou sentest mighty waters to the sea, that, Indra, is. thy hero strength. For ever unattainable is this power of him to whom the worlds. have called aloud.
;;; X ???
20.10.1 These songs of ours exceeding sweet, these hymns of praise as- cend to thee, Like ever-conquering chariots that display their strength, gain wealth and give unfailing aid.
20.10.2 The Bhrigus are like suns, like Kanvas, and have gained all that their thoughts were bent to win. The living men of Priyamedha's race have sung exalting Indra with their lauds.
;;; XI ???
20.11.1 Fort-render, Lord of Wealth, dispelling foemen, Indra with lightnings hath o'ercome the Dasa. Impelled by prayer and waxen great in body, he hath filled earth and heaven, the bounteous Giver.
20.11.2 I stimulate this zeal, the Strong, the Hero, decking my song of praise for thee Immortal. O Indra, thou art equally the leader of heavenly hosts and human generations.
20.11.3 Leading his band Indra encompassed Vritra; weak grew the wily leader enchanters. He who burns fierce in forests slaughtered Vyansa, and made the milch-kine of nights apparent.
20.11.4 Indra, light-winner, days' creator, conquered, as guardian, hostile bands with those who loved him. For man the days' bright ensign he illumined, and found the light for his great joy and gladness.
20.11.5 Forward to fiercely falling blows pressed Indra, hero-like doing many hero exploits. Those holy songs he taught the bard who praised him, and widely spread these Dawns' resplendent colour.
20.11.6 They laud the mighty acts of him the mighty, the many glorious deeds performed by Indra. He in his strength, with all-surpassing prowess, through wond- rous arts crushed the malignant Dasyus.
20.11.7 Lord of the brave, Indra who rules the people gave freedom to the Gods by might and battle. Wise singers glorify with chanted praises these his achievements in Vivasvan's dwelling.
20.11.8 Excellent, conqueror, the victory-giver, the winner of the light and godlike waters, He who hath won this broad earth and this heaven,--in Indra they rejoice who love devotions.
20.11.9 He gained possession of the Sun and horses; Indra obtained the cow who feedeth many. Treasure of gold he won; he smote the Dasyus and gave protec- tion to the race of Aryas.
20.11.10 He took the plants and days for his possession; he gained the forest trees and air's mid-region. Vala he cleft, and chased away opponents: thus was he tamer of the overweening.
20.11.11 Call we on Maghavan, auspicious Indra, best Hero in the fight where spoil is gathered, The Strong, who listens, who gives aid in battles, who slays the Vritras, wins and gathers treasures.
;;; XII ???
20.12.1 Prayers have been offered up through love of glory: Vasishtha, honour Indra in the battle. He who with might extends through all existence hears words which I, his faithful servant, utter.
20.12.2 A cry was raised which reached the Gods, O Indra, a cry to them to send us strength in combat. None among men knows his own life's duration: bear us in safety over these our troubles.
20.12.3 The Bays, the booty-seeking car I harness: my prayers have reached him who accepts them gladly. Indra, when he had slain resistless Vritras, forced with his might the two world-halves asunder.
20.12.4 Like barren cows, moreover, swelled the waters: the singers sought thy holy rite, O Indra. Come unto us as with his team comes Vayu: thou, through our solemn hymns, bestowest booty.
20.12.5 So may these gladdening draughts rejoice thee, Indra, the Mighty, very bounteous to the singer. Alone among the Gods thou pitiest mortals: O Hero, make thee glad at this libation.
20.12.6 Thus the Vasishthas glorify with praises Indra, the Mighty One, whose arm wields thunder. Praised, may he guard our wealth in kine and heroes. Ye Gods,. preserve us evermore with blessings.
20.12.7 Impetuous, Thunderer, strong, quelling the mighty, King, potent, Vritra-slayer, Soma-drinker, May he come hither with his yoked bay horses. May Indra glad- den him at noon libation.
;;; XIII ???
20.13.1 Lords of great wealth, Brihaspati and Indra, rejoicing at this sacrifice drink Soma. Let the abundant drops sink deep within you: vouchsafe us riches with full store of heroes.
20.13.2 Let your swift-gliding coursers bear you hitherward with their fleet pinions. Come ye forward with your arms. Sit on the grass; a wide seat hath been made for you: delight yourselves, O Maruts, in the pleasant food.
20.13.3 For Jatavedas, worthy of our praise, will we frame with our mind this eulogy as 'twere a car. For good in his assembly is this care of ours. Let us not in thy friendship, Agni, suffer harm.
20.13.4 With these, borne on one car, Agni, approach us; or borne on many, for thy steeds are able. Bring, with their Dames, the Gods, the Three-and-Thirty, after thy Godlike nature, and he joyful.
;;; XIV ???
20.14.1 We call on thee, O peerless One. We, seeking help, possessing nothing firm ourselves, Call on thee wonderful in fight.
20.14.2 On thee for aid in sacrifice. This youth of ours, the bold, the mighty, hath gone forth. We, therefore, we thy friends, Indra, have chosen thee, free- giver, as our guardian God.
20.14.3 Him who of old hath brought to us this and that blessing, him I magnify for you, Even Indra, O my friends, for help:
20.14.4 Borne by bay steeds, the Lord of heroes, ruling men, for it is he who takes delight. The Bounteous Lord bestows on us his worshippers hundreds of cattle and of steeds.
;;; XV ???
20.15.1 To him most liberal, lofty Lord of lofty wealth, verily powerful and strong, I bring my hymn, Whose checkless bounty, as of waters down a slope, is spread abroad for all that live, to give them strength.
20.15.2 Now all this world, for worship, shall come after thee--the offerer's libations like descending floods, When the well-loved one seems to rest upon the hill, the thun- derbolt of Indra, shatterer wrought of gold.
20.15.3 To him the terrible, most worthy of high praise, like radiant Dawn, bring gifts with reverence in this rite, Whose being, for renown, yea, Indra-power and light, have been created, like bay steeds, to move with speed.
20.15.4 Thine, Indra, praised by many excellently rich! are we who trusting in thy help draw near to thee. Lover of praise, none else but thou receives our laud: as Earth loves all her creatures, love thou this our hymn.
20.15.5 Great is thy power, O Indra, we are thine. Fulfil, O Maghavan, the wish of this thy worshipper. After thee lofty heaven hath measured out its strength to thee and to thy power this earth hath bowed itself.
20.15.6 Thou, who hast thunder for thy weapon, with thy bolt hast shattered into pieces this broad massive cloud. Thou hast sent down obstructed floods that they may flow: thou hast, thine own for ever, all victorious might.
;;; XVI ???
20.16.1 Like birds who keep their watch, plashing in water, like the loud voices of the thundering rain-cloud, Like merry streamlets bursting from the mountain thus to Brihaspati our hymns have sounded.
20.16.2 The son of Angiras, meeting the cattle, as Bhaga, brought in Aryaman among us. As Friend of men he decks the wife and husband. As for the race, Brihaspati, nerve our coursers.
20.16.3 Brihaspati, having won them from the mountains, strewed down, like barley out of winnowing-baskets, The vigorous, wandering cows who aid the pious, desired of all, of blameless form, well-coloured.
20.16.4 As the Sun dews with meath the seat of Order, and casts a flam- ing meteor down from heaven, So from the rock Brihaspati forced the cattle, and cleft the earth's skin as it were with water.
20.16.5 Forth from mid-air with light he draye the darkness, as the gale blows a lily from the river. Like the wind grasping at the cloud of Vala, Brihaspati gathered to himself the cattle.
20.16.6 Brihaspati, when he with fiery lightnings cleft through the weapon of reviling Vala, Consumed him as tongues eat what teeth have compassed: he threw the prisons of the red cows open.
20.16.7 That secret name borne by the lowing cattle within the cave Brihaspati discovered, And draye, himself, the bright kine from the mountain, like a bird's young after the eggs' disclosure.
20.16.8 He looked around on rock-imprisoned sweetness as one who eyes a fish in scanty water. Brihaspati, cleaving through with varied clamour, brought it forth like a bowl from out the timber.
20.16.9 He found the light of heaven, and fire, and Morning: with lucid rays he forced apart the darkness. As from a joint, Brihaspati took the marrow of Vala as he gloried in his cattle.
20.16.10 As trees for foliage robbed by winter, Vala mourned for the cows Brihaspati had taken. He did a deed ne'er done, ne'er to be equalled, whereby the sun and moon ascend alternate.
20.16.11 Like a dark steed adorned with pearl, the Fathers have decorat- ed heaven with constellations. They set the light in day, in night the darkness, Brihaspati cleft the rock and found the cattle.
20.16.12 This homage have we offered to the Cloud-God who thunders out to many in succession. May this Brihaspati vouchsafe us fulness of life with kine and horses, men, and heroes.
;;; XVII ???
20.17.1 In perfect unison all yearning hymns of mine that find the light of heaven have sung forth Indra's praise. As wives embrace their lord, the comely bridegroom, so they compass Maghavan about that he may help.
20.17.2 Directed unto thee my spirit never strays, for I have set my hopes on thee, O much-invoked! Sit, wonderful! as King upon the sacred grass, and let thy drinking-place be by the Soma juice.
20.17.3 From indigence and hunger Indra turns away: Maghavan hath dominion over precious wealth. These the Seven Rivers flowing on their downward path increase the vital vigour of the Mighty Steer.
20.17.4 As on the fair-leafed tree rest birds, to Indra flow the gladden- ing Soma juices that the bowls contain. Their face that glows with splendour through their mighty power hath found the shine of heaven for man, the Aryas' light.
20.17.5 As in the game a gambler piles his winnings, so Maghavan, sweeping all together, gained the Sun. This mighty deed of thine none other could achieve, none, Maghavan, before thee, none in recent time.
20.17.6 Maghavan came by turns to all the tribes of men: the Steer took notice of the people's songs of praise. The man in whose libations Sakra hath delight by means of potent Somas vanquisheth his foes.
20.17.7 As waters flow together to the river, thus Somas to Indra flow, as rivulets to the lake. In place of sacrifice sages exalt his might, as the rain swells the corn by moisture sent from heaven.
20.17.8 He rushes through the region like a furious bull, he who hath made these floods the dames of worthy lords. This Maghavan hath found light for the man who brings oblation, sheds the juice, and promptly pours his gifts.
20.17.9 Let the keen axe come forth together with the light: here be, as erst, the teeming cow of sacrifice. Let the Red God shine pure with his refulgent ray, and let the Lord of heroes glow like heaven's clear sheen.
20.17.10 O much-invoked, may we subdue all famine and evil want with store of grain and cattle. May we allied, as first in rank, with princes, obtain possessions by our own exertion.
20.17.11 Brihaspati protect us from the rearward, and from above, and from below, from sinners. May Indra from the front, and from the centre, as friend to friends, vouchsafe us room and freedom.
20.17.12 Ye twain are Lords of wealth in earth and heaven, thou, O Brihaspati, and thou, O Indra. Mean though he be, give wealth to him who lauds you. Preserve us evermore, ye Gods, with blessings.
;;; XVIII ???
20.18.1 This, even this, O Indra, we implore: as thy devoted friends, The Kanvas praise thee with their hymns.
20.18.2 Naught else, O Thunderer, have I praised in the skilled singer's eulogy: On thy laud only have I thought.
20.18.3 The Gods seek him who presses out the Soma; they desire not sleep: Incessantly they punish sloth.
20.18.4 Faithful to thee we loudly sing, heroic Indra, songs to thee. Mark, gracious Lord, this act of ours.
20.18.5 Give us not up to man's reproach, to foeman's hateful calumny: In thee alone is all my strength.
20.18.6 Thou art mine ample coat of mail, my champion, Vritra-slayes, thou. With thee for Friend I brave the foe.
;;; XIX ???
20.19.1 O Indra, for the strength that slays the foe and conquers in the fight We turn thee hitherward to us.
20.19.2 O Indra, Lord of Hundred Powers, may those who praise thee hitherward. Direct thy spirit and thine eye.
20.19.3 O Indra, Lord of Hundred Powers, with all our songs we invocate. Thy names for triumph over foes.
20.19.4 We strive for glory through the powers immense of him whom many praise, Of Indra who supports mankind.
20.19.5 For the foe's slaughter I address Indra whom many invocate, To win us booty in the wars.
20.19.6 In battles be victorious. We seek thee, Lord of Hundred Powers, O Indra, that the foe may fall.
20.19.7 In splendid combats of the hosts, in glories where the fight is won, Indra, be victor over foes.
;;; XX ???
20.20.1 Drink thou the Soma for our help, bright, vigilant, exceeding strong, O Indra, Lord of Hundred Powers.
20.20.2 O Satakratu, powers which thou mid the Five Races hast dis- played These, Indra, do I claim of thee.
20.20.3 Indra, great glory hast thou gained. Win splendid fame which none may mar: We make thy might perpetual.
20.20.4 Come to us either from anear, or, Sakra, come from far away. Indra, wherever be thy home, come to us thence, O Thunder- armed.
20.20.5 Verily Indra, conquering all, driveth even mighty fear away; For firm is he and swift to act.
20.20.6 Indra be gracious unto us: sin shall not reach us afterward . And good shall be before us still,
20.20.7 From all the regions of the world let Indra send security. The foe-subduer, swift to act.
;;; XXI ???
20.21.1 We will present fair praise unto the Mighty One, our hymns to Indra in Vivasvan's dwelling-place; For he hath ne'er found wealth in those who seem to sleep; those who give wealth to men accept no paltry praise.
20.21.2 Giver of horses, Indra, giver, thou, of kine, giver of barley, thou art Lord and guard of wealth: Man's helper from of old, not disappointing hope, Friend of our friends, to thee as such we sing this praise.
20.21.3 Indra, most splendid, powerful, rich in mighty deeds, this treasure spread around is known to be thine own. Gather therefrom. O Conqueror, and bring to us: fail not the hope of him who loves and sings to thee.
20.21.4 Well-pleased with these bright flames and with these Soma drops, take thou away our poverty with steeds and kine. With Indra scattering the Dasyu through these drops, freed from their hate may we obtain abundant food.
20.21.5 Let us obtain, O Indra, plenteous wealth and food, with strength exceeding glorious, shining to the sky. May we obtain the Goddess Providence, the strength of heroes, special source of cattle, rich in steeds.
20.21.6 These our libations, strength inspiring Soma draughts, gladdened thee in the fight with Vritra, Hero-Lord, What time thou slewest for the singer with trimmed grass ten thousand Vritras, thou resistless in thy might.
20.21.7 Thou goest on from fight to fight intrepidly, destroying castle after castle here with strength; Thou Indra, with thy friend who makes the foe bow down, slewest from far away the guileful Namuchi.
20.21.8 Thou hast stuck down in death Karanja, Parnaya, in Atithigva's very glorious going forth: Unyielding, when Rijisvan compassed them with siege, thou hast destroyed the hundred towns of Vangrida.
20.21.9 With all-outstripping chariot wheel, O Indra, thou far-famed, hast overthrown the twice ten kings of men, With sixty thousand nine-and-ninety followers, who came in arms to fight with friendless Susravas.
20.21.10 Thou hast protected Susravas with succour, and Turvayana with thine aid, O Indra: Thou madest Kutsa, Atithigva, Ayu subject unto this king, the young, the mighty.
20.21.11 May we protected by the Gods hereafter remain thy very pro- sperous friends, O Indra. Thee we extol, enjoying through thy favour life-long and joyful and with store of heroes.
;;; XXII ???
20.22.1 Hero, the Soma being pressed I pour the juice for thee to drink Sate thee and finish thy carouse.
20.22.2 Let not the fools, or those who mock, beguile thee when they seek thine aid: Love not the enemies of prayer.
20.22.3 Here let them with rich milky draught cheer thee to great munificence: Drink as the wild bull drinks the lake.
20.22.4 Praise, even as he is known, with song Indra, the guardian of the kine, The Son of Truth, Lord of the brave.
20.22.5 Hither his bay steeds have been sent, red steeds are on the sacred grass. Where we in concert sing our songs.
20.22.6 For Indra, Thunder-armed, the kine have yielded mingled milk and meath, What time he found them in the vault.
;;; XXIII ???
20.23.1 Invoked to drink the Soma juice come with thy bay steeds, Thunder-armed! Come, Indra, hitherward, to me.
20.23.2 Our priest is seated true to time; the grass is regularly strewn; The pressing-stones were set at morn.
20.23.3 These prayers, O thou who bearest prayer, are offered. Seat thee on the grass. Hero, enjoy the offered cake.
20.23.4 O Vritra-slayer, be thou pleased with these libations, with these hymns, Song-loving Indra, with our lauds.
20.23.5 Our hymns caress the Lord of Strength, vast, drinker of the Soma's juice, Indra, as mother-cows their calf.
20.23.6 Delight thee with the juice we pour for thine own great munificence: Yield not thy singer to reproach.
20.23.7 We, Indra, dearly loving thee, bearing oblation, sing thee hymns: Thou, Vasu, nearly lovest us.
20.23.8 O thou to whom thy Bays are dear, loose not thy horses far from us: Here glad thee, Indra, Lord Divine.
20.23.9 May long-maned courses, dropping oil, bring thee on swift car hitherward. Indra, to seat thee on the grass.
;;; XXIV ???
20.24.1 Come to the juice that we have pressed, to Soma, Indra! blent with milk: Come, favouring us, thy bay-drawn car!
20.24.2 Come, Indra, to this gladdening drink, placed on the grass, pressed out with stones: Wilt thou not drink thy fill thereof?
20.24.3 To Indra have my songs of praise gone forth, thus rapidly sent hence, To turn him to the Soma-draught.
20.24.4 Hither with songs of praise we call Indra to drink the Soma. juice: Will he not come to us by lauds?
20.24.5 Indra, these Somas are expressed, Take them within thy belly, Lord Of Hundred Powers, thou Prince of wealth.
20.24.6 We know thee winner of the spoil and resolute in battles, Sage! Therefore thy blessing we implore.
20.24.7 Borne hither by thy stallions, drink, Indra, this juice which we have pressed, Mingled with barley and with milk.
20.24.8 Indra, for thee in thine own place I urge the Soma for thy draught: Deep in thy heart let it remain.
20.24.9 We call on thee, the Ancient One, Indra, to drink the Soma juice, We Kusikas who seek thine aid.
;;; XXV ???
20.25.1 Indra, the mortal man well guarded by thine aid goes foremost in the wealth of horses and of kine. With amplest wealth thou fillest him, as round about the waters clearly seen afar fill Sindhu full.
20.25.2 The heavenly waters come not nigh the priestly bowl: they but look down and see how far mid-air is spread: The Deities conduct the pious man to them: like suitors they delight in him who loveth prayer.
20.25.3 Praiseworthy blessing hast thou laid upon the pair who with uplifted ladle serve thee, man and wife. Unchecked he dwells and prospers in thy law: thy power brings blessing to the sacrificer pouring gifts.
20.25.4 First the Angirases won themselves vital power, whose fires were kindled through good deeds and sacrifice. The men together found the Pani's hoarded wealth, the cattle, and the wealth in horses and in kine,
20.25.5 Atharvan first by sacrifices laid the path; then, guardian of the Law, sprang up the loving Sun. Usana Kavya drove the kine hither with him: let us with offer- ings honour Yama's deathless birth.
20.25.6 When sacred grass is trimmed to aid the auspicious work, or the hymn makes its voice of praise sound to the sky, Where the stone rings as 'twere a singer skilled in laud,--Indra in truth delights when these come near to him.
20.25.7 To make thee start, a strong true draught I offer to thee the Bull, O thou whom bay steeds carry. Here take delight. O Indra, in our voices while thou art hymned with power and all our spirit.
;;; XXVI ???
20.26.1 In every need, in every fray we call, as friends, to succour us Indra the mightiest of all.
20.26.2 If he will hear us let him come with succour of a thousand kinds, And all that strengthens, to our call.
20.26.3 I call him, mighty to resist, the Hero of our ancient home, Thee whom my sire invoked of old.
20.26.4 They who stand round him as he moves harness the bright, the ruddy steed: The lights are shining in the sky.
20.26.5 On both sides of the car they yoke the two bay coursers dear to him, Bold, tawny, bearers of the thief.
20.26.6 Thou, making light where no light was, and form, O Men! where form was not, Wast born together with the Dawns.
;;; XXVII ???
20.27.1 If I, O Indra, were, like thee, the single sovran of all wealth. My worshipper should be rich in kine.
20.27.2 I should be fain, O Lord of Might, to strengthen and enrich the sage, Were I the lord of herds of kine,
20.27.3 To worshippers who press the juice thy goodness, Indra, is a cow. Yielding in plenty kine and steeds.
20.27.4 None is there, Indra, God or man, to hinder thy munificence, The wealth which, lauded, thou wilt give.
20.27.5 The sacrifice made Indra strong when he unrolled the earth and made Himself a diaden in heaven.
20.27.6 Thine aid we claim, O Indra, thine who after thou hast waxen great. Hast won all treasures for thine own.
;;; XXVIII ???
20.28.1 In Soma's ecstasy Indra spread the firmament and realms of light. When he cleft Vala limb from limb.
20.28.2 Showing the hidden he draye forth the cows for the Angirases, And Vala he cast headlong down.
20.28.3 By Indra were the luminous realms of heaven established and secured. Firm and immovable in their place.
20.28.4 Indra, thy laud moves quickly like a joyous wave of water-floods. Bright shine the drops that gladden thee.
;;; XXIX ???
20.29.1 For thou, O Indra, art the God whom hymns and praises magnify: Thou blessest those who worship thee.
20.29.2 Bay horses with their long manes bring Indra to drink the Soma juice, The Bountiful to our sacrifice.
20.29.3 With waters' foam thou torest off, Indra, the head of Namuchi, Subduing all contending hosts.
20.29.4 The Dasyus, when they fain would climb by magic arts and mount to heaven, Thou, Indra, castest down to earth.
20.29.5 As Soma-drinker conquering all, thou scatteredst to every side Their band who poured no gifts to thee.
;;; XXX ???
20.30.1 In the great synod will I laud thy two bay steeds: I prize the sweet strong drink of thee the Warrior-God, His who pours lovely oil as'twere with yellow drops. Let my songs enter thee whose form hath golden tints.
20.30.2 Ye who--in concert sing unto the gold-hued place, like bay steeds driving onward to the heavenly seat, For Indra laud ye strength allied with tawny steeds, laud him whom cows content as'twere with yellow drops.
20.30.3 His is that thunderbolt, of iron, golden-hued, gold-coloured, very dear, and yellow in his arms; Bright with strong teeth, destroying with its tawny rage. In Indra are set fast all forms of golden hue.
20.30.4 As if a lovely ray were laid upon the sky, the golden thunder- bolt spread out as in a race. That iron bolt with yellow jaw smote Ahi down. A thousand flames had he who bore the tawny-hued.
20.30.5 Thou, thou, when praised by men who sacrificed of old, hadst pleasure in their lauds, O Indra golden-haired. All that befits thy song of praise thou welcomest, the perfect: pleasant gift, O golden-hued from birth.
;;; XXXI ???
20.31.1 These two dear Bays bring hither Indra on his car, thunder- armed, joyous, meet for laud, to drink his fill. Many libations flow for him who loveth them: to Indra have: the gold-hued Soma juices run.
20.31.2 The gold-hued drops have flowed to gratify his wish: the yellow. drops have urged the swift Bays to the Strong. He who speeds on with bay steeds even as he lists hath satisfied his longing for the golden drops.
20.31.3 At the swift draught the Soma-drinker waxed in might, the iron. One with yellow beard and golden hair, He, Lord of tawny coursers. Lord of fleet-foot mares, will bear his bay steeds safely over all distress.
20.31.4 His yellow-coloured jaws, like ladles, move apart, what time,. for strength, he makes the yellow-tinted stir, When. while the bowl stands there, he grooms his tawny steeds, when he hath drunk strong drink, the sweet juice that he: loves.
20.31.5 Yea, to the dear one's seat in homes of heaven and earth the- bay steeds' Lord hath whinnied like a horse for food. Then the great wish hath seized upon him mightily, and the beloved One hath gained high power of life.
;;; XXXII ???
20.32.1 Thou, comprehending with thy might the earth and heaven, acceptest the dear hymn for ever new and new. O Asura, disclose thou and make visible the Cow's beloved home to the bright golden Sun.
20.32.2 O Indra, let the eager wishes of the folk bring thee the golden- jawed, delightful, on thy car. That, pleased with sacrifice wherein ten fingers toil, thou mayest at the feast drink of our offered mead.
20.32.3 Juices aforetime, Lord of Bays, thou drankest, and thine, and only thine, is this libation. Gladden thee, Indra, with the mead-rich Soma: pour it down ever, Mighty One, within thee.
;;; XXXIII ???
20.33.1 Drink of the juice which men have washed in waters and fill the- full, O Lord of tawny horses. O Indra, hearer of the laud, with Soma which stones have mix- ed for thee enhance thy rapture.
20.33.2 To make thee start, a strong true draught I offer to thee the Bull, O thou whom bay steeds carry. Here take delight, O Indra, in our voices while thou art hymned with power and all our spirit.
20.33.3 O mighty Indra, through thine aid, thy prowess, obtaining life, zealous, and skilled in worship. Men in the house who share the sacred banquet stand singing praise that brings them store of children.
;;; XXXIV ???
20.34.1 He who just born, chief God of lofty spirit, by power and might became the God's protector, Before whose breath, through greatness of his valour, the two worlds trembled, He, O men, is Indra.
20.34.2 He who fixed fast and firm the earth that staggered, and set at rest the agitated mountains, Who measured out air's wider middle region and gave the heaven support, He, O men, is Indra.
20.34.3 Who slew the Dragon, freed the Seven Rivers, and draye the kine forth from the cave of Vala, Begat the fire between both stones, the spoiler in warrior's battle, He, O men, is Indra.
20.34.4 By whom this universe was made to tremble, who chased away the humbled brood of demon, Who, like a gambler gathering his winnings, seized the foe's riches, He, O men, is Indra.
20.34.5 Of whom, the terrible, they ask, Where is He? or verily they say of him, He is not. He wastes the foeman's wealth like stakes of gamblers. Have faith in him for He, O men, is Indra.
20.34.6 Stirrer to action of the poor and lowly, of priest, of suppliant who sings his praises Who, fair-faced, favours him who presseth Soma with stones adjusted, He, O men, is Indra.
20.34.7 He under whose supreme control are horses, all chariots, and the hamlets, and the cattle: He who begat the Sun, begat the Morning, leader of waters. He, O men, is Indra.
20.34.8 To whom both armies cry in close encounter, foe against foe, the stronger and the weaker; Whom two invoke upon one chariot mounted, each for himself, He, O ye men, is Indra.
20.34.9 He, without whom men conquer not in battle, whom, warring, they invoke for help and succour; He, all this universe's type and image, who shakes what never shook, He, men, is Indra.
20.34.10 He who hath smitten, ere they know their danger, with his hurl- ed weapon many grievous sinners: Who pardons not his boldness who provokes him, who slays the Dasyu, He, O men, is Indra.
20.34.11 He who discovered in the fortieth autumn Sambara dwelling in the midst of mountains: Who slew the Dragon putting forth his vigour, the demon lying there, He, men, is Indra.
20.34.12 Who drank the juice poured at the seas of Order, subduing Sambara by superior prowess, Who hoarded food within the mountain's hollow wherein he grew in strength, He, men, is Indra.
20.34.13 Who, with seven guiding reins, the Bull, the mighty, set the Seven Rivers free to flow at pleasure; Who, thunder-armed, rent Rauhina in pieces when scaling heaven, He, O ye men, is Indra.
20.34.14 Heaven, even, and the earth bow down before him, before his very breath the mountains tremble. Known as the Soma-drinker, armed with thunder, the wielder of the bolt, He, men, is Indra.
20.34.15 Who aids with favour him who pours the Soma, and him who brews it, sacrificer, singer; Whose strength our prayer and offered Soma heighten, and this our gift, He, O ye men, is Indra.
20.34.16 Born, manifested in his Parents' bosom, He knoweth as a son the Highest Father. He who with vigorous energy assisted the companies of Gods, He, men, is Indra
20.34.17 Lord of Bay steeds, who loves the flowing Soma, He before whom all living creatures tremble. He who smote Sambara and slaughtered Sushna, He the Sole Hero, He, O men, is Indra.
20.34.18 Thou verily art true strong God who sendest wealth to the man who brews and pours libation. So may we evermore, thy friends, O Indra, address the synod with brave sons about us.
;;; XXXV ???
20.35.1 To him, to him swift, strong, and high-exalted, I bring my song of praise as dainty viands; My thought to him resistless, meet for praises, prayers offered most devotedly to Indra.
20.35.2 To him I offer praise as choice refreshment, bring forth my song, with seemly laud besiege him. For Indra, Lord of olden time, the singers shall deck their hymns with heart and mind and spirit.
20.35.3 To him then with my lips my song of praises, excellent, winning heavenly light, I offer, To magnify with hymns of invocation and eulogies the Lord, most bounteous Giver.
20.35.4 Even for him I frame a laud--so fashions the wright a chariot for the man who needs it Songs for wise Indra hymned with invocation, a song composed with care and all-impelling.
20.35.5 So with my tongue I deck, to please that Indra, my hymn as't- were a horse, through love of glory, To reverence the Hero, bounteous Giver, famed far and wide, destroyer of the castles.
20.35.6 Even for him hath Tvashtar forged the thunder, most deftly wrought, celestial, for the battle. Wherewith he reached the vital parts of Vritra, striking--the vast, the mighty--with the striker,
20.35.7 As soon as, at libations of his mother, great Vishnu had drunk up the draught, he plundered. The dainty cates, the cooked mess; but One stronger transfixed the wild boar, shooting through the mountain.
20.35.8 To him, to Indra when he slew the Dragon, the Dames too, Consorts of the Gods, wove praises. The mighty heaven and earth hath he encompassed: thy great- ness heaven and earth, combined, exceed not.
20.35.9 Yea, of a truth, his magnitude surpasseth the magnitude of earth, mid-air and heaven. Indra whom all men praise, the Sovran Ruler, waxed in his home loud-voiced and strong for battle.
20.35.10 Through his own strength with bolt of thunder Indra smote piece-meal Vritra, drier up of waters. He let the floods go free, like cows imprisoned, for glory, with a heart inclined to bounty.
20.35.11 Through his resplendent power still stood the rivers when with his bolt on every side he stayed them. With lordly might favouring him who worshipped, he made a ford, victorious, for Turviti.
20.35.12 Vast, with thine ample power, with eager movement against this Vritra cast thy bolt of thunder. Rend thou his joints, as of an ox dissevered, with bolt oblique that floods of rain may follow.
20.35.13 Sing with new lauds his exploits wrought aforetime, the deeds of him, yea, him who moveth swiftly, When, hurling forth his weapons in the battle, he with impetuous wrath lays low the foemen.
20.35.14 When he, yea, he is born the firm-set mountains and the whole heaven and earth tremble in terror. May Nodhas ever lauding the protection of this dear Friend win straightway strength heroic.
20.35.15 Now unto him of these things hath been given what he, who rules alone o'er much, electeth. Indra helped Etasa, the Soma presser, contending in the chariot- race with Surya.
20.35.16 Thus to thee, Indra, yoker of bay coursers, the Gotamas have brought their prayers and praises. Bestow upon them thought, decked with all beauty. May he, enriched with prayer, come soon and early.
;;; XXXVI ???
20.36.1 With these my hymns I glorify that Indra who is alone to be invoked by mortals. The Lord, the Mighty One, of manly vigour, victorious, Hero, true, and full of wisdom.
20.36.2 Our ancient sires, Navagvas, sages seven, while urging him to show his might, extolled him, Dweller on heights, swift smiting down opponents, guileless in word, and in his thoughts most mighty.
20.36.3 We seek that Indra to obtain his riches that yield much food, and men, and store of heroes. O Lord of Bay Steeds, bring to make us joyful, celestial wealth abundant, undecaying.
20.36.4 Declare to us--if at thy hand aforetime the earlier singers have obtained good fortune What is thy share and portion, strong Subduer, Asura-slayer, rich, invoked of many?
20.36.5 He who for car-borne, thunder-wielding Indra, hath a hymn, craving deeply-piercing, fluent, Who sends a song effectual, firmly-grasping, and strength- bestowing, he comes near the mighty.
20.36.6 Strong of thyself! thou with this art hast shattered with thought- swift Parvata, him who waxed against thee; And, Mightiest! rager! boldly rent in pieces things that were firmly fixed and never shaken..
20.36.7 Him will we fit for you with new devotion, the strongest, Ancient One, in ancient manner. So way that Indra, boundless, faithful leader, conduct us o'er all places hard to traverse.
20.36.8 Thou for the people who oppress hast kindled the earthly firma- ment and that of heaven. With heat, O Bull, on every side consume them heat earth and flood for him who hates devotion:
20.36.9 Of all the heavenly folk, of earthly creatures, thou art the King, O God of splendid aspect. In thy right hand, O Indra, grasp the thunder: Eternal! thou destroyest all enchantments.
20.36.10 Give us confirmed prosperity, O Indra, vast and exhaustless for the foes' subduing. Strengthen therewith the Arya's hate and Dasa's; and let the arms of Nahushas be mighty.
20.36.11 Come with thy teams which bring all blessings, hither, disposer, much-invoked, exceeding holy! Come to me swiftly with these teams of coursers, these which no fiend, no God may stay or hinder.
;;; XXXVII ???
20.37.1 He, like a bull with sharpened horns, terrific, singly excites and agitates all the people. Then givest him who largely pours libation his wealth who pours not, for his own possession.
20.37.2 Thou verily, Indra, gavest help to Kutsa, willingly lending ear to him in battle. When, aiding Arjunneya, thou subduedst to him both Kuyava and the Dasa Sushna.
20.37.3 O Bold One, thou with all thine aids hast boldly helped Sudas whose offerings were accepted, Puru in winning land and slaying foemen, and Trasadasyu son of Purukutsa.
20.37.4 At the Gods' banquet, Hero-souled! with heroes, Lord of Bay Steeds, thou slewest many Vritras. Thou sentest in swift death to sleep the Dasyu, both Chumuri and Dhuni, for Dabhiti,
20.37.5 These were thy mighty powers that, Thunder-wielder! then swiftly crushedst nine-and ninety castles. Thou capturedst the hundredth in thine onslaught; thou slewest Namuchi, thou slewest Vritra.
20.37.6 Old are the blessings, Indra, which thou gavest Sudas the wor- shipperwho brought oblations. For thee, the strong I yoke thy strong bay horses: let them, approach our prayers and wealth, Most Mighty!
20.37.7 Give us not up, Lord of Bay Horses, victor, in this our time of- trouble, to the wicked. Deliver us with true and faithful succour: dear may we be to thee among the princes.
20.37.8 May we men, Bounteous Lord, the friends thou lovest, near i thee be joyful under thy protection. Fain to fulfil the wish of Atithigva, bow Turvasa, bow down,. the son of Yadu.
20.37.9 Swiftly, in truth, O Bounteous Lord, about thee men skilled im hymning sing their songs and praises. Elect us shares of their love and friendship who by their calls on, thee despoiled the niggards.
20.37.10 Thine are these Lauds, O manliest of heroes, Lauds which revert to us and give us riches. Favour these, Indra, when they strike the foemen, as Friend and Hero and the heroes' helper.
20.37.11 Now, lauded for thine aid, heroic Indra, sped by our prayer,, wax mighty in thy body. To us apportion wealth and habitations. Ye Gods, protect us- evermore with blessings.
;;; XXXVIII ???
20.38.1 Come, we have pressed the juice for thee. O Indra, drink the Soma here. Sit thou on this my sacred grass.
20.38.2 O Indra, let thy long-maned Bays, yoked by prayer, bring thee hitherward. Give ear and listen to our prayers.
20.38.3 We, Soma-bearing Brahmans, call thee, Soma-drinker, with thy friend, We, Indra, bringing juice expressed.
20.38.4 Indra the singers with high praise, Indra reciters with their lauds, Indra the choirs have glorified.
20.38.5 Indra hath ever close to him his two bay steeds and word-yoked: car, Indra, the golden, Thunder-armed.
20.38.6 Indra hath raised the Sun aloft in heaven that he may see afar. He burst the mountain for the kine.
;;; XXXIX ???
20.39.1 For you, from every side, we call Indra away from other men: Ours, and none others,' let him be.
20.39.2 In Soma's ecstasy Indra spread the firmament and realms of light. When he cleft Vala limb from limb.
20.39.3 Showing the hidden cows he draye them forth for the Angirases, And Vala he cast headlong down.
20.39.4 By Indra were the luminous realms of heaven established and secured, Firm and immovable from their place.
20.39.0 5. Indra, thy laud moves quickly like a joyous wave of waters: bright. Have shone the drops that gladden thee.
;;; XL ???
20.40.1 Mayest thou verily be seen coming by fearless Indra's side: Both joyous: equal in your sheen.
20.40.2 With Indra's well-beloved hosts, the blameless, hastening to heaven, The sacrificer cries aloud.
20.40.3 Thereafter they, as is their wont, threw off the state of babes unborn, Assuming sacrificial name.
;;; XLI ???
20.41.1 With bones of Dadhyach for his arms, Indra, resistless in attack, Struck nine-and-ninety Vritras dead,
20.41.2 He, searching for the horse's head, removed among the moun- tains, found At Saryanavan what he sought.
20.41.3 Then verily they recognized the essential form of Tvashtar's Bull. Here in the mansion of the Moon.
;;; XLII ???
20.42.1 From Indra have I measured an eight-footed and nine-cornered. song, Delicate, faithful to the Law.
20.42.2 Indra, both worlds complained to thee when uttering thy fearful roar, What time thou smotest Dasyus dead.
20.42.3 Arising in thy might thy jaws thou shookest, Indra, having quaffed The Soma poured into the bowls.
;;; XLIII ???
20.43.1 Drive all our enemies away, smite down the foes who press around, And bring the wealth for which we long;
20.43.2 O Indra, that which is concealed in firm strong place precipitous: Bring us the wealth for which we long:
20.43.3 Great riches which the world of men shall recognize as sent by thee: Bring us the wealth for which we long,
;;; XLIV ???
20.44.1 Praise Indra whom our songs must laud, great Sovran of man- kind, the Chief Most liberal who controlleth men.
20.44.2 In whom the hymns of praise delight, and all the glory-giving songs, Like the flood's longing for the sea.
