20.44.3 Him I invite with eulogy, best King, effective in the fight, Strong for the gain of mighty spoil.
;;; XLV ???
20.45.1 This is thine own. Thou drawest near, as the dove turneth to his mate. Thou carest too for this our prayer.
20.45.2 O Hero, Lord of Bounties, praised in hymns, may power and pleasantness Be his who signs the laud to thee.
20.45.3 Lord of a Hundred Powers, stand up to lend us succour in this fight: In others too let us agree.
;;; XLVI ???
20.46.1 Him who advances men to wealth, sends light to lead them in their wars, And quells their foemen in the fray:
20.46.2 May he, the saviour much-invoked, may Indra bear us in a ship Safely beyond all enemies.
20.46.3 As such, O Indra, honour us with wealth and treasure: further us, And lead us to felicity.
;;; XLVII ???
20.47.1 We make this Indra show his strength, to strike the mighty Vritra dead: A vigorous Hero shall he be.
20.47.2 Indra was made for giving, most powerful, friendly in carouse, Bright, meet for Soma, famed in song.
20.47.3 By song, as 'twere, the mighty bolt, which none may parry, was prepared: Lofty, invincible he grew.
20.47.10 They who stand round him as he moves harness the bright, the ruddy Steed: The lights are shining in the sky.
20.47.11 They yoke on both sides to the car the two bay coursers dear to him, Bold, tawny, bearers of the Chief.
20.47.12 Thou, making light where no light was, and form, O Men r where no form was, Wast born together with the Dawns,
20.47.13 His bright rays bear him up aloft, the God who knoweth all that= is, Surya, that every one may see.
20.47.14 The constellations pass away, like thieves, together with their- beams, Before the all-beholding Sun.
20.47.15 His herald rays are seen afar refulgent o'er the world of men, Like fiery flames that burn and blaze.
20.47.16 Swift and all-beautiful art thou, O Surya, maker of the light. Illuming all the radiant realm.
20.47.17 Thou guest to the troops of Gods, thou comest hither to man- kind, Hither, all light for us to see.
20.47.18 Thou with that eye of thine wherewith thou seest, brilliant. Varuna, The active one throughout mankind.
20.47.19 Pervadest heaven and wide mid-air, melting the days out with. thy beams, Sun, seeing all things that have birth.
20.47.20 Seven bay steeds, harnessed to thy car, bear thee, O.thou far- seeing One, God, Surya, thee with radiant hair.
20.47.21 Surya hath yoked the seven bright mares, the daughters of the car: With these, His own dear team, he travelleth.
;;; XLVIII ???
20.48.1 The swiftly-moving songs of praise pour on thee streams of vital strength As mother cows refresh the calf.
20.48.2 Swift move the bright ones while they blend the Milk with vital vigour, as A dame her infant with her heart.
20.48.3 Fair hymns bring glory to the Strong, and Indra-vigour; unto, me Fatness and milk and length of days.
20.48.4 This brindled Bull hath come and sat before the Mother in the east, Advancing to the Father Heaven.
20.48.5 As expiration from breath she moves along the lucid spheres: The Bull shines forth through all the sky.
20.48.6 Song is bestowed upon the Bird. It reigns supreme throughout thirty realms Throughout the days at break of morn.
;;; XLIX ???
20.49.1 When voices, fain to win mid-air, ascended to the Mighty One, The vigorous God was filled with joy.
20.49.2 Praise with the voice the Mighty, praise the awful with the voice: in heaven He, the most bounteous, hath been glad.
20.49.3 Praise with the voice the Mighty: he rules in each realm. In transport he Hath set upon the sacred grass.
20.49.4 As cows low to their calf in stalls, so with our songs we glorify This Indra, even your wondrous God who checks attack, who joys in the delightful juice.
20.49.5 Celestial, bounteous Giver, God, with power and might, rich, mountain-like, in precious things. Him soon we see for foodful booty rich in kine, brought hundredfold and thousandfold.
20.49.6 I crave of thee that hero strength--that thou mayst first regard this prayer Wherewith thou helpest Bhrigu and the Yatis and Praskanva when the prize was staked.
20.49.7 Wherewith thou sentest mighty waters to the sea--Indra, that manly strength of thine. For ever unattainable is this power of him to whom the worlds have cried aloud.
;;; L ???
20.50.1 What newest of imploring hymns shall, then, the zealous mortal sing? For have not they who laud his might and Indra-power won for themselves the light of heaven?
20.50.2 When shall they keep the Law and praise thee mid the Gods? Who counts as Rishi and as sage? When wilt thou ever, Indra, Bounteous Lord, come nigh to presser's or to praiser's call?
;;; LI ???
20.51.1 For you will I sing Indra's praise who gives good gifts as well we know; Praise of the Bounteous Lord who, rich in treasure, aids his singers with wealth thousandfold.
20.51.2 As with a hundred hosts he rushes boldly on, and for the offerer slays his foes. As from a mountain flow the water-brooks, thus flow his gifts who feedeth many a one.
20.51.3 Sakra I praise, for victory, far-famed, exceeding bountiful. Who gives, as 'twere in thousands, precious wealth to him who sheds the juice and worships him.
20.51.4 Arrows with hundred points, unconquerable, are this Indra's mighty arms in war. He streams on liberal worshippers like a hill with springs, when juices poured have gladdened him.
;;; LII ???
20.52.1 We compass thee like waters, we whose grass is trimmed and Soma pressed. Here where the filter pours its stream thy worshipper round thee, O Vritra-slayer, sit.
20.52.2 Men, Vasu! by the Soma, with lauds call thee to the foremost place. When comest thou athirst unto the juice as home, O Indra, like a bellowing bull?
;;; LIII ???
20.53.1 Who knows what vital power he wins, drinking beside the flowing juice? This is the fair-cheeked God who, joying in the draught, breaks down the castles in his strength.
20.53.2 As a wild elephant rushes on, this way and that way, mad with heat. None may restrain thee; yet come hither to the draught: thou movest mighty in thy power.
20.53.3 When he, the mighty, ne'er o'erthrown, stedfast, made ready for the fight. When Indra, Bounteous Lord, lists to his praiser's call, he will not stand aloof, but come.
;;; LIV ???
20.54.1 Of one accord they made and formed for kingship Indra, the Hero who in all encounters overcometh, Most eminent for power, destroyer in the conflict, fierce and exceeding strong, stalwart and full of vigour.
20.54.2 Bards joined in song to Indra so that he might drink the Soma juice, The Lord of Light, that he whose laws stand fast might aid with power and with help he gives.
20.54.3 The holy sages form a ring, looking and singing to the Ram. Your very bright inciters, void of all deceit, are with the chan- ters nigh to hear.
;;; LV ???
20.55.1 Oft, oft I call that Indra, Maghavan the mighty, who evermore possesses power, ever resistless. Holy, most liberal, may he lead us on to riches, and, thunder armed, make all our pathways pleasant for us.
20.55.2 Indra, what joys as Lord of Light thou broughtest from the Asuras, Prosper therewith, O Maghavan, him who lauds that deed, and those whose grass is trimmed for thee.
20.55.3 The wasteless share of steeds and kine which, Indra, thou hast fast secured. Grant to the worshipper who presses Soma and gives guerdon, not unto the churl.
;;; LVI ???
20.56.1 Indra, foe-slayer, hath been raised to joy and power by the men. Him, verily, we invocate in battles whether great or small: be he our aid in fights for spoil.
20.56.2 For, Hero, thou art like a host, art giver of abundant prey. Strengthening even the feeble, thou aidest the sacrificer, thou givest the worshipper ample wealth.
20.56.3 When war and battles are on foot, booty is laid before the bold. Yoke thou thy wildly rushing Bays. Whom wilt thou slay and whom enrich? Do thou, O Indra, make us rich,
20.56.4 He, righteous-hearted, at each time of rapture gives us herds of kine. Gather in both thy hands for us treasures of many hundred sorts. Sharpen thou us, and bring us wealth.
20.56.5 Refresh thee, Hero, with the juice outpoured for bounty and for strength. We know thee Lord of ample store, to thee have sent our heart's desires: be therefore our protector thou.
20.56.6 These people, Indra, keep for thee all that is worthy of thy choice. Discover thou, as Lord, the wealth of men who offer up no gifts: bring thou to us this wealth of theirs.
;;; LVII ???
20.57.1 As a good cow to him who milks, we call the doer of fair deeds. To our assistance day by day.
20.57.2 Come thou to our libations, drink of Soma, Soma-drinker thou! The rich One's rapture giveth kine.
20.57.3 So may we be acquainted with thine innermost benevolence: Neglect us not, come hitherward.
20.57.4 Drink for our help the Soma bright, vigilant, and exceeding strong, O Indra, Lord of Hundred Powers.
20.57.5 O Satakratu, powers which thou mid the Five Races hast dis- played, These, Indra, do I claim of thee.
20.57.6 Indra, great glory hast thou gained. Win splendid fame which none may mar. We make thy might perpetual.
20.57.7 Come to us either from anear, or, Sakra, come from far away. Indra, wherever be thy home, come thence, O Caster of the Stone.
20.57.8 Verily Indra, conquering all, driveth even mighty fear away. For firm is he and swift to act.
20.57.9 Indra be gracious unto us: sin shall not reach us afterward, And good shall be before us still.
20.57.10 From all the regions of the world let Indra send security. The foe-subduer, swift to act.
20.57.14 We compass thee like waters, we whose grass in trimmed and Soma pressed. Here where the filter pours its stream thy worshippers round thee, O Vritra-slayer, sit.
20.57.15 Men, Vasu, by the Soma with lauds call thee to the foremost place. When comest thou athirst unto the juice as home, O Indra, like a bellowing bull?
20.57.16 Boldly, bold Hero, bring us spoil in thousands for the Kanvas' sake. O active Maghavan, with eager prayer we crave the yellow-hued with store of kine.
;;; LVIII ???
20.58.1 Turning, as 'twere, to meet the Sun, enjoy from Indra all good things. When he who will be born is born with power we look to treasures as our heritage.
20.58.2 Praise him who sends us wealth, whose bounties injure none. Good are the gifts which Indra gives. He is not wroth with one who satisfies his wish: he turns his mind to granting boons.
20.58.3 Verily, Surya, thou art great; truly, Aditya, thou art great. As thou art great indeed thy greatness is admired: yea, verily, great art thou, O God.
20.58.4 Yea, Surya, thou art great in fame: thou evermore, O God, art great. By greatness thou art President of Gods, divine, far-spread, inviolable light.
;;; LIX ???
20.59.3 His portion is exceeding great, like a victorious soldier's spoil. Him who is Indra, Lord of Bays, no foes subdue. He gives the Soma-pourer strength.
20.59.4 Make for the holy Gods a hymn that is not mean, but well arranged and fair in form. Full many snares and bonds subdue not him who dwells with Indra through his sacrifice.
;;; LX ???
20.60.1 For so thou art the hero's Friend, a Warrior too art thou, and strong: So may thy heart be won to us.
20.60.2 So hath the offering; wealthiest Lord, been paid by all the worshippers: So dwell thou, Indra, even with me.
20.60.3 Be not thou, like a slothful priest, O Lord of wealth and spoil: rejoice. In the pressed Soma blent with milk.
20.60.4 So also is his excellence, great copious, rich in cattle, like A ripe branch to the worshipper.
20.60.5 For verily thy mighty powers, Indra, are saving helps at once Unto a worshipper like me.
20.60.6 So are his lovely gifts: let laud be said and praise to Indra sung. That he may drink the Soma juice.
;;; LXI ???
20.61.1 We sing this strong and wild delight of thine which conquers in the fray, Which, Caster of the Stone, gives room and shine like gold.
20.61.2 Wherewith thou also foundest lights for Ayu and for Manu's sake: Now joying in!!this sacred grass thou beamest forth.
20.61.3 This day to singers of the hymn praise, as of old, this, might of thine. Win thou the waters, day by day, thralls of the strong.
20.61.4 Sing forth to him whom many men invoke, to him whom many laud: Invite the potent Indra with your songs of praise;
20.61.5 Whose lofty might--for doubly strong is he--supports the heaven and earth. And hills and plains and floods and light with manly power.
20.61.6 Such, praised by many! thou art King: alone thou smitest foe- men dead, To gain, O Indra, spoils of war and high renown.
;;; LXII ???
20.62.5 To Indra sing a Saman, sing to the high Sage a lofty song, To him who keeps the Law, inspired and fain for praise.
20.62.6 Thou, Indra, art preeminent: thou gavest splendour to the Sun. Maker of all things, thou art mighty and All-God.
20.62.7 Radiant with light thou wentest to the sky, the luminous realms: of heaven. The Gods, O Indra, strove to win thee for their friend.
20.62.8 Sing forth to him whom many men invoke, to him whom many laud: Invite the potent Indra with your songs of praise;
20.62.9 Whose lofty might--for doubly strong is he--supports the heaven and earth, And hills and plains and floods and light with manly power.
20.62.10 Such, praised by many! thou art King. Alone thou smitest foe- men dead, To gain, O Indra, spoils of war and high renown.
;;; LXIII ???
20.63.1 We will, with Indra, and all Gods to aid us, bring these existing. worlds into subjection. Our sacrifice, our bodies, and our offspring, let Indra form to- gether with the Adityas.
20.63.2 With the Adityas with the band of Maruts, may Indra be pro- tector of our bodies; As when the Gods came, after they had slaughtered the Asuras,. keeping safe their godlike nature,
20.63.3 Brought the Sun hitherward with mighty powers, and looked! about them on their vigorous God-head. With this may we obtain strength God-appointed, and brave sons gladden us through a hundred winters.
20.63.4 He who alone bestoweth might on mortal man who offereth gifts, The ruler of resistless power, is Indra, sure.
20.63.5 When will he trample like a weed the man who hath no gift for him? When verily will Indra hear our songs of praise?
20.63.6 He who with Soma juice prepared among the many harbours. thee, Verily Indra gains thereby tremendous might.
20.63.7 Joy, mightiest Indra, known and marked, sprung most from Soma draughts, wherewith Thou smitest down the greedy fiend, for that we pray.
20.63.8 Wherewith thou helpest Adhrigu, the great Dasagva, and the God Who stirs the sunlight, and Sea, for that we pray.
20.63.9 Wherewith thou dravest forth like cars Sindhu and all the mighty floods. To go the way ordained by Law, for that we pray.
;;; LXIV ???
20.64.1 Come unto us, O Indra, dear, still conquering, unconcealable, Vast as a mountain spread on all sides, Lord of heaven.
20.64.2 O truthful Soma-drinker, thou art mightier than both the worlds. Thou strengthenest him who pours libation, Lord of heaven.
20.64.3 For thou art, he, O Indra, who stormest all castles of the foe, Slayer of Dasyus, man's supporter, Lord of heaven.
20.64.4 O ministering priest, pour out of the sweet juice what gladdens most. So is the Hero praised who ever prospers us.
20.64.5 Indra whom tawny coursers bear, praise such a thine,. preeminent None by his power or by his goodness hath attained
20.64.6 We seeking glory, have invoked this Master of all power and' might. Who must be glorified by constant sacrifice.
;;; LXV ???
20.65.1 Come, sing we praise to Indra, friends! the Hero who deserves the laud, Him who with none to aid o'ercomes all tribes of men.
20.65.2 To him who wins the kine, who keeps no cattle back, celestial God, Speak wondrous speech more sweet than butter and than mead.
20.65.3 Whose hero powers are measureless, whose bounty ne'er may be surpassed, Whose liberality, like light, is over all.
;;; LXVI ???
20.66.1 As Vyasva did, praise Indra, praise the strong unfluctuating guide. Who gives the foe's possessions to the worshipper.
20.66.2 Now, son of Vyasva, praise thou him who to the tenth time still is new. The very wise, whom living men must glorify.
20.66.3 Thou knowest, Indra, thunder-armed, how to avoid destructive Powers, As one secure from pitfalls each succeeding day.
;;; LXVII ???
20.67.1 The pourer of oblations gains the home of wealth pouring his gift conciliates hostilities, yea, the hostilities of Gods. Pouring he strives, unchecked and strong, to win him riches thousandfold. Indra gives lasting wealth to him who pours forth gifts; yea, wealth he gives that long shall last.
20.67.2 Ne'er may those manly deeds of yours for us grow old, never may your bright glories fall into decay, never before your time decay. What deed of yours, new every age, wondrous, surpassing man,. rings forth, Whatever, Maruts may be difficult to gain grant us whate'er is hard to win.
20.67.3 I think on Agni, Hotar, the munificent, the gracious Son of strength, who knoweth all that live, as holy Sage who knoweth all. Lord of fair rites, a God with form erected turning to the Gods. He, when the flame hath sprung forth from the holy oil, the offered fatness, longeth for it with his glow.
20.67.4 Busied with sacrifice, with spotted deer and spears, gleaming. upon your way with ornaments, yea, our friends, Sitting on sacred grass, ye sons of Bharata, drink Soma from the Potar's bowl, O Men of heaven.
20.67.5 Bring the Gods hither, Sage, and offer sacrifice. At the three altars seat thee willingly .O Priest. Accept for thy delight the proffered Soma mead: drink from the Kindler's bowl and sate thee with thy share.
20.67.6 This is the strengthener of thy body's manly might: strength,. victory for all time are laid within thine arms. Pressed for thee, Maghavan, it is offered unto thee: drink from the chalice of this Brahman, drink thy fill.
20.67.7 Him whom of old I called on, him I call on now. He is to be invoked: his name is He who Gives. Here brought by priests in Soma mead. Granter of Wealth, drink Soma with the Seasons from the Hotar's Cup.
;;; LXVIII ???
20.68.4 Go to the wise unconquered One, ask thou of Indra, skilled in song, Him who is better than thy friends.
20.68.5 Whether the men who mock us say, Depart unto another place, Ye who serve Indra and none else;
20.68.6 Or whether, God of wondrous deeds, all our true people call us blest, Still may we dwell in Indra's care.
20.68.7 Unto the swift One bring the swift, man-cheering, grace of sacrifice. That to the Friend gives wings and joy.
20.68.8 Thou, Satakratu, drankest this and wast the Vritras' slayer; thou. Helpest the warrior in the fray.
20.68.9 We strengthen, Satakratu, thee, yea, thee the powerfull in fight, That, Indra, we may win us wealth.
20.68.10 To him the mighty stream of wealth, prompt Friend of him who pours the juice, Yea, to this Indra sing your song.
20.68.41 O come ye hither, sit ye down: to Indra sing ye forth your song, Companions, bringing hymns of praise.
20.68.12 To him the richest of the rich, the Lord of treasures excellent, Indra, with Soma juice outpoured.
;;; LXIX ???
20.69.1 May he stand by us in our need and in abundance for our wealth: With riches may he come to us;
20.69.2 Whose pair of tawny horses yoked in battles foemen challenge not: To him, to Indra, sing your song.
20.69.3 Nigh to the Soma-drinker come, for his enjoyment, these bright drops, The Somas mingled with the curd.
20.69.4 Thou, grown at once to perfect strength, wast born to drink the Soma juice, strong Indra, for preeminence.
20.69.5 O Indra, lover of the song, may these quick Somas enter thee: May they bring bliss to thee the Sage.
20.69.0 6. O Lord of Hundred Powers, our chants of praise and lauds have strengthened thee: So strengthen thee the songs we sing!
20.69.7 Indra, whose succour never fails, accept this treasure thousand- fold, Wherein all manly powers abide.
20.69.8 O Indra, thou who lovest song, let no man hurt our bodies, keep. Slaughter far from us, for thou canst.
20.69.12 Thereafter they, as is their wont, threw off the state of babes urborn, Taking their sacrificial name.
;;; LXX ???
20.70.1 Thou, Indra, with the Tempest-Gods, the breakers down of what is firm, Foundest the kine even in the cave.
20.70.2 Worshipping even as they list, singers laud him who findeth wealth, The far-renowned, the mighty One.
20.70.3 Then, faring on by Indra's side, the fearless, let thyself be seen,. Both gracious and in splendour peers.
20.70.4 With Indra's well-beloved hosts, the blameless, tending heaven- ward, The sacrificer cries aloud.
20.70.5 Come from this place, O wanderer, or downward from the light of heaven! Our songs of praise all yearn for this.
20.70.6 Or Indra we implore for help from here, from heaven above the earth, Or from the spacious firmament.
20.70.7 Indra the singers with high praise, Indra reciters with their lauds, Indra the choirs have glorified.
20.70.8 Indra hath ever close to him his two bay steeds and word-yoked car, Indra the golden, Thunder-armed.
20.70.9 Indra hath raisedjthe Sun on high in heaven, that he may see afar: He burst the mountain for the kine.
20.70.10 Help us, O Indra, in the frays, yea, frays where thousand spoils are gained, With awful aids, O awful One.
20.70.11 In mighty battle we invoke, Indra, Indra in lesser fight, The friend who bends his bolt at fiends.
20.70.12 Unclose, our manly Hero, thou for ever bounteous, yonder cloud, For us, thou irresistible.
20.70.13 Still higher, at each strain of mine, thunder-armed Indra's, praises rise: I find no laud worthy of him.
20.70.14 Even as the bull drives on the herds, he drives the people with his might, The ruler irresistible:
20.70.15 Indra who rules with single sway men, riches, and the fivefold race. Of those who dwell upon the earth.
20.70.16 For your sake from each side we call Indra away from other men: Ours, and none others', may he be.
20.70.17 Indra, bring wealth that gives delight, the victor's ever-conquer- ing wealth, Most excellent, to be our aid;
20.70.18 By means of which we may repel our foes in battle hand to hand. By thee assisted with the car.
20.70.19 Aided by thee, the Thunder-armed, Indra; may we lit up the bolt, And conquer all our foes in fight.
20.70.20 With thee, O Indra, for ally, with missile-darting heroes may We conquer our embattled foes.
;;; LXXI ???
20.71.1 Mighty is Indra, yea, supreme; greatness becomes the Thunderer! Wide as the heaven extends his power;
20.71.2 Which aideth those to win them sons who come as heroes to the fight, Or singers loving holy thoughts.
20.71.3 His belly drinking deepest draughts of Soma like an ocean swells, Like wide streams from the cope of heaven.
20.71.7 Come, Indra, and delight thee with the juice at all the Soma feasts, Protector, mighty in thy strength.
20.71.8 To Indra pour ye forth the juice, the active gladdening juice, to him The gladdening omnific God.
20.71.9 O Lord of all men, fair of cheek, rejoice thee in the gladdening buds, Present at these drink-offerings.
20.71.10 Songs have outpoured themselves to thee, Indra, the strong, the guardian Lord. And raised themselves unsatisfied.
20.71.11 Send to us bounty manifold, O Indra, worthy of our wish, For power supreme is only thine.
20.71.12 O Indra, stimulate thereto us emulously fain for wealth. And glorious, O most splendid One.
20.71.13 Give, Indra, wide and lofty fame, wealthy in cattle and in strength, Lasting our life-time, failing not.
20.71.14 Grant us high fame, O Indra, grant riches bestowing thousands, those Fair fruits of earth borne home in wains.
20.71.15 Praising with songs the praise-worthy who cometh to our aid, we call Indra, the Treasure-Lord of wealth.
20.71.16 To lofty Indra, dweller by each libation, the pious man Sings forth aloud a strengthening hymn.
;;; LXXII ???
20.72.1 In all libations men with hero spirit urge thee, Universal, One, each seeking several light, each fain to win the light apart. Thee, furthering like a ship, will we set to the chariot pole of strength, As men who win with sacrifices Indra's thought, men who win Indra with their lauds.
20.72.2 Couples desirous of thine aid are storming thee, pouring their presents forth to win a stall of kine, pouring gifts, Indra, seeking thee. When two men seeking spoil or heaven thou bringest face to face in war, Thou showest Indra, then the bolt thy constant friend, the bull that ever waits on thee,
20.72.3 Also this morn may he be well inclined to us, mark at our call our offerings and our song of praise, our call that we may win the light. As thou, O Indra Thunder-armed, wilt, as the Strong One, slay the foe, Listen, thou to the prayer of me a later sage, hear thou a later sage's prayer.
;;; LXXIII ???
20.73.1 All these libations are for thee, O Hero: to thee I offer these my prayers that strengthen. Ever, in every place, must men invoke thee.
20.73.2 Never do men attain, O Wonder-worker, thy greatness, Mighty One who must be lauded, Nor, Indra, thine heroic power and bounty.
20.73.3 Bring to the Wise, the Great who waxeth mighty your offerings and make ready your devotion: To many clans he goeth, man's Controller.
20.73.4 When, with the Princes, Maghavan, famed of old, comes nigh the thunderbolt of gold and the Controller's car Which his two tawny coursers draw, then Indra is the Sovran Lord of power whose fame spreads far and wide.
20.73.5 With him too is this rain of his that comes like herds: Indra throws drops of moisture on his yellow beard. When the sweet juice is shed he seeks the pleasant place, and stirs the worshipper as the wind disturbs the wood.
20.73.6 We laud and praise his several deeds of valour who, fatherlike,. with power hath made us stronger; Who with his voice slew many thousand wicked ones who spake in varied manner with contemptuous cries.
;;; LXXIV ???
20.74.1 O Soma-drinker, ever true, utterly hopeless though we be, Do thou, O Indra, give us hope of beauteous horses and of kine, In thousands, O most wealthy One.
20.74.2 O Lord of strength, whose jaws are strong, great deeds are thine, the powerful: Do thou, O Indra, give us hope of beauteous horses and of kine, In thousands, O most wealthy One.
20.74.3 Lull thou asleep, to wake no more, the pair who on each other look: Do thou, O Indra, give us hope of beauteous horses and of kine, In thousands, O most wealthy One.
20.74.4 Hero, let hostile spirits sleep, and every gentler Genius wake: Do thou, O Indra, give us hope of beauteous horses and of kine, In thousands, O most wealthy One.
20.74.5 Destroy this ass, O Indra, who in tones discordant brays to thee: Do thou, O Indra, give us hope of beauteous horses and of kine, In thousands, O most wealthy One.
20.74.6 Far distant on the forest fall the tempest in a circling course; Do thou, O Indra, give us hope of beauteous horses and of kine, In thousands, O most wealthy One.
20.74.7 Slay each reviler and destroy him who in secret injures us: Do thou, O Indra, give us thope of beauteous horses and of kine, In thousands, O most wealthy One.
;;; LXXV ???
20.75.1 Couples desirous of thine aid are storming thee, pouring their presents forth to win a stall of king pouring gifts, Indra, seeking thee. When two men seeking spoil or heaven thou bringest face to face in war, Thou showest, Indra, then the bolt, thy constant friend, the bull that ever waits on thee.
20.75.2 This thine heroic power full well the people knew, wherewith thou brakest down, Indra, autumnal forts, brakest them down with conquering might. Thou hast chastised. O Indra, Lord of strength, the man who worships not, And made thine own this great earth and these water-floods, with joyous heart these water-floods.
20.75.3 And they have bruited far this hero might, when thou, O Strong One, in thy joy helpest thy suppliants who sought to win thee for their Friend. Their battle-cry thou madest sound victorious in the shocks of war. One stream after another have they gained from thee, eager for glory have they gained.
;;; LXXVI ???
20.76.1 As sits the young bird on the tree rejoicing, ye, swift pair, have been roused by clear laudation, Whose Hoter-priest through many days is Indra, earth's guardian, friend of men, the best of heroes.
20.76.2 May we, when this Dawn and the next dance hither, be thy best servants, most heroic Hero! Let the victorious car with triple splendour bring hitherward the hundred chiefs with Kutsa.
20.76.3 What was the gladdening draught that pleased thee, Indra? Speed to our doors, our songs, for thou art mighty. Why comest thou to me, what gift attracts thee? Fain would I bring thee food most meet to offer.
20.76.4 Indra, what fame hath one like thee mid heroes? With what plan wilt thou act? Why hast thou sought us? As a true friend, Wide-Strider! to sustain us, since food absorbs the thought of each among us.
20.76.5 Speed happily those, as Surya ends his journey, who meet his wish as bridegrooms meet their spouses; Men who support, O Indra strong by nature, with food the many songs that tell thy praises.
20.76.6 Thine are two measures, Indra, wide, well-meted, heaven for thy majesty, earth for thy wisdom. Here for thy choice are Somas mixed with butter: may the sweet meath be pleasant for thy drinking.
20.76.7 They have poured out a bowl to him, to Indra, full of sweet juice, for faithful is his bounty. O'er earth's expanse hath he grown great by wisdom, the friend of man, and by heroic exploits.
20.76.8 Indra hath conquered in his wars the mighty: men strive in multitudes to win his friendship. Ascend thy chariot as it were in battle, which thou shalt drive to us with gracious favour,
;;; LXXVII ???
20.77.1 Impetuous, true, let Maghavan come hither, and let his tawny coursers speed to reach us. For him have we pressed juice exceeding potent: here, praised with song, let him effect his visit.
20.77.2 Unyoke, as at thy journey's end, O Hero, to gladden thee to-day at this libation. Like Usana, the priest a laud shall utter, a hymn to thee, the Lord Divine, who markest.
20.77.3 When the Bull quaffing praises our libation, as a sage paying holy rites in secret, Seven singers here from heaven hath he begotten, who e'en by day have wrought their works while singing.
20.77.4 When heaven's fair light by hymns was made apparent. (they made great splendour shine at break of morning), He with his succour, best of heroes, scattered the blinding dark- ness so that men saw clearly.
20.77.5 Indra, impetuous One, hath waxed immensely: he with his vastness hath filled earth and heaven. E'en beyond this his majesty extendeth who hath exceeded all the worlds in greatness,
20.77.6 Sakra who knoweth well all human actions hath with his eager friends let loose the waters. They with their songs cleft e'en the mountain open, and willingly disclosed the stall of cattle.
20.77.7 He smote away the flood's obstructer Vritra: Earth conscious lent her aid to speed thy thunder. Thou sentest forth the waters of the ocean as Lord through power and might, O daring Hero.
20.77.8 When, Much-invoked! the waters' rock thou deftest, Sarama showed herself and went before thee. Hymned by Angirases, bursting the cowstalls, thou foundest ample strength for us as leader.
;;; LXXVIII ???
20.78.1 Sing this, what time the juice is pressed, to him your Hero much-invoked, To please him as a mighty, Bull.
20.78.2 He, excellent, withholdeth not his gift of power and wealth in kine, When he hath listened to our songs.
20.78.3 May he with might disclose for us the cows' stall, whosesoe'er it be, To which the Dasyu-slayer goes.
;;; LXXIX ???
20.79.1 O Indra, give us wisdom as a sire gives wisdom to his sons. Guide us, O Much-invoked, on this our foray: may we, living, still enjoy the light.
20.79.2 Grant that no mighty foes, unknown, malevolent, unhallowed, tread us to the ground. With thine assistance, Hero! may we pass through all the waters that are rushing down.
;;; LXXX ???
20.80.1 Bring us, O Indra, name and fame, enriching, mightiest, excellent, Wherewith, O wondrous God, fair-cheeked and thunder-armed, thou hast filled full this earth and heaven.
20.80.2 We call on thee, O King, mighty among the Gods, ruler of men, to succour us, All that is weak in us, excellent God, make firm: make our foes easy to subdue.
;;; LXXXI ???
20.81.1 O Indra, if a hundred heavens and if a hundred earths were: thine No, not a hundred suns could match thee at thy birth, not, both, the worlds, O Thunderer.
20.81.2 Thou, Hero, hast performed thy hero needs with might, yea, all+ with strength, O Strongest One. Maghavan, help us to a stable full of kine, O Thunderer, with) wondrous aids.
;;; LXXXII ???
20.82.1 If I, O Indra, were the lord of riches ample as thine own, I should support the singer, God who scatterest wealth! and! not abandon him to woe.
20.82.2 Each day would I enrich the man who sang my praise, in what- soever place he were. No kinship is there better, Maghavan, than thine: a father even) is no more.
;;; LXXXIII ???
20.83.1 O Indra, grant a happy home, a triple refuge, triply strong. Bestow a dwelling-place on the rich lords and me, and keep thy dart afar from these.
20.83.2 They who with minds intent on spoil subdue the foe, boldly attack and smite him down. From these, O Indra, Bounteous Lord who lovest song, be closest guardian of our lives.
;;; LXXXIV ???
20.84.1 O Indra marvellously bright, come, these libations long for thee, Thus by fine fingers purified.
20.84.2 Urged by the holy singer, sped by song, come, Indra, to the prayers. Of the libation-pouring priest.
20.84.3 Approach, O Indra, hasting thee, Lord of Bay Horses, to the prayers: Take pleasure in the juice we pour.
;;; LXXXV ???
20.85.1 Glorify naught besides, O friends; so shall no sorrow trouble you. Praise only mighty Indra when the juice is shed, and say your lauds repeatedly:
20.85.2 Even him, eternal, like a bull who rushes down, men's con- queror, bounteous like a cow; Him who is cause of both, of enmity and peace, to both sides most munificent.
20.85.3 Although these men in sundry ways invoke thee to obtain thine aid. Be this our prayer, addressed, O Indra, unto thee, thine exalta- tion every day.
20.85.4 Those skilled in song, O Maghavan, among these men o'ercome with might the foeman's songs, Come hither, bring us strength in many a varied form most near that it may succour us.
;;; LXXXVI ???
20.86.1 Those who are yoked by prayer with prayer I harness, the two. fleet friendly Bays who joy together. Mounting thy firm and easy car, O Indra, wise and all-knowing come thou to the Soma.
;;; LXXXVII ???
20.87.1 Priests, offer to the Lord of all the people the milked-out stalk of Soma, radiant-coloured. No wild bull knows his drinking-place like Indra who ever seeks him who hath pressed the Soma.
20.87.2 Thou dost desire to drink, each day that passes, the pleasant food which thou hast had aforetime. O Indra, gratified in heart and spirit, drink eagerly the Soma set before thee.
20.87.3 Thou, newly-born, for strength didst drink the Soma; thy mother told thee of thy future greatness. O Indra, thou hast filled mid-air's wide region, and given the Gods by battle room and freedom.
20.87.4 When thou hast urged the arrogant to combat, proud in their strength of arm, we will subdue them. Or, Indra, when thou fightest girt by heroes, we in the glorious fray with thee will conquer.
20.87.5 I will declare the earliest deeds of Indra, and recent acts which Maghavan hath accomplished. When he had conquered godless wiles and magic, Soma became his own entire possession.
20.87.6 Thine is this world of flocks and herds around thee, which with the eye of Surya thou beholdest. Thou, Indra, art alone the Lord of cattle: may we enjoy the treasure which thou givest.
20.87.7 Ye twain are Lords of wealth in earth and heaven, thou, O Brihaspati, and thou, O Indra . Mean though he be, give wealth to him who lauds you. Preserve us evermore, ye Gods, with blessings.
;;; LXXXVIII ???
20.88.1 Him who with might hath propped earth's ends, who sitteth in threefold seat, Brihaspati, with thunder, Him of the pleasant tongue have ancient sages, deep thinking,. holy singers, set before them.
20.88.2 Wild in their course, in well-marked wise rejoicing were they,. Brihaspati, who pressed around us Preserve, Brihaspati, the stall uninjured,r,this company's raining. ever-moving birth-place.
20.88.3 Brihaspati, from thy remotest distance have they sat down who love the law eternal. For thee were dug wells springing from the mountain, which murmuring round about pour streams of sweetness.
20.88.4 Brihaspati, when first he had his being from mighty splendour in supremest heaven. Strong, with his sevenfold mouth, with noise of thunder, with his seven rays blew and dispersed the darkness.
20.88.5 With the loud-shouting band who sang his praises, with thunder, he destroyed malignant Vala. Brihaspati thundering drave forth the cattle, the lowing cows who make oblations ready.
20.88.6 Serve we with sacrifices, gifts, and homage even thus the Steer of all the Gods, the Father. Brihaspati, may we be lords of riches, with noble progeny and, store of heroes.
;;; LXXXIX ???
20.89.1 Even as an archer shoots afar his arrow, offer the laud to him with meet adornment. Quell with your voice the wicked's voice, O sages, Singer, make Indra rest beside the Soma.
20.89.2 Draw thy Friend to thee like a cow at milking: O singer, wake up Indra as a lover. Make thou the Hero haste to give us riches even as a vessel filled brimful with treasure.
20.89.3 Why, Maghavan, do they call thee bounteous Giver? Quicken me: thou, I hear, art he who quickens. Sakra, let my intelligence be active, and bring us luck that finds great wealth, O Indra.
20.89.4 Standing, in battle for their rights, together, the people, Indra, in the fray invoke thee. Him who brings gifts the Hero makes his comrade: with him who pours no juice he seeks not friendship.
20.89.5 Whoso with plenteous juice for him expresses strong Somas as much quickly-coming treasure, For him he everthrows in early morning his swift well-weapon- ed foes and slays the tyrant.
20.89.6 He unto whom we offer praises, Indra, Maghavan, who hath joined to ours his wishes Before him even afar the foe must tremble: low before him must bow all human glories.
20.89.7 With thy fierce bolt, O God invoked of many, drive to a distance from afar the foeman. O Indra, give us wealth in corn and cattle, and make the singer's prayer gain strength and riches.
20.89.8 Indra the swallower of strong libations with their thick residue, the potent Somas, He, Maghavan, will not restrict his bounty: he brings much wealth unto the Soma-presser.
20.89.9 Yea, by superior play he wins advantage when he, a gambler, piles his gains in season. Celestial-natured, he o'erwhelms with riches the devotee who keeps not back his money.
20.89.10 O much-invoked, may we subdue all famine and evil want with store of grain and cattle. May we allied, as first in rank, with princes,:obtain possessions by our own exertion
20.89.11 Brihaspati protect us from the rearward, and from above and from below, from sinners. May Indra from the front and from the centre, as friend to friends, vouchsafe us room and freedom.
;;; XC ???
20.90.1 Served with oblations, first-born, mountain-render, Angiras' Son, Brihaspati the holy. With twice-firm path, dwelling in light, our Father, roars loudly, as a bull, to earth and heaven.
20.90.2 Brihaspati who made for such a people wide room and verge when Gods were invocated-- Slaying his foe he breaketh down their cattles, quelling his enemies and those who hate him.
20.90.3 Brihaspati in war hath won rich treasures, hath won, this God, the great stalls filled with cattle. Striving to win waters and light, resistless, Brihaspati with light- ning smites the foeman.
;;; XCI ???
20.91.1 This holy hymn sublime and seven-headed, sprung from eternal Law, our sire discovered. Ayasya, friend of all men, hath engendered the fourth hymn as he sang his laud to Indra.
20.91.2 Thinking aright, praising eternal Order, the sons of Dyaus the Asura, those heroes, Angirases, holding the rank of sages, first honoured sacrifice's holy statute.
20.91.3 Girt by his friends who cried with swanlike voices, bursting the stoney barriers of the prison, Brihaspati spake in thunder to the cattle, and uttered praise and. song when he had found them.
20.91.4 Apart from one, away from two above him, he draye the kine that stood in bonds of falsehood. Brihaspati, seeking light amid the darkness, draye forth the bright cows: three he made apparent.
20.91.5 When he had cleft the lairs and western castle, he cut off three from him who held the waters. Brihaspati discovered, while he thundered like Dyaus, the dawn,. the sun, the cow, the lightning.
20.91.6 As with a hand, so with his roaring Indra cleft Vala through,. the guardian of the cattle. Seeking the milk-draught with sweat-shining comrades he stole: the Pani's kine and left him weeping.
20.91.7 He with bright faithful friends, winners of booty, hath rent the milker of the cows asunder. Brihaspati with wild boars strong and mighty sweating with heat hath gained a rich possession.
20.91.8 They, longing for the kine, with faithful spirit incited with their hymns the Lord of cattle. Brihaspati freed the radiant cows with comrades self-yoked,. averting shame from one another.
20.91.9 In our assembly with auspicious praises exalting him who roareth. like a lion. May we in every fight where heroes conquer rejoice in strong. Brihaspati the victor.
20.91.10 When he had won him strength of every nature and gone to heaven and its most lofty mansions, Men praised Brihaspati the mighty, bringing the light within their mouths from sundry places.
20.91.11 Fulfil the prayer that begs for vital vigor: aid in your wonted manner e'en the humble. Let all our foes be turned and driven backward. Hear this, O Heaven and Earth, ye all-producers.
20.91.12 Indra with mighty strength hath cleft asunder the head of Arbuda the watery monster, Slain Ahi, and set free the Seven Rivers. O Heaven and Earth, with all the Gods, protect us.
;;; XCII ???
20.92.1 Praise, even as he is known, with song Indra the guardian of the kine, The Son of Truth, Lord of the brave.
20.92.2 Hither his bay steeds have been sent, red steeds are on the sacred grass. Where we in concert sing our songs.
20.92.3 For Indra thunder-armed the kine have yielded mingled milk and meath. What time he found them in the vault.
20.92.4 When I and Indra amount on high up to the bright One's place and home, We, having drunk of meath, will reach his seat whose Friends are three-times-seven.
20.92.5 Sing, sing ye forth your songs of praise, ye Priyamedhas, sing your songs: Yea, let young children sing their lauds: as a strong castle praise ye him.
20.92.6 Now loudly let the viol sound, the lute send out its voice with might, Shrill be the music of the string. To Indra is the hymn upraised.
20.92.7 When hither speed the dappled cows, unflinching, easy to be milked, Seize quickly, as it bursts away, the Soma juice for Indra's drink.
20.92.8 Indra hath drunk; Agni hath drunk all Deities have drunk their fill. Here Varuna shall have his home, to whom the floods have sung aloud as mother-kine unto their calves.
20.92.9 Thou, Varuna, to whom belong the Seven Streams, art a glorious God. The waters flow into thy throat as'twere a pipe with ample mouth.
20.92.10 He who hath made the fleet steeds spring, well-harnessed, to the worshipper, He, the swift guide, is that fair form thot loosed the horses near at hand.
20.92.11 Indra, the very mighty, holds his enemies in utter scorn. He, far away, and yet a child, cleft the cloud smitten by his voice.
20.92.12 He, yet a boy exceeding small, mounted his newly-fashioned car. He for his Mother and his Sire cooked the wild mighty buffalo.
20.92.13 Lord of the Home, with beauteous cheeks, ascend thy chariot wrought of gold. We will attend the heavenly One; the thousand-footed, red of hue, matchless, who blesses where he goes.
20.92.14 With reverence they come hitherward to him as to a sovran lord, That they may bring him near for this man's good success, to prosper and bestow his gifts.
20.92.15 The Priyamedhas have observed the offering of the men of old, Of ancient custom, while they strewed the sacred grass and spread their sacrificial food.
20.92.16 He who as sovran Lord of men moves with his chariots unrestrained, The Vritra-slayer, queller of all fighting hosts, preeminent, is praised in song.
20.92.17 Honour that Indra, Puruhanman! for his aid, in whose sustain- ing hand of old. The splendid bolt of thunder was deposited, as the great Sun was set in heaven.
20.92.18 No one by deed attains to him who works and strengthens evermore: No, not by sacrifice, to Indra praised of all, resistless, daring, bold in might;
20.92.19 The potent Conqueror, invincible in war, him at whose birth the mighty ones, The kine who spread afar, sent their loud voices out, heavens, earths sent their loud voices out.
20.92.20 O Indra, if a hundred heavens and if a hundred earths were thine No, not a thousand suns could match thee at thy birth, not both the worlds, O Thunderer.
20.92.21 Thou, Hero, hast performed thy hero deeds with might, yea, all with strength, O Strongest One. Maghavan, help us to a stable full of kine, O Thunderer, with wondrous aids.
;;; XCIII ???
20.93.1 May our hymns give thee great delight. Display thy bounty, Thunderer. Drive off the enemies of prayer.
20.93.2 Crush with thy foot the niggard churls who bring no gifts. Might art thou: There is not one to equal thee.
20.93.3 Thou art the Lord of Soma pressed, Soma unpressed is also thine, Thou art the Sovran of the folk.
20.93.4 Swaying about the active Ones came nigh to Indra at his birth, And shared his great heroic might.
20.93.5 Based upon strength and victory and power, O Indra is thy birth. Thou, Mighty One, art strong indeed.
20.93.6 Thou art the Vritra-slayer, thou, Indra, hast spread the firmament: Thou hast with might upheld the heavens.
20.93.7 Thou, Indra, bearest in thine arms the lightning that accords with thee, Whetting thy thunderbolt with might.
20.93.8 Thou, Indra, art pre-eminent over all creatures in thy strength: Thou hast pervaded every place.
;;; XCIV ???
20.94.1 May Sovran Indra come to the carousal, he who by holy Law is strong and active. The overcomer of all conquering forces with his great bull-like power that hath no limit.
20.94.2 Firm-seated is thy car, thy steeds are docile: thy hand, O King, holds, firmly grasped, the thunder. On thy fair path, O Lord of men, come quickly: we will increase thy power when thou hast drunken.
20.94.3 Let strong and mighty steeds who bear this mighty Indra, the Lord of men, whose arm wields thunder, Bring unto us, as shares of our banquet, the Bull of conquering might, of real vigour.
20.94.4 So like a bull thou rushest to the Lord who loves the trough, the Sage, the prop of vigour, in the vat. Prepare thine energies, collect them in thyself: be for our profit as the Master of the wise.
20.94.5 May precious treasures come to us,-- so will I pray. Come to the votary's gift offered with beauteous laud. Thou art the Lord, as such sit on this holy grass: thy vessels are inviolate as Law commands.
20.94.6 Far went our earliest invocations of the Gods, and won us glories that can never be surpassed. They who could not ascend the ship of sacrifice sink down in desolation, trembling with alarm.
20.94.7 So be the others, evil-hearted, far away, whose horses difficult to harness have been yoked. Here in advance man stand anear to offer gifts, by whom full many a work that brings reward is done.
20.94.8 He firmly fixed the plains and mountains as they shook. Dyaus thundered forth and made the air's mid-region quake. He stays apart the two confronting bowls; he sings lauds in the potent Soma's joy when he hath drunk.
20.94.9 I bear this deftly-fashioned goad of thine wherewith thou, Maghavan, shalt break the strikers with the hoof. At the libation mayst thou be well satisfied. Partake the juice, partake the banquet, Bounteous Lord.
20.94.10 O Much-invoked, may we subdue all famine and evil want with store of grain and cattle. May we allied, as first in rank, with princes, obtain possessions by our own exertions.
20.94.11 Brihaspati protect us from the rearward, and from above, and from below, from sinners! May Indra from the front and from the centre, as friend to friends, vouchsafe us room and freedom.
;;; XCV ???
20.95.1 From the three jars the Great and Strong hath drunk drink blent with meal. With Vishnu hath he quaffed the flowing Soma juice, all that he would. That hath so heightened him the Great, the Vast, to do his mighty work. So may the God attend the God, true Indu Indra who is true.
20.95.2 Sing strength to Indra that shall set his chariot in the foremost place. Giver of room in closest fight, slayer of foes in shock of war, be thou our great encourager. Let the weak bowstrings break upon the bows of feeble enemies.
20.95.3 Thou didst destroy the Dragon: thou sentest the rivers down to earth. Foeless, O Indra, wast thou born. Thou tendest well each choicest thing. Therefore we draw us close to thee. Let the weak bowstrings break upon the bows of feeble enemies.
20.95.4 Destroyed be all malignities and all our enemy's designs. Thy bolt thou castest at the foe, O Indra, who would smite us dead: thy liberal bounty gives us wealth. Let the weak bow- strings break upon the bows of feeble enemies.
;;; XCVI ???
20.96.1 Taste this strong draught that gives thee vital vigour: with all thy chariot here unyoke thy coursers. Let not those other sacrificers stay thee, Indra: these juices shed for thee are ready.
20.96.2 Thine is the juice effused, thine are the juices yet to be pressed: our resonant songs invite thee. O Indra, pleased to-day with this libation, come, thou who knowest all, and drink the Soma.
20.96.3 Whoso, devoted to the God, effuses Soma for him with yearning heart and spirit, Never doth Indra give away his cattle: for him he makes the lovely Soma famous.
20.96.4 He looks with loving favour on the mortal who, like a rich man, pours for him the Soma. Maghavan in his bended arm supports him: he slays, unasked, the men who hate devotion.
20.96.5 We call on thee to come to us, desirous of booty, and of cattle, and of horses. For thy new love and favour are we present: let us invoke thee, Indra, as our welfare.
20.96.6 For life I set thee free by this oblation from the unknown decline and from consumption; Or, if the grasping demon have possessed him, free him from her, O Indra, thou and Agni.
20.96.7 Be his days ended, be he how departed, be he brought very near to death already, Out of Destruction's lap again I bring him, save him for life to last a hundred autumns.
20.96.8 With thousand-eyed oblation, hundred-autumned, bringing a hundred lives, have 1 restored him. That Indra for a hundred years may lead him safe to the farther shore of all misfortune.
20.96.9 Live waxing in thy strength a hundred autumns, live through a hundred springs, a hundred winters. Through hundred-lived oblation Indra, Agni, Brihaspati, Savitar yield him for a hundred!
20.96.10 So have I found and rescued thee: thou hast returned with youth renewed. Whole in thy members! I have found whole sight and all thy life for thee.
20.96.11 May Agni yielding to our prayer, the Rakshas-killer, drive away. The malady of evil name that hath beset thy labouring womb.
20.96.12 Agni, concurring in the prayer, drive off the eater of thy flesh, The malady of evil name that hath attacked thy babe and womb.
20.96.13 That which destroys the sinking germ, the settled, moving embryo, That which would kill the babe at birth, even this will we drive far away.
20.96.14 That which divides thy legs that it may lie between the married pair, That penetrates and licks thy side, even this will we exterminate.
20.96.15 What rests by thee in borrowed form of brother, lover, or of lord, And would destroyed the progeny,--even this will we exter- minate.
20.96.16 That which through sleep or darkness hath deceived thee and lies down by thee, And will destroy thy progeny,--even this will we exterminate.
20.96.17 From both thy nostrils, from thine eyes, from both thine ears and from thy chin, Forth from thy head and brain and tongue I drive thy malady away.
20.96.18 From the neck-tendons and the neck, from the breast-bones and from the spine, From shoulders, upper, lower arms, I drive thy malady away.
20.96.19 From viscera and all within, forth from the rectum, from the heart, From kidneys, liver and from spleen, I drive thy malady away.
20.96.20 From thighs, from knee-caps, and from heels, and from the forepart of the feet, From hips, from stomach, and from groin, I drive thy malady away.
20.96.21 From what is voided from within, and from thy hair, and from thy nails, From all thyself, from top to toe, I drive thy malady away.
20.96.22 From every member, every hair, disease that comes in every joint, From all thyself, from top to toe, I drive thy malady away.
20.96.23 Avaunt, thou Master of the Mind, I Depart and vanish far away. Look on Destruction far from us. The live man's mind is manifold.

20.97.1 Here verily yesterday we let the Thunder-wielder drink his fill. So in like manner, offer him the juice to day. Now range you. by the Glorious One.
20.97.2 Even the wolf, the savage beast that rends the sheep, follows the path of his decrees. So, India, graciously accepting this our praise, with wondrous. thought come forth to us.
20.97.3 What manly deed of vigour now remains that Indra hath not done? Who hath not heard his glorious title and his fame, the Vritra- slayer from his birth?

;;; CVI ???
20.106.1 That lofty energy of thine, thy strength and thine intelligence, Thy thunderbolt for which we long, our wish makes keen.
20.106.2 O Indra, heaven and earth augment thy manly power and thy renown, The waters and the mountains stir and urge thee on.
20.106.3 Vishnu, the lofty Ruling Power, Varuna, Mitra sing thy praise: In thee the Maruts' company hath great delight.
;;; CVII ???
20.107.1 Before his hot displeasure all the peoples, all the men bow down, As rivers bend them to the sea.
20.107.2 This power of his shone brightly forth when Indra brought to- gether like A skin the worlds of earth and heaven.
20.107.3 The fiercely-moving Vritra's head he severed with his thunder- bolt, His hundred-knotted thunderbolt.
20.107.4 In all the worlds That was the best and highest whence sprang the mighty God, of splendid valour. As soon as born he overcomes his foemen, he in whom all who lend him aid are joyful.
20.107.5 Grown mighty in his strength, with ample vigour, he as a foe strikes fear into the Dasa, Eager to win the breathing and the breathless. All sang thy praise at banquet and oblation.
20.107.6 All concentrate on thee their mental vigour, what time these, twice or thrice, are thine assistants. Blend what is sweeter than the sweet with sweetness: win quickly with our meath that meath in battle.
20.107.7 Therefore in thee too, thou who winnest riches, at every banquet are the sages joyful With mighter power, bold God, extend thy firmness: let not malignant Yatudhanas harm thee.
20.107.8 Proudly we put our trust in thee in battles, when we behold great wealth the prize of combat. I with my words impel thy weapons onward, and sharpen with my prayer thy vital vigour.
20.107.9 Worthy of praises many-shaped, most skilful, most energetic, Aptya of the Aptyas: He with his might destroys the seven Danus, subduing many who were deemed his equals.
20.107.10 Thou in that house which thy protection guardedh bestowest- wealth, the higher and the lower. Thou stablishest the two much-wandering Mothers, and bringest many deeds to their completion.
20.107.11 Brihaddiva, the foremost of light-winners, repeasts these holy prayers, this strength to Indra. He rules the great self-luminous fold of cattle, and all the doors of light hath he thrown open.
20.107.12 Thou hath Brihaddiva the great Atharvan, spoken to Indra as himself in person. The Matarisvaris, the spotless sisters, with power exalt him and impel him onward.
20.107.13 Bright, Presence of the Gods, the luminous herald, Siirya hath mounted the celestial regions. Day's maker, he hath shone away the darkness, and radiant passed o'er places hard to traverse.
20.107.14 The brilliant Presence of the Gods hath risen, the eye of Mitra, Varuna, and Agni. The soul of all that moveth not or moveth, Surya hath filled the earth and air and heaven.
20.107.15 Even as a lover followeth a maiden, so doth the Sun the Dawn, refulgent Goddess: Where pious men extend their generations before the Gracious One for happy fortune.
